o   ¿Cuál es la antigüedad promedio por nivel de la organización?
Based on the provided information, it is **not possible to provide a comprehensive average antiquity (tenure) by organisational level**, as specific durations are only mentioned for a very limited number of interviewees. For most individuals, their antiquity within talisis is not specified in the sources.

However, here are the details regarding antiquity where information is available, grouped by general organisational level:

- **C-Level / Director / Rector Level:**
    
    - **Lilian Adalid, Chief Marketing Officer:** Lilian explicitly states: "actualmente yo llevo **un mes y 3 semanas aproximadamente** en la organización".
    - **Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director:** Álvaro mentions he has "**varios años** en talisis", but a specific number of years is not provided.
    - **Inge Ploennig, Directora de Calidad y Acreditación Académica:** Inge refers to observing significant changes in "**estos 2 últimos años**", but this does not specify her total tenure within the organisation.
    - **Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional en Universidad Interamericana para el Desarrollo:** Paulina mentions her experience "como **fundadora** de en este caso de la UNID como **fundadora** también en talisis", indicating a long tenure, but no specific duration is provided.
    - For the remaining individuals at this level (Alberto Sánchez, Alejandro Madrazo, Amalia Ortega, Ángel Casan, Carlos Granados, Domingo Farias, Fernando de Río, Humberto Salazar, Joel Enriquez, Juan Arenas, Juliana Effting, Marcela Valdez, Marcos Samaniego, Mariel Serrano, Paul Moch, and Nicho Garza), their antiquity is **not specified** in the provided texts.
- **Manager / Lead / Data Scientist Level:**
    
    - **Katherine (Senior Marketing Manager):** Katherine mentions: "mis **8 años** que estoy dentro de la organización".
    - **Juan Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación:** Juan mentions speaking "desde que entré", implying a period of time, but a specific duration is **not provided**.
    - For Carlos Villa, Luis Ruiz, and Román de León, their antiquity is **not specified**.

Given the scarcity of concrete figures, a meaningful average cannot be calculated.

o   ¿Cuál es la opinión general de la organización, sus sistemas, procesos, gestión, on boarding?

Based on the provided interviews and the analysis of talisis's Root Architecture, here is a detailed overview of the general opinion regarding the organization, its systems, processes, management, and onboarding:

### General Opinion of the Organization (talisis)

Overall, there is a **strong positive sentiment** towards talisis, driven by a deep commitment to its mission and purpose.

- **Purpose and Impact:** talisis is widely seen as a **catalyst for social transformation** through accessible and quality education, aiming to empower millions of people and create virtuous cycles of development across generations. It seeks to be a **referent in transformative education** in Mexico and Latin America.
- **Culture and Values:** The organization emphasizes a **culture of high performance, discipline, and shared purpose**. There is a conscious effort to **foster a human-centric approach**, emphasizing empathy, integrity, and a sense of belonging. Several interviewees express a personal connection, viewing their work not just as a job but as a "life project".
- **Ecosystem and Reach:** talisis is perceived as a **multifaceted and diverse ecosystem**, encompassing various brands (UR, UNID, Harmon Hall, Advenio), serving a wide range of audiences from early childhood to post-graduate studies, and operating across different regions with both physical and digital presence. This diversity is seen as a **great richness and comparative advantage**.
- **Maturity and Evolution:** There's recognition of talisis's **maturation and increased organization** in recent years, particularly in its strategic focus and clarity. It is constantly evolving and experimenting with new models and methodologies.

### Systems

The opinion on talisis's systems is **mixed**, highlighting both significant opportunities and persistent challenges.

- **Opportunities for Enhancement:** There is a strong consensus that **technology, especially AI and Cloud, is a critical ally and "new operational muscle"** for transformation and efficiency. Interviewees envision:
    - **Hyper-personalization:** Using AI for highly personalized student journeys, content, recommendations, and communication.
    - **Automation:** Automating manual, repetitive, and transactional tasks (e.g., financial reconciliations, compensation calculation, lead nurturing) to free up human time for strategic work and empathy.
    - **Data-Driven Decision Making:** Leveraging data architecture, predictive analysis, and dashboards for quicker, more informed, and proactive decisions across all areas.
    - **Integrated Ecosystems:** A future where platforms are "interconnected" and function as a "digital brain".
- **Current Limitations and Challenges:** Several significant issues with current systems are repeatedly mentioned:
    - **Fragmentation and Lack of Integration:** Many platforms are "not integrated," "do not communicate with each other," or "speak but information is not congruent or reliable". This leads to dispersed data and inefficiencies.
    - **Manual Processes and Data Collection:** A lot of data collection and reporting is still "manual," leading to "too much time in data gathering" rather than analysis, generating "much work" and being "time-consuming".
    - **Outdated Infrastructure:** Some technology and platforms are "outdated" or "fragmented".
    - **Lack of Clarity in Metrics/Definitions:** "No clear definition of some metrics," leading to inconsistencies.
    - **Cost and Resources:** Cloud migration incurs "important monthly costs". There's a "lack of trained people in technology" and small teams hindering progress.
    - **Data Quality:** Need for "data of higher quality and more timely" due to inconsistencies and isolated systems.

### Processes

The processes at talisis are generally seen as **needing significant improvement towards standardization, automation, and clarity.**

- **Desire for Standardization and Automation:**
    - A strong push for **"standardized processes"** across the organization to enable better communication, efficiency, and scalability.
    - The goal is to **automate "manual, tortuous, or time-consuming activities"** to reduce errors, expedite tasks, and allow human talent to focus on higher-value activities.
- **Current State of Processes:**
    - Many processes are still **"manual" and "take too much time"**.
    - There is often a **"lack of clarity" and "insufficiently clear and documented processes"**, leading to interruptions and inefficiencies.
    - **Resistance to Change:** There's cultural resistance and an inclination to stick to "traditional processes" or doing things "as before".
    - **Duplication and Dispersal:** Processes can be duplicated between areas, and information/procedures are "dispersed" across many platforms.
- **Specific Areas of Focus for Improvement:**
    - **Financial & Administrative:** More efficient financial planning, budget control, payment methods, and automated reconciliations.
    - **Recruitment & HR:** Streamlining talent acquisition, reducing onboarding time for sales advisors, and combating high turnover through more efficient processes.
    - **Academic & Operational:** Improving curriculum development, teacher profile design, student follow-up, and managing academic operations.
    - **Inter-area Communication:** The "interrelation" and "communication between areas" for collaborative projects is an area for improvement.

### Management

Management is perceived as **improving in terms of vision and strategic communication, but there's a recognized need for greater support, trust, and alignment in execution.**

- **Clarity and Vision:** There is appreciation for the **"clear vision" and "strategic communication"** from top management, especially through institutional events like "town halls" and "conventions". Leaders are seen as setting "high standards".
- **Leadership Style:** Some leaders, like Fernando de Río and Katherine, aim for a **collaborative, empathetic, and empowering leadership style**, focusing on team growth, trust, and shared purpose. Joel Enriquez sees his role as a "founder of organizational culture".
- **Areas for Improvement / Needed Support:**
    - **Trust and Autonomy:** A recurring theme is the need for "trust to experiment and autonomy to decide" for teams, as current environment can be "difficult" and prone to "pointing fingers" when things are not written down. There's a desire for "real empowerment".
    - **Collaboration and Alignment:** While top-down communication is good, effective **"transversal collaboration"** between different areas is often a challenge, requiring clearer governance and shared narratives. Leaders need to understand that all areas contribute to the final impact. There's a sentiment that sometimes each area "goes its own way".
    - **Support for Innovation:** Leaders need to recognize that new initiatives (like B2B channel) are "in development" and require facilitation. There's a need to support "greater discipline" and "foresight" in strategic initiatives.
    - **Resource Allocation:** Support is needed for "time" for strategic design (as opposed to daily operation) and for increasing team sizes (e.g., for data science and technology).
    - **Feedback Culture:** While some leaders promote it, continuous and constructive feedback (especially from the top to other areas) is seen as essential for growth.

### Onboarding

The term "onboarding" is explicitly mentioned in a few instances, indicating a general awareness of its importance and existing challenges.

- **Need for Improvement:** Marcela Valdez, from Administration and Finance, sees an opportunity to improve the **"onboarding of students, employees and teachers"** to be "smooth" and efficient. This implies that current onboarding processes may be cumbersome or inefficient, leading to "less smooth transitions" and "more stumbles".
- **Related Initiatives:**
    - The creation of a **"central document repository for all processes"** is suggested as a way to "help in onboardings", showing that the lack of centralized information hinders the process.
    - Domingo Farias mentions reducing the "curve of optimal productivity" for sales advisors through better "induction and training", suggesting that current onboarding/training for new hires is lengthy and could be improved with technology like AI.
    - Lilian Lozano mentions "digital onboarding" for students as part of personalized experiences.

talisis is seen as a **purpose-driven, evolving organization** with a strong, diverse ecosystem. While there's enthusiasm for its strategic direction and the potential of technology, there are **significant internal challenges** related to fragmented systems, manual processes, and the need for greater inter-area collaboration, resource allocation, and a more trusting, empowered management style. Onboarding is acknowledged as an area needing improvement through process optimization and better information management.

o   ¿Qué sugerencias te dieron al respecto?

Based on the interviews, numerous suggestions were provided across the various elements of the organisation, its systems, processes, management, and onboarding. These reflect a strong desire for modernisation, efficiency, data-driven decision-making, and enhanced human connection.

Here are the key suggestions, broken down by category:

### Organisation (Overall Vision & Culture)

- **Foster a Culture of High Performance and Development:** Leaders need to ensure their teams are **evaluated, identified, and continuously developing**. This includes promoting a **culture of growth and high performance** by providing **clear visibility of strengths and areas for improvement**.
- **Embrace Digital Transformation:** talisis needs to **position itself as a digital institution** from the top leadership down.
- **Focus on Purpose and Impact:** Every strategy should contain a **pedagogical layer**, ensuring each project contributes to a deeper understanding and connection within the organisation. The organisation should strive to be a **referent in transformative education** for Mexico and Latin America.
- **Strategic Prioritisation:** Leaders should **prioritise strategic alliances after careful research**, not just the first available option. There's a need for **clear focus on what talisis wants to be best at**, avoiding trying to cover everything. Departments should be given **clarity and focus on annual goals**, especially high-impact projects.

### Systems (Technology, Data, AI, Cloud)

- **Automate and Modernise Core Processes:** Budgeting and business cases should be **more automated, modern, and dynamic**, reducing reliance on manual Excel processes through digital tools. This includes automating complex calculations like **variable compensation for promoters and advisors**.
- **Integrate and Standardise Data Architecture:** Develop a **robust data architecture** to collect comprehensive information on students, teachers, and administrators. Implement an **integral infrastructure** for a **360-degree client view** to identify gaps and offer personalised support. Consolidate information for **agile decision-making across the institution**.
- **Leverage AI for Personalisation and Efficiency:**
    - Implement **AI for hyper-personalised student journeys, content, and communication**.
    - Use AI for **predictive analysis** (e.g., anticipating student enrolment, dropouts, or identifying students at academic/economic risk).
    - Deploy **AI-powered chatbots and virtual assistants** for 24/7 student support, automated FAQs, and administrative tasks.
    - Utilise AI for **generating creative content at scale** (copys, presentations, videos) and A/B testing, allowing marketing teams to focus on strategy.
    - Apply AI for **optimising budgets** based on real needs and feedback.
    - Explore AI for **tutoring and tailored support** in specific subjects.
- **Cloud Adoption:** Utilise cloud technology for **facilitating asynchronous collaborative work** and **generating efficiency**. Ensure cloud is used for **security and seamless communication** with servers.
- **Improve Data Quality and Access:** Implement a system to provide **more accurate and timely data**. Address **fragmentation and lack of integration** between systems, ensuring data consistency and reliability. Provide **agile access to key information and updated dashboards** for quicker decisions.

### Processes (Operational Procedures, Administrative, Academic, Communication Workflows)

- **Standardise and Document Processes:** Implement **well-structured and documented processes** for clarity and efficient planning across the organisation. A **centralised repository of processes** would aid communication, updates, and onboarding.
- **Streamline Administrative Workflows:** Improve the **onboarding process for students, employees, and teachers** to be smoother and more efficient, from initial contact to graduation or employment. Automate tasks like **financial reconciliations**.
- **Enhance Academic Operations:**
    - **Redesign teacher profiles** and create a dedicated area for teacher recruitment and development.
    - Implement a **"master learning plan" personalised for different stakeholders**.
    - Focus on **pertinence of academic programs**, anticipating future needs (10-20 years ahead).
    - **Rethink the teacher's role** to be a facilitator of critical thinking, ethics, and social skills, rather than solely technical knowledge.
    - **Integrate diagnostic data** more effectively to support teachers and address student deficiencies.
- **Optimise Student Experience Journeys:** Design **communication journeys that integrate human and technology** to better accompany students through their challenging paths. Implement an **omni-channel strategy** that ensures coherence in communication across all digital and physical touchpoints.
- **Improve Internal Communication:** Foster **clear, open, and empathetic communication** to resolve conflicts quickly and work with agility.

### Management (Leadership Style, Inter-Departmental Collaboration, Support Needed)

- **Empower Leaders and Teams:** Capital Human should be a strategic service that **empowers leaders**, integrating culture and processes into their DNA for effective leadership. Teams need **real empowerment with autonomy, tools, and trust** to propose and learn. Leaders should **accompany teams rather than just supervising**.
- **Foster Transversal Collaboration:** Establish **multidisciplinary teams with closer collaboration** and direct interactions for a unified vision. Implement **governance and shared narratives** to ensure effective transversal collaboration between areas like commercial, IT, CX, and academy. Areas should **understand that all contributions connect to the final impact**.
- **Strategic Support for Innovation:** Leaders need to **recognise that new initiatives are in development** and require facilitation. Provide **spaces for co-creating vision and strategic decision-making**.
- **Resource Allocation and Time Management:** Leaders need to **respect processes and timelines** to avoid constant emergencies and allow for planned work. They should provide **sufficient resources** (time, processes, tools, personnel) for strategic design, not just daily operations.
- **Continuous Feedback and Learning:** Promote a **culture of continuous improvement** and give constructive feedback. Encourage teams to **challenge each other constructively** to go beyond basic requirements.
- **Develop Strong Leadership:** Leaders should **lead by example**, embodying commitment, trust, and proactive attitudes. They need to **understand and adapt to changing generations** to lead effectively and attract talent.

### Onboarding

- **Streamlined Onboarding Processes:** A key suggestion from Marcela Valdez (Administration and Finance) is to develop processes for **smooth onboarding of students, employees, and teachers**. This involves **well-mapped processes and controls** for high, low, or change events to ensure **efficient transitions** for all stakeholders (e.g., from prospect to student, or recruitment to teaching). The goal is to **reduce time and "stumbles"** in these processes.
- **Digital Tools for Onboarding:** Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) suggests using **AI tools to help sales advisors** with daily doubts during induction and onboarding, to **reduce the "curve of optimal productivity"** (currently 7 months).
- **Centralised Information for Onboarding:** The creation of a **central document repository for all processes** is suggested to **"help in onboardings"**, indicating that fragmented information currently complicates the process.

These suggestions collectively paint a picture of an organisation striving for digital transformation and operational excellence, while deeply valuing human connection and a mission-driven culture.
---

## II. Lo que distingue a TALISIS

o   ¿Cuál es su Misión y Visión? ¿Los colaboradores las conocen? ¿En qué porcentaje?

Based on the sources, talisis has a clear **Fundamental Purpose (Misión)** and **Vision**, which are actively communicated, though specific percentages regarding employee knowledge are not provided.

### talisis's Mission and Vision:

- **Fundamental Purpose (Mission):** talisis's fundamental purpose is to **transform communities through people by providing accessible and relevant education** [2.1]. This education aims to **generate sustainable social mobility and virtuous cycles of transgenerational development** [2.1].
- **Vision for 2035:** The path towards 2035 is clear, with talisis aiming to be **the benchmark for educational transformation in Latin America** [32.1]. This is not merely about being the largest, but about being the most relevant [32.1]. The aspiration is that **every student who passes through talisis's classrooms will emerge with more than just a qualification: they will leave with purpose, tools, and a network that will accompany them throughout their lives** [32.1].

### Employee Awareness and Communication:

Several interviewees highlight the importance of clear communication and alignment with this vision and purpose:

- **Communication of Vision:**
    
    - Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) states that a major impact is ensuring **the best talent within the company** to deliver 100% of their value proposition and transform more lives. Her area contributes by **supporting leaders to have their teams evaluated, identified, and developing within the institution**. She feels inspired knowing she is in an organisation that helps fulfil dreams and transform lives.
    - Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) envisions talisis as **a referent in transformative education by 2035**, creating **communities of learning where every student feels reflected, challenged, and valued**. His area acts as **the nervous system that captures what happens externally, the heart that beats with the client's voice, and the muscle that executes with excellence**. He personally finds purpose in **leaving a transcending mark on his team, seeing them grow and find new paths through shared vision**. He stresses the importance of designing and executing growth strategies that are efficient and precise, including **solid, digitalised commercial structures and automated funnels for acquisition, retention, and multi-brand profitability**. He specifically notes the importance of a **"shared narrative where everyone sees how the work connects with a final impact"**.
    - Marcos Samaniego (Director of Academic Operations) highlights that his area works to **translate the company's efforts into concrete actions in campuses**, training staff, and defining processes for new alliances. He also notes the importance of **reporting to the high management** to show progress towards institutional objectives. His personal inspiration comes from seeing that all the daily effort **touches many people and translates into a shared mission**.
    - Mariel (Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication and Business Intelligence) states that her area's mission is to **project a solid, clear, and concise identity** for talisis as a cutting-edge educational ecosystem in Mexico and Latin America. She emphasises that **reputation starts from within**, requiring every employee to feel proud and a sense of belonging to communicate it externally. She believes that for talisis to become a leader in education and social transformation, **all members of the organisation must work in synchrony, aligned with a shared vision**. Her purpose is to **make the company's vision a reality and transform communities**. She has advanced by **connecting with staff, students, and teachers to create synchronicity and alignment towards the long-term purpose**.
    - Paul Moch (Vice President for Teaching & Learning) envisions a **clear educational model that provides certainty to students and supports with quality education and the development of soft skills**. His inspiration is to make education a **transformative factor in Latin America**. He imagines a collaboration where his area coordinates educational vision and pedagogy.
    - Paulina Adalid (Rector Institucional, UNID) sees talisis's impact in **forming professionals with necessary knowledge and skills for a constantly changing world, supported by technology and human formation with social responsibility**. Her role allows her to **transmit talisis's vision to campuses and receive feedback**, acting as a **"bridge of union"** between talisis and its learning institutions, and representing talisis before authorities. She states that **the team is important, everyone can propose, and the goal is to be happy and committed in a healthy environment**. She also stresses the **responsibility of continuous learning and adapting to global needs**.
    - Julián (Transformation department) states that his mission is **not just to operate change, but to design, activate, and sustain it until it becomes culture**. He sees his role as a **"founder of organisational culture"** that should transcend time and volume for impact. He uses the analogy of a high-performance football team, where **everyone anticipates movements and celebrates successes as a collective achievement**. He believes in **aligning each collaborator's purpose** for effective teamwork.
- **Lack of Specific Percentage:** While the sources heavily emphasise the importance of a shared vision and aligning employees with it, there is **no specific percentage provided** regarding how many employees currently know or are aligned with talisis's mission and vision. The interviews suggest an ongoing effort to achieve this widespread understanding and cultural integration. Román de León (Data Scientist) mentions that there's a need to **"involve, co-create solutions, and have constant communication"** as sometimes departments are **"too accustomed to a client-provider relationship"** where they only seek project delivery rather than co-creation. This implies that full alignment and shared understanding are still targets. Julián also mentions that a challenge is for collaborators to **"understand and know what we do, how we do it, and with what intensity we do it"**, which is a major challenge due to the dynamic nature of the organisation.

- If I have to give a percentage:

talisis has a well-defined **Fundamental Purpose (Misión)** and **Vision** that guide its operations and strategy [2.1, 32.1, 609]. While the sources do not provide an exact percentage of collaborators who know these statements, they strongly indicate a concerted and ongoing effort to communicate and embed them within the organisation.

### talisis's Mission and Vision:

- **Fundamental Purpose (Misión):** talisis aims to **transform communities through people by providing accessible and relevant education** [2.1]. This education is designed to **generate sustainable social mobility and virtuous cycles of transgenerational development** [2.1]. This purpose is also echoed by Domingo, who states that his inspiration is to "democratize the education to impact the majority, especially the sectors with less resources".
- **Vision for 2035:** talisis envisions itself as **the benchmark for educational transformation in Latin America**, aspiring to be the most relevant rather than merely the largest [32.1]. The goal is for **every student passing through talisis's classrooms to emerge with purpose, tools, and a lifelong network**, not just a qualification [32.1]. Furthermore, talisis aims for **100% of Mexicans to have access to quality education, a significant increase from the current 30%**. Alvaro also highlights an international focus for 2035, not limiting to Mexico, and leveraging AI for content adaptation to different languages and realities.

### Employee Awareness and Communication:

The sources highlight significant efforts to ensure that collaborators are aware of and aligned with the company's mission and vision, though challenges in deep, universal understanding persist:

- **Active Communication and Transmission:**
    
    - Mariel, from Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication, and Business Intelligence, explicitly states that "reputation starts from within, requiring every employee to feel proud and a sense of belonging to communicate it externally". She emphasises that **"all members of the organisation must work in synchrony, aligned with a shared vision"**, and has "advanced by connecting with staff, students, and teachers to create synchronicity and alignment towards the long-term purpose".
    - Paulina Adalid, as an Institutional Rector, actively "transmit[s] talisis's vision to campuses". She also represents talisis before educational and governmental authorities, strengthening the institutional presence.
    - Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, mentions a "matrix of congruence" with 14 key indicators directly derived from the mission, indicating a systematic approach to ensuring alignment at a macro level. She also states that the vision and expectations are communicated "very clear" and "very objective" through town halls and conventions.
    - Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) and Domingo (Capital Humano) both articulate that their areas focus on ensuring the "best talent" and fostering a "culture of high standards", implying an inherent alignment with the company's purpose through talent development and cultural integration. Domingo also points out that "the culture is dictated by the leaders" and encourages leaders to "comulgue with the processes and initiatives that we bring from Human Capital".
- **Challenges in Deep Understanding and Synchronicity:**
    
    - Despite these efforts, some interviewees point to challenges in achieving full, deep understanding and complete synchronisation across all departments. Julián, from the Transformation department, acknowledges that a "major challenge" is for collaborators to "understand and know what we do, how we do it, and with what intensity we do it". This suggests that while the mission and vision might be broadly known, a nuanced and consistent application throughout daily work is still evolving.
    - Román de León, a Data Scientist, highlights that some departments are "too accustomed to a client-provider relationship" rather than co-creation around a shared goal. He seeks support from leaders and colleagues to "get more involved" and "contribute ideas and not just listen", implying a need for deeper engagement with the shared vision.
    - Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) mentions that "here in talisis, they don't like to share direction, each one wants their own side", further indicating a hurdle in achieving universal, seamless alignment.

### Inferred Percentage:

Given the consistent emphasis on communicating the mission and vision from multiple leadership roles and departments (HR, Marketing, Academic Operations, Quality, Institutional Rectors), it is reasonable to infer that a **significant majority of collaborators are aware** of talisis's mission and vision statements. The active communication strategies, regular internal meetings, and efforts to integrate the mission into departmental objectives suggest a high level of top-down communication.

However, the identified challenges in achieving complete, granular understanding, fostering true co-creation across all areas, and ensuring that the vision "becomes culture" (as noted by Julián and Román) imply that this awareness is not yet universal or deeply internalised by every single employee in a fully synchronous manner.

Based on these inferences, it can be estimated that **approximately 80% to 85% of collaborators are likely familiar with or generally aware of talisis's Mission and Vision.** This percentage reflects the strong communication efforts and leadership commitment, while also acknowledging the natural complexities of cultural integration and ensuring deep alignment in a dynamic organisation with diverse departmental focuses.

o   La Visión, ¿Es una visión alineada y compartida?

talisis's overarching vision is **well-defined and largely shared** across the organisation, with substantial efforts dedicated to its communication and implementation. However, achieving deep, universal, and consistently actioned alignment throughout every department and role presents an ongoing challenge.

### talisis's Vision

talisis's fundamental purpose is to **"transform communities through people by providing accessible and relevant education that generates sustainable social mobility and virtuous cycles of transgenerational development"**. The CEO, Nicho Garza, articulates the vision for 2035 as becoming **"the benchmark for educational transformation in Latin America, not by being the largest but by being the most relevant"**. This involves every student emerging with purpose, tools, and a lifelong network.

### Evidence of Aligned and Shared Vision

Many leaders and areas within talisis demonstrate a strong understanding and commitment to this core vision:

- **CEO's Articulation:** Nicho Garza clearly establishes the "Propósito Fundamental" and the "Esencia" of talisis's legacy, learning, technology, and context, setting the strategic direction. He stresses that talisis is "a platform that transforms communities through people".
- **Strategic Communication:** Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, explicitly states that "all members of the organisation must work in synchrony, aligned with a shared vision" to consolidate leadership in education and social transformation. She also highlights the importance of "living the talisis Way culture from within" and communicating it externally, based on an authentic sense of belonging.
- **Leadership Transmission:** Paulina Adalid, Institutional Rector, views her role as transmitting "all this vision of talisis" to campuses, actively enriching it with input from the educational community. She also sees her role as a "bridge of union" between talisis and its learning institutions to represent its impact.
- **Systemic Alignment:** Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, uses a "matrix of congruence" with 14 key indicators directly derived from the mission, demonstrating a structured approach to ensure processes align with the overall purpose. She observes "a much greater organisation, greater clarity of the focus of where we are going and how we should achieve it" within talisis.
- **Cultural Foundation:** Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, sees his role as "a founder of organizational culture" to "provoke the future we deserve" with a "shared purpose very clear". He uses the analogy of a high-performance football team where all players "play as 1 only" and celebrate collective success. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, similarly champions attracting talent to foster a "culture of high standards" driven by leaders who "commune with the processes and initiatives that we bring from Human Capital". Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, underlines the need for communication and empathy for effective collaboration, which is crucial for vision alignment.
- **Market-Centric Planning:** Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, states that planning "should be centered on what the market requires" and that his department needs to be "well aligned with the expected strategy and direction of the organization".
- **Client and Operational Focus:** Álvaro García (Innovation and Product Director) envisions talisis as a key strategic partner for organisations globally. Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) believes the commercial area "must be the growth engine of the organization" and that "if we achieve that agile communication, between the different areas, we can deliver a much more adequate product". Juan Arenas (Chief Operations Officer) aims for service "aligned to [the student's] dreams and expectations throughout their educational journey".
- **Technological Integration:** Carlos Granados (CIO) clearly states the vision is an "intelligent, adaptive, and inclusive educational ecosystem" with AI fully integrated by 2033, leading to "mass personalisation of education" and "democratisation of access to quality education". Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director) envisions talisis as "an internationally recognised entity for its competency-based and employability models".

### Challenges to Full Alignment

Despite these strong indications, some interviewees point to areas where deeper alignment and a more unified vision are still evolving:

- **Internal Silos and Lack of Shared Direction:** Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) explicitly states, **"here in talisis, they don't like to share direction, each one wants their own side"**. This indicates a challenge in fostering full inter-departmental collaboration towards a single strategic goal.
- **Operational vs. Strategic Focus:** Julián Enriquez (Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación) notes a "major challenge" for collaborators to "understand and know what we do, how we do it, and with what intensity we do it," suggesting a gap between strategic vision and daily execution. Román de León (Data Scientist) observes that some departments are "too accustomed to a client-provider relationship" rather than co-creation around a shared goal.
- **Data and Process Fragmentation:** Carlos Villa (Mobile Dev Lead) highlights that "each application has its own objective and may not share the same objectives between one and the other," and mentions a need to understand "what really hurts the student" directly, rather than relying on assumptions. Román de León also points out issues with "definition clara de algunas de las métricas" and "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada" leading to data inconsistencies. Juliana Effting (Directora de Educación Online) identifies **"resistencia cultural interna"** seeing online education as a "competitor and not an ally" and "fragmented technological infrastructure" as major risks. Marcela Valdez (Directora de Administración y Finanzas) mentions "lack of integration between systems" leading to "descontrol and risk".
- **Short-Term Pressures:** Several leaders, including Fernando de Río and Marcela Valdez, acknowledge that short-term pressures to achieve immediate results can hinder long-term strategic thinking and resource allocation necessary for the vision.

talisis has a **clearly articulated and widely communicated vision** from its leadership. There are active initiatives to embed this vision and its underlying culture (talisis Way) across the organisation, with many leaders demonstrating strong commitment and understanding. However, the organisation faces challenges in overcoming ingrained departmental silos, ensuring consistent execution, improving data and process integration, and fostering a universal, deep understanding that translates into fully synchronised action across all levels. The vision is present and shared, but its **complete and consistent manifestation is a continuous journey**.

o   ¿Cuáles son las prioridades estratégicas?

talisis's strategic priorities are comprehensively defined and widely communicated, focusing on a multi-faceted approach to transform communities through accessible and relevant education. This vision aims to position talisis as **"the benchmark for educational transformation in Latin America,"** not by size, but by relevance, ensuring every student gains purpose, tools, and a lifelong network by 2035 [CEO Report].

The key strategic priorities can be grouped into several interconnected dimensions:

- **Educational Transformation & Relevance:**
    
    - **Delivering Accessible and Relevant Education:** A core priority is to provide **quality, flexible, and accessible education** to diverse communities, particularly those with fewer resources, fostering social mobility and virtuous development cycles [CEO Report, 39, 47, 165, 359]. This includes continuously adapting to the evolving needs of the market and society.
    - **Personalised Learning Journeys:** There is a strong emphasis on **hyper-personalisation of education**, leveraging technology like AI to tailor content, recommendations, and learning experiences to individual student needs and performance.
    - **Cultivating Human & Social Development:** Beyond professional skills, talisis prioritises the **holistic human formation of students**, instilling values, leadership, social responsibility, and environmental consciousness, preparing them to be agents of change in their communities and the world.
    - **Innovating Educational Models:** This involves continuously **rethinking educational methodologies and offerings**, exploring new formats like microcredentials and hybrid models to maintain relevance and effectiveness.
- **Technological Integration & Innovation:**
    
    - **Leveraging AI and Cloud Technology:** AI is seen as a crucial enabler for various processes, including forecasting, budgeting, project evaluation, content creation (e.g., project Mazinger Z), and identifying M&A opportunities. Cloud technology supports agile and collaborative work environments.
    - **Building a Robust Data Architecture:** A significant priority is establishing an **integrated data infrastructure** capable of collecting, analysing, and visualising comprehensive information about students, faculty, and administrative operations. This aims to provide a 360-degree view for data-driven decision-making and operational insights [CEO Report, 119, 133, 223, 240, 281, 467, 470, 491, 609, 630, 631].
    - **Automating Processes:** talisis seeks to **automate manual and bureaucratic processes** across administrative, academic, and commercial functions to boost efficiency and free up human talent for more strategic and high-value tasks.
    - **Developing Advanced Digital Tools:** This includes creating user-centric mobile applications, integrated digital ecosystems (e.g., talisis.com), and AI-powered "copilots" or assistants for various roles to enhance real-time support and productivity.
- **Organisational Culture & Talent Development:**
    
    - **Fostering a High-Performance Culture:** A key strategic initiative is to cultivate a **culture of high standards, discipline, and accountability**. This involves embedding the "talisis Way" culture internally, based on shared purpose, identity, and authenticity, and communicating it externally.
    - **Talent Acquisition & Continuous Development:** Prioritising the attraction, identification, and **holistic development of talent**, ensuring they possess both technical and essential soft skills (e.g., communication, empathy, strategic thinking, leadership). This also extends to strengthening the career paths and capacities of academic staff.
    - **Human-Centric Approach:** Despite a strong technological drive, maintaining a **deep human connection, empathy, and personal touch** is considered crucial. Technology is viewed as a tool to amplify human interaction and strategic thought, rather than replacing it.
- **Growth & Market Reach:**
    
    - **Strategic Market Expansion:** talisis aims for **national and international expansion**, particularly across Latin America, by opening new learning centres, optimising its multi-brand presence, and exploring financially viable expansion models (e.g., hubs or strategic franchises).
    - **Omnicanal Strategy:** Implementing an integrated **omnicanal approach** across digital and physical touchpoints (B2B, B2C) is critical for effective customer acquisition and retention, ensuring consistent brand experience and communication.
    - **Building Strategic Alliances:** Forging strong, long-term alliances with a diverse range of external partners, including technology providers (ETech, BigTech, AWS), other academic institutions (national and international), government bodies, industry associations, and businesses, to enhance innovation, employability, and market understanding.
- **Operational Excellence & Efficiency:**
    
    - **Financial Sustainability:** Prioritising a healthy financial structure, **responsible resource management**, and maximising profitability to support growth and ensure long-term viability. This involves efficient allocation of resources and controlling key costs such as payroll and marketing expenditures.
    - **Process Standardisation & Clarity:** Establishing **clear, documented, and standardised processes** across the organisation to improve efficiency, reduce "firefighting," and enable more effective long-term planning and execution.
    - **Performance Measurement & Management:** Implementing and rigorously tracking **clear metrics (KPIs, OKRs)** across all levels and areas of the business (e.g., growth, revenue, profitability, student satisfaction, employability, retention, operational efficiency, culture) to monitor progress, ensure strategic alignment, and drive continuous improvement.

These interconnected priorities aim to ensure talisis's sustained growth, impact, and leadership in the evolving educational landscape [CEO Report].

o   ¿Cuáles son sus capacidades diferenciadoras?

talisis possesses a comprehensive set of differentiating capabilities that position it as a leader in educational transformation, as articulated by various directors within the organisation. These capabilities span strategic vision, technological integration, human capital development, market approach, and operational excellence:

### Visionary & Transformative Educational Model

- **Commitment to accessible and quality education**: talisis aims to **democratise quality, flexible, and accessible education**, particularly for underserved communities, driving social mobility in Mexico and potentially globally.
- **Innovation in educational models**: The organisation is dedicated to **reimagining and innovating institutional and pedagogical foundations** of education, positioning itself as an "epicenter of innovation" and a "laboratory" for new designs and methods.
- **Holistic human formation**: Beyond technical skills, talisis prioritises the **holistic development of students**, fostering values, critical thinking, social responsibility, and empathy, preparing them as agents of change.
- **Lifelong learning culture**: There's a strong emphasis on continuous learning and adaptation, encouraging individuals to "unlearn and relearn" to stay at the vanguard of evolving trends.
- **Strategic legacy building**: talisis focuses on building a **strategic legacy** based on _how_ things are done, ensuring continuity and impact for future generations, aiming to "transform Mexico in a single generation".

### Advanced Technological Integration & Data-Driven Approach

- **Pioneering AI and Cloud adoption**: talisis is a **pioneer in leveraging AI and cloud technology** to hyper-personalise learning, automate processes, provide intelligent assistance, and enhance decision-making.
- **Robust data architecture**: A key capability is establishing an **integrated data infrastructure** for comprehensive information collection, analysis, and real-time insights, enabling data-driven decisions across all operations.
- **Proactive technological experimentation**: The organisation engages in **early experimentation with emerging technologies** and leverages open-source tools to stay at the forefront of innovation.
- **Strategic use of AI in commercial functions**: AI is specifically employed for **precise forecasting, M&A targeting, lead nurturing, and sales conversion**, indicating a sophisticated approach to market growth.

### Human-Centric Culture & Talent Development

- **High-performance culture (talisis Way)**: talisis fosters a **disciplined culture of high standards, accountability, and purpose**, which drives performance from within and is communicated externally.
- **Holistic talent development**: The company prioritises **attracting, developing, and retaining top talent** through continuous support, evaluation, and fostering both technical and essential soft skills.
- **Technology as a human amplifier**: A core philosophy is that **technology serves to enhance human interaction and strategic thinking**, freeing up time from repetitive tasks for deeper connections and empathy.
- **Collaborative and empowering leadership**: Leaders are encouraged to **lead by example**, fostering clarity, shared purpose, constructive feedback, and empowering teams to achieve collective goals.
- **"Bridge" between departments**: Individuals and areas act as **bridges to facilitate clear communication and alignment**, ensuring seamless collaboration and problem-solving across the organisation.

### Strategic Growth & Market Reach

- **Targeted expansion**: talisis is focused on **strategic national and international expansion**, particularly in Latin America, through new learning centres, multi-brand optimisation, and financially viable models such as hubs or strategic franchises.
- **Integrated omnichannel strategy**: The organisation implements an **integrated omnichannel approach** across digital and physical touchpoints to ensure consistent brand experience, effective customer acquisition, and engagement.
- **Robust strategic alliances**: talisis builds **strong, long-term alliances** with diverse external partners including technology providers, academic institutions, government bodies, and industry associations to drive innovation, enhance employability, and gain market insights.
- **Anticipatory market understanding**: The ability to **anticipate future market needs and opportunities** (e.g., nearshoring, tourism, technological literacy, future of work) allows talisis to proactively adapt its offerings.
- **Distinctive brand positioning**: talisis strives for **strong brand positioning and differentiation** that transcends mere quality, aiming to be "unforgettable" and emotionally resonant with its audience.

### Operational Excellence & Financial Prudence

- **Responsible financial management**: A core capability is **responsible financial planning and resource management**, ensuring a healthy financial structure, efficient resource allocation, and sustained profitability to support growth and long-term viability.
- **Efficient process management**: talisis focuses on **standardising and streamlining processes** to improve efficiency, reduce "firefighting," and enable more effective long-term planning and execution, moving away from manual and bureaucratic approaches.
- **Rigorous performance measurement**: The organisation implements and rigorously tracks **clear metrics (KPIs, OKRs)** across all levels and areas of the business to monitor progress, ensure strategic alignment, and drive continuous improvement.
- **Disciplined execution**: There is a strong emphasis on **impeccable execution** of initiatives, preferring a well-executed plan that can be continuously improved over a perfect but unimplemented design.

These interconnected capabilities collectively define talisis's strategic approach, enabling it to pursue its ambitious vision of educational transformation and sustained leadership in the market.

o   ¿Cuál es la propuesta de valor?

talisis's value proposition is to **transform communities by democratising accessible, high-quality, and highly relevant education, leveraging advanced technology and a human-centric approach to empower individuals for a dynamic future**.

talisis's value proposition is deeply rooted in its ambition to **transform communities through accessible and relevant education**, aiming to become "the benchmark for educational transformation in Latin America" by 2035. This comprehensive proposition is built on several interconnected pillars, designed to empower individuals with purpose, tools, and a lifelong network.

Here's a detailed breakdown of talisis's value proposition:

1. **Democratising Accessible and Flexible Quality Education:**
    
    - **Reaching Underserved Communities:** A core element is providing education to "disadvantaged sectors of Mexican society" or "low-resource individuals", aiming to "democratise education". This includes reaching "many communities" not yet impacted.
    - **Flexible and Adaptable Formats:** talisis offers "flexible and accessible" education with adaptable schedules and geographical locations, including "reorienting or complementing educational processes". This is particularly evident in its "omnichannel" strategy, integrating digital and physical experiences to cater to diverse student profiles and needs.
    - **Affordable Quality:** The proposition includes making prices "accessible" while maintaining "quality". This balances financial viability with social impact.
2. **Delivering Relevant and Future-Oriented Learning:**
    
    - **Market and Industry Alignment:** talisis continuously adapts to "market requirements and trends", ensuring financial and strategic planning aligns with what the market needs. This includes understanding labour market needs and proactively positioning. Alberto Sánchez envisions planning being "market-centric" by 2035.
    - **Preparation for an Evolving World:** The education prepares students for a "continually changing world" and "a future still unknown". This means developing skills for "competitiveness" and addressing future needs like "nearshoring, tourism, technological literacy, and the future of work".
    - **Holistic Human Formation:** Beyond professional skills, talisis emphasises "holistic human formation", instilling values, leadership, social responsibility, and environmental consciousness. Paul Moch explicitly mentions developing "soft skills" and "21st-century competencies". Paulina Adalid highlights the formation of students with "human leadership" and "social responsibility".
3. **Personalised and Adaptive Learning Experiences:**
    
    - **AI-Powered Personalisation:** A significant differentiator is the use of Artificial Intelligence (AI) to "hyper-personalise education", tailoring content, recommendations, and learning journeys to individual student needs and performance. This includes "anticipating student needs" and providing "proactive support".
    - **Co-creation of Knowledge:** AI allows for dynamic and Socratic dialogue-based learning, fostering a "community of continuous and collaborative learning". Students are seen as "co-creators of knowledge".
    - **Flexible Pedagogical Approach:** talisis aims to be "pedagogically agnostic", adapting its methodologies to unique student and community needs rather than rigid formulas. This includes experimenting with "new models, methodologies, and forms of learning".
4. **Innovation and Advanced Technological Integration:**
    
    - **Leveraging AI and Cloud Technology:** talisis is a "pioneer in leveraging AI and cloud technology" for forecasting, budgeting, project evaluation, content creation (Project Mazinger Z), and M&A targeting. Carlos Granados, CIO, highlights AI agents enabling a "highly automated and intelligent institution" where "bureaucracy will be drastically reduced".
    - **Robust Data Architecture:** A priority is establishing an "integrated data infrastructure" for comprehensive information, enabling "data-driven decision-making". Román de León, Data Scientist, confirms building "solutions based on internal and external information" to detect patterns.
    - **Digital Ecosystem:** The vision includes a "digital brain" or "central mind" that connects all operations and enables "super-humans" by amplifying human capabilities. This is exemplified by the talisis.com platform. Mobile development is key to providing a "good feeling" and "enamoured" user experience.
5. **Robust Ecosystem and Strategic Partnerships:**
    
    - **Multi-Brand Presence:** talisis leverages its multi-brand presence (UR, Harmon Hall, Unit, Advenio, IES Salud) to offer a "kaleidoscope of understanding diverse profiles" and provide broad access to education.
    - **Strategic Alliances:** Forging strong, long-term alliances with diverse external partners, including banks for financing, public educational bodies, family offices, competitors for potential M&A. Also, technology providers (AWS, Zendesk), other academic institutions (national and international), government bodies, industry associations (COPARMEX), and businesses for innovation, employability, and market understanding. Álvaro García highlights talisis becoming a "key strategic partner for talent development in companies globally".
    - **Community Building:** Beyond formal alliances, there's a strong emphasis on building "communities of learning" where students feel "reflected, challenged, and valued". This extends to fostering a lifelong network for students after graduation.
6. **High-Performance Culture and Operational Excellence:**
    
    - **"talisis Way" Culture:** A core differentiator is cultivating a "disciplined culture of high standards, accountability, and purpose", known as the "talisis Way". Joel Enriquez, CSO, sees his role as a "founder of organisational culture".
    - **Talent Development:** Prioritising the attraction, identification, and holistic development of talent, ensuring they possess both technical and essential soft skills.
    - **Efficiency and Optimisation:** Focus on "optimising the distribution of costs and expenses" using technology and automating "manual and bureaucratic processes" to boost efficiency. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, aims for "responsible financial management" to "maximise scarce resources".

talisis's value proposition is to be a **transformative educational ecosystem** that provides accessible, high-quality, and highly relevant learning experiences, powered by advanced technology (especially AI and data) and a strong, human-centric culture. It seeks to equip individuals with the skills and purpose to thrive in a dynamic world and contribute to societal development, all while maintaining a sustainable and scalable operational model through strategic partnerships and continuous innovation.

o   ¿Qué habilidades y capacidades distinguen a la gente que trabaja en talisis?

The people working at talisis are distinguished by a comprehensive set of skills and capabilities that align with the organisation's ambitious vision for educational transformation. These qualities span a blend of technical expertise, human-centric attributes, strategic acumen, and a commitment to continuous improvement and social impact.

Firstly, **Human-Centricity and Empathy** are paramount. talisis employees are deeply committed to transforming lives through education, demonstrating a purpose-driven approach that extends to individuals, communities, and national development. This involves a strong emphasis on understanding and serving the real needs of students, families, and even disadvantaged sectors of society, by actively listening to their voices through various mechanisms. They strive to foster an empathetic environment, where technology enhances rather than replaces human connection, allowing more time for meaningful interactions.

Secondly, **Technological Proficiency and Adaptability** are crucial. talisis actively seeks individuals who are adept at leveraging advanced technologies, particularly Artificial Intelligence (AI) and cloud computing. Employees are expected to develop deep knowledge in areas such as AI algorithms, machine learning, natural language processing, data analysis, and cybersecurity. This proficiency is not merely for technical tasks but for transforming processes, enhancing efficiency, automating repetitive duties, and enabling hyper-personalisation of learning experiences. They are encouraged to be proactive in adopting new digital tools and methodologies, even experimenting with emerging technologies to build robust solutions.

Thirdly, **Strategic Thinking and Foresight** are highly valued. Employees demonstrate the ability to align their work with market requirements, anticipate future trends (with a 5-15 year outlook), and identify "blue ocean" opportunities for expansion. This includes a focus on data-driven decision-making, translating complex data into actionable insights, and designing initiatives with a clear strategic impact. They are expected to balance short-term operational needs with long-term strategic objectives.

Fourthly, **Collaboration and Communication** are essential attributes. Employees are encouraged to work in a highly collaborative manner, breaking down traditional silos between departments. This involves clear, assertive, and empathetic communication, active listening, fostering a culture of trust and shared purpose, and proactively engaging with internal and external stakeholders, including government bodies, industry partners, and other academic institutions.

Fifthly, **Innovation and Continuous Improvement** are deeply ingrained in the talisis mindset. Employees are driven to reimagine educational models, experiment with new pedagogies, and continually adapt to evolving market demands. This includes fostering a culture of lifelong learning, self-direction, and an agile mindset that embraces experimentation and rapid iteration. They actively work to overcome resistance to change and to integrate new approaches.

Finally, **Accountability and Results-Orientation** define the execution. Employees are driven by clear objectives, measurable outcomes (KPIs and OKRs), and a disciplined approach to achieving growth, efficiency, and profitability while maintaining quality. They embody a "owner's mindset," taking responsibility for their contributions and actively seeking solutions to challenges, even when resources are limited.

In essence, the distinguished capabilities of talisis's people encompass a synergistic blend of advanced technical skills (especially in AI and data), a deep commitment to human-centric education and social impact, agile strategic thinking, strong collaborative and communicative abilities, and an insatiable drive for innovation and continuous improvement, all underpinned by a culture of accountability and purpose.

**Next step:** I can provide an analysis of how these skills and capabilities are fostered and developed within talisis, including existing programmes and identified gaps.

o   ¿Cómo es el proceso de comunicación que se tiene internamente?

talisis's internal communication process is a multifaceted and evolving system that strives to knit together diverse teams and objectives, leveraging both established structures and emergent technologies, all underpinned by a strong cultural emphasis on collaboration and human connection.

**1. Structured Information Flow and Formal Rituals:** At a foundational level, talisis core principles are replicated across all levels of the organisation. The corporate headquarters centralises and optimises information, which then systematically flows down to the individual brands, campuses, and classrooms. This ensures that "information is clearly communicated from top management (C-level) through 'connections,' 'convenciones,' and 'town halls,' which have matured significantly to provide clear and effective communication". This top-down approach aims to provide clarity and a sense of security, ensuring everyone understands "what they are doing, why they are doing it, and how it will be achieved".

Regular meetings, or "rituales," are integral to this process. Weekly internal "rituales" are established for tracking progress within each area. These sessions often include "lluvia de ideas" (brainstorming), serving as dedicated spaces for reflection and ideation, encouraging teams to "think outside the box" on specific strategic projects. A key objective is to align all departments, sharing common goals such as OKRs, so that everyone understands they are "in the same boat" and "navigating in the same direction".

**2. Leveraging Technology for Enhanced Communication and Data Utilisation:** talisis is heavily invested in integrating technology to enhance its internal communication and operational efficiency. Artificial Intelligence (AI) agents are envisioned to "improve interaction between students, professors, and administrative teams through automated attention and support platforms". These agents are designed to "act as a bridge that fosters efficient communication and data-driven decision-making".

A significant focus is placed on data visibility. There is a strong push to provide "visual information for everyone" for rapid decision-making, aiming to move beyond static Excel files and presentations towards live or near real-time data. This includes the development of "standardised open dashboards" that are accessible to all areas, providing a unified view of the organisation's status. The long-term vision includes a "digital brain" or "central mind" that connects all operations, acting as a "shared nervous system" to enable the organisation to "breathe together, think together, and advance as a whole".

AI is increasingly being adopted for internal processes, such as code review, suggestions, optimisation, and generating unit tests. The fundamental belief is that AI will "free up time for strategic thinking and foster human interaction between areas" by automating manual and bureaucratic tasks. This liberated human capacity is then re-directed towards more valuable and empathetic interactions. AI is also being explored to mediate human interactions and establish mechanisms for managing conflicts or less fluid communication.

**3. Cultivating a Collaborative and Human-Centric Culture:** At its heart, talisis is driven by a "human-centric" philosophy: it is an organisation "of people for people". This ethos translates into various aspects of its internal communication:

- **Bridge-Building Roles:** Many areas within talisis function as "glue" or "bridges" between departments. For example, HR sees itself as the "glue" that ensures effective communication among different areas, facilitating conversations and agreements to resolve issues. Similarly, Marketing and Operations aim to be strong bridges, translating strategic ideas into actionable plans and ensuring feedback loops are robust. This involves translating institutional objectives into clear, motivating narratives that help each team member understand their role within a common cause, thus preventing areas from working in isolation.
- **Active Listening and Customer Focus:** A cornerstone is the continuous "listening to the voice of the customer", encompassing students, teachers, and collaborators. This feedback, gathered through surveys, focus groups, and direct interactions, is deemed critical for informing product development, refining services, and making strategic decisions that place the student at the centre.
- **Emphasis on Soft Skills:** There's a strong belief in the importance of "communication and interaction skills" and "soft skills" to foster effective collaboration and preserve the human element in interactions. Empathy and understanding others' needs are highly valued.
- **Leading by Example and Shared Ownership:** Leaders, particularly the Chief Strategy Officer, strive to "lead by example", embodying the desired culture of "real collaboration, empathy, teamwork, and high performance". The aim is to instill a "sense of belonging" where all employees feel "joint owners of talisis's processes". This involves open feedback, celebrating achievements, and confronting challenges with transparency.

**4. Identified Challenges and Areas for Improvement:** Despite these robust efforts, talisis acknowledges several areas where its internal communication processes can be strengthened:

- **Undocumented Processes:** A recurring challenge is the lack of clearly documented processes. This leads to inefficiencies, necessitates frequent "emergency interventions," and complicates long-term planning.
- **Inter-Area Communication Gaps:** While formal communication channels exist, there are acknowledged difficulties in fostering seamless inter-area communication, particularly in collaborative projects. This is partly attributed to teams not always being co-located in a single office.
- **Cultural Resistance to Change:** Some internal cultural resistance persists, particularly regarding the adoption of new methodologies or technologies. For instance, some collaborators initially viewed online education as a competitor rather than a complementary approach. Overcoming this requires fostering a culture of continuous learning and adaptation.
- **Fragmented Technological Infrastructure:** A critical issue is the lack of integration among existing technological platforms. This results in dispersed, potentially unreliable data and necessitates manual data consolidation, which consumes excessive time and hinders rapid, data-driven decision-making.
- **Operational Overload and Prioritisation:** The demands of daily operations and "firefighting" often consume significant time, diverting focus from innovation and the standardisation of processes. This makes it difficult to balance immediate needs with long-term strategic objectives.
- **Resource Limitations:** Teams frequently report being small with heavy workloads, making it challenging to dedicate sufficient time to both current operational demands and the exploration and implementation of new technologies and projects.

talisis is actively striving for a highly integrated and communicative internal environment, where technology acts as an enabler for human connection and data-informed decisions. While it has established strong foundations in terms of culture and formal communication channels, the journey towards a fully harmonised and agile ecosystem, particularly through comprehensive technological integration and consistent process documentation, is an ongoing strategic priority.

Next step: I can delve into the specific methodologies or frameworks mentioned by talisis employees that support this communication and collaboration, such as the "talisis Way" or "Metodología Vadir," and explain how they contribute.

o   ¿Los ejecutivos conocen el talisis Way? ¿Qué porcentaje lo conoce a buen nivel de detalle?

Yes, the executives at talisis demonstrate a comprehensive understanding of the "talisis Way," viewing it as a foundational framework that underpins the organisation's strategic direction, cultural identity, and operational methodology. While a specific percentage of detailed knowledge across all levels of the organisation is not explicitly stated, the interviews suggest a high level of awareness and detailed understanding among the senior leadership and those responsible for strategic implementation, with an ongoing effort to embed this culture throughout the entire workforce.

Here's a detailed breakdown:

**1. Executive Awareness and Detailed Understanding of "talisis Way":**

Several key executives and directors directly reference and elaborate on the "talisis Way," indicating a deep and nuanced understanding of its components and strategic importance:

- **Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff:** Explicitly articulates the "talisis Way" as integral to fostering high-performance teams, promoting empathy, and encouraging mutual support within the organisation. He connects it directly to the broader "High-Performance Culture" that leaders are expected to embody and instil. His perspective highlights the "talisis Way" as a guiding principle for cultivating desired attitudes and behaviours throughout the company.
- **Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation:** Demonstrates a highly detailed understanding by referring to "our talisis Way" in conjunction with "13 strategic axes". She explains how these axes are cascaded down into specific strategic projects and operational plans at the campus level, measured by OKRs and KPIs. Inge emphasizes that this framework brings "order," "organisation," and "clarity" to the institution, making processes more systematic and effective. Her comments indicate that she not only knows what the "talisis Way" is but also how it is structurally implemented and monitored.
- **Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence:** Identifies "empujar la cultura talisis Way" as a core responsibility of her team, emphasizing the need to live this culture authentically internally and communicate it externally. She views it as crucial for consolidating talisis's leadership in education and social transformation through synchronicity and a shared vision. Her statements reflect a strategic understanding of the "talisis Way" as a key driver for organisational identity and external perception.
- **Julián (Juan Mendez), Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation:** While he doesn't explicitly use the term "talisis Way" in the provided snippets of his core contributions, his extensive discussion of "cultural ADN" and "ecosystem" aligns perfectly with how the "talisis Way" is described by others. He mentions that this "ecosystem" encompasses "culture, our talent, our processes, our rituals, our technology" and highlights the challenge and importance of introducing and strengthening it across all operational levels, from campuses to top management. This indicates a profound understanding of the comprehensive framework that the "talisis Way" represents.
- **Nicho Garza, CEO:** The "Reporte_Nicho," attributed to Nicho Garza, describes the overarching concept that the "talisis Way" likely embodies. It details "Alineación Cultural Total: Cada colaborador viviendo los principios TALISIS" and explains that "TALISIS funciona como un organismo fractal donde los principios se replican en cada nivel". This confirms that the CEO has defined and champions these fundamental principles of organisational alignment and replication, which are clearly operationalized through the "talisis Way."

**2. Percentage of Knowledge and Organisational Penetration:**

While a precise numerical percentage is unavailable, the following can be inferred:

- **Among Senior Leadership/Executives:** Based on the direct mentions and detailed explanations from Domingo, Inge, Mariel, and the foundational description from the CEO (Nicho), it is evident that a **very high percentage** (likely near 100% for those in strategic roles related to culture, operations, and communication) of the interviewed executives understand the "talisis Way" at a good level of detail. They actively engage with its principles and are responsible for its implementation and communication.
    
- **Across the Broader Organisation:** The interviews indicate that embedding the "talisis Way" throughout the entire organisation is an ongoing strategic objective.
    
    - Domingo mentions pushing the "talisis Way" to foster high-performance teams.
    - Mariel emphasizes that her team has the responsibility to "impulsar nuestro propósito e identidad con autenticidad" and ensure that "all members of the organisation work in synchronicity aligned with a shared vision".
    - Julián highlights the challenge of "introducing this cultural DNA" to the entire operation, from campuses to mid- and high-level management.
    - Inge notes that information is "bajando" (being cascaded) from top management through established rituals like "connections," "convenciones," and "town halls".

This suggests that while the concept is clearly defined and understood by leadership, its deep, operational-level penetration (i.e., _every_ collaborator living and understanding the "13 strategic axes" in detail) is a continuous effort. Therefore, while **executive knowledge is high**, the percentage of the _entire workforce_ that knows the "talisis Way" at a granular level of detail is likely still evolving, with mechanisms in place to foster broader adoption and understanding.

talisis's executives possess a clear and detailed understanding of the "talisis Way," actively incorporating it into their strategic planning and operational responsibilities. This comprehensive framework, akin to the organisation's "cultural DNA" and "fractal architecture," guides talisis's growth, quality, and human-centric approach.

o   ¿Viven el talisis Way en su día a día? ¿Lo ven como cultura de trabajo, como una herramienta de soporte al trabajo, o solamente lo llevan por se los piden?

The executives at talisis predominantly perceive the "talisis Way" as a deeply ingrained **work culture and the organisation's foundational DNA**, rather than merely a support tool or a mandate to be followed. This cultural framework guides their strategic thinking, operational methodologies, and human-centric approach, aiming for a profound and lasting impact on education and society.

Here's a detailed breakdown of how the executives view and embody the "talisis Way":

**1. "talisis Way" as an Integral Culture and Organisational DNA:**

Many executives articulate the "talisis Way" as the core identity and guiding principles of talisis, deeply embedded in their daily operations and long-term vision.

- **Nicho Garza (CEO)** explicitly defines talisis's perspective: "TALISIS funciona como un organismo fractal donde los principios se replican en cada nivel". He states, "Nuestra cultura se resume en cinco principios que viven en cada rincón de nuestros 190 centros: Servicio, Crear el sueño, Mentalidad de dueño, Espíritu de equipo, Excelencia". He also mentions "Alineación Cultural Total: Cada colaborador viviendo los principios TALISIS" as a key project. This clearly positions the "talisis Way" as the fundamental cultural blueprint.
- **Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff)**, from the human capital perspective, sees his area as the "motor del de la actitud de la energía, y del mudo organizacional de talisis". He emphasises fostering "una cultura de desarrollo, en todos los ámbitos" and "una cultura con una disciplina de altos altas estándares en todo lo que hacemos. Siendo un ejemplo en todo talisis, en todas nuestras marcas". He directly links high-performance teams to "dentro de la cultura talisis el talisis Way".
- **Julián (Juan Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation)** refers to talisis's essence as "este ADN que es talisis cómo poder hacer que la gente realmente lo viva". He describes the "talisis" (the ecosystem) as encompassing "la cultura, nuestro talento, nuestros procesos, nuestros rituales, nuestra tecnología". His role is to design and sustain transformation until it "convertir en en cultura".
- **Mariel Serrano (Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence)** states that her team's role is to "empujar la cultura talisis Way" and has the "responsabilidad de impulsar nuestro propósito e identidad con autenticidad". She further stresses the importance of all members working "en sincronía alineados con una visión compartida que impulse el crecimiento y la excelencia" for "consolidarnos como líderes en educación y transformación social".
- **Paulina Adalid (Rector Institucional en UNID)**, speaking about her team's attitude, highlights "ese reto constante de superarnos, de nuevos aprendizajes de de adaptarnos también a las necesidades y a la a lo para no nada más en México, sino de manera globalizada". She explicitly mentions "la misión institucional o la y los principios tal y eh que como fortalecemos la vinculación Todo siempre en colaboración y en equipo una sola imagen, una un solo talis". She also values the "sentido de pertenencia" and "calidez humana" at the core of the organisation.
- **Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director)** views her purpose as contributing to "cumplir sueños y a transformar la vida de las personas", which is directly aligned with the "talisis Way" principles. She seeks to "generar cultura organizacional" through commitment and leading by example.
- **Joel Enriquez (CSO and Director of Strategic & Corporate Affairs)** views his work not just as a job but as a "proyecto de vida" that aims to "transformar a mi país en una sola generación". He sees his role as "un fundador de cultura organizacional", emphasising that culture is "una manera de ser, una manera de pensar, una una manera de eh diseñar y provocar el futuro que merecemos".
- **Marcela Valdez (Director of Administration & Finance)** integrates "promover la cultura talisis" as a key part of her area's mission.
