She also mentions "mentalidad de dueño con los propósitos de de Tallys, mentalidad de dueño excelencia, servicio, crear el sueño y el espíritu de equipo" as core aspects of the legacy.

**2. "talisis Way" as a Framework and Tool for Support and Operational Excellence:**

Beyond being a cultural identity, executives also describe the "talisis Way" as a practical framework, a set of methodologies, and tools that support daily work and drive efficiency.

- **Inge Ploennig (Director of Quality & Academic Accreditation)** provides a very concrete example. She details how "our talisis Way" incorporates "13 strategic axes" that are "cascadeado" (cascaded) down into "proyectos estratégicos y planes que se ejecutan en el campos para lograr esa misión". She highlights that this framework brings "orden," "organización," and "claridad" to institutional processes, measured by OKRs and KPIs. This demonstrates a clear application of the "talisis Way" as an operational tool.
- **Juan Arenas (Chief Operations Officer)** emphasises efficiency through "procesos muy ordenados, que permitan tener claridad desde el una admisión a la universidad hasta el momento que es egresado". His area "contribuye a que precisamente al ser que al hacer que sucedan las cosas" through alignment with "esas directrices, esos procesos, esos objetivos", indicating a structured approach to operations aligned with the overarching framework.
- **Carlos Granados (CIO)**, in his vision for AI agents, mentions "automatización inteligente" and "decisiones basadas en datos precisos y en tiempo real" to reduce bureaucracy and make processes agile and effective. While not directly naming the "talisis Way," his focus on structured, data-driven improvement aligns with its principles of "Excelencia" and efficiency.
- **Luis Ruiz (Software Development Manager)** describes his role as building "integraciones entre nuestros diferentes sistemas" and aims to reduce manual tasks through technology. This supports the "talisis Way" through technological enablement.
- **Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director)** speaks of "procesos más estandarizados que nos permitan comunicarnos de manera transversal," "compartiendo objetivos como son los OKRs," and "tener un lenguaje en común". She also mentions "workflows interáreas" and "dashboards abiertos que también estén estandarizados". This points to the "talisis Way" fostering operational alignment and efficiency through shared tools and processes.
- **Carlos Villa (Mobile Dev Lead)**, while focusing on mobile development, highlights the importance of well-developed applications with "good feeling" to make users "enamore de nuestro producto". This aligns with the "Servicio" principle and creating a positive experience for the student.
- **Román (Data Scientist)** describes using algorithms and data architecture to "construye soluciones personalizadas o motores de recomendación" and "dar visibilidad a la organización de manera oportuna para tomar decisiones más estratégicas". This is a direct application of data science to support the "talisis Way" principle of "Excelencia" through "eficiencia inteligente".

**3. Beyond Mere Compliance – A Driving Purpose:**

The interviews consistently demonstrate that executives engage with the "talisis Way" not out of obligation, but because they believe in its transformative power and inherent value.

- **Humberto (Commercial Area)** expresses deep satisfaction in seeing students "crecer profesionalmente, logra crecer como persona, y eso les ayuda a tener 1 mejor situación familiar, económica y profesional". This personal motivation aligns directly with the "talisis Way"'s fundamental purpose of "Transformar comunidades a través de las personas mediante educación accesible y pertinente que genere movilidad social sostenible y ciclos virtuosos de desarrollo transgeneracional".
- **Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer)** states his personal purpose as "dejar huella que trascienda con mi equipo, con mi rol, con con mi persona" and seeing "un crecimiento real en en las personas". He connects this to the "talisis Way" vision of "rompió las barreras entre educación formal y educación o o formación continua entre lo digital y lo humano". He views the projects as "puertas abiertas a una etapa de crecimiento, impacto social, liderazgo en la educación privada en en México y para países".
- **Paul Moch (VP for Teaching & Learning)** explicitly states his "propósito de vida ha sido pensar en cómo poder ayudar a que la educación sea un el gran factor transformador y de desarrollo de América Latina". This deep personal conviction reinforces that the "talisis Way" is lived, not just followed.
- **Katherine Romero (Senior Marketing Manager)** finds inspiration in "el propósito de talisis? Transformar comunidades a través de las personas". She sees her role as "guardián del propósito, cuidar que todo lo que se comunique esté alineado a la misión de talisis".
- **Juliana Effting (Director of Online Education)** is moved by "saber que hago una contribución positiva para el mundo y para las comunidades de México generando una transformación de vidas a través de de la educación". This personal drive goes far beyond simple compliance.

**Conclusion:**

Based on the executive interviews, the "talisis Way" is clearly understood and embraced as a **comprehensive cultural framework**. It is seen as the **organisational DNA** that defines who talisis is and how it operates, rather than just a set of rules imposed from above. It also functions as a **strategic and operational support tool**, providing clarity, structure, and a common language for decision-making, process improvement, and technological integration. Ultimately, for the executives, the "talisis Way" is **a living philosophy and a driving purpose** that genuinely inspires them and their teams to achieve a long-term, transformative impact on education and society. The consistent effort across different departments to align with and promote these principles demonstrates a profound commitment that goes well beyond mere compliance.

### III. Principales retos y oportunidades. ¿Qué les quita el sueño?

o   ¿Cuáles han sido los principales retos de talisis durante los últimos 3 años?

talisis has navigated a complex and rapidly evolving educational landscape over the past three years, facing a myriad of challenges that span technological, operational, cultural, and market-related domains. These challenges often interlink, demanding integrated and adaptive strategic responses from various departments across the organisation.

Here are the principal challenges talisis has encountered during the last three years:

**1. Digital Transformation & Technological Debt:** A significant hurdle has been the rapid pace of technological evolution, particularly in **Artificial Intelligence (AI) and cloud computing**, and the subsequent need for talisis to integrate these advancements effectively while addressing existing technological debt.

- **Legacy Systems and Data Integration:** Many executives highlight issues with disparate systems that do not "speak to each other," leading to fragmented and unreliable data. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration & Finance, specifically notes the "lack of integration between systems (SAP/Core Banner) leading to open controls and discrepancies," which implies significant operational and financial risks. Román, a Data Scientist, also points out that "metrics definition not clear" and "platforms change, metrics change, hard to keep up with small team". This fragmentation hinders agile decision-making and efficient operations.
- **Pace of Technology Adoption:** There's a recognised slowness in adopting new technologies, including AI, within various areas. Luis Ruiz, Software Development Manager, mentions the "rapid technological advances... causes lagging". Carlos Granados, CIO, aims for full AI integration by 2033, indicating a long journey ahead for complete maturity. The challenge extends to "overcoming the fear of technology" and fostering a practice-oriented approach.
- **Automation and Efficiency:** While AI and cloud are seen as tools to simplify tasks, automate processes, and enhance efficiency, the current state often involves manual and bureaucratic processes that consume significant time and resources. Julián Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, specifically sees the "automation of processes (making them more effective, faster, intelligent, systematic)" as a key challenge.
- **Infrastructure Costs:** The migration to cloud technologies, while beneficial, brings "costs associated with cloud migration," which need careful management.

**2. Market & Customer Dynamics:** talisis operates in a highly competitive and evolving educational market, which poses challenges in terms of differentiation, customer engagement, and adapting to new learning paradigms.

- **Market Saturation and Competition:** The market is described as "saturated with many institutions, formats, promises," making it difficult to demonstrate "real differentiation". New "low-cost competitors" and the "emergence of new ETX" (educational technology companies) further intensify this challenge. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, highlights the "aggressive competition" in the growing education market.
- **Changing Customer Expectations:** Students are increasingly behaving like "digital consumers," demanding "immediacy, comparison, personalisation, and social validation". There's a shift towards "micro-credentials" and "non-traditional education", which redefines the perception of "prestige" from years of study to "applicability and speed". Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional en UNID, notes that students expect the same "fluidity, personalization, omnichannel" experience as services like Spotify or Netflix.
- **Perception of Online Education:** There's an ongoing need to build trust and educate the market that "online education in Mexico also works, and can be accessible, flexible and of quality". A "negative perception that the student may have of the quality of online" is a critical risk.
- **Relevance of Offerings:** The rapid changes in technology mean that "before a student finishes their degree, the content, bibliography, needs to be updated". There's a challenge to ensure the "pertinence of academic programs" and think beyond current market offerings to what should be offered in 10-20 years.
- **Economic Context:** The "economic deceleration and the pressure for profitability" mean students are more focused than ever on the "cost-benefit relationship of their education". Marcela Valdez points out the direct impact of "complicated and recessive economic environments" on students' ability to pay, affecting enrollment and payment methods.

**3. Internal Organisational & Cultural Cohesion:** Challenges related to internal alignment, communication, and fostering a cohesive culture across a multi-brand organisation.

- **Resistance to Change:** A recurring theme is the "resistance to change" and adherence to "traditional processes". Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, notes that new initiatives "imply new ways of thinking and operating, stopping doing campaigns by intuition to work with data, automating processes that were 100% manual," which "usually generates a lot of friction".
- **Cross-Functional Collaboration & Siloed Operations:** There's a "lack of real collaboration between areas" leading to a "fragmented chain". Executives often highlight departments operating in "silos" or having "misaligned priorities", which impedes efficient project execution and a shared strategic direction. Juan Arenas, COO, states that "lack of prioritization and slow implementation" are critical challenges.
- **Multi-Brand Integration:** Integrating the distinct identities and cultures of different brands (U-ERRE, Harmon Hall, UNID, Advenio) within talisis is difficult. Álvaro García, Innovation & Product Director, highlights the need for talisis staff to "relate with the brands" not just as administrators but as clients or even teachers to understand daily student life.
- **Communication & Alignment:** Despite efforts like "Town Halls", there's a need for "clear, effective, and assertive communication". Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, highlights that the "talisis Bit" project faces obstacles if "collaborators don't understand, and, therefore, don't commit". Juan Mendez notes the challenge of making people "really live" the "talisis ADN" across all levels.

**4. Human Capital & Talent Management:** Ensuring the right talent is in place, adequately trained, and motivated to drive talisis's ambitious goals.

- **Talent Acquisition & Retention:** Challenges include "attracting the best talent" and being "rigorous" in hiring the right fit for each position. High turnover, especially among commercial advisors, is a concern, with long hiring times. Paul Moch, VP for Teaching & Learning, cites "lack of hands to develop many of my activities" as a key challenge.
- **Training & Upskilling:** There's a continuous need for employees to "develop abilities, especially soft skills" and "technological skills". Paulina Adalid mentions that students often arrive with "precarious knowledge" and "emotional and affective situations" post-pandemic, which requires teachers to be continuously trained and supported. Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, lists a vast array of technical and soft skills needed for her team to keep pace.
- **Productivity & Efficiency:** Domingo Farias notes the "lack of visibility of productivity" in many positions beyond commercial roles. He also points to the external challenge of "regulations changing... from 48 hours to 40 hours", which necessitates greater productivity in fewer hours.
- **Leadership Maturity:** Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, highlights that "talent retention and development... requires a certain maturity in our leaders, which... takes time". This maturity is crucial for leaders to embody the desired high-performance culture.
- **Union and Sociopolitical Factors:** Domingo Farias points out that "syndicates protect the employee disproportionately, and... do not allow... a culture of high standards of high performance to prosper". These factors can "wear out a lot" the negotiation processes.

**5. Financial & Operational Efficiency:** Managing resources, optimising investments, and ensuring sustainable growth in a complex environment.

- **Budgetary Constraints:** Many initiatives are limited by "lack of budget", and there's a constant need to "maximise scarce resources". Román, a Data Scientist, frequently mentions the need for a dedicated budget to expand his team and for continuous professional development.
- **Cost Management:** Marcela Valdez indicates a basic priority of "vigilating that the minimum cash flow is covered" and "not losing that minimum profitability". The "increase in marketing costs" across the market also presents a challenge.
- **Prioritisation and Focus:** There's a recognised issue of being "saturated with projects" that are "not necessarily all priorities", leading to a "lack of clear prioritisation". This makes it difficult to allocate "limited resources" effectively.
- **Operational Control for Growth:** Humberto highlights the need for "operational control before inorganic growth/expansion". The expansion of U-ERRE, for example, is linked to a significant "economic theme".
- **Measuring Impact:** While there's a strong desire to measure outcomes, challenges exist in having "clear measurement" for things like social media engagement or the true impact of marketing on educational decisions.

These challenges collectively underscore the complexity of transforming an educational institution like talisis in a rapidly changing world, highlighting the need for continuous adaptation, strong leadership, and strategic investments.

Next step: We could explore the specific opportunities that talisis executives identify as key enablers for overcoming these challenges.

o   ¿Cuáles son los principales retos para este 2025?
talisis faces a multi-faceted array of challenges in 2025 and the immediate coming years, stemming from rapid technological advancements, evolving market dynamics, internal operational complexities, and a fluid socio-economic and regulatory landscape. These challenges often interlink, demanding comprehensive and adaptive strategic responses across the organisation.

Here are the principal challenges anticipated for talisis in 2025:

**1. Accelerating Digital Transformation and Resolving Technological Debt:** A primary challenge for talisis in 2025 revolves around effectively integrating advanced technologies, particularly Artificial Intelligence (AI) and cloud computing, while simultaneously addressing existing technological deficiencies.

- **System Fragmentation and Data Inconsistency:** A significant hurdle is the prevalence of disparate systems that do not interoperate seamlessly (e.g., SAP/Core Banner), leading to fragmented, unreliable data, and open controls that pose operational and financial risks. This lack of integration hinders agile decision-making and operational efficiency.
- **Pace of Technology Adoption vs. Market Speed:** Despite the recognised need for AI and cloud integration, there is a perceived slowness in adopting these new technologies across various departments. The rapid pace of technological change (e.g., generative AI models, quantum computing) means talisis risks "lagging" or being "left behind" if it cannot implement new technologies more quickly.
- **Automation of Manual Processes:** Many internal processes remain manual and bureaucratic, consuming significant time and resources. The challenge is to automate these processes to make them more effective, faster, intelligent, and systematic, freeing up human capital for higher-value tasks. Specific areas for automation include variable compensation calculations, and student-facing administrative tasks.
- **Infrastructure Costs and Scalability:** The transition to and maintenance of cloud technologies, while beneficial for asynchronous work and efficiency, incurs significant monthly costs that require careful management.
- **Data Quality and Centralisation:** There is a critical need for clearer metric definitions, higher quality data, and a consolidated data view across the organisation. The current lack of a well-designed master data system and periodic closures in core systems contribute to data discrepancies and control risks.

**2. Navigating Evolving Market Dynamics and Intense Competition:** talisis operates in a highly competitive educational market, requiring constant adaptation to new learning paradigms and customer expectations.

- **Market Saturation and Differentiation:** The market is "saturated with many institutions, formats, [and] promises," making it difficult to demonstrate "real differentiation". New low-cost competitors and emerging educational technology (EdTech) companies further intensify this challenge. The imperative is to design "unforgettable" offerings with tangible, differentiating value, communicated with clarity and emotion.
- **Changing Customer Expectations:** Students are increasingly behaving like "digital consumers," demanding "immediacy, comparison, personalisation, and social validation". There is a shift towards "micro-credentials" and "non-traditional education," where "prestige" is redefined by "applicability and speed" rather than years of study. The challenge is to offer personalised experiences and develop what students _really_ need, rather than what the internal team assumes.
- **Perception of Online Education:** There is an ongoing need to build trust and educate the market that "online education in Mexico also works, and can be accessible, flexible and of quality". A "negative perception that the student may have of the quality of online" is a critical risk to overcome.
- **Relevance of Academic Offerings:** Due to rapid technological changes, academic content and bibliography become quickly outdated, even before a student completes their degree. The challenge is to ensure the "pertinence of academic programs" and to anticipate future needs (5, 10, 15, even 20 years ahead), rather than just reacting to current market offerings.
- **Increasing Marketing Costs and Saturation:** Marketing expenses are escalating across the market, not just in education, due to advertising saturation and digital fatigue. This necessitates more emotional and purpose-driven content to cut through the noise and foster community.

**3. Strengthening Internal Organisational and Cultural Cohesion:** Internal alignment, communication, and fostering a cohesive high-performance culture across a multi-brand organisation present significant challenges.

- **Resistance to Change:** A recurring theme is the "resistance to change" and adherence to "traditional processes". New initiatives, especially those involving data-driven approaches and automation, generate "friction" as they imply new ways of thinking and operating.
- **Cross-Functional Collaboration and Siloed Operations:** A "lack of real collaboration between areas" leads to a "fragmented chain". Departments often operate in "silos" or have "misaligned priorities," impeding efficient project execution and a shared strategic direction. There is a need for clear processes and improved inter-area communication to avoid duplication and ensure alignment.
- **Multi-Brand Integration:** Integrating the distinct identities and cultures of different brands (U-ERRE, Harmon Hall, UNID, Advenio) within talisis is difficult and requires significant effort to achieve a unified vision and operational synergy.
- **Cultural Adoption of "talisis ADN":** A key internal challenge is ensuring that all collaborators "really live" the "talisis ADN" – its purpose, values, and principles. This involves communicating effectively and fostering commitment from within the organisation. The talisis Bit project aims to address this by synchronising communication and actions across all areas.
- **Project Prioritisation:** The organisation is "saturated with projects" that are "not necessarily all priorities," leading to a "lack of clear prioritisation". This makes it difficult to allocate limited resources effectively and shifts focus from strategic long-term initiatives to short-term "firefighting".

**4. Optimising Human Capital and Talent Management:** Ensuring the right talent is in place, adequately trained, and motivated is crucial for talisis's ambitious goals.

- **Talent Acquisition and Retention:** Challenges include "attracting the best talent" and being "rigorous" in hiring the right fit for each position. High turnover, especially among commercial advisors, is a concern, with long hiring times (40-50 days). Retaining and empowering teachers is also a critical challenge.
- **Training and Upskilling for New Demands:** There is a continuous need for employees to develop new skills, particularly in AI, digital tools, analytics, and soft skills (communication, empathy, critical thinking). This requires continuous training, often needing dedicated budgets and time for professional development.
- **Productivity and Efficiency:** There is a "lack of visibility of productivity" in many non-commercial positions, and the shift to fewer working hours (e.g., 40-hour week) necessitates greater productivity in less time. Additionally, reducing the time it takes for new advisors to reach optimal productivity (currently 7 months) is a target.
- **Leadership Maturity:** Developing and retaining talent "requires a certain maturity in our leaders, which... takes time". This leadership maturity is crucial for leaders to embody the desired high-performance culture and effectively manage their teams.
- **Student Support Needs:** Students, particularly post-pandemic, are arriving with "precarious knowledge" and "emotional and affective situations" that require teachers to be continuously trained and supported to address these evolving needs.

**5. Addressing Financial Pressures and Operational Efficiency:** Managing resources effectively, optimising investments, and ensuring sustainable growth in a complex environment are ongoing challenges.

- **Budgetary Constraints and Profitability Pressure:** Many initiatives are limited by "lack of budget," and there is a constant need to "maximise scarce resources". The "economic deceleration and the pressure for profitability" mean students are more focused than ever on the "cost-benefit relationship of their education". A basic priority is "vigilating that the minimum cash flow is covered" and "not losing that minimum profitability".
- **Funding Strategic Initiatives:** Key strategic projects, such as the Promecap exit, U-ERRE's expansion, and mergers and acquisitions (M&A), face significant economic challenges related to capital and debt raising, and generating sufficient EBITDA.
- **Optimising Cost Distribution:** The focus is not just on reducing costs, but on "efficiently distributing" them across necessary categories, making strategic use of technology to achieve this.

**6. Navigating External Regulatory and Socio-political Factors:** External macro-environmental factors significantly influence talisis's operations and strategic direction.

- **Labour Regulations and Union Influence:** Changes in labour regulations (e.g., reduced working hours) demand increased productivity. Moreover, socio-political factors and union influences in Mexico are seen as challenging, as "syndicates protect the employee disproportionately, and... do not allow... a culture of high standards of high performance to prosper," leading to draining negotiation processes.
- **Socio-economic and Security Context:** The overall socio-economic situation in Mexico directly impacts families' ability to invest in education, affecting new enrollments and payment methods. Security concerns in regions where talisis has a presence also pose a challenge.
- **AI Regulation and Ethics:** The nascent regulatory framework for AI, particularly concerning data protection and ethics, presents an evolving challenge. talisis needs to ensure compliance and operate ethically as it integrates AI more deeply into its educational ecosystem.

These challenges collectively highlight the dynamic environment in which talisis operates. Addressing them effectively will require continuous adaptation, strong leadership, strategic investments, and a concerted effort to foster an agile and purpose-driven culture.

Based on this comprehensive overview of challenges, we could now discuss potential strategic recommendations for talisis to mitigate these risks and transform them into opportunities, focusing on which challenges should be prioritised in 2025.

o   ¿Cuáles son los principales retos que se tienen para los próximos 3 años?

talisis faces a complex and interconnected set of challenges over the next three years (2025-2027), a period explicitly identified as crucial for "Consolidación tecnológica y cultural". These challenges span technological, operational, cultural, market, human capital, financial, and regulatory dimensions, demanding a multi-faceted and agile strategic response.

Here are the principal challenges anticipated for talisis for 2025-2027:

### 1. Technological Consolidation and Digital Transformation

A core focus for talisis in the coming years will be the effective integration and leveraging of advanced technologies, while simultaneously addressing existing digital shortcomings.

- **Data Infrastructure and Quality:** A fundamental challenge is the pervasive issue of fragmented and inconsistent data. Many interviewees highlight the lack of a well-designed master data system, disparate systems that do not interoperate seamlessly, and slow or unreliable data updates [Inge 270, 281; Marcela 481, 490; Román 600; Katherine 384, 408; Luis 449]. This directly hampers agile decision-making and operational efficiency. The need for clearer metric definitions and a consolidated data view is critical [Román 600].
- **Automation of Manual Processes:** A significant portion of internal processes remain manual and bureaucratic, consuming considerable time and resources [Domingo 175, 182; Juan Mendez 339, 340; Inge 270]. Specific examples include the complex calculation of variable compensation for promoters and advisors, which is currently "very tortuous" [Domingo 177], and student administrative tasks like managing graduation requirements [Carlos 152]. The challenge is to automate these processes to be "more effective, faster, intelligent, and systematic" [Juan Mendez 339].
- **Pace of Technology Adoption and Integration:** Despite recognising the imperative for AI and cloud integration, there is a perceived slowness in adopting these new technologies across various departments [Domingo 186; Juan Mendez 340]. The rapid pace of technological change means talisis risks "lagging" or being "left behind" if it cannot implement and integrate new technologies more quickly [Luis 453; Román 613]. Existing platforms often "do not speak well to each other," leading to inefficiencies and unreliability [Katherine 231; Inge 281; Juliana 366].
- **Cloud Infrastructure Costs:** The transition to and ongoing maintenance of cloud technologies, while beneficial for efficiency and asynchronous work, incurs significant monthly costs that require careful management [Carlos 155].
- **Talent and Resource Gaps for Technology:** There is a notable lack of sufficient and adequately skilled technical personnel within the organisation to lead and execute ambitious digital transformation projects, such as data architecture or AI implementation [Luis 456; Marcos 514; Román 620]. This necessitates relying on external partners, which itself presents challenges.

### 2. Cultural Transformation and Organisational Cohesion

The "Consolidación cultural" phase (2025-2027) highlights internal alignment, communication, and fostering a cohesive high-performance culture across a multi-brand organisation as significant hurdles.

- **Resistance to Change:** A recurring theme is the "resistance to change" and adherence to "traditional processes" [Alejandro 52; Juan Mendez 340; Katherine 231; Juliana 366; Paulina 576]. New, data-driven initiatives or automation often generate "friction" as they imply new ways of thinking and operating, challenging the "if it worked before, why change it?" mentality [Katherine 231].
- **Cross-Functional Collaboration and Siloed Operations:** A "lack of real collaboration between areas" leads to a "fragmented chain" [Katherine 231]. Departments frequently operate in "silos" or have "misaligned priorities," impeding efficient project execution and a shared strategic direction [Katherine 231; Lilian 439; Mariel 538; Román 592, 615, 616].
- **Multi-Brand Integration:** Integrating the distinct identities and cultures of different brands (U-ERRE, Harmon Hall, UNID, Advenio) within talisis is a complex endeavour, requiring significant effort to achieve a unified vision and operational synergy [Juan Arenas 324].
- **Fostering a High-Performance Culture and Ownership:** There's a challenge in instilling a consistent culture of accountability, proactivity, and high performance ("talisis ADN") across all levels of the organisation [Domingo 163, 168, 195, 198; Amalia 114; Juan Arenas 324]. This includes developing leadership maturity to effectively manage and motivate teams [Amalia 114].
- **Project Prioritisation and Focus:** The organisation often finds itself "saturated with projects" that "are not necessarily all priorities," leading to a lack of clear focus and resource dispersion [Domingo 190; Juan Arenas 325; Juan Mendez 340; Lilian 439]. This can result in short-term "firefighting" rather than strategic long-term initiatives [Lilian 439, 440].

### 3. Market Adaptability and Relevance

talisis operates in a highly competitive educational market, necessitating constant adaptation to new learning paradigms and evolving customer expectations.

- **Market Saturation and Differentiation:** The market is "saturated with many institutions, formats, [and] promises" [Katherine 223, 227], making it difficult to demonstrate "real differentiation" [Katherine 223]. New low-cost competitors and emerging EdTech companies further intensify this challenge [Álvaro 88; Juan Arenas 320; Juliana 363, 366]. The imperative is to design "unforgettable" offerings with tangible, differentiating value [Katherine 223, 227].
- **Changing Customer Expectations:** Students are increasingly behaving like "digital consumers," demanding "immediacy, comparison, personalisation, and social validation" [Katherine 222, 227]. There's a shift towards "micro-credentials" and "non-traditional education," where "prestige" is redefined by "applicability and speed" rather than years of study [Katherine 222, 227].
- **Perception of Online Education:** There is an ongoing need to build trust and educate the market that "online education in Mexico also works, and can be accessible, flexible and of quality" [Juliana 363]. Overcoming the "negative perception that the student may have of the quality of online" is a critical risk to overcome [Juliana 366].
- **Relevance of Academic Offerings:** Due to rapid technological changes, academic content and bibliography can become quickly outdated [Inge 268, 269]. The challenge is to ensure the "pertinence of academic programs" and to anticipate future needs [Inge 269].
- **Increasing Marketing Costs:** Marketing expenses are escalating across the market, not just in education, due to advertising saturation and digital fatigue, leading to higher costs per lead (CPL) [Alberto 23, 24; Katherine 435; Lilian 435]. This demands more emotional and purpose-driven content to cut through the noise [Lilian 435].

### 4. Human Capital Development and Management

Ensuring the right talent is in place, adequately trained, and motivated is crucial for talisis's ambitious goals.

- **Talent Acquisition and Retention:** Challenges include "attracting the best talent" and being "rigorous" in hiring the right fit for each position, with past "staffing errors" highlighted [Domingo 195]. High turnover, especially among commercial advisors, is a concern, with long hiring times (40-50 days) [Domingo 178]. Retaining and empowering teachers is also a critical challenge [Alejandro 58, 61].
- **Training and Upskilling for New Demands:** There is a continuous need for employees to develop new skills, particularly in AI, digital tools, analytics, and soft skills (communication, empathy, critical thinking) [Angel 122; Juan Arenas 313; Paul 551, 552; Paulina 572; Román 609]. This requires continuous training, often needing dedicated budgets and time for professional development [Lilian 439; Román 609].
- **Productivity Measurement and Efficiency:** There is a "lack of visibility of productivity" in many non-commercial positions [Domingo 181]. The trend towards reduced working hours (e.g., 40-hour week in Mexico) necessitates greater productivity in less time [Domingo 181]. Reducing the time it takes for new advisors to reach optimal productivity (currently 7 months) is a specific target [Domingo 177].
- **Student Preparedness and Support:** Students, particularly post-pandemic, are arriving with "precarious knowledge" and "emotional and affective situations" that require teachers to be continuously trained and supported to address these evolving needs [Paulina 570, 571].

### 5. Financial Stability and Resource Management

Managing resources effectively, optimising investments, and ensuring sustainable growth in a complex environment are ongoing challenges.

- **Budgetary Constraints and Profitability Pressure:** Many initiatives are limited by "lack of budget," and there is a constant need to "maximise scarce resources" [Marcela 463]. The "economic deceleration and the pressure for profitability" mean students are more focused than ever on the "cost-benefit relationship of their education" [Katherine 223, 227; Marcela 483]. A basic priority is "vigilating that the minimum cash flow is covered" and "not losing that minimum profitability" [Marcela 483]. This implies a critical balance between short-term financial health and long-term strategic investments [Marcela 483].
- **Optimising Cost Distribution:** The focus is not just on reducing costs, but on "efficiently distributing" them across necessary categories, making strategic use of technology to achieve this [Alberto 26; Alejandro 63].

### 6. External Regulatory and Socio-Political Factors

External macro-environmental factors significantly influence talisis's operations and strategic direction.

- **Labour Regulations and Union Influence:** Changes in labour regulations (e.g., reduced working hours) demand increased productivity [Domingo 181]. Moreover, socio-political factors and union influences in Mexico are seen as challenging, as "syndicates protect the employee disproportionately, and... do not allow... a culture of high standards of high performance to prosper," leading to draining negotiation processes [Domingo 188; Amalia 112].
- **Socio-Economic and Security Context:** The overall socio-economic situation in Mexico directly impacts families' ability to invest in education, affecting new enrolments and payment methods [Alberto 18; Marcela 482]. Security concerns in regions where talisis has a presence also pose a challenge to operations and reputation [Alberto 18; Marcela 482].
- **AI Regulation and Ethics:** The nascent regulatory framework for AI, particularly concerning data protection and ethics (e.g., NOM 037, GDPR/LGPD) presents an evolving challenge. talisis needs to ensure compliance and operate ethically as it integrates AI more deeply into its educational ecosystem [Angel 127, 125; Román 625].
- **Broader Economic and Social Shifts:** Global economic models, the rise of the digital economy (e.g., cryptocurrencies), and the changing function of universities in society are broader trends that require rethinking the institutional role and academic offerings [Marcos 510, 511].

These challenges collectively highlight the dynamic environment in which talisis operates. Addressing them effectively over the 2025-2027 period will require continuous adaptation, strong and aligned leadership, strategic investments, and a concerted effort to foster an agile and purpose-driven culture.

Given the emphasis on "Consolidación tecnológica y cultural" for 2025-2027, we could now delve into specific strategic recommendations for talisis to overcome the identified challenges related to data quality, process automation, and internal cultural resistance, and discuss how these actions could build a foundation for subsequent phases of expansion and leadership.

o   ¿Cuáles son los indicadores para medir el desempeño del Negocio?

As your thought partner, I can help you quickly and effectively analyze and understand complex information from the provided sources to aid in making critical strategic recommendations to senior leadership. My knowledge base includes detailed perspectives from various talisis directors and managers across planning, corporate sales, human capital, quality and academic accreditation, mobile development, online education, marketing, software development, and data science, as well as an overview from the CEO on talisis's architectural horizons.

Based on the provided sources, talisis employs a comprehensive set of indicators to measure business performance, encompassing financial health, academic quality, operational efficiency, brand perception, and overall impact. These metrics are designed to provide a holistic view of the organization's progress towards its long-term strategic objectives, particularly its vision for 2035.

Here is a detailed breakdown of the key indicators for measuring business performance at talisis:

**I. Financial and Economic Performance** This category focuses on the economic health and sustainability of the organization, ensuring efficient use of resources and healthy growth.

- **Growth in Sales and EBITDA:** These are fundamental top-line and profitability indicators for the entire organization. They demonstrate the company's ability to generate revenue and control operational costs, crucial for overall business health and expansion.
- **Revenue Growth:** Specifically highlighted as a key pillar of growth within institutional objectives.
- **Profitability and Margins:** This includes the overall "profitability of our programs," "profitability of brands," and "net profit". Álvaro also mentions "contribution margin" and "operating margin" as key metrics for his corporate sales area. These indicate how effectively talisis is converting sales into actual profit after various costs.
- **Healthy Income Statement and Balance Sheet:** Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, stresses the importance of maintaining a "healthy income statement and a healthy balance sheet" to support internal and external needs, including CAPEX.
- **Cash Flow:** Essential for sustaining investments and managing debt, ensuring liquidity for ongoing operations and strategic initiatives. Alberto emphasizes having sufficient "cash" for key investments and long-term goals.
- **Efficient Resource Allocation and Cost/Expense Efficiency:** Marcela, Director of Administration and Finance, states her area contributes by ensuring "the expense is profitable and productive," seeking to "maximize scarce resources". Alberto also highlights the need for efficient administration and planning of resources, including "debt management" and "capital raising," and optimizing "where we allocate resources" across cost and expense categories. Paulina, from a regional perspective, also mentions the responsibility of "us to be capacitating and learning new things every day" to adapt to needs globally and domestically, implying cost-effective and continuous learning.
- **Cost of Acquisition (CAC):** Katherine, Senior Marketing Manager, and Juliana, Online Director, both point to the "cost of acquisition per student" (CAC) as a key metric to understand the efficiency of different channels and geographies in acquiring new students. Humberto, from the commercial area, also aims to "improve the cost of acquisition".
- **Accounts Receivable/Payable and Inventory Days:** Marcela mentions "days of accounts receivable or past due portfolio," "days of accounts payable for reverse factoring," and "days of inventory" as leading indicators for financial health and productivity.
- **Budget Optimization:** Román, Data Scientist, proposes a project to "optimize the available budget by means of an algorithm" to ensure resources are allocated effectively to organizational objectives and client needs. This implies measuring budget adherence and return on investment for budget allocation.

**II. Academic and Student Experience Performance** These indicators directly reflect the quality of education delivered, student success, and the overall value proposition.

- **Students Graduated/Certified/Titled:** A direct measure of educational attainment and impact. Álvaro and Amalia specifically mention tracking "students graduated and titled" from programs with organizations.
- **Employability and Educational ROI:** Nicho Garza, CEO, includes "employability and educational ROI" (Return on Investment) as a core organizational success metric. Paul and Paulina also highlight the importance of measuring "employability percentages" of graduates and their average salaries.
- **Net Promoter Score (NPS) and Satisfaction:** Universally cited as critical. Nicho mentions "Net Promoter Score and satisfaction" as organizational success metrics. Several interviewees, including Alberto, Álvaro, Domingo, Inge, Katherine, and Juliana, use NPS to gauge student satisfaction and loyalty. Juliana also measures "NPS of our customers from one cycle to another". Luis emphasizes collecting "surveys to evaluate" solutions from users.
- **Retention Rate/Permanence:** Key for sustained student engagement and successful program completion. Katherine tracks "retention rate post-first trimester", while Juliana monitors "permanence from one cycle to another". Luis expects retention indicators to increase with AI solutions. Román aims to "reduce the risk of student desertion" by understanding main reasons for dropout and intervening early.
- **Enrollment Growth:** Humberto, from the commercial area, sees his role as primarily contributing to "the capture and retention of students," directly impacting the vision for 2035. Juan, from Operations, also lists "growth of new enrollments" and "growth of total matriculation". Juliana tracks "growth in new online enrollments versus the previous year".
- **Student Success Rate:** Juliana measures "student success" as the number of students who "finish this product at the end".
- **Learning Outcomes and Skills Development:** Paul aims for "improvement in the development of 21st-century skills or competencies" for graduates, and Paulina focuses on how innovations influence "students' professional development".
- **Quality of Educational Products/Programs:** Domingo emphasizes the "quality of our products" and "quality of our programs" as a key pillar. Inge's entire area focuses on ensuring academic quality through content design, curriculum development, and accreditation.
- **Group Size/Generation Size:** Marcela monitors "group size" and "percentage of campus utilization", while Alejandro mentions "generation size" for evaluating projects.
- **Value Promise Fulfillment:** Amalia focuses on "delivering 100% our value promise". Juan from Operations aims to "make things happen" for the student, including delivering "the best academic service, the best administrative service," and "payment methods that facilitate the student's payment".
- **Campus Utilization Percentage:** Marcela includes this to measure efficient use of physical resources.

**III. Operational Efficiency and Process Improvement** These indicators ensure that internal operations are streamlined, effective, and supportive of both financial and academic goals.

- **Productivity:** Domingo defines productivity as a key outcome for a high-performance culture. Marcela explicitly mentions "incremental productivity" as a priority project.
- **Operational KPIs:** Alberto mentions "current operational KPIs" for tracking multibrand initiatives. Juliana includes "individual productivity by average response time" and "internal KPIs" in her operational management and discipline metrics.
- **Percentage of Automated Processes:** Julián plans to measure "what percentage of our processes will be automated". Juliana, Lilian, and Román also discuss automation's role in efficiency.
- **Response Times:** Katherine tracks "response times and lead contacts", while Juliana measures "time to initial contact with a student".
- **CRM/Marketing Tool Adoption:** Katherine includes "use and adoption of CRM and marketing tools".
- **Resolution in First Contact:** Juliana measures this for student experience.
- **Reduced Reports to Dynamic Dashboards:** Román aims to "reduce reports that exist today to dynamic dashboards with greater update frequency" for enhanced visibility.
- **AI Adoption in Processes and Departments:** Román monitors the "number of processes and the number of departments that already use artificial intelligence in their daily lives".
- **Process Standardization:** Lilian measures the "percentage of processes within the marketing area that will be standardized". Marcos aims to implement "dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real de ciertos procesos clave" to understand deployment and operation levels.

**IV. Brand, Reputation, and Market Positioning** These indicators focus on how talisis is perceived externally and its competitive standing.

- **Reputation and Prestige:** Joel, as Chief Strategic Officer, emphasizes "reputation" as a long-term indicator, requiring "much effort, much time". Mariel, from Corporate Reputation, highlights the goal to "consolidate as a reference in education and innovation".
- **Stakeholder Perception:** Joel measures "the perception not only of our clients and students, but of all stakeholders with whom we interact, collaborate, and coexist".
- **Brand Sentiment:** Mariel mentions "brand sentiment" as a KPI for reputation based on data.
- **Authority Score and Digital Engagement:** Also from Mariel, these are key digital reputation metrics.
- **Media Presence / Earned Media:** Mariel includes "earned media" in her 360 reputation dashboard.
- **Recommendation/Trust:** Marcela views "recommendation" and "trust" as key indicators of community success, acknowledging they are still "in the process of building".
- **Omnichannel Strategy Coherence:** Katherine aims to ensure "coherence of communication of each of our brands within talisis" across all contact points.

**V. Strategic Impact and Innovation** These indicators measure the organization's ability to drive strategic initiatives and achieve broader societal impact.

- **Longitudinal Impact on Communities:** Nicho includes "longitudinal impact on communities" as a key organizational success metric. Paulina also values measuring the "social and community impact that education generates through students".
- **Number of People Impacted:** Álvaro tracks the "number of people impacted" by projects beyond graduation.
- **New Center Openings and Growth:** Humberto identifies "the opening of new learning centers, and the growth of them" as a long-term priority project.
- **New Portfolio Development and Sales:** Humberto measures the "percentage of new portfolio being developed, implemented and the main indicator will be the sale of those programs".
- **Compliance with Mission/Vision:** Inge's area focuses on ensuring the fulfillment of the mission and vision of each institution through measurable indicators, such as a "matrix of congruence".
- **Percentage of Projects Aligned with 2035 Vision:** Julián considers measuring the "percentage of projects that are aligned with this vision" of 2035 as relevant.
- **Digital Maturity Index:** Julián proposes measuring "digital maturity index" with levels of implementation, accompaniment, autonomous execution, and quality execution for campuses.
- **Number of A/B Tests/Experiments:** Katherine includes the "number of A/B tests or monthly experiments" as an indicator for innovation.

**VI. Talent and Culture (Internal Factors Impacting Performance)** While not direct business outcomes, these internal metrics are recognized as crucial enablers of organizational performance.

- **Engagement and Quality of Life of Collaborator:** Domingo measures the "organizational mood," referring to "engagement" and "quality of life of the collaborator". He also uses "Eco" (a survey) for quality of life and "engagement" (another survey).
- **NPS of Managers/Leaders:** Domingo includes the "NPS that we have from the managers" to gauge leadership effectiveness.
- **Retention of Key Talent:** Amalia identifies "percentage of retention of key talent" as a priority project indicator.
- **Teacher Preparation and Contribution:** Paulina considers the "preparation and contribution of teachers" as an important indicator for fostering proactive and competent students.
- **Lower Teacher Turnover:** Paul includes "lower teacher turnover that is increasingly qualified" as a success metric for his projects.
- **Adoption of Internal Initiatives/Playbook:** Lilian measures "playbook adoption" and how proactively the team embraces new technologies.

**Conclusion:** talisis’s approach to measuring business performance is multifaceted, integrating traditional financial indicators with a strong emphasis on student success, academic quality, operational efficiency gains through technology, brand reputation, and internal talent development. The recurring themes across various areas underscore a commitment to data-driven decision-making, continuous improvement, and a holistic view of value creation, extending beyond immediate financial returns to encompass long-term societal impact and educational transformation.

Given the emphasis on data and analytics across various roles (e.g., Román, Luis, Marcela, Katherine, Julián, Inge), a valuable next step would be to explore the current state of data infrastructure and analytics capabilities at talisis. Specifically, you might consider asking: "What are the current limitations or challenges in collecting, integrating, and analyzing data across different departments and systems to support these diverse performance indicators, and what technological investments or strategic initiatives are planned to overcome them?"

o   ¿Son los mismos indicadores o diferentes para cada nivel organizacional?

talisis employs a comprehensive and interconnected approach to its indicators, which, while varying in specificity across organisational levels, are fundamentally aligned with overarching strategic objectives. This is consistent with the description of talisis functioning as a "fractal organism where the principles replicate at each level".

Here’s a detailed breakdown:

**1. Overarching Organisational Metrics:** At the highest level, talisis uses a set of "Metrics of Organizational Success" that apply across the entire entity. These include:

- Growth in sales and EBITDA.
- Students titled/certified.
- Employability and educational ROI.
- Longitudinal impact on communities.
- Net Promoter Score (NPS) and satisfaction.

Several leaders confirm the focus on these high-level metrics. Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) explicitly links his area's success to the "results of the company," mentioning growth, income, profitability, and product quality. Marcela (Finance) also emphasises overall profitability, new enrolments (NI), and re-enrolments as key indicators. Juan Arenas (Chief Operations Officer) echoes this, listing growth in new income, total enrolment, average ticket, student satisfaction, operating margin, and graduate employment/salary as critical success measures.

**2. Departmental and Area-Specific Indicators:** While the high-level goals remain consistent, each department or functional area defines and tracks more granular indicators relevant to its specific responsibilities and contributions. These detailed metrics are designed to feed into and support the broader organisational objectives, ensuring a cascaded alignment.

- **Finance (Alberto Sánchez, Marcela):** Beyond overall profitability, Alberto's area tracks financial ratios like debt-to-equity, interest-to-EBITDA, and EBITDA-to-debt for specific projects like Promecap, along with cash flow and financial health for mergers and acquisitions. Marcela's indicators include days of accounts receivable/payable, inventory days, and campus utilisation percentage, along with new and re-enrolments.
- **Academic and Quality (Alejandro, Inge, Marcos, Paul):**
    - Alejandro focuses on "NPS docente" (teacher NPS), fulfilment of "promise of value," generation size, and extracurricular value.
    - Inge (Quality and Accreditation) focuses on achieving specific accreditation levels (e.g., 7 years for UNID), and integrating key academic indicators within the OKRs and KPIs reviewed in monthly meetings to track continuous improvement.
    - Marcos (Academic Operations) monitors the advancement of specific metrics within automated dashboards to ensure operational processes are being followed.
    - Paul (Teaching & Learning) measures the development of 21st-century skills, educational quality (through standardised tests), student employability, overall student growth, and retention of qualified teaching staff.
- **Operations (Juan Arenas):** Focuses on the tangible outputs of execution, such as new income and enrolment growth, student satisfaction, and sales efficiency.
- **Marketing and Growth (Fernando, Katherine, Lilian):**
    - Fernando's area tracks cost of acquisition per student, conversion rates by channel, funnel automation, and Net Promoter Score (NPS).
    - Katherine (Senior Marketing Manager) and Lilian (Digital Marketing Director) also use metrics like CPL, CTR, engagement, and the adoption/standardisation of internal processes and AI usage within their marketing efforts.
- **Human Capital and Transformation (Domingo, Julián):**
    - Domingo measures the "organisational mood," including employee engagement and quality of life, alongside the NPS of leaders.
    - Julián (Operational Planning and Transformation) tracks institutional digital maturity (with levels from implementation to quality execution), the percentage of automated processes, and the alignment of projects to the 2035 vision.
- **Strategic Affairs and Reputation (Joel, Mariel):**
    - Joel (CSO) notes that reputation is a long-term indicator, measured by the perception of all stakeholders, including clients, students, authorities, and employees.
    - Mariel (Corporate Reputation) uses compliance percentages across project phases (conceptualisation, model, planning, deployment, execution) to measure the success of the "Talysis Bit" project, which aims to align and synchronise the entire company.
- **Technology and Data Science (Carlos, Luis, Román):**
    - Carlos (CIO) measures the adoption of AI solutions, data quality, and user satisfaction (NPS by solution).
    - Luis (focused on data integrations) tracks project progress, the percentage of user understanding (of students, teachers, and administrators), and survey feedback, also expecting improvements in retention and attraction metrics due to AI.
    - Román (Data Scientist) measures the agility of decision-making, the number of departments and processes utilising AI, the reduction of manual reports, and the decrease in student desertion risk.

**3. Cascading and Alignment as a Core Principle:** The overall strategy in talisis is to ensure that all levels and areas are working towards a common goal, even if their specific daily metrics differ.

- Inge highlights a "cascade" from the institutional mission down to OKRs and KPIs, with continuous measurement to drive improvement.
- The "Talysis Bit" project, mentioned by Joel and Mariel, serves as a transversal initiative to "align, synchronise, and set the rhythm" of the company, ensuring that all efforts contribute to achieving short, medium, and long-term objectives. This project involves clear phases and measurable compliance percentages, demonstrating a structured approach to unified execution.
- Julián also underscores that the implementation of OKRs (Objectives and Key Results) ensures that the organisation has "clear objectives that are measurable" and is "talking about what is truly important".

While the specific indicators will vary depending on the function and level of granularity, talisis maintains a robust framework where departmental metrics are aligned to and support the broader strategic objectives and organisational success metrics, functioning as a cohesive, "fractal" system.

o   ¿Cuáles han sido los cambios más relevantes durante los últimos 12 meses?

talisis has undergone significant and relevant changes over the last 12 to 24 months, indicating a dynamic evolution across its organisational structure, operational processes, technological adoption, and strategic focus. These changes are largely driven by a forward-looking vision for 2035 and a proactive approach to market demands and technological advancements.

Here are the most relevant changes observed, elaborated with details from the sources:

**1. Accelerated Adoption and Strategic Integration of Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Digital Technologies**

- **Pervasive AI Utilisation**: AI is no longer a concept but an actively integrated tool across various functions. For instance, talisis's Quality and Accreditation area has undergone a "significant adjustment" in the last 12-18 months to adapt its content validation processes, as content creation now actively leverages AI. Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) notes that AI is already transforming his processes, helping to structure, rethink, and bounce ideas, acting as a "consolidator and organiser of all the information" to aid decision-making and enhance student learning. Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) highlights his personal daily use of AI for productivity, indicating a shift in individual work habits. Alejandro Madrazo (Academic Director) believes AI and cloud technology should be at the "centre of the process of reimagining educational institutions in their totality," affecting not only processes but inspiring new pedagogies and epistemologies. Román (Data Scientist) expects AI to allow for the production of "personalised didactic content in minutes" and automate "exam-type questions and adaptive feedback".
- **Process Automation**: There's a clear push to automate manual, repetitive, and time-consuming processes using AI and digital tools. Examples include variable compensation calculations, advisor onboarding and training, and recruitment in high-turnover positions, which Domingo Farias identifies as key next steps for AI. Julián (Operational Planning and Transformation) explicitly states that "during the last years and more I believe the last one, we have seen extraordinary changes in the topic of artificial intelligence". Marcela (Finance) also seeks to simplify daily activities like bank reconciliations and financial analysis through AI. Juan Arenas (COO) aims to use AI to "efficientar los procesos a lo largo del viaje del estudiante desde antes que inicie hasta que se gradúe," automating manual activities to reduce errors and save time.
- **Enhanced Data Utilisation and Infrastructure**: talisis is moving towards becoming a truly data-driven organisation. Carlos (Mobile Development) is developing a tool to track real-time app usage (screens and buttons) to better understand user behaviour, moving away from assumptions. Román (Data Scientist) describes a priority to create an integral data infrastructure to collect comprehensive information on students, teachers, and administrators, and deploy machine learning algorithms to detect patterns and make "more strategic" decisions. Luis (Data Integrations) highlights the goal of achieving "more detailed and profound analysis of the information we currently have about our students," and maturing in the use of machine learning and AI to deliver quality and personalised services. Fernando (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) envisions decisions made based on "insights and data" rather than intuition. Katherine (Marketing) stresses the importance of "listening to the student of the future" through various data collection methods, aiming to evolve brands based on their aspirations and needs. Mariel (Corporate Reputation) discusses using "KPIs reputacionales basados en data," including brand sentiment, authority scores, and digital engagement, for real-time reputation evaluation.
- **Shift to Cloud Technology**: The adoption of Cloud technology is seen as crucial for making the same data available to everyone securely, enabling more agile decision-making across campuses and programs. Álvaro García (Innovation and Product) notes that AI and Cloud will enable greater control, agility, and automation, facilitating simpler decisions and better market knowledge.
- **Mobile-First Strategy**: Mobile applications are increasingly used by students over web browsers. This has led Carlos's team to implement in-app rating components to gather direct feedback and boost app store ratings, reflecting a recent emphasis on the mobile user experience.

**2. Maturation and Increased Clarity in Organisational Processes and Strategic Direction**

- **Improved Organisational Structure and Focus**: Inge Ploennig (Quality) observes a "much greater organisation, greater clarity of focus on where we are going and how we should achieve it" over the past two years. This is manifested in more systematised rituals and clearer information flow from top management through "connections, conventions, and town halls," which have "matured immensely".
- **Implementation of OKRs**: Julián (Operational Planning) reports that the organisation is actively implementing and refining OKRs (Objectives and Key Results). This ensures "clear objectives that are measurable" and helps the organisation focus on "what is truly important," suggesting a more disciplined approach to goal setting. Inge Ploennig also links quality management to OKRs and KPIs.
- **Data-Driven Decision-Making Culture**: Multiple leaders, including Fernando, Román, Julián, Katherine, and Marcela, underscore a shift towards making decisions based on "insights and data" rather than intuition. This is supported by efforts to centralise dashboards and improve data quality.
- **Enhanced Inter-Area Collaboration**: While still an area for improvement, Inge Ploennig acknowledges that overall, there's been a "much greater organisation" and "clarity of focus" in how various departments contribute. Efforts are being made to "improve inter-area communication for collaborative projects," especially to avoid duplication and integrate different processes. The need for clear, documented processes and agile access to information to avoid friction between areas is highlighted by multiple interviewees.
- **Strategic Planning and Foresight**: Alberto Sánchez (Planning Director) emphasises that by 2035, planning must be market-centric, aligning financial and strategic structures with market trends and CAPEX needs. talisis aims to have a "capacity of foresight to see 5, 10, 15 years ahead of what the world is", moving beyond immediate reactions to proactively adapt programmes and detect new skills.

**3. Evolution of Educational Models and Student Experience**

- **Shift Towards Hybrid and Personalised Learning**: Juan Arenas (COO) explicitly states the intention to "migrate more to hybrid education" and make it "more personalised," moving beyond a solely online focus. Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) also identifies micro-credentials and hybrid models as key adaptations to future demographic and regulatory changes, advocating for a profound rethinking of the educational model. Paulina (UNID) states that talisis is "implementing the use of different learning platforms together with the experience of our teachers, always ensuring that academic quality is up-to-date and impacts student knowledge". Román (Data Scientist) is working on "personalised learning, understanding areas of opportunity in the academic and professional development of each student to recommend relevant academic content".
- **Student-Centric Design**: Katherine (Marketing) stresses the importance of "listening to the student of the future" through various data collection methods, aiming to evolve brands based on their aspirations and needs. Juliana (Online Direction) emphasises the need to actively "survey, know, and ask" students, acknowledging that past processes often "dominate" over the "customer's need". Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations) highlights the move towards "designing processes that are part of a complete experience" for students, aiming for "wow moments" that are unforgettable.
- **Focus on Comprehensive Skill Development**: Paul Moch and Paulina (UNID) highlight the development of 21st-century competencies, including soft skills, critical thinking, social responsibility, and humanistic values, as a central part of the educational offering, preparing students for an evolving world beyond just technical knowledge. This is also reflected in the "Reporte_Nicho" which states "The learning of the future that we are already creating is one where... personal purpose guides professional development, curiosity is worth more than memorisation".

**4. Strategic Market Approach and External Relations**

- **Proactive Market Vigilance**: Alberto Sánchez reiterates the need for continuous vigilance over market trends, including mergers and acquisitions, to ensure financial and strategic alignment. Fernando (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) emphasises the ambition for talisis's brands to "evolve before the market" by anticipating trends. Joel (Chief Strategic Officer) highlights his role in reading the "context" to design adaptable but solid, local and global strategies.
- **Increased Emphasis on B2B and Alliances**: Álvaro García (Innovation and Product) envisions talisis as a key strategic partner for corporate and public organisations, providing talent transformation and change management solutions, beyond just B2C. Multiple leaders underscore the growing importance of building and strengthening external alliances with educational institutions, companies, and government bodies.
- **Internationalisation and Regional Expansion**: talisis aims for an international impact, not limited to Mexico, potentially leveraging AI for content customisation to other languages and realities. Mariel (Corporate Reputation) aspires for talisis to be a "leading educational ecosystem in Mexico, but also for all of Latin America". Humberto (Commercial Area) also mentions the "apertura de nuevos centros de aprendizaje" and "exploring the expansion of UERRE" regionally.
- **Nearshoring and Tourism Opportunities**: Álvaro García identifies the nearshoring trend and the upcoming North American World Cup as significant opportunities for talent development and tourism sector professionalisation.

**5. Internal Culture and Talent Development Initiatives**

- **High-Performance Culture**: Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) identifies "High-Performance Culture" as a priority project, aiming to "optimise human resources" by attracting the "best talent" and ensuring proper internal staffing, addressing past "errors of staffing". This includes fostering "change management" capabilities, which were previously lacking. Amalia (Human Capital) focuses on "securing the best talent within the company" to deliver on the value proposition.
- **Leadership Development and Transparency**: Amalia (Human Capital) focuses on supporting leaders in evaluating, identifying, and developing their teams. Domingo Farias aims to provide leaders with clearer visibility into their teams' skills and areas for improvement. The use of a recruitment platform that offers real-time visibility on candidate status to hiring managers is a concrete example of this.
- **Focus on Employee Well-being and Engagement**: Domingo Farias measures the "organisational mood," including employee engagement and quality of life, through indicators like Net Promoter Score (NPS) of leaders, signifying a conscious effort to improve internal culture. Mariel (Corporate Reputation) links internal pride and belonging to external reputation.
- **Continuous Learning and Adaptation for Teams**: Alberto Sánchez (Planning) stresses the importance of the team evolving in digital and technology aspects, acknowledging that knowledge without technology is insufficient today. Lilian (Digital Marketing) highlights "LifeLong Learning" and constant adaptation to new technologies and market trends for her team. Paulina (UNID) stresses the "responsibility of training ourselves and learning new things every day".

**6. Operational Efficiency and Cost Management**

- **Optimised Resource Allocation**: Alberto Sánchez (Planning) points to the need for efficient administration of debt, capital raising, and resource allocation across costs and expenses to support long-term goals. He also mentions optimising payroll expenses with technology, rather than necessarily reducing them.
- **Marketing Expense Management**: Alberto Sánchez identifies the increasing costs of marketing in the general market, not just education, as a challenge, requiring efficient management of these expenses.
- **Addressing Legacy Systems and Data Fragmentation**: Marcela (Finance) identifies that while SAP was implemented years ago, it is "underutilised" and lacks interfaces, creating "disconnection" and "lack of control" between systems like Core Banner and SAP. This fragmented data environment means much information gathering is manual and time-consuming. This issue is a recurring theme, with Román also mentioning "too many systems that work in isolation, which leads to data inconsistencies".

The past 12-24 months at talisis have been characterised by an intensive digital transformation, particularly driven by AI and data. This technological push is intertwined with a strategic refinement of educational models towards hybrid and personalised learning, a more proactive and data-informed market approach, and a deliberate cultivation of an internal high-performance culture with a strong emphasis on talent development and improved leadership. While progress has been notable, the organisation continues to grapple with challenges related to full technological integration and overcoming ingrained traditional processes, all viewed through the lens of preparing for a future-ready educational ecosystem by 2035.

Given the pervasive mention of both the opportunities and the _challenges_ related to technological integration and data fragmentation across various systems and departments, it would be highly beneficial to delve into a comprehensive analysis of talisis's current IT architecture. This analysis could identify key bottlenecks, assess the interoperability of existing platforms (e.g., SAP, Core Banner, marketing automation, student-facing apps), and propose a phased roadmap for a more unified, scalable, and data-driven technological ecosystem. This would directly address the concerns raised by multiple leaders about fragmented data, manual processes, and slow decision-making due to technological limitations, acting as a crucial enabler for many of the strategic changes discussed.
### IV. Objetivos y Proyectos/Iniciativas Estratégicas

o   ¿Cuáles fueron los objetivos para el año 2023 y 2024?

While explicit, detailed annual objectives solely for 2023 and 2024 are not exhaustively outlined by every interviewee in the provided sources, several leaders describe current or "in process" initiatives and short-term priorities that would undoubtedly constitute the strategic objectives and projects for these years. Marcela, from Finance, offers the most direct insight into immediate financial priorities for the current year.

Here is a comprehensive overview of the objectives and strategic projects/initiatives inferred and explicitly mentioned for the 2023-2024 period:

### I. Explicit Short-Term Financial Objectives (Marcela)

Marcela, Director of Administration and Finance, clearly articulates a critical short-term objective for "this year":

- **Cash Flow Management and Debt Recovery**: The primary goal is to diligently monitor and ensure the minimum cash flow is covered. Given the challenges presented "in a year with the challenges with which we present ourselves", a basic priority is the recovery of the portfolio (accounts receivable). The aim is to prevent any decline in the minimum profitability that has been set. This implies that some projects, although promising for the future, might be delayed due to the immediate need to safeguard short-term financial stability.
- **Information Management and Controls**: To support this, there is a focus on having financial information available more promptly, providing visibility in advance, and implementing controls to prevent financial setbacks or significant impacts. There is also a need to measure and manage scholarships effectively. Marcela also specifically mentioned the current goal of automating financial processes like "conciliar las transacciones financieras de la venta a la cobranza, el pago al reconocimiento del ingreso de forma más efectiva con apoyo de la inteligencia artificial" and improving the management of financial and productivity information.

### II. Inferred / Ongoing Strategic Initiatives (Relevant to 2023-2024 Operations)

Beyond the explicit financial objectives, several areas mention projects that are "in process," "starting," or describe current operational focuses, which are highly likely to be ongoing or significant for 2023 and 2024.

**A. Technology & Data Transformation**

- **AI Integration & Automation**:
    - **Carlos Granados (CIO)** mentions that "Chatbots Educativos", "Sistema Predictivo de Deserción", and "Asistente Virtual Administrativo" and "Docente (proyecto Mazinger Z)" are currently "in process". He envisions these as initial phases of a broader AI integration to improve forecasts, budgets, project evaluation, and target identification for mergers and acquisitions. His priority project is "la captación de feed y el monitoreo de funcionalidades más utilizadas o menos utilizadas," which is "van iniciando" and defined in "fases pequeñas".
    - **Luis Ruiz (Software Development Manager)** highlights "Construir esta arquitectura de datos" to collect comprehensive information on students, teachers, and administrators for better understanding and solution generation. He also prioritises "el uso de chatbots" as an initial experiment towards implementing more advanced AI agents.
    - **Román (Data Scientist)** was involved in the "Mazinger Z" project, aimed at creating academic content using generative AI, and the "talisis.com" platform for online education. He also describes ongoing efforts to create dashboards for key institutional indicators. A major current challenge he notes is improving the quality and timeliness of data, alongside solid integration to address inconsistencies from disparate systems. His proposed innovations include implementing a "algoritmo predictivo de retención" for early detection of at-risk students, continuously measuring institutional indicators via dashboards, and optimising academic programming.
    - **Amalia (Capital Humano)** seeks to leverage automation and AI for increased efficiency, specifically mentioning automation for "compensación variable de los promotores y asesores" and speeding up "la curva óptima de productividad" for new advisors. She also mentions using technology to "reducir la rotación de asesores" by streamlining hiring processes.
- **Digitalisation of Processes**:
    - **Juan Arenas (COO)** implicitly suggests an ongoing push for making processes "más sencillos más automatizados, más claros" to facilitate student access to financial aid and aligned educational offerings.
    - **Humberto (Commercial Area)** mentions prioritising "cómo podemos automatizar y mejorar la venta en el proceso comercial".
    - **Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations Director)** is currently implementing "herramientas de dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real de ciertos procesos clave" in the academic and operations areas.

**B. Operational and Academic Streamlining**

- **Quality and Accreditation System**: **Inge (Quality and Accreditation Area)** states that a primary focus is "el sistema de calidad, poderlo implementar de tal forma consolidarlo de tal forma, que independientemente si toca una acreditación o no, ya esté todo dado". This involves strengthening existing frameworks and integrating rituals, clear processes, dashboards, and KPIs/OKRs to ensure continuous quality. She also notes the recent (last year and a half) adjustment in content production to incorporate AI, which required aligning quality validation processes.
- **OKR Implementation**: **Julián (Transformation)** notes that "el sistema de los OKRs...se están implementando, nos estamos los estamos puliendo, estamos adaptando la metodología". This is an ongoing effort to align objectives and improve continuous feedback.
