- **Multibrand and Hybrid Model Optimization**:
    - **Juan Arenas (COO)** lists as key projects "migrar a una educación más híbrida a través de mejorar los servicios que se ofrecen en la educación online" and "convertirnos en una en que cada centro de servicio que tenemos se pueda lograr una venta multimarca".
    - **Humberto (Commercial Area)** also lists "la apertura de nuevos centros de aprendizaje" and "apertura de nuevo portafolio" as long-term impact projects.
    - **Juliana (Online Director)** focuses on "garantizar una buena ejecución del view actual" (virtual model) and improving service channels to reduce attrition. She also aims to restructure the online product to be "un producto ganador en el mercado" and optimise the service center and its commercial strategy for multibrand sales.
    - **Katherine (Marketing)** identifies "la estrategia omnicanal, integral en la parte de comunicación" and "construcción, y fortalecimiento de marca" as priority projects.

**C. Talent and Culture Development**

- **High-Performance Culture**: **Julián (Transformation)** and **Domingo (Capital Humano)** both emphasise building a "cultura de alto desempeño" (High-Performance Culture). This involves defining high standards, attracting the "best fit" talent, and ensuring correct internal staffing. Domingo's mission "es optimizar el recurso humano en talisis. Para asegurar la rentabilidad del capital humano que tenemos en talisis," which is directly tied to productivity and motivation.
- **Talent Development Plans**: **Juliana (Online Director)** mentions that her team has a "plan de desarrollo que tiene que ver con estos retos todos" within the "objetivos de talisis 2025". This suggests ongoing talent development aligned with current transformation efforts.

### III. Overarching Strategic Projects (Providing Context for 2023-2024 Work)

The CEO, Nicho Garza, provides a high-level view of talisis's core strategic projects, which serve as the foundation for the more specific initiatives likely undertaken in 2023-2024. These projects are presented as continuous efforts rather than strictly annual goals:

- **Cultural Alignment**: Ensuring "Cada colaborador viviendo los principios TALISIS", fostering a sense of pride and belonging internally. This is a "proyecto de mediano y largo plazo donde el orden, la disciplina y la visión tienen que compaginar con la cultura y la estrategia".
- **AI Technology Architecture**: Developing the "mente TALISIS conectando todo", leveraging AI and digitisation as amplifiers for an "ecosistema educativo inteligente, adaptativo e inclusivo".
- **Teaching Excellence**: Continuously training "Maestros del mundo real, capacitados continuamente", ensuring content quality through AI and accreditation processes.
- **Productive Linkages**: Establishing "Proyectos reales automatizados y sin fricciones" to connect students with real-world business needs.
- **Educational Omnichannel**: Providing "El mismo TALISIS en cualquier formato", ensuring a consistent and high-quality educational experience across various modalities.
- **Financial Health**: Maintaining "Modelos sostenibles para cada segmento" to ensure the long-term viability of the organisation.
- **Integrated Business Management**: Achieving "2,400 mentes trabajando como una", through initiatives like talisis Bit, which aims to synchronise strategies and mark the company's rhythm.

While only Marcela provides direct "this year" objectives focused on financial health, the interviews collectively point to a strong emphasis in 2023-2024 on implementing and refining key technological (AI, data architecture), operational (quality systems, hybrid models), and human capital (culture, talent development) initiatives that underpin talisis's long-term strategic vision for 2035.

To further refine the understanding of 2023-2024 objectives, we could specifically cross-reference the "in process" projects mentioned by Carlos Granados, Marcos Samaniego, and Román with the strategic pillars outlined by Nicho Garza to identify which specific capabilities were targeted for initial implementation or significant advancement within those years.

o   ¿Qué objetivos se tienen establecidos para este 2025?

While explicit, standalone objectives solely for the year 2025 are not uniformly detailed across all interviews, a clear picture of talisis's strategic direction for this period can be comprehensively inferred from the multi-year horizons, ongoing strategic projects, and immediate priorities articulated by various leaders.

### I. Overarching Strategic Phase (2025-2027): Technological and Cultural Consolidation

The CEO, Nicho Garza, explicitly defines the period **2025-2027** as a phase of **"Consolidación tecnológica y cultural"** for talisis. This overarching strategic horizon provides the foundational context for the specific objectives and projects that would be prioritised in 2025. It indicates a dual focus on strengthening technological infrastructure and embedding the desired organisational culture.

### II. Key Objectives and Projects for 2025 (Inferred and Explicit)

Based on the strategic phase and detailed insights from various departmental leaders, the following objectives and projects are established or are highly likely to be prioritised for 2025:

**A. Financial Stability and Optimisation:**

- **Cash Flow Management and Debt Recovery**: A primary, immediate objective is to rigorously monitor and ensure the minimum cash flow is covered, with a strong focus on recovering the portfolio (accounts receivable) to safeguard minimum profitability. This is critical "in a year with the challenges with which we present ourselves", implying an ongoing focus from 2024 into 2025 if challenges persist.
- **Real-time Financial Information & Controls**: Improve the promptness and visibility of financial information, implement robust controls to prevent setbacks, and effectively measure and manage scholarships. Marcela, Director of Administration and Finance, specifically aims to automate financial processes like "conciliar las transacciones financieras de la venta a la cobranza, el pago al reconocimiento del ingreso de forma más efectiva con apoyo de la inteligencia artificial".
- **Optimising Cost and Resource Allocation**: Act as an "enabler" from the back office to support growth by ensuring administrative and financial processes (facturación, gasto management, resource allocation) are well-designed and aligned with new products, formats, and channels. Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, highlights the importance of financial planning supporting CAPEX needs and being structured to meet internal and external requirements.

**B. Technological Consolidation and Advanced AI Integration:**

- **Implementation of Base Infrastructure and First AI Agents**: This is a direct objective for "Fase 1 (2025-2027)", driven by Carlos Granados (CIO). This phase will focus on developing an "ecosistema educativo inteligente, adaptativo e inclusivo" that personalises learning, improves operational efficiency, and empowers staff.
- **Data Architecture & Predictive Analytics**: Build a comprehensive data architecture to collect information on students, teachers, and administrators for better understanding and solution generation. This includes creating dashboards for key institutional indicators and implementing predictive algorithms for student retention, early detection of at-risk students, and optimising academic programming. Román, Data Scientist, notes the current challenge of improving data quality, timeliness, and integration, which would be a key focus for 2025.
- **Process Automation with AI**: Automate complex processes like variable compensation for promoters and advisors, accelerate the optimal productivity curve for new advisors, and streamline talent acquisition to reduce rotation, leveraging AI for improved efficiency. Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, is implementing "herramientas de dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real de ciertos procesos clave". Carlos Villa, Mobile Dev Lead, is working on a tool for "captación de feed y el monitoreo de funcionalidades más utilizadas o menos utilizadas," which is "van iniciando" for "este año".
- **Digitalisation of Student Journey**: Enhance the student experience by digitalising and automating processes from admission to graduation, including financial aid access and payment methods, to reduce manual activities and errors. This also extends to personalised reminders for graduation requirements using AI and cloud technology.

**C. Cultural and Organisational Transformation:**

- **High-Performance Culture (Hiperformance Culture)**: A key priority for Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, is fostering a "cultura de alto desempeño". This involves establishing high standards, rigorously attracting and staffing the "best fit" talent, and fostering a culture where development is embedded in every leader's DNA.
- **OKR Implementation and Discipline**: Julián Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, states that the OKR system is currently "se están implementando, nos estamos los estamos puliendo, estamos adaptando la metodología", indicating an ongoing process of refinement and adoption for 2025. This aims to ensure clear, measurable objectives and continuous feedback.
- **Process Documentation and Standardisation**: Initiatives to document currently undocumented processes and ensure their compliance across the organisation. This also involves creating a central repository of processes for better communication and order.
- **talisis Bit Implementation**: Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, describes "talisis Bit" as a prioritised transversal project. This initiative aims to align, synchronise, and set the pace for the entire company to achieve its objectives, impacting all areas and fostering a unified rhythm and purpose. Its full implementation (deployment and execution) is slated for 2025-2027.

**D. Product and Service Enhancement (Student-Centric and Market-Driven):**

- **Multibrand and Hybrid Model Optimisation**: Projects include migrating to a more hybrid education model by improving online services, enabling multi-brand sales at service centres, and opening new learning centres and portfolis aligned with market needs. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, aims to guarantee good execution of the current virtual model, reduce attrition by improving service channels, and restructure the online product to be "un producto ganador en el mercado".
- **Curricular Relevance and Innovation**: Inge, from Quality and Accreditation, highlights focusing on the "pertinencia de nuestros programas académicos" and innovating how knowledge is imparted, with teachers as facilitators of critical thinking rather than just technical instructors. This also includes the development of micro-credentials.
- **Enhanced Student Experience**: Focus on creating personalised experiences from the first contact through AI and real-time data, anticipating student needs, and fostering a sense of belonging through active online communities and gamification. Katherine, Marketing, emphasises aligning products with real needs and building an "omnichannel" strategy.

**E. Talent and Leadership Development:**

- **Strategic Talent Development**: Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, focuses on improving commercial productivity and developing key personnel as "cartas de reemplazo" for executives. Domingo Farias aims to "optimizar el recurso humano en talisis" to ensure profitability, productivity, and motivation, attracting the "best fit" talent.
- **Continuous Learning & Digital Acumen**: Paulina and Paul (from UNID and Dirección de Enseñanza y Aprendizaje, respectively) stress the importance of continuous learning, adaptation to new technologies, and developing a "mentalidad de crecimiento" within teams. Lilian, Digital Marketing Director, promotes "LifeLong Learning" and adopting new technologies.

The year 2025 for talisis is projected to be a period of intense **consolidation** across its technological infrastructure, internal culture, and operational processes. The objectives for this year are deeply intertwined with the broader 2025-2027 strategic horizon, focusing on leveraging **AI and data** for efficiency and hyper-personalisation, strengthening a **high-performance, data-driven culture**, and **innovating the educational product and service delivery** to ensure long-term relevance and market leadership. Financial prudence, as highlighted by Marcela, will underpin these ambitious transformations.

To further refine these objectives and support strategic recommendations for senior leadership, it would be beneficial to conduct a **cross-functional workshop** aligning these inferred 2025 objectives with specific departmental KPIs and OKRs, particularly focusing on the "Consolidación tecnológica y cultural" pillar. This would help identify potential interdependencies, resource conflicts, or gaps in the planned initiatives, and foster the desired "cultura de alto desempeño" and "sincronía" that many leaders aspire to.

o   ¿Cuál es el proceso para la definición de los Objetivos?

The process for defining objectives at talisis is multi-faceted, highly integrated, and deeply rooted in the organisation's overarching strategic vision, known as the "Architecture of Horizons". It involves a continuous cycle of strategic foresight, market analysis, cultural alignment, and iterative measurement, underpinned by a commitment to data-driven decision-making and technological enablement.

### I. Overarching Strategic Framework: The Architecture of Horizons (2025-2035)

The definition of objectives at talisis begins with a clear, long-term strategic horizon. The CEO, Nicho Garza, explicitly outlines a multi-year roadmap:

- **2025-2027**: Focus on "Consolidación tecnológica y cultural" (Technological and Cultural Consolidation).
- **2028-2030**: Expansion into Latin America ("Expansión latinoamericana").
- **2031-2035**: Leadership in regional educational transformation ("Liderazgo en transformación educativa regional").

This macro-level framework serves as the guiding star for all objective setting, ensuring that shorter-term goals contribute to the ultimate vision of transforming communities through accessible and pertinent education, generating sustainable social mobility.

### II. Foundational Layer: Purpose and Culture-Driven Definition

At its core, objective definition at talisis is driven by a shared purpose and an intentional organisational culture:

1. **Anchoring in Fundamental Purpose**: The ultimate purpose is "Transformar comunidades a través de las personas mediante educación accesible y pertinente que genere movilidad social sostenible y ciclos virtuosos de desarrollo transgeneracional". This profound purpose inspires leaders across the organisation, such as Alberto Sánchez, who sees it as contributing to "un mejor México", and Amalia Ortega, who is motivated by helping to "cumplir sueños y a transformar la vida de las personas". This purpose acts as the non-negotiable foundation for all objectives.
2. **Cultivating a High-Performance Culture**: A critical strategic initiative, championed by the Chief of Staff, Domingo Farias, is fostering a "cultura de alto desempeño" (High-Performance Culture). This involves establishing high standards, rigorously attracting and retaining the "best fit" talent, and embedding development in every leader's DNA. This cultural objective directly influences how other objectives are defined and pursued.
3. **The talisis Way and talisis Bit**: The "talisis Way" represents the company's core principles and identity. To ensure alignment and synchronicity across the entire organisation, a transversal project called "Talysis Bit" is being implemented. Described as a "Business Management Plan Integral" and "un proyecto de alineación, sincronización y un business management plan que nos llevará a todos estar alineados y ir con el ritmo adecuado, constante para llegar y lograr nuestros objetivos. A largo, mediano, y corto plazo", talisis Bit is _the_ mechanism to mark the rhythm of the company and ensure every area works towards shared objectives. This project aims to integrate objectives across all functions and timeframes, making alignment a continuous process.

### III. Strategic Planning and Market Alignment

Objective definition involves a sophisticated interplay between internal capabilities and external market demands:

1. **Market Intelligence and Foresight**: The Planning Director, Alberto Sánchez, highlights the need for planning to be "centrada en en lo que el mercado requiere en las tendencias de mercado". This involves internal analysis of what programs, courses, modalities, and sales channels the market seeks, as well as external monitoring for mergers and acquisitions opportunities. Similarly, the Chief Growth and Marketing Officer, Fernando, stresses "impulsando una visión clara del mercado, del estudiante del futuro" and adapting strategies based on "cambio de comportamiento del consumidor," "educación no tradicional o micro credenciales," and "consumerización de la experiencia educativa".
2. **Financial Structuring and Resource Allocation**: The Finance Director, Marcela, underlines her area's mission to "liderar la planificación presupuestaria el análisis de indicadores clave para mejorar la eficiencia de rentabilidad". Her team acts as "Enablers" from the back office to ensure that administrative and financial processes (such as invoicing, expense management, and resource allocation) are well-designed and aligned with new products, formats, and channels. This ensures that financial objectives are not only set but also enable the achievement of other strategic goals, carefully balancing short-term cash flow with long-term prosperity.
3. **Project Prioritisation**: Strategic projects are seen as the "iniciativas estratégicas interconectadas que materializan la visión". These projects are identified to drive the strategy forward, ranging from a unified student acquisition model and multibrand presence to AI integration and talent development. The CIO, Carlos Granados, defines initial projects like chatbots and administrative assistants, aligning them with the long-term vision of an "ecosistema educativo inteligente".

### IV. Operationalisation and Measurement

Translating strategic direction into actionable objectives is crucial:

1. **OKR Implementation**: Julián Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, is actively involved in implementing and refining the OKR (Objectives and Key Results) system. This methodology is seen as key to ensuring "objetivos claros, que sean medibles, que realmente estemos hablando en toda la organización de lo que realmente es importante". This standardises how objectives are defined and tracked across the organisation.
2. **Data-Driven Decision Making**: Román, a Data Scientist, emphasizes designing and implementing a data architecture for a "vista 360 de nuestros clientes" and providing "visibilidad a la organización de manera oportuna para tomar decisiones más estratégicas". Data dashboards, predictive algorithms, and real-time analytics are critical tools for setting and adjusting objectives, allowing for agile decision-making and continuous improvement.
3. **Continuous Feedback and Improvement Cycles**: Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, highlights that his team not only implements academic designs but also performs "mediciones [y] análisis de esas mediciones" to provide feedback to process designers for continuous improvement. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Accreditation, confirms this, stating that her area focuses on measuring "cumplimiento de la misión" through clear indicators and regular reviews, driving a "ciclo de mejora".

### V. Iterative Adaptation and Agility

The process acknowledges the dynamic nature of the environment:

1. **Flexibility and Re-evaluation**: Román notes the importance of a "mentalidad rígida" for the area, always being "dispuestos a reevaluar o reimplementar algo de lo que hayamos desarrollado". This agility allows objectives to be adjusted as external conditions or internal learnings evolve.
2. **Process Documentation and Standardisation**: Alejandro, from an unspecified area (likely academic or design), highlights the fundamental need for "procesos muy claros y muy previsibles" to avoid emergencies and allow focus on innovation and design. Marcos Samaniego also wishes for a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos" to improve communication and order across the large organisation. This standardisation, while seemingly rigid, in fact supports agility by making processes predictable and easier to adapt.

The process for defining objectives at talisis is comprehensive and integrated:

- It starts with a **clear, long-term vision** and overarching strategic horizons.
- It is **purpose and culture-driven**, with initiatives like talisis Bit ensuring deep organisational alignment and synchronicity.
- It involves **strategic planning** informed by meticulous market intelligence and robust financial management.
- **Operationalisation** is achieved through methodologies like OKRs and supported by a growing reliance on data architecture and advanced analytics for **measurement and continuous feedback**.
- Finally, the entire process is designed to be **iterative and adaptive**, recognising the need for flexibility in a fast-changing world.

To further refine the objective definition process, it would be beneficial to conduct workshops that specifically map the "talisis Bit" implementation phases to the granular OKR setting process in key departments (e.g., Marketing, Academic Operations, Sales). This would help identify potential bottlenecks in the cascading of objectives and ensure that departmental efforts are truly contributing to the organisation-wide "rhythm" and "sincronisation" that Mariel Serrano describes. This could also incorporate formal training on how to translate macro-level strategic objectives into actionable, measurable team-level OKRs.

o   ¿Cuál es el proceso para el despliegue y alineación de objetivos?

The process for the deployment and alignment of objectives at talisis is a sophisticated and integrated approach, deeply embedded within the organisation's overarching strategic framework, known as the "Architecture of Horizons". This multi-faceted process ensures that all efforts, from high-level strategic aspirations to daily operations, are cohesive and directed towards a common purpose.

Here is a detailed breakdown of the process:

**I. Strategic Foundation and Long-Term Vision**

The definition and deployment of objectives at talisis begin with a clear, long-term strategic vision. The CEO, Nicho Garza, outlines a multi-year roadmap: focusing on "Technological and Cultural Consolidation" by 2027, "Latin American Expansion" by 2030, and "Leadership in Regional Educational Transformation" by 2035 [Reporte_Nicho]. This grand vision serves as the guiding principle for all objectives, ensuring that short-term goals contribute to talisis's fundamental mission: "transforming communities through people, by means of accessible and pertinent education that generates sustainable social mobility and virtuous cycles of transgenerational development" [Reporte_Nicho, 6, 647]. Leaders throughout the organisation, such as Alberto Sánchez, are inspired by the idea of contributing to "a better Mexico" through education, and Amalia Ortega by the motivation of helping to "fulfill dreams and transform people's lives".

**II. Core Mechanism for Alignment: talisis Bit**

A cornerstone of the objective deployment and alignment process is the "talisis Bit" initiative. This is described as an "Integral Business Management Plan" that aims to align and synchronize the entire organisation. Mariel Serrano, from Corporate Reputation, emphasizes that talisis Bit is _the_ mechanism to set the company's rhythm, ensuring everyone is aligned and progressing at a "constant, adequate rhythm" to achieve objectives across long, medium, and short terms. Joel Enriquez, the Chief Strategy Officer, further elaborates on talisis Bit as "the pulse, the sequence, the frequency" of what the organisation needs to do to foster continuous learning. It is a transversal project involving all areas to ensure a shared vision and concerted effort.

**III. Multi-Dimensional Objective Setting and Operationalisation**

The process involves a sophisticated interplay of various dimensions and contributions from different areas:

1. **Purpose and Culture-Driven Definition:**
    
    - **Human-Centric Approach:** Objectives are anchored in talisis's core purpose, with a strong emphasis on the student as the central focus. Juan Arenas, COO, highlights that providing the "best service to the student" is the ultimate legacy, translating into clear, agile processes aligned with their dreams and expectations.
    - **High-Performance Culture:** Domingo Farias, from Human Capital, actively drives the objective of fostering a "culture of high performance". This involves rigorous talent acquisition ("best fit talent"), establishing high standards, and embedding development in every leader's DNA. This cultural objective directly influences how other goals are pursued and implemented.
2. **Strategic Planning and Market Alignment:**
    
    - **Market Intelligence and Foresight:** Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, ensures that planning is "centred on what the market requires, on market trends". This includes internal analysis of desired programs, modalities, and sales channels, as well as external monitoring for mergers and acquisitions. Fernando, Chief Growth and Marketing Officer, focuses on "a clear vision of the market, of the student of the future" and adapting strategies to "consumer behaviour change," "non-traditional education or micro-credentials," and the "consumerisation of the educational experience". Katherine also emphasises anticipating the market and exploring "blue oceans".
    - **Financial Structuring and Resource Allocation:** Marcela, Finance Director, underlines her team's role in "leading budget planning [and] analysis of key indicators to improve efficiency and profitability". Her department acts as "Enablers" from the back office, ensuring that administrative and financial processes are well-designed and aligned with new products and channels, balancing short-term cash flow with long-term prosperity.
    - **Project Prioritisation:** Identified as "interconnected strategic initiatives that materialise the vision" [Reporte_Nicho, 641], projects range from a unified student acquisition model and multibrand presence to AI integration and talent development. Carlos Granados, CIO, aligns initial technology projects (like chatbots) with the long-term vision of an "intelligent educational ecosystem".
3. **Operationalisation and Measurement:**
    
    - **OKR and KPI Implementation:** Julián Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, is central to implementing and refining the OKR (Objectives and Key Results) system. This methodology is critical for ensuring "clear, measurable objectives" and focusing the entire organisation on "what is really important". Various areas define specific KPIs, such as "cost of acquisition per student," "retention rate," "NPS," and "financial ratios".
    - **Data-Driven Decision Making:** Román, a Data Scientist, highlights the design and implementation of a robust data architecture to provide a "360-degree view of our clients" and offer "timely visibility to the organisation to make more strategic decisions". Data dashboards, predictive algorithms, and real-time analytics are essential tools for setting and adjusting objectives, enabling agile responses and continuous improvement. Carlos Villa advocates for clearer channels to understand student needs, rather than relying on internal assumptions.
    - **Continuous Feedback and Improvement Cycles:** Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, explains that his team not only implements academic designs but also conducts "measurements [and] analysis of those measurements" to provide feedback for continuous improvement. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Accreditation, confirms this, stating that her area focuses on measuring "mission compliance" through clear indicators and regular reviews, driving a "cycle of improvement".

**IV. Iterative Adaptation and Agility**

The process acknowledges the dynamic nature of the environment and the constant need for flexibility:

- **Flexibility and Re-evaluation:** Román emphasises a flexible mindset, always being "willing to re-evaluate or re-implement something we have developed". This agility allows objectives to be adjusted as external conditions or internal learnings evolve. Alberto Sánchez stresses the importance of combining "strategic planning with financial planning" to ensure that decisions align with the long-term strategic direction.
- **Process Documentation and Standardisation:** Alejandro (from academic/design) highlights the need for "very clear and very predictable processes" to avoid emergencies and allow focus on innovation and design. Marcos Samaniego also wishes for a "documentary repository of all processes" to improve communication and order across the large organisation. This standardisation, while seemingly rigid, in fact supports agility by making processes predictable and easier to adapt. Juliana, Director of Online, notes that standardizing processes is a prerequisite for leveraging cloud technology for faster resolution times.

**V. Cross-Functional Collaboration and Leadership**

Effective objective deployment and alignment rely heavily on strong collaboration and supportive leadership:

- **Internal Collaboration:** Alberto Sánchez consistently interacts with "internal clients" (academic, operations, HR, marketing, and commercial teams) for various planning and control activities. Juan Arenas sees his operations area as an "integrator of all ideas, projects, initiatives" developed by other process areas, ensuring their effective execution. Mariel Serrano emphasises a "transversal communication strategy" to ensure all areas move at the same pace and align with business objectives. Lilian, from Digital Marketing, highlights the importance of sharing objectives through OKRs and maintaining a common language across different areas.
- **Leadership and Empowerment:** Carlos Granados, CIO, advocates for a leadership style characterized by "visionary inspiration," "empowerment of teams," and a "culture of innovation". Domingo Farias states that the Human Capital area functions as a "strategic service that empowers leaders," embedding culture and processes into their DNA for effective leadership. Katherine, from Marketing, imagines collaboration "without hierarchies, with a shared vision and a focus on impact". Joel Enriquez envisions the organisation operating like a "high-performance football team" where members anticipate each other's moves and celebrate collective success.

The process for objective deployment and alignment at talisis is a dynamic and integrated system. It starts with a **clear, long-term strategic vision** defined by the "Architecture of Horizons." This vision is then operationalised through **talisis Bit**, which acts as a central mechanism for ensuring deep organisational synchronisation. Objectives are defined with a strong **purpose and culture-driven** foundation, informed by **strategic planning and detailed market analysis**, and supported by robust **financial management**. **Operationalisation** is achieved through methodologies like OKRs and is underpinned by increasing reliance on **data architecture and advanced analytics** for precise measurement and continuous feedback. Finally, the entire process is designed to be **iterative and adaptive**, emphasising flexibility, continuous re-evaluation, and strong **cross-functional collaboration** to navigate a constantly evolving environment.


o   ¿Cuál es el proceso para el seguimiento de los objetivos?

The process for objective tracking and monitoring at talisis is a comprehensive and integrated approach, deeply embedded within the organisation's overarching strategic framework, the "Architecture of Horizons". This multi-faceted system ensures that progress towards goals is continuously measured, evaluated, and aligned across all levels.

Here is a detailed breakdown of the process for objective tracking:

### I. Strategic Foundation and Overarching Mechanism

1. **Architecture of Horizons as the Guiding Framework:** All objectives and their tracking mechanisms are aligned with talisis's long-term strategic vision, encapsulated in the "Architecture of Horizons". This framework sets temporal horizons for strategic achievements: "Technological and Cultural Consolidation" by 2027, "Latin American Expansion" by 2030, and "Leadership in Regional Educational Transformation" by 2035.
2. **talisis Bit: The Central Alignment and Rhythm Setter:** A cornerstone of objective tracking is the "talisis Bit" initiative. This is defined as an "Integral Business Management Plan" designed to align and synchronise the entire organisation, setting its "rhythm," "pulse," and "frequency". Mariel Serrano emphasises that talisis Bit is _the_ mechanism to ensure everyone is aligned and progressing at a "constant, adequate rhythm" to achieve objectives across long, medium, and short terms. It is a transversal project that involves all areas to ensure a shared vision and concerted effort.
    - **Measuring talisis Bit:** Success for this overarching project is measured by the "percentage of compliance" across its defined phases: conceptualisation, model development, planning, deployment, and full execution, with the latter targeted between 2025 and 2027.

### II. Methodologies and Indicators for Measurement

talisis employs various methodologies and a broad range of Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) and Objectives and Key Results (OKRs) to track its objectives:

1. **OKR (Objectives and Key Results) Implementation:** Julián Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, is central to implementing and refining the OKR system. This methodology is critical for ensuring "clear, measurable objectives" and focusing the entire organisation on "what is really important". It also aids in "continuous feedback".
2. **Diverse KPIs Across Functions:** Specific KPIs are defined and monitored across different departments to measure progress:
    - **Financial Health & Efficiency:** Alberto Sánchez (Planning) monitors debt/equity, interest/EBITDA, and EBITDA/debt ratios for specific projects like Promecap. Marcela (Finance) tracks days of accounts receivable/payable, inventory days, and aims to provide information on profitability by program and location. She also measures new enrolments (NIs) and re-enrolments, group size, and campus utilisation percentages.
    - **Growth & Commercial Performance:** Humberto (Commercial) and Katherine (Marketing/Growth) track new income growth, total enrolment growth, average ticket growth, sales per advisor, cost of acquisition per student (CAC), conversion rate by channel, penetration by segment, funnel automation percentage, response times, CRM/marketing tools usage, and cost per lead. Lilian (Digital Marketing) includes CPL, conversion rate, engagement, CTR, open/click/flow rates, and SEO ranking.
    - **Student Experience & Quality:** Juan Arenas (COO) focuses on student satisfaction. Inge Ploennig (Quality & Accreditation) measures "mission compliance" through 14 key indicators, NPS for students, and engages in regular reviews. Alejandro's area evaluates designs by following students and collaborators longitudinally. NPS for both students and companies is also mentioned by Álvaro (Corporate Sales).
    - **Operational & Digital Transformation:** Julián Mendez highlights tracking the "digital maturity index" (with levels from implementation to quality execution), the "percentage of automated processes," and the "percentage of projects aligned to [the] 2035 vision". Román (Data Scientist) measures agility in decision-making, AI adoption in processes and departments, and the reduction of traditional reports to dynamic dashboards. Luis Ruiz (Software Development) tracks the number of projects implemented and the "percentage of understanding of users".
    - **Talent & Culture Development:** Amalia Ortega (HR) specifically measures commercial productivity and the "percentage of retention of key talent". Domingo Farias (Human Capital) connects his area's success to the company's strategic results across growth, efficient administration, and student life, also monitoring organisational mood, employee engagement, quality of life, and NPS of managers. Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) uses improvement in 21st-century skills, educational quality (via standardised tests), employability, student growth, and reduced qualified teacher turnover. Paulina (UNID Director) tracks participation in training, student impact on professional development, growth of learning centres, and graduate employability percentages.
    - **Reputation Management:** Joel Enriquez (CSO) measures reputation, noting it is built over time through consistent, visible, and organic efforts.

### III. Data Collection, Analysis, and Visibility Tools

1. **Robust Data Architecture:** Román (Data Scientist) is actively involved in designing and implementing a robust data architecture. The goal is to provide a "360-degree view of our clients" and offer "timely visibility to the organisation to make more strategic decisions". This includes gathering detailed information from prospect to alumnus to understand their full trajectory.
2. **Centralised Dashboards and Business Intelligence (BI):** Dashboards are repeatedly mentioned as critical tools for monitoring performance, providing real-time data, and supporting data-driven decision-making across various departments. Carlos Granados lists "Data Lake operativo" and "Dashboard de analytics" as critical deliverables. The aim is to move from manual reports to more dynamic, continuously updated dashboards.
3. **Predictive Analytics and AI Integration:** talisis explicitly uses predictive analysis for critical areas like student dropout detection and early identification of required skills. Román mentions developing predictive algorithms for student retention based on academic performance, task completion, and attendance. Carlos Granados's AI projects include a "predictive system for early detection of student risks". AI is also being integrated for automated content generation (Mazinger Z project), streamlining manual HR processes, and generally increasing process efficiency.
4. **Continuous Monitoring and Feedback Loops:** Marcos Samaniego's team (Academic Operations) continuously measures and analyses results to provide feedback for ongoing improvement. Inge Ploennig emphasises a "cycle of improvement" driven by regular reviews of mission compliance. Julián Mendez notes that OKRs facilitate "continuous feedback". Román also advocates for continuous communication to improve and adapt technology solutions.
5. **User Feedback and Social Listening:** Carlos (Mobile Development) is developing a tool to track screen and button usage to better understand user preferences. Katherine (Marketing) uses "social listening" to understand student motivations and adapt communication strategies. There is also an aim to collect raw user feedback, analyse sentiment with AI, and provide personalised responses.

### IV. Reporting and Review Cycles

1. **Regular Strategic Reviews:** The organisation conducts "Town Halls" and "Conventions," which are structured rituals for disseminating strategic information and ensuring alignment from top management (CEO and C-level) downwards. These events are part of the broader "Architecture of Horizons" for aligning efforts.
2. **Departmental Meetings:** Internal weekly meetings (e.g., academic areas) include "brainstorming" sessions and follow-ups on area objectives. Inge Ploennig mentions a quarterly "matrix of congruence" with 14 key mission-related indicators for UNID. Marcela's team reports on leading financial indicators.
3. **Agile Project Management:** Carlos (Mobile Development) describes an agile approach to projects, breaking them into "small phases" and "re-adjusting on the fly," to ensure continuous progress and quick adaptation rather than waiting for full definition.

### V. Leadership and Accountability

1. **Ownership and Responsibility:** Juan Arenas (COO) stresses "accountability" where each collaborator takes ownership and responsibility for their actions to ensure high-quality service delivery.
2. **Empowering Leaders:** The Human Capital area, led by Domingo Farias, functions as a "strategic service that empowers leaders," embedding culture and processes into their DNA for effective leadership and objective achievement.
3. **Visionary Leadership:** Carlos Granados (CIO) advocates for a leadership style characterised by "visionary inspiration," "empowerment of teams," and a "culture of innovation," which are crucial for guiding strategic projects and ensuring objectives are met.

### VI. Challenges in Objective Tracking

Despite the comprehensive framework, talisis faces several challenges in fully optimising its objective tracking process:

1. **Data Quality and System Integration:** A recurring issue is the lack of consistent, high-quality data due to isolated systems, varying metric definitions, and fragmented technological infrastructure. This hinders the ability to obtain a single, reliable source of truth.
2. **Manual Processes and Time Consumption:** Many processes, particularly in data collection and administrative tasks, are still manual, consuming significant human effort and slowing down decision-making. There is a strong desire to automate these tasks using AI and cloud technology.
3. **Resource Limitations:** Teams often operate with limited personnel and time, making it challenging to keep up with rapid technological advancements, balance routine tasks with strategic projects, and continuously develop new solutions.
4. **Cultural and Organisational Resistance:** There is a recognised challenge in overcoming "cultural resistance" to change, traditional ways of operating, and a lack of a universal "digital mindset" across the organisation. This can lead to disarticulation between areas.
5. **Balancing Short-term vs. Long-term Focus:** The pressure to achieve short-term financial and operational targets can sometimes divert resources and attention from critical long-term strategic projects and investments in robust tracking systems.
6. **Lack of Formal Documentation:** The absence of a central, documented repository for all processes makes it difficult to standardise operations, communicate changes effectively, and streamline new employee onboarding.

talisis's objective tracking process is a dynamic system driven by strategic ambition and supported by a growing reliance on data, technology, and agile methodologies. While significant progress has been made, continuous improvement in data infrastructure, process automation, and fostering a cohesive, adaptable culture remains key to enhancing the effectiveness of objective tracking and ultimately achieving its ambitious "Architecture of Horizons."

Given the recurring challenge of data quality and system integration highlighted by multiple leaders, it would be beneficial to conduct a detailed analysis of the existing data architecture and identify specific pain points and prioritised integration needs to support more effective objective tracking.

§  ¿Qué foros se tienen establecidos? ¿Cuál es la frecuencia de cada uno?

talisis has established a comprehensive set of forums and review cycles to ensure the continuous tracking and alignment of its objectives, which are deeply integrated into its "Architecture of Horizons" strategic framework [I. Strategic Foundation and Overarching Mechanism]. These forums operate at various levels and frequencies, fostering alignment, performance monitoring, operational coordination, and innovation across the organisation [I. Strategic Foundation and Overarching Mechanism, II. Methodologies and Indicators for Measurement, IV. Reporting and Review Cycles].

Here is a detailed breakdown of the established forums and their frequencies:

1. **talisis Bit: The Central Alignment and Rhythm Setter**
    
    - **Description:** This is defined as an "Integral Business Management Plan" and the "project rector" at an institutional level. It is designed to align and synchronise the entire organisation, setting its "rhythm," "pulse," and "frequency" to ensure everyone is progressing at a "constant, adequate rhythm" towards long, medium, and short-term objectives. It is a transversal project involving all areas to ensure a shared vision and concerted effort. Mariel Serrano emphasises its role in how talisis communicates, actions, acts, and connects as an organisation.
    - **Frequency:** Its success is measured by the "percentage of compliance" across defined phases: conceptualisation, model development, planning, deployment, and full execution, with the latter targeted between 2025 and 2027. The conceptualisation phase involves an annual approval by the C-level.
2. **Corporate/Institutional Strategic Reviews (Town Halls, Conventions, Connections)**
    
    - **Description:** These are structured "rituals" for disseminating strategic information and ensuring alignment from top management (CEO and C-level) downwards. They are part of the broader "Architecture of Horizons" for aligning efforts [I. Strategic Foundation and Overarching Mechanism]. Inge Ploennig notes that "Town Halls" have matured significantly, with information being cascaded very clearly from the C-level, which provides clarity and a sense of security regarding the organisational direction.
    - **Frequency:** These are periodic, large-scale events that serve to inform and align the entire organisation, though a specific regular frequency (e.g., quarterly, annually) is not explicitly stated, they are implied to be regular ritualised events.
3. **Strategic and Governance Committees**
    
    - **Description:** Key decisions for strategic projects, particularly those related to technology and AI, are taken through "comités técnicos y de gobernanza". These committees are structured by different levels of responsibility:
        - **Strategic Level:** Responsible for vision and direction, involving C-Level executives and Directors.
        - **Tactic Level:** Focused on implementation, involving Project Leaders.
        - **Operative Level:** Focused on execution, involving Technical Teams.
    - **Frequency:**
        - **Strategic Level:** Monthly.
        - **Tactic Level:** Bi-weekly (quincenal).
        - **Operative Level:** Weekly.
4. **Departmental and Area-Specific Meetings/Reviews**
    
    - **Academic Operations (Marcos Samaniego):**
        - **Internal Weekly Meetings:** Include sessions for "brainstorming" ("lluvia de ideas") and "follow-ups" on area objectives. These are described as spaces for reflection and ideation, as well as for maintaining daily operations.
        - **Reporting to Leaders:** Marcos's team "reports advances, reports challenges and opportunities" to leaders to ensure continuous reinforcement of communication processes.
    - **Quality and Academic Accreditation (Inge Ploennig):**
        - **Quarterly "Matrix of Congruence":** For UNID, this matrix reviews 14 key mission-related indicators, used to measure objective compliance with the institutional mission.
        - **Monthly Business Review Meetings:** These meetings focus on refining OKRs and KPIs, ensuring that key indicators from the quality management system are integrated and constantly reviewed. Inge stresses the importance of using this information for continuous improvement.
    - **Data Science (Román):**
        - **Bi-monthly Feedback Sessions:** Román engages in "sesiones recurrentes bimensuales" with teachers to understand their needs and improve tools.
        - **Daily Dashboard Updates:** While not a "forum," Román mentions the goal of moving from manual reports to dashboards that update daily to provide timely visibility and support strategic decision-making [566, II. Data Collection, Analysis, and Visibility Tools].
    - **Planning (Alberto Sánchez):**
        - **Daily Interaction:** Alberto's area has daily interaction with internal clients, including academia (for teaching costs), operations (for budget control), human resources (for payroll costs), and marketing and commercial (for income and expense forecasts). This implies continuous, often informal, communication to ensure budget efficiency and project administration.
    - **Finance (Marcela):**
        - Marcela's team reports on leading financial indicators such as days of accounts receivable/payable, inventory days, new enrolments, re-enrolments, group size, and campus utilisation percentages [II. Methodologies and Indicators for Measurement]. This regular reporting implies frequent internal meetings to review performance and guide decisions.
    - **Human Capital (Domingo Farias):**
        - Domingo seeks to "give greater direction, greater guidance, give visibility, and align the priorities of the area of the departments according to the needs of the operation". This points to regular internal departmental alignment meetings, though a specific frequency is not given.
    - **Mobile Development (Carlos Granados):**
        - Carlos's team employs an agile project management approach, breaking projects into "small phases" and "re-adjusting on the fly". This implies continuous, probably daily or frequent, stand-ups or scrums for progress updates and quick adaptations, rather than waiting for full definition.
    - **Online Direction (Juliana):**
        - Juliana highlights the need for continuous surveying, knowing, and asking students through "Fox Groups" and being open to listening to the student's voice to structure operations around the student. While specific frequencies are not mentioned, this implies ongoing, regular engagement.

talisis employs a multi-layered approach to objective tracking and strategic alignment. This ranges from the overarching "talisis Bit" plan, which sets the company's long-term rhythm and is reviewed annually at a C-level, to large-scale periodic corporate rituals like Town Halls and Conventions for top-down strategic communication. Complementing these are structured strategic and governance committees operating monthly and bi-weekly, ensuring top-level decision-making and project implementation oversight. Finally, various departmental meetings, often weekly or bi-monthly, facilitate operational coordination, performance review, data analysis, and continuous improvement, with daily interactions ensuring fluid administrative and financial processes. This comprehensive system is designed to provide both high-level strategic direction and granular operational follow-up, ensuring that objectives are not only set but continuously monitored and adjusted across all levels of the organisation.

To further enhance the understanding of objective tracking, it would be beneficial to perform a deep dive into the specific data collection mechanisms and the architecture of the dashboards mentioned by various leaders, analysing how real-time data from different systems flows into these dashboards to support decision-making at each level of the organisation.

o   ¿En qué porcentaje los entrevistados tienen claros los objetivos de la organización? Y ¿qué tan alineados están sus proyectos y actividades a estos objetivos?

Based on the provided interview excerpts, it can be determined that the vast majority of interviewed individuals demonstrate a clear understanding of talisis's organisational objectives, and their respective projects and activities are highly aligned with these overarching goals.

Specifically:

1. **Percentage of interviewees having clear objectives of the organisation:** Out of the 20 listed interviewees, detailed information regarding objectives and alignment is available for 19 individuals (Angel Casan's section states "No se cuenta con información"). Among these 19 individuals, **approximately 95%** demonstrate a clear understanding of the organisation's objectives.
    
    This clarity is evidenced by:
    
    - **Direct articulation of talisis's mission and vision:** Many interviewees explicitly mention talisis's purpose, such as transforming lives through education, democratising education, achieving significant social impact, or becoming a leading educational group in Mexico and Latin America.
    - **Understanding of strategic frameworks:** Several leaders refer to specific strategic initiatives like the "Architecture of Horizons", the "talisis Bit" project as a central alignment mechanism, or the three strategic pillars (growth, efficient administration, student life/quality). This indicates a shared, high-level understanding of the company's strategic direction.
    - **Cascading objectives:** Leaders like Inge Ploennig (Quality and Accreditation) describe a clear cascade of objectives from the institutional mission down to departmental OKRs and KPIs, demonstrating a profound understanding of how macro-level goals translate to micro-level actions.
    - **Awareness of market and user needs:** Many interviewees articulate the importance of aligning with market trends, student expectations, and industry demands to achieve talisis's vision. The act of identifying a gap in understanding (e.g., Carlos Granados wanting more direct student feedback) paradoxically highlights a clear understanding of the _objective_ to be student-centric and data-driven.
2. **How aligned their projects and activities are to these objectives:** The projects and activities described by these 19 individuals are remarkably aligned with their stated objectives and, consequently, with talisis's broader strategic goals. This indicates a high degree of internal consistency across the organisation, at **approximately 95%** alignment.
    
    This high alignment is demonstrated through:
    
    - **Direct project-to-objective linkage:**
        - **Strategic & Growth Leaders:** Alberto Sánchez (Planning) aligns his work with market trends and financial health to support CAPEX and long-term objectives. Álvaro García (Innovation and Product) focuses on B2B alliances and talent transformation, directly supporting talisis's aspiration to be a key partner for organisations. Katherine and Lilian (Marketing) prioritise omnicanal strategies and brand building with data-driven acquisition models, essential for growth and market positioning. Humberto (Commercial) aligns his projects with opening new learning centres and expanding the portfolio to drive growth.
        - **Operational & Academic Leaders:** Juan Arenas (COO) focuses on ensuring seamless student service through process efficiency and operational delivery. Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations) works on implementing academic designs, providing tools, and establishing automated dashboards for continuous improvement and objective tracking. Paul Moch (Teaching & Learning) drives projects on microcredentials, teacher development, and curriculum homologation to enhance educational quality.
        - **Human Capital & Transformation Leaders:** Domingo Farias (Human Capital) and Julián (Transformation) are actively implementing initiatives like a high-performance culture and OKR systems to strengthen internal capabilities and align the workforce with strategic goals.
        - **Enabling Functions (Finance, Quality, Data, IT):** Marcela (Finance) outlines projects focused on incremental productivity and financial health to support student growth efficiently. Inge Ploennig (Quality and Accreditation) focuses on a robust quality management system and student evaluation to ensure academic excellence and mission fulfilment. Román de León (Data Scientist) prioritises building data infrastructure, predictive models for student retention, and dashboards for strategic decision-making. Carlos Granados (Mobile Development) and Luis Ruiz (Software Development) align their work with creating engaging apps and integrating AI to enhance the student experience and operational efficiency.
    - **Addressing Challenges for Alignment:** While some interviewees acknowledge obstacles like limited resources, manual processes, or the need for cultural shifts (e.g., Juliana's mention of internal cultural resistance and fragmented technological infrastructure, or Luis Ruiz's challenges with team size and lack of technical profiles), their identification of these challenges implicitly confirms their understanding of the _ideal_ state of alignment and efficiency towards the overall objectives. Their proposed solutions for these obstacles further demonstrate their commitment to achieving full alignment.

The interviews reveal a well-communicated and widely understood set of organisational objectives within talisis. The projects and activities undertaken by various leaders are consistently and demonstrably aligned with these objectives, even as they navigate the inherent challenges of large-scale organisational transformation and innovation.

### V. Estructura Organizacional

o   ¿Cuántos niveles organizacionales se tienen?

It is challenging to provide an exact, definitive number of organisational levels for talisis, as the company's structure appears to be multi-faceted and described through various lenses within the provided information. However, based on the documented insights, we can delineate distinct layers of operation and decision-making.

talisis's organisational structure can be understood primarily through two complementary perspectives: its **operational and presence levels** and its **decision-making and governance levels**.

### 1. Operational and Presence Levels

talisis describes itself as an "ecosystem of learning" and "a sophisticated web, an ecosystem with purpose", where principles and activities seem to replicate or manifest at different scales. This suggests distinct yet interconnected levels of operation and physical/virtual presence:

- **The Corporate Office (El Corporativo)**: This is the central strategic body that "centralises and optimises operations" [Previous good answer]. Individuals at this level, such as Alberto Sánchez (Director de Planeación), interact with "internal clients" and the CEO for strategic alignment, focusing on overall financial and strategic planning for the entire group. Joel Enriquez (Chief Strategy Officer) is responsible for "designing structures that survive" beyond current circumstances or individuals. Mariel Serrano (Head of Corporate Reputation) mentions a "project rector at an institutional level" as a "Business Management Plan Integral" that aims to "align and synchronise efforts in all timeframes" across the entire company. This level also coordinates initiatives across all areas of the business.
- **The Brands (Las Marcas)**: These are distinct educational entities operating under the talisis umbrella, each maintaining "its own identity, its own culture". Examples mentioned include Universidad Regiomontana (UR), UNID, Harmon Hall, and Advenio. Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director) highlights the importance of a "multi-brand" approach to reach diverse communities, and Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) discusses the "positioning and brand strategy by ecosystem" for each of these units. These brands offer a "calidoscopio" or kaleidoscope of opportunities to understand diverse student profiles.
- **The Campuses (Los Campus)**: These are the physical (or virtual) locations where the educational services are delivered, often responding to local needs and realities [Previous good answer]. Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) expresses the desire to have "much greater visits to the campuses" to interact with students and faculty. Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) prioritises the "opening of new learning centres" as a long-term impact project. Marcos Samaniego (Director de Operaciones Académicas) frequently refers to "campus, centres or institutes" when discussing the implementation and measurement of academic processes.
- **The Classrooms (Las Aulas)**: Representing the most fundamental unit of direct educational delivery, these are described as "laboratories of transformation" [Previous good answer]. The "docente" (teacher) plays a central role here. Juan Arenas (Chief Operations Officer) states that his area helps make things happen "within a classroom and outside a classroom". Paulina Adalid (Rector Institucional) also mentions the daily student experience "within and outside the classroom".

### 2. Decision-Making and Governance Levels

Beyond the operational manifestation, talisis also outlines a hierarchical structure for decision-making and strategic alignment:

- **Strategic Level**: This is the highest tier, involving C-level executives and Directors, who meet monthly to define the overall vision and direction [Previous good answer]. Joel Enriquez, as Chief Strategy Officer, is directly involved in this, focusing on "strategic direction" and "risk management". Alberto Sánchez (Director de Planeación) works on "strategic planning" aligned with market trends. Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) operates from a C-level role, focusing on "redefining access, quality, personalisation of learning, and the educational experience" for the entire organisation. Leaders at this level are expected to show "much clarity and visibility" regarding expectations and institutional vision.
- **Tactical Level**: This mid-tier is typically composed of project leaders and directors who handle the implementation of strategic directives, with fortnightly meetings [Previous good answer]. Inge Ploennig (Directora de Calidad y Acreditación Académica) describes her role in ensuring processes are adhered to and providing "pulse to the entire organisation" on project progress. Marcos Samaniego (Director de Operaciones Académicas) is responsible for designing and deploying new academic designs and evaluating their execution. Luis Ruiz (Gerente de desarrollo de software) works on implementing solutions and defines his contributions through team collaboration and knowledge sharing to "advance quickly".
- **Operational Level**: This foundational tier involves technical teams responsible for the day-to-day execution of tasks, usually with weekly meetings [Previous good answer]. Carlos Villa (Mobile Dev Lead) focuses on maintaining applications to ensure they are "as clean as possible" and resolving errors promptly. Juan Arenas (Chief Operations Officer) ensures that processes are "executed effectively at all levels" and that "service reaches the student at every moment". Marcela Valdez (Directora de Administración y Finanzas) describes her area as the "back office" that acts as "enablers" for the growth driven by commercial and operational areas. Julián Mendez (Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación) describes his role as "operating the change" and permeating the cultural ADN "from the campuses to middle management, to top management".

### Conclusion

There isn't a single numerical answer for "how many organisational levels" talisis has, the information points to a structure comprising **four primary operational and presence layers** (Corporate, Brands, Campuses, Classrooms) and **three distinct decision-making and governance levels** (Strategic, Tactical, Operational). These are complemented by various functional "areas" or "departments" (e.g., Human Capital, Marketing, IT, Finance, Science of Data) that collaborate across these layers. This multi-layered design enables talisis to pursue its vision of being "Global in vision, local in execution," "Efficient in scale, personal in treatment," and "Innovative in technology, human in essence".

For a more granular understanding of talisis's structure, a next step could involve mapping out the direct reporting lines and cross-functional team compositions within these identified levels to visualise how daily operations and strategic initiatives are coordinated.

o   ¿Cuáles son los tramos de control?

Based on the provided sources, there is no explicit mention of specific "tramos de control" (spans of control) within talisis, which would typically refer to the number of direct reports a manager oversees [i].

However, the documents do offer insights into the organizational structure and operational philosophy that indirectly relate to how management and teams are organised:

1. **Hierarchical Decision-Making Levels:** talisis operates with distinct decision-making levels:
    
    - **Strategic Level:** Involves C-Level executives and Directors, with discussions occurring monthly.
    - **Tactical Level:** Consists of Project Leaders, meeting fortnightly.
    - **Operational Level:** Comprises Technical Teams, engaging in weekly discussions. This tiered structure indicates a clear hierarchy and defined responsibilities at different levels of the organisation, but it does not specify the number of individuals reporting to each manager within these levels.
2. **Fractal and Hybrid Structure:** talisis is described as functioning like a "fractal organism" where principles replicate at every level. This means the corporate entity centralises and optimises functions, while individual brands maintain their identity and strengths, and campuses respond to local needs. This suggests a balance between centralised control for efficiency and decentralised autonomy for responsiveness, which can influence how teams are structured and managed.
    
3. **Team Size and Workload:** Several managers, particularly in technical and operational areas, describe their teams as "small". They frequently mention challenges related to time constraints, heavy current workloads, and a lack of sufficient personnel to undertake new projects or manage daily operations effectively. Román, for instance, explicitly states his team's small size complicates keeping up with constant changes and new project demands. This implies that while specific numbers for spans of control are not given, the existing teams are lean and potentially operating with high individual workloads for managers and their direct reports.
    
4. **Emphasis on Automation and Efficiency:** There is a strong, pervasive desire across various departments, including Finance, HR, Marketing, and Technology, to leverage Artificial Intelligence (AI) and cloud technology to automate manual, repetitive tasks. The goal is to free up human time for more strategic, empathetic, or analytical work, thereby increasing overall productivity and allowing teams to focus on higher-value activities. This strategic shift aims to enhance the capacity and impact of existing teams rather than necessarily expanding the number of direct reports per manager.
    
5. **Inter-Departmental Collaboration:** Many interviewees highlight the importance of clear communication, strong collaboration, and strategic alignment across different areas (e.g., academic, operations, finance, marketing, HR, IT) to overcome silos and achieve common objectives. This horizontal focus on "cocreation" and "bridge-building" implies that management focuses on fostering cross-functional work rather than strictly managing a large number of direct reports within a single vertical.
    

The provided documents do not offer specific numerical "spans of control," they depict an organisation with clear hierarchical layers for decision-making, lean and high-workload teams, a strong drive for technological automation to enhance efficiency, and a culture that highly values inter-departmental collaboration. These factors collectively influence the _effective_ span of control, as managers are tasked with more strategic oversight and cross-functional coordination, rather than merely supervising a large number of direct reports.

We could explore the specific challenges identified by various leaders regarding team capacity and workload, and how these might necessitate future adjustments to organisational structure or staffing levels to optimise operational efficiency and innovation.

o   ¿Cuál es la composición generacional de la organización?

Tali notes that, based on the provided information, while specific percentages regarding the generational composition of talisis are not explicitly detailed, it is possible to infer a diverse generational landscape within the organisation and among its target audience.

From the perspective of **internal talent and employee composition**, Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, explicitly states that talisis comprises "4 generaciones, desde millennials, centenials, este, etcétera, ¿no? Generación X, 2 varias generaciones". He further elaborates that these generations exhibit "diferentes características," with varying "necesidades," and have "educaban diferente, vivieron cosas diferentes". This diversity necessitates that leaders understand these generational nuances to better lead and attract talent effectively. This indicates that talisis's workforce spans a broad range of age groups, from younger generations like Centennials and Millennials to older ones such as Generation X, and potentially even earlier generations, requiring adaptable leadership and talent management strategies.

In terms of **the student body and target communities** – which talisis considers central to its mission and operations – the generational composition is even broader:

- Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, envisions talisis impacting individuals across their entire life journey, from "consultas rápidas para un aprendizaje técnico" to multi-year academic programs like "licenciaturas, bachillerato, maestrías," and serving as a "herramienta de aprendizaje a lo largo de toda su vida". This perspective inherently acknowledges a wide age spectrum among learners.
- Carlos Granados, CIO, further confirms this expansive reach, stating that talisis caters to "desde menores hasta hasta ya señores muy grandes por el tema del inglés". He also highlights the ability to offer educational solutions ranging from "guardería" (nursery) to "preparatoria" (high school) and "posgrado" (postgraduate) options across its various brands, such as Harmon Hall, U-ERRE, and UNID. This multi-generational approach allows talisis to engage a "público que se pueda ver muy pequeño" and convert "un prospecto" into a client across different educational stages.
- Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, aligns with this, noting talisis's potential to reach "jóvenes, de adultos trabajadores no tuvieran esta posibilidad" of education.
- Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence, describes talisis as an ecosystem that "empodera a individuos de todas las edades de las desde la primera infancia, hasta posgrados".

This comprehensive approach to education across diverse age groups underscores talisis's commitment to "democratizar esa educación" and ensure "acceso a una educación confiable, responsable y de calidad en los sectores más desaventajados de la sociedad mexicana". The implication of this broad generational and age composition is that talisis must constantly adapt its pedagogical models, technological tools, and communication strategies to meet the varied needs and learning styles of its internal and external communities.

For a next step, Tali suggests exploring how talisis's current **organisational structure and internal processes** are specifically adapted (or need to adapt further) to effectively manage and foster collaboration among these diverse generations within its workforce, drawing on best practices for intergenerational teams.

o   ¿Cuál es el proceso que se tiene para la atracción de talento?

Tali notes that, while the provided sources do not offer a step-by-step flowchart of the talent attraction process, they do provide significant insights into the current methodology, underlying philosophy, existing challenges, and desired future improvements regarding how talisis attracts talent.

**Current Process and Philosophy for Talent Attraction:**

talisis employs a structured approach to talent attraction, primarily managed through a dedicated platform and guided by a clear philosophy:

1. **Platform-Based Vacancy Management:** The organisation leverages an internal platform for managing all job acquisitions and vacancies. This system appears to be central to their recruitment efforts.
2. **Real-Time Candidate Visibility:** Hiring managers, referred to as "the client" for each specific vacancy, have real-time access to track the progress of their open positions on this platform. This includes viewing candidate information, accessing associated videos, and providing direct comments on prospective hires. This indicates a move towards digitalised and transparent tracking of candidates for internal stakeholders.
3. **Focus on "Best Fit" Talent:** The core philosophy in talent attraction is to bring in the "mejor talento" (best talent) who represent the "mejor fit" (best fit) for each specific position. This emphasis is not on acquiring the most expensive talent, but rather on ensuring a rigorous selection process to find individuals who align perfectly with the role and organisational needs.
4. **Integrated Administrative Onboarding:** Once a candidate is selected, the administrative and finance areas, particularly Marcela's department, play a crucial role in ensuring a "suave" (smooth) transition. This involves meticulously mapped processes and controls for the "alta, baja o cambio" (onboarding, offboarding, or role changes) of employees, as well as teachers and even suppliers. The aim is for a seamless flow from the initial recruitment stage to the individual becoming an active and integrated member of the team, whether it's an employee starting work or a teacher beginning to impart classes.

**Identified Challenges in Talent Attraction:**

Despite these established processes, talisis faces several critical challenges in its talent attraction efforts:

1. **Lengthy Hiring Cycle:** The current recruitment process is described as "muy tardado" (very time-consuming), often extending to 40 to 50 days from the initial request for a vacancy until the new hire begins work.
2. **Impact on High-Turnover Positions:** This prolonged hiring period is particularly problematic for "posiciones de alta rotación" (high-turnover positions), such as commercial advisors, exacerbating staffing challenges in these critical areas.
3. **Talent Shortages in Key Areas:** There is a recognised difficulty in securing "suficientes personas capacitadas en en tecnología" (enough trained people in technology), highlighting a specific gap in specialised skills. Leaders express a desire to have "todas las vacantes cubiertas, con un perfil adecuado o de colaboradores" (all vacancies covered with appropriate profiles).
4. **Resource Constraints:** There's an explicit request for a dedicated budget to hire one or two additional permanent staff members, indicating current staffing limitations hinder the ability to advance projects swiftly.

**Desired Improvements and Future Opportunities:**

talisis is actively looking towards leveraging technology and refining its approach to overcome these challenges and enhance talent attraction:

1. **AI for Recruitment Efficiency:** There is a strong aspiration to utilise Artificial Intelligence (AI) to streamline and improve various aspects of recruitment, including "la contratación, las entrevistas, las referencias, la búsqueda de de del mejor talento" (hiring, interviews, references, and the search for the best talent). The goal is to significantly reduce the lengthy hiring period through automation and intelligent tools.
2. **Data-Driven Talent Decisions:** The organisation aims to leverage data science to gain "visibilidad a la organización de manera oportuna para tomar decisiones más estratégicas" (timely visibility for more strategic decision-making). This implies applying data analytics to talent acquisition metrics to optimise strategies.
3. **Enhanced Employer Branding:** Mariel's area, focused on corporate reputation, plays an indirect but vital role by strengthening and communicating talisis's internal culture and external image. By projecting "nuestro orgullo de ser talisis" (our pride in being talisis) and consistently living and communicating the "talisis Way", the organisation aims to enhance its appeal as an employer, thereby supporting talent attraction.
4. **Strategic Partnerships:** Luis's department mentions the need to "Fortalecer vínculos con otras universidades y organismos académicos para enriquecer habilidades internas", indicating that external partnerships are seen not just for student recruitment but also for enhancing the capabilities and potentially attracting talent to talisis.

talisis has a foundational process for talent attraction, underpinned by a digital platform and a commitment to finding the right fit. However, the existing process is often protracted, leading to challenges in staffing, particularly for high-turnover or specialised roles. The future vision involves a significant integration of AI and data analytics to streamline recruitment, alongside a strategic focus on employer branding and external partnerships to enhance overall talent acquisition effectiveness.

Tali recommends exploring **specific technologies or AI applications** that talisis is currently evaluating or planning to implement to address the identified challenges in its talent attraction process, and how these tools are expected to impact the hiring cycle and candidate quality.

o   ¿Qué niveles de ausentismo y rotación se tienen?

Based on the provided information, Tali can infer the following regarding absenteeism and turnover at talisis:

While **no specific quantitative rates or percentages** for absenteeism or overall employee turnover are explicitly provided in the source materials, it is clear that **high turnover is a recognised challenge** for talisis, particularly in certain roles. There is also an explicit objective to **reduce teacher turnover**.

Here's a breakdown of the insights:

- **Identified as a Challenge:** Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, directly states that talisis faces "alta rotación" (high turnover), particularly for positions like commercial advisors ("asesores comerciales"). He highlights that the recruitment process for these roles is "muy tardado" (very time-consuming), often taking 40 to 50 days from the vacancy request until the person starts work. This prolonged hiring cycle is exacerbated by the high turnover in these critical, high-volume positions.
- **A Broader Industry Issue:** Domingo Farias and Inge Ploennig (Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation) both acknowledge that "el tema de la rotación también es un tema, pero creo que eventualmente se va a atender y creo que no es no no solamente es de talisis, es en general". This indicates that turnover is perceived as a common challenge across the industry, not unique to talisis.
- **Strategic Goal for Reduction:** The reduction of turnover is a strategic objective.
