    - Domingo Farias's area aims to "identificar realmente esa alta rotación, y y cómo atacarla puntualmente para bajar esa rotación". This suggests a focused effort to understand and mitigate the causes of high turnover.
    - Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, explicitly states that one of the indicators for project success is "menor rotación de personal docente que sea cada vez más calificada" (lower turnover of increasingly qualified teaching staff). This indicates that teacher retention is a specific metric they are working to improve, implying it is currently a challenge.
    - Luis Ruiz, Software Development Manager, mentions that current "indicadores de retención de atracción deberían aumentar conforme se liberen soluciones de inteligencia artificial que colaboren con nuestros asesores, o nuestros directores de carrera para el tema de retención y atracción". This points to the use of AI as a tool to improve retention (and attraction).
- **Impact on Resources and Capacity:** The challenge of turnover is linked to broader issues of resource availability and capacity within the organisation.
    - Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning, cites "la falta de manos" and the need for "todas las vacantes cubiertas, con un perfil adecuado o de colaboradores" as a significant challenge that impacts his ability to dedicate time to strategic design rather than daily operations. This suggests that understaffing, potentially due to difficulties in filling roles or retaining staff, creates a burden.
    - Luis Ruiz notes that a "reto importante el no tener dentro de la organización suficientes personas capacitadas en en tecnología" further hinders progress on new projects. Such shortages, if persistent, can contribute to burnout and subsequent turnover among existing staff.
- **Human Capital Strategy:** Domingo Farias's mission is to "optimizar el recurso humano en talisis" to ensure "la rentabilidad del capital humano" through "resultados de productividad de motivación," fostering "el talento adecuado con una cultura saludable, y una estrategia de recursos humanos efectiva para alcanzar sus objetivos de largo plazo". While not directly measuring turnover, this holistic approach to human capital management, including focusing on "engagement" and "calidad de vida del colaborador," implicitly addresses factors that typically influence retention and can help mitigate absenteeism. The emphasis on "Productividad" (Productivity) is also a key outcome he aims to improve.

talisis acknowledges facing **high turnover** in specific operational roles like commercial advisors and among teaching staff, viewing it as a critical and pervasive challenge. While specific figures for absenteeism or turnover rates are not disclosed, the organisation is actively seeking to address this issue through strategic talent attraction, retention initiatives, and the leveraging of technology, particularly AI, to streamline processes and improve employee experience. The overall health of its human capital, including aspects like engagement and productivity, is closely monitored as an indicator of success.

For the next step, Tali suggests delving into how talisis plans to **implement specific AI-driven solutions** to directly address the high turnover in commercial advisory roles and reduce teacher attrition, beyond just general recruitment efficiency.

o   ¿Qué programas se tienen establecidos para el desarrollo del talento?

talisis has established several programmes and initiatives for talent development, focusing on continuous learning, skill enhancement, and adapting to technological advancements. These programmes target various segments of the organisation, from leadership and academic staff to commercial teams and technical personnel.

Here is a detailed overview of the talent development programmes and strategies at talisis:

**1. Holistic Professional Development for All Employees:**

- **Integrated Growth:** talisis aims for the full professional and personal development of its employees, ensuring they acquire the critical experiences needed for career progression within the organisation. This is supported by a culture of continuous development that is seen as integral to both personal and professional life.
- **Skill-Based Training:** The organisation focuses on developing both soft skills (e.g., communication, collaborative work, decision-making, empathy) and technical skills, particularly related to technology usage to enhance the student journey.
- **Cultural Alignment:** There is an emphasis on leaders understanding and embodying talisis's culture and processes, promoting a disciplined culture of high standards where talent and attitude, combined with good development tools, can make a difference. This includes ensuring that development is part of every leader's DNA.
- **Lifelong Learning Mindset:** talisis promotes a culture of continuous learning and adaptation, encouraging teams to constantly update their knowledge and skills. This involves pushing an empathetic and collaborative mindset within the teams. Employees are encouraged to take responsibility for their own continuous learning and self-improvement.

**2. Specialised Programmes for Academic and Teaching Staff:**

- **Teacher Career Path:** A key initiative is to review and redesign the teaching career path within talisis. This involves offering not just training but also designing a critical route for professional development that meets teachers' economic, professional, and intellectual needs.
- **Digital Pedagogy Training:** Teachers receive specific training to align with the needs of digital education. The goal is to develop teachers who are experts in their subject matter _and_ in pedagogical methods that effectively support student learning.
- **Technological Proficiency for Educators:** Efforts are made to equip teachers with skills to use digital platforms effectively, not just for content delivery but to inspire new teaching methods. This includes training on advanced AI tools like ChatGPT for content creation and analysis.
- **Knowledge Dissemination:** There is a recognised need to help academic staff access and digest relevant information from research and external evaluations (like PISA), which can be challenging due to time constraints. Technology could play a role in providing this information in a more digestible format.
- **Faculty Training & Support:** Regular training and support are provided to faculty, with a focus on improving classroom performance and the practical application of academic designs.

**3. Enhancing Commercial and Sales Teams' Capabilities:**

- **Commercial Professionalisation:** Sales teams (e.g., commercial advisors) are targeted for professional development to enhance their commercial capabilities. This involves moving from client-by-client prospecting to a more massive drive, utilising technology for scalable solution design, and daring to propose ambitious impacts to organisations.
- **Productivity Optimisation with AI:** talisis aims to use AI tools to significantly reduce the "optimal productivity curve" for new commercial advisors. By providing quick access to answers for daily queries through AI, the goal is for new hires to reach full productivity much faster than the current 7-month average.
- **Specific B2B Training:** There's a request for specific professional training for the B2B sales area to boost commercial and strategic performance.

**4. Technology and AI-Driven Development:**

- **AI and Cloud Transformation:** The organisation actively embraces AI and cloud technology to transform processes and responsibilities across all areas. This involves automatising repetitive tasks, leveraging data for strategic decision-making, and personalising learning experiences.
- **AI Training and Certification:** Programs for training and certification in AI, machine learning, natural language processing, data science, UI/UX design, AI systems architecture, and cybersecurity are being established.
- **Structured Learning Phases:** Carlos Granados (CIO) outlines a structured approach to fostering an AI-driven culture, including foundational training, experimentation through Proofs of Concept (POCs) and pilot projects, implementation of strategic projects with cross-mentoring, and continuous improvement through feedback sessions and communities of practice.
- **Innovation Labs and Partnerships:** talisis encourages the use of internal innovation laboratories and collaborations with universities, research centres, and technology partners (like AWS) to stay updated on AI advancements and best practices.
- **Data Literacy:** There is a strong focus on developing data literacy and analytical skills across teams to enable data-driven decision-making and strategic planning. The goal is to have a comprehensive "map" of talent and skills for strategic placement.
- **Automation of Manual Processes:** A key objective is to identify and automate manual processes, such as variable compensation calculations for promoters and advisors, or the administrative onboarding/offboarding of employees, teachers, and suppliers, freeing up human talent for more strategic work.
- **Early Technology Adoption:** Teams are encouraged to adopt new technologies early for proof-of-concept testing, which can then evolve into robust solutions.

**5. Leadership and Strategic Thinking Development:**

- **Strategic Vision:** Leaders are expected to develop strong strategic thinking skills, focusing on long-term goals and how current decisions align with the future direction of the company.
- **Cross-Functional Collaboration:** Training and fostering collaboration are vital, with an emphasis on aligning priorities, understanding interdependencies, and fostering shared narratives across different departments (e.g., marketing, sales, IT, academia, operations, finance).
- **Managerial Skills:** Programmes aim to equip leaders with management skills that enable them to develop talent, lead teams effectively, and foster a high-performance culture.

**6. Specific Tools and Methodologies for Development:**

- **talisis Beat:** A key initiative that seeks to implement an organisational system to ensure that over 1,500 people work with focus, rhythm, and common sense. Technology acts as a "shared nervous system" to consolidate and align efforts across the organisation.
- **Dashboards and KPIs/OKRs:** Implementation of centralised dashboards and automated, real-time measurements of key performance indicators (KPIs) and objectives and key results (OKRs) to monitor operational processes and strategic progress. This provides clear visibility for leaders and supports continuous improvement.
- **Gamification:** Use of gamification in campaigns and interactions, including profile tests, challenges, badges, and rankings, to make marketing a "playful extension of learning".
- **Open Source Tools:** Adoption of open-source tools like Sentry (for error detection) and GrowthBook (for real-time adjustments) to streamline development processes and enhance efficiency.

talisis's talent development programmes are comprehensive, deeply integrated with the organisation's strategic goals, and heavily reliant on adopting and leveraging advanced technologies like AI and cloud computing. The overarching aim is to foster a culture of continuous learning, empower employees with future-proof skills, and ensure that every individual contributes to talisis's mission of transforming lives through education.

For the next step, Tali recommends exploring **how talisis measures the effectiveness and ROI of these talent development programmes**, specifically asking for details on the metrics and methodologies used to evaluate the impact of training and development on employee performance, retention, and overall organisational objectives.

o   ¿Los entrenamientos que se realizan cuentan con certificación?

Yes, talisis has established programmes for talent development that include certification.

talisis's approach to talent development is comprehensive, aiming to foster continuous learning and skill enhancement across various organisational segments. This includes both formal and informal learning pathways, with an explicit focus on certification in key strategic areas.

**Specific Programmes and Initiatives with Certification:**

1. **Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Digital Skills Certification:** Carlos Granados, the CIO of talisis, explicitly states that "programas de capacitación y certificación en IA" (training and certification programmes in AI) are to be established to maintain talent collaboration. He further elaborates that a culture of continuous learning will be promoted through "certificaciones especializadas" (specialised certifications). These programmes are part of the structured learning phases outlined, which include "Capacitación técnica especializada en IA" (specialised technical training in AI) and "Programas de certificación" (certification programmes) as a method for obtaining necessary knowledge. This indicates a clear intent to equip employees with verified AI and digital competencies, crucial for the organisation's technological transformation.

**Broader Context of Talent Development Supporting Formal Recognition:**

While explicit mentions of "certification" are concentrated in the context of AI and technology, other interviews highlight a strong emphasis on professionalisation, skill development, and continuous learning across the organisation, which often aligns with or could lead to formal recognition or certification:

- **Professional Development Pathways:** There is a recognised need to review and redesign the teaching career path, "diseñando una ruta crítica para su desarrollo profesional dentro del sistema talisis que satisfaga sus necesidades económicas, profesionales e intelectuales" (designing a critical path for their professional development within the talisis system that satisfies their economic, professional, and intellectual needs). Such structured development paths frequently incorporate certifications or formal qualifications.
- **Specialised Skills Training:** The organisation focuses on developing a wide range of skills, from technical competencies (e.g., in finance, project evaluation, M&A) to soft skills (e.g., communication, collaborative work, decision-making, empathy). Training for teachers to align with digital education needs and effectively use digital platforms and AI tools is also prioritised. While not always explicitly certified internally, these skill developments are often built upon industry standards that might offer external certification.
- **Microcredentials and Continuous Education:** Álvaro mentions the offering of "modelos flexibles de capacitación de microcredenciales" (flexible microcredential training models). Microcredentials are, by definition, certifications that validate specific skills or competencies. Additionally, talisis offers "cursos de educación continua" (continuous education courses) and aims to allow students access to "rutas de formación complementarias como skilling, cursos, diplomados" (complementary training paths such as upskilling, courses, diplomas). Diplomas and specialised courses often culminate in some form of certification or professional recognition.
- **Industry Alignment and External Alliances:** talisis aims to align its training with market needs, collaborating with enterprises to "cocrear contenidos, certificar a las habilidades" (co-create content, certify skills). This external validation or co-creation implies a focus on industry-recognised standards, which may lead to or include certifications. The collaboration with accreditation bodies like Finpes and Cambridge for Harmon Hall's Toefl and TOEIC certifications also underscores a commitment to recognised standards, even if these are primarily for student outcomes, they reflect a general quality assurance mindset that could extend to internal training.

talisis has clear programmes and intentions to provide certification, particularly in cutting-edge technological fields like AI, as a core component of its talent development strategy. This is complemented by a broader focus on professional and skill development across various roles, which also includes or can lead to formal recognition.

For the next step, I recommend we delve into **the specific metrics and evaluation frameworks talisis uses to assess the effectiveness and return on investment (ROI) of these certified training programmes**. This would help determine if the certifications translate into tangible improvements in employee performance, retention, and overall organisational objectives.

o   ¿Qué niveles de movilidad interna se tiene?

While the provided sources do not offer specific metrics or "levels" (e.g., percentages of promotions or lateral moves) of internal mobility within talisis, they strongly indicate a **strategic intent and existing commitment to fostering internal professional development and progression**. This emphasis on talent development, skill enhancement, and succession planning inherently supports and drives internal mobility within the organisation.

Here's a detailed breakdown:

**1. Strategic Intent for Internal Progression and Succession Planning:**

- **Clear Pathway for Career Advancement:** Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, explicitly states a key objective is for her team members to acquire "experiencias críticas que necesitan para poder dar su siguiente paso en su carrera profesional? Dentro de la organización". This clearly articulates a vision where employees are expected and enabled to advance their careers internally.
- **Talent Development for Executive Succession:** Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff (representing Capital Humano), highlights that a priority is the "desarrollo de nuestro personal clave, de nuestro talento clave, el mediano o largo plazo que puedan ser las cartas de reemplazo de nuestros ejecutivos". This indicates a formal strategy for vertical internal mobility, preparing key talent to assume leadership roles.
- **Strategic Placement of High-Performing Talent:** Domingo also expresses a desire to understand "dónde puedo acomodar esos top performance en los proyectos más estratégicos", implying a deliberate effort to position high-potential individuals in roles where they can have the greatest impact, which often involves internal transitions.

**2. Robust Framework for Continuous Professional Development (Enabling Mobility):**

talisis places a significant emphasis on equipping its workforce with new skills and knowledge, which serves as a foundational enabler for internal mobility. This includes:

- **Technological and Digital Skills:** There's a strong push for employees to evolve in "el tema digital, en el tema de tecnología" and to gain expertise in "inteligencia artificial" and "tecnología cloud". Carlos Granados, the CIO, further underlines the establishment of "programas de capacitación y certificación en IA" (training and certification programmes in AI) and "certificaciones especializadas" (specialised certifications) to foster continuous learning. This focus on cutting-edge skills makes employees adaptable for future roles.
- **Strategic and Analytical Acumen:** Teams are encouraged to develop "habilidades de mayor sí, o sea, desarrollar habilidades estratégicas" and to think "estratégicamente en lo que estamos haciendo". Juan Mendez notes the organisation's maturity in "la medición de de datos", indicating an increasing analytical capability across teams.
- **Soft Skills and Leadership:** Development extends to "habilidades blandas" such as "comunicación, trabajo colaborativo, toma de decisiones", and fostering an "actitud de superación". There is a desire to form "líderes que estén comprometidos con la transformación".
- **Specialised Training:** Specific areas, like sales, focus on "profesionalizar su capacidad comercial", while others emphasize mastering "plataformas avanzadas" and "herramientas de BI". Lilian Lozano stresses "LifeLong Learning".
- **Knowledge Sharing and Experimentation:** Teams are encouraged to explore "librerías nuevas que salen, metodologías este, innovadoras, frameworks de desarrollo también novedosos" and "experimentación temprana de tecnologías emergentes", indicating a culture that supports learning and application of new knowledge, making employees versatile for new internal roles.

**3. Implied or Desired Internal Movement and Talent Optimisation:**

While explicit internal mobility figures are not provided, several statements suggest that movement and flexible deployment of talent are part of the organisational dynamic or aspiration:

- **Addressing Internal Job Seeking:** The desire to offer "sueldos suficientes para no estar buscando oportunidades en otros espacios dentro de talisis" implicitly confirms that employees do, or might, look for new opportunities _within_ the company as an alternative to leaving entirely.
- **Cross-functional Collaboration as a Precursor:** The strong emphasis on "colaboración transversal" between various areas (e.g., marketing, sales, IT, academia, operations) and the desire for "workflows interáreas" can naturally lead to greater understanding of other functions, facilitating lateral moves or cross-functional projects that build broader organisational experience.
- **Leaders' Desire for New Internal Roles:** Paul Moch's personal ambition to "poder dar clases para ser docente dentro de la institución y también conocer tanto los procesos como a los estudiantes de primera mano" demonstrates a personal drive for internal role transition, suggesting that such opportunities might be considered or sought.
- **Organisational Adaptability:** The "Reporte Nicho" highlights talisis's "flexibilidad en nuestro ADN, capacidad de pivotar sin perder esencia" and functioning as a "organismo fractal" where "innovación puede surgir en cualquier punto y escalar a todo el sistema". This organisational agility implicitly supports the ability to move talent to where it's most needed or where new opportunities arise.

**4. Challenges and Constraints Impacting Mobility:**

Despite the strong intent, some challenges are mentioned that could affect the _ease_ or _rate_ of internal mobility:

- **Capacity and Resource Constraints:** Luis Ruiz and Román mention "el tiempo y la carga de trabajo actual, el equipo no es grande", and "no tener dentro de la organización suficientes personas capacitadas", which can limit the ability to release employees for new internal roles or invest heavily in extensive internal training programmes for new positions. Román also highlights that a small team and constant project load make it difficult to keep up with changes and potentially re-implement solutions, affecting the adoption of new technologies or roles.
- **Cultural and Process Resistance:** Juliana Effting points out "la resistencia cultural interna" and a "falta de mentalidad de transformación digital" as obstacles. Such resistance could impede smooth transitions into new roles or acceptance of new ways of working that come with internal mobility. Alejandro also desires clear and documented processes, which, if lacking, could make internal transitions less efficient.

Specific "levels of internal mobility" data is not provided, talisis demonstrates a clear and consistent commitment to internal talent development and succession planning, which are direct drivers of internal mobility. The organisation focuses on continuously upskilling its workforce, fostering cross-functional collaboration, and strategically deploying talent. However, challenges related to resource limitations and cultural resistance may influence the practical execution and scale of these internal movements.

For the next step, I recommend exploring **the specific programmes or initiatives talisis has in place to facilitate internal mobility beyond general training, such as formal mentorship programmes, rotational assignments, or internal job posting systems.** This would provide a clearer picture of how the organisation translates its intent into actionable pathways for employee movement.

### VI. Resultado Financiero del Negocio

o   ¿Se alcanzaron los resultados esperados durante el 2024?

Based on the provided sources, there is **no explicit statement confirming whether talisis reached its expected financial results for 2024** [All sources].

However, the interviews provide insights into:

- **Current Financial Focus and Challenges:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, indicates that the current year (implicitly 2024, given the interview context) presents specific challenges. She states that a primary short-term objective is to "vigilar y propiciar que el flujo de efectivo mínimo se cubra". This suggests that securing minimum cash flow and recovering outstanding accounts are critical priorities, implying that expected financial results might be under pressure or not yet fully assured for the year. She also notes that this situation necessitates carefully choosing projects, as some that "suenan muy este, muy prósperos para el futuro" might be deferred due to the need to "cuidar este el corto plazo".
- **General Financial Health Objectives:** Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, mentions that for the "siguientes 10 años" (which includes 2024), planning is centred on ensuring the financial structure "soporte todas las necesidades internas y externas". He aims for a "estado de resultados y un balance saludable" and "tener flujo". However, these are aspirational statements for long-term financial health rather than a report on 2024's actual performance.
- **Current Year Operational Objectives:** Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, indicates that departments are focused on "las necesidades actuales de la operación" and are clarifying "qué se quiere lograr este año". This suggests ongoing efforts to meet current objectives in areas such as technology, talent attraction, and critical positions, but does not confirm their achievement.
- **External Pressures on Profitability:** Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, identifies "la desaceleración económica y la presión por por la rentabilidad" as a critical external challenge. This highlights the demanding economic environment that could influence financial outcomes, but again, it does not confirm the achievement of specific targets.
- **Overall Organisational Success Metrics (Long-Term):** Nicho Garza, CEO of talisis, outlines several key organisational success metrics, including "Crecimiento en ventas y EBITDA", "Empleabilidad y ROI educativo", and "Net Promoter Score y satisfacción". He also mentions that "81% de egresados que consiguen empleo antes de graduarse" and that "cada peso invertido en educación que genera 14 pesos de retorno social". While these metrics demonstrate overall impact and long-term success, they are not presented as specific achieved financial results for the year 2024.

The sources do not provide a definitive 'yes' or 'no' regarding the achievement of 2024 financial results, they strongly indicate that the year is characterised by **active management of financial challenges** and a **strategic focus on maintaining profitability and cash flow** in a demanding economic environment.

For a more precise understanding of the 2024 financial performance, it would be beneficial to **request access to specific internal financial reports for the current fiscal year**, as this would provide the detailed data needed to assess whether expected results were met.

o   ¿Se tiene alguna gráfica que muestre el ranking de cada unidad/centro en base a sus resultados?

Not in these interviews. 

o   ¿Cuáles son los principales elementos de Costo? (Top 3)

As Tali, I can confirm that based on the provided insights, the top three principal cost elements for talisis are **Personnel Costs (including Payroll and Faculty Costs), Marketing and Customer Acquisition Costs, and Technology and Infrastructure Costs**. These categories represent significant areas of investment and, at times, present challenges in terms of efficiency and management.

Allow me to elaborate on each of these crucial cost elements:

### 1. Personnel Costs (Payroll and Faculty Costs)

This category encompasses all expenses related to talisis's workforce, including salaries, benefits, and the compensation of both administrative staff and the vital teaching faculty. It is consistently highlighted as a substantial and complex cost to manage effectively.

- **Significance and Scope:** Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, explicitly states that "the issue of faculty cost" and "payroll costs" are significant. He elaborates that payroll is an "important cost for us, the issue of payroll, and it's how to make that payroll efficient – it doesn't mean reducing it, it doesn't necessarily mean increasing it, but how the payroll expense works in the most efficient way with the support of technology". Juan Arenas, COO, also points to the central role of "professors, academics, school services personnel" in delivering the student experience, implicitly highlighting their cost significance.
- **Efficiency Challenges:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, notes that ensuring "minimum cash flow is covered" and "recovery of the outstanding portfolio" are basic priorities, suggesting that personnel costs, among others, are under scrutiny for efficiency. Alejandro Madrazo, Academic Director, mentions "the lack of an adequate budget, particularly in faculty cost", underscoring financial constraints in this area.
- **Talent Acquisition and Retention:** Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, points to "high turnover in advisors" and the "very slow" hiring process (50 days) for high-turnover positions, which directly translates into significant recruitment and training costs. Román de León, Data Scientist, also expresses the need for a "budget to expand the team with one or two permanent people" due to the current team size and lack of adequate profiles, indicating a need for more investment in human capital.
- **Operational Impact:** Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning, expresses a desire to "give classes to be a teacher" to better understand day-to-day operations, implying a need for closer alignment or understanding of faculty operational realities, which can impact their effective cost. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, mentions that the use of AI has "reduced both financial and personnel resources" in content creation, showing an effort to manage personnel costs through technological integration.

### 2. Marketing and Customer Acquisition Costs (CAC)

These are the investments made to attract new students and retain existing ones, encompassing advertising, digital campaigns, lead generation, and the efforts of the sales teams. This cost element is critical for talisis's growth trajectory but is facing increasing pressure.

- **Rising Costs:** Alberto Sánchez highlights that "in recent years, marketing expenses, not only in the educational sector but in all sectors, have increased considerably". He monitors "the relationship of how much we are spending in marketing and sales versus what we are bringing in new revenue".
- **Acquisition Efficiency:** Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales, states his area's primary contribution is "capturing and retaining students" and aims to "improve the acquisition cost". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, emphasizes the importance of "optimizing the CPL (Cost Per Lead) and the funnel per cycle", noting that the "CPL is getting higher" due to advertising saturation.
- **Strategic Role:** Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, views his area as "the engine that converts strategy into real, sustainable growth", underscoring the necessity of these expenditures. He points out that "the economic slowdown and pressure for profitability" are critical external challenges influencing these costs. Katherine Romero, Senior Marketing Manager, echoes this, stating that "marketing is a key piece to materialize talisis's vision" and that their goal is to "capture attention in an oversaturated market".
- **Omnichannel Strategy:** The need for "omnichannel activations" and "a clear commercial strategy" across digital and offline channels implies a diversified and potentially higher investment in marketing efforts to reach various segments.

### 3. Technology and Infrastructure Costs (including AI and Cloud)

This category includes expenses for software licenses, hardware, network infrastructure, cloud computing services, artificial intelligence development, and the specialised IT and data science personnel required to implement and maintain these solutions. It is crucial for talisis's digital transformation and operational efficiency.

- **Modernization and Automation:** Alberto Sánchez stresses the need for "digital tools" to move "beyond Excel" and make budgeting and business cases "more automated, more modern, less artisanal". Juan Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, highlights "the automation of our processes" as a significant opportunity to make them "more effective, easier, more technological, with much faster real-time responses".
- **Integration Challenges and Investment:** Inge Ploennig identifies "technology" as an "Achilles' heel" due to a "lack of integrated systems", leading to manual processes that consume significant time. She strongly believes that "without technology, we cannot achieve it, and increasingly so". Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, notes that current "technological limitations" such as fragmented platforms and dispersed data imply "a strong investment and very capable people in data" to resolve.
- **Cloud and AI Impact:** Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, sees cloud technology as bringing "a lot of speed" and enabling "resolution of cases for our students". Carlos Villa, Mobile Dev Lead, envisions AI assisting students with "tutorials" and "solving doubts", and personally uses AI for "code review, suggestions, unit tests", indicating its operational value. Luis Ruiz, Software Development Manager, prioritises "building this data architecture" and "the use of chatbots" to leverage AI and data for better insights. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, explicitly mentions the challenges of an "underutilized SAP" system and a "lack of interface" with the core student banner system, leading to "open controls" and "discontrol", directly pointing to the need for investment in integrated technological solutions. Román de León, Data Scientist, advocates for a "strategic technological partner" to homologate architectures and improve data flow.
- **Strategic Imperative:** Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional, states that "today we could not think that without using these tools of artificial intelligence and all the online tools that exist, this is what is guiding us to do things correctly". This emphasizes that technology is no longer optional but a fundamental requirement for competitive operation.

These three cost elements are deeply interconnected, and managing them efficiently is paramount for talisis to achieve its ambitious vision of educational transformation and sustained growth.

To further refine our strategic recommendations, I propose we conduct a deeper analysis into the **Return on Investment (ROI) of talisis's technology initiatives**, particularly focusing on how successful implementation of AI and cloud solutions directly translates into demonstrable savings in personnel costs or a significant increase in marketing efficiency and customer acquisition. This would allow us to prioritize investments in technology that yield the highest financial and operational impact.

o   ¿Qué gestión se tiene establecida para dar seguimiento a los elementos del costo?

Based on the provided information, talisis has a multifaceted and evolving approach to cost management, involving strategic planning, continuous monitoring, and an increasing reliance on technology for efficiency. The management of cost elements is not merely about reduction but about optimising distribution and ensuring value generation.

Here is a detailed overview of the established cost management practices:

### 1. Centralised Financial Planning and Budgetary Control

The core of cost management at talisis resides in its financial and strategic planning functions. Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, highlights the importance of a well-structured financial setup, ensuring economic resources, a healthy profit and loss statement (P&L), balance sheet, and sufficient cash flow. His area is responsible for "administering debt and capital raising more efficiently" and "organising more efficiently where we allocate resources, in what cost item, in what expense item". This indicates a deliberate approach to resource allocation rather than reactive spending. The department engages in daily interactions with internal clients, including academic teams for faculty costs, operations for budget control, human resources for payroll, and marketing for revenue and expenditure forecasts. This broad interaction ensures a company-wide alignment on budget adherence and financial forecasting.

Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, reinforces this by stating her mission includes "leading budgetary planning" and "analysis of key indicators to improve efficiency and profitability". Her team provides financial information and analysis, guiding other departments on the responsible use of economic resources through "coaching or internal consulting" on business cases, productivity analysis, and cost-benefit assessments. A crucial short-term priority for her area is to "ensure that the minimum cash flow is covered" and manage the "recovery of the outstanding portfolio". This highlights a strong focus on immediate financial health in addition to long-term planning.

### 2. Strategic Cost Efficiency and Optimisation

talisis's approach to costs is centred on efficiency and optimisation rather than just cuts. Alberto Sánchez explicitly states that the goal for payroll is "how to make that payroll efficient – it doesn't mean reducing it, it doesn't necessarily mean increasing it, but how the payroll expense works in the most efficient way with the support of technology". This philosophy extends to all costs and expenses, where the aim is to distribute them "as efficiently as possible" by "making use of technology".

Marcela Valdez also champions "incremental productivity" as a key project, aiming to "serve more students with economies of scale". Her department acts as an "enabler" from the back office, ensuring administrative and financial processes support the growth and transformation driven by commercial and operational areas. This involves designing processes to support multi-channel and multi-product strategies, ensuring accurate financial reading and effective resource allocation. Simplification of administrative structures, such as reducing the number of legal entities, is also envisioned to "reduce the burden" and avoid unnecessary inter-company transactions.

Alejandro Madrazo, Academic Director, points to the need to "reduce the dispersion and atomisation of groups so that the teaching cost is naturally efficient," indicating an operational approach to managing faculty costs.

### 3. Leveraging Technology for Cost Management

Technology is increasingly seen as a critical enabler for efficient cost management.

- **Automation of Processes:** Alberto Sánchez envisions moving "beyond Excel" with "digital tools" to make budgeting and business cases "more automated, more modern, less artisanal". Juan Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, highlights "the automation of our processes" as a significant opportunity to make them "more effective, easier, more technological, with much faster real-time responses". Marcela Valdez also plans to use AI to "simplify the steps" in daily activities, from reconciliations to financial analysis.
- **Data-Driven Decisions:** Juan Arenas, COO, emphasises that AI will "automatise all activities that are not providing added value and are very manual" to reduce errors and facilitate "more exact data to make decisions that allow us to advance faster". Román de León, Data Scientist, also aims for agile decision-making and savings through "digital processes with reliable data" and "hyper-personalisation". His team is also proposing to "optimise the budget through an algorithm" for agile resource allocation.
- **Impact on Personnel and Resources:** Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, notes that AI has already "reduced both financial and personnel resources" in content creation. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, details plans to use AI to automate complex variable compensation calculations for sales advisors and to accelerate their productivity curve by providing quick access to information.
- **Addressing System Fragmentation:** Marcela Valdez explicitly highlights the "underutilised SAP" system and a "lack of interface" with the core student banner system, which leads to "open controls" and "discontrol". This fragmentation results in inefficient data collection and analysis, underscoring the need for integrated technological solutions. Román de León also points out "too many systems that work in isolation," causing "inconsistencies of data".

### 4. Key Cost Elements under Specific Management

Specific cost categories are under close scrutiny and have tailored management approaches:

- **Personnel (Payroll and Faculty):** This is consistently identified as an "important cost". Management focuses on making it "efficient" without necessarily reducing it, enhancing advisor productivity through AI, and addressing high turnover through technology-supported recruitment processes.
- **Marketing and Customer Acquisition (CAC):** Alberto Sánchez notes the considerable increase in marketing expenses in recent years and monitors the "relationship of how much we are spending in marketing and sales versus what we are bringing in new revenue". Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales, aims to "improve the acquisition cost". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, strives to "optimise the CPL (Cost Per Lead)" which is "getting higher" due to market saturation. Katherine Romero, Senior Marketing Manager, views marketing as "key" to talisis's vision, aiming to capture attention in an "oversaturated market", and uses CAC as an indicator. This indicates a strategic approach to managing advertising spend and lead generation efficiency.
- **Technology and Infrastructure:** While technology is a cost-saving enabler, its own costs are managed. Carlos Villa, Mobile Dev Lead, acknowledges the "cost" associated with migrating to the cloud. The focus is on optimising server usage and leveraging open-source tools to avoid development from scratch, thus managing the expense. There's an ongoing effort to build "data architecture" and use "chatbots" to leverage AI and data for better insights and efficiency.

### 5. Measurement and Indicators of Success

To ensure effective cost management, various indicators and metrics are employed across different areas:

- **Financial Indicators:** These include debt-to-equity ratios, interest-to-EBITDA ratios, and EBITDA-to-debt ratios for specific projects like Promecap. Overall company results, including income growth, profitability, and net profit, are paramount. Marcela Valdez tracks "days of accounts receivable" and "days of accounts payable," along with "inventory days".
- **Productivity and Efficiency Metrics:** Marcela Valdez focuses on "incremental productivity" and monitors "new enrolments," "re-enrolments," "generation size," and "campus utilisation percentage". Humberto Salazar measures sales force productivity and acquisition cost. Lilian Lozano tracks CPL, conversion rates, and engagement for digital campaigns, along with the "percentage of processes within the marketing area that will be standardised" and the "percentage of our activities are supported by artificial intelligence".
- **Technology Adoption and Impact:** Juan Mendez measures "digital maturity index," "adoption of tools," "integration of tools," and "percentage of automated processes". Román de León also measures the "agility in the decision-making" process, the "number of departments that already use artificial intelligence in how many processes," and the "number of reports that currently exist that we can reduce to dynamic dashboards".
- **Quality and Satisfaction:** Juan Arenas monitors student satisfaction. Inge Ploennig's area monitors key academic indicators and aims for historical data to enable longitudinal analysis and deeper understanding of performance.

talisis's cost management is a dynamic and integrated process. It is established through rigorous financial planning, constant monitoring of key cost categories, a strong drive for operational and administrative efficiency (often through simplification), and a rapidly increasing reliance on advanced technology and data analytics to inform decisions and automate tasks. This comprehensive approach aims to ensure financial health while supporting the organisation's strategic objectives and transforming its educational offerings.

Given the emphasis on technology for cost efficiency and the challenges of system integration, I recommend a deep dive into the **Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) and Return on Investment (ROI) of current and planned technology investments**. This analysis should specifically quantify how integrated systems and AI/Cloud solutions are projected to reduce manual labour, improve data accuracy for decision-making, and directly impact key cost elements like personnel and marketing. This would provide concrete evidence for future investment prioritisation and highlight areas where technology adoption could yield the greatest financial benefits.

o   ¿Qué estrategias y/o proyectos se tienen establecidos para los principales elementos del costo?

talisis has established a comprehensive and dynamic set of strategies and projects to manage and optimise its principal cost elements, reflecting a shift from mere cost reduction to efficient resource allocation, strategic investment, and value creation. This approach is deeply integrated with the organisation's overall strategic planning and increasingly leverages technology.

The main cost elements under specific management include:

1. **General Costs and Financial Management**
2. **Personnel and Faculty Costs**
3. **Marketing and Customer Acquisition Costs**
4. **Technology and Infrastructure Costs**
5. **Strategic Investments and Expansion (CAPEX/OPEX)**

Here are the established strategies and projects for each:

### 1. General Costs and Financial Management

**Overall Strategy:** talisis's core financial strategy, led by the Director of Planning, Alberto Sánchez, focuses on maintaining a robust financial structure, ensuring sufficient economic resources, a healthy profit and loss (P&L) statement, a strong balance sheet, and adequate cash flow. The objective is to manage costs and expenses as "efficiently as possible" rather than simply reducing them, by strategically distributing resources "in what cost item, in what expense item". Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, adds that her mission includes "leading budgetary planning" and "analysis of key indicators to improve efficiency and profitability". Her team acts as an "enabler" from the back office, ensuring administrative and financial processes support multi-channel and multi-product growth.

**Key Projects & Initiatives:**

- **Budgetary Control and Forecasting:** The planning department is deeply involved in "control presupuestal" and "forecast" activities on a daily basis with operations, human resources, and marketing and commercial teams. They aim to make budgeting and business cases "more automated, more modern, less artisanal, less manual" through "digital tools".
- **Responsible Resource Utilisation:** The finance team provides "coaching or internal consulting" to other departments on business cases, productivity analysis, and cost-benefit assessments, to ensure the responsible use of economic resources across the organisation.
- **Cash Flow and Portfolio Management:** A critical short-term priority is to "ensure that the minimum cash flow is covered" and manage the "recovery of the outstanding portfolio" to maintain immediate financial health. Financial education and responsible payment practices are considered essential.
- **Incremental Productivity:** A key project is "incremental productivity," aiming to "serve more students with economies of scale". This involves optimising processes to cater to more students while achieving better cost efficiency.
- **Streamlining Administrative Processes:** While not explicitly detailed as a project, the overall strategy includes "simplification of administrative structures" such as reducing the number of legal entities to "reduce the burden" and avoid unnecessary inter-company transactions. This also extends to standardising and automating processes for "highs, lows and changes" for students, employees, and suppliers, which currently takes significant time and creates "descontrol".
- **Integrated Business Management:** The overarching "Business Management" project aims to have "2,400 mentes trabajando como una", indicating a unified and efficient management approach across the entire organisation, inherently driving cost optimisation. This is a "proyecto de mediano y largo plazo donde el orden, la disciplina y la visión tienen que compaginar con la cultura y la estrategia".

### 2. Personnel and Faculty Costs

**Overall Strategy:** Personnel costs, including payroll and faculty expenses, are identified as "un costo importante". The strategy is to "efficientar esa nómina," which "no quiere decir reducirla, no quiere decir aumentarla, necesariamente, sino es cómo es el gasto en nómina trabaja de la manera más eficiente con apoyo de tecnología". The academic department aims to "reducir la dispersión y atomización de grupos para que el costo docente naturalmente sea eficiente". There is also a focus on attracting, developing, and retaining key talent, particularly in high-turnover positions like sales advisors.

**Key Projects & Initiatives:**

- **Payroll Efficiency through Technology:** The main challenge is to make payroll efficient with the support of technology.
- **Automating Variable Compensation:** A specific initiative is to automate the "compensación variable de los de los promotores y asesores" which has been "muy complejo" due to the numerous variables involved. Automation would provide "muchísimo mayor visibilidad" to advisors and management.
- **Reducing Productivity Curve for Sales Advisors:** Utilise AI tools to help sales advisors "consultar las dudas que vaya teniendo en el día a día para que su desarrollo sea más rápido, y puedan ser y puedan tener esa productividad óptima en menos tiempo." The current optimal productivity curve is around 7 months, and the goal is to reduce it significantly.
- **Optimising Talent Acquisition:** Address high turnover by automating "contratación, las entrevistas, las referencias, la búsqueda de de del mejor talento" to reduce the current 40-50 day hiring process. The goal is to "traer el mejor talento" and ensure a "mejor fit para esa posición," focusing on rigour in internal staffing processes.
- **Strengthening Teaching Career (Carrera Docente):** A priority project is to "fortalecer la carrera docente", which aims to provide certainty and inspiration to faculty by supporting them with training to improve their practices.
- **Professional Development:** The formation of teams will focus on developing "habilidades blandas" (soft skills) like communication and empathy, alongside "habilidades tecnológicas" to enhance the student experience. For the planning team, the focus is on mastering finance, project evaluation, M&A, strategic planning, and communication, always "apoyándose en tecnología para optimizar tiempo y recursos". This includes continuous learning in new methodologies and technological advancements.
- **"Hiperformance Culture" Project:** This major initiative, led by Human Capital, aims to "optimizar el recurso humano en talisis" to "asegurar la rentabilidad del capital humano." It involves establishing high standards, attracting the best fit talent, clarity in roles, and continuous development. This culture aims to be the "principal driver" covering "relaciones laborales, del desarrollo de la estrategia, tema de comprensión y beneficios, el estilo estilo de mando de la gente que que necesitamos tener, los procesos de atracción y reclutamiento y evaluación de gente, tener la estructura organizacional óptima para operar de forma productiva los procesos de análisis, la cultura de chain management, y de mejora continua".

### 3. Marketing and Customer Acquisition Costs

**Overall Strategy:** Marketing expenses have increased "de manera considerable" in recent years, not just in education but across all sectors. The challenge is to manage these costs "de manera eficiente" while competing on the same platforms. The strategy involves optimising marketing and sales spend against new revenue generated, aiming to "mejorar el costo de adquisición" and "optimise the CPL (Cost Per Lead)". This requires evolving from traditional marketing to an approach that prioritises emotional connection, clear differentiation, and long-term relationships with students.

**Key Projects & Initiatives:**

- **Omnichannel Strategy:** A priority project is to implement an "estrategia omnicanal, integral" across all digital and physical touchpoints to ensure "coherencia de comunicación de cada una de nuestras marcas". This involves integrating "medios digitales, experiencias presenciales, contenidos y aliados estratégicos con visión de largo plazo".
- **Brand Building and Strengthening:** Another key project is the "construcción, y fortalecimiento de marca, por cada una de nuestras unidades de de negocio," consolidating "narrativas diferenciadas coherentes" aligned with the 2035 vision. The goal is to create brands that resonate emotionally and reflect talisis's capacity to transform lives.
- **Automation and Personalisation with AI:** Leveraging AI for "segmentación hiper personalizada" to tailor messages, channels, and experiences for each buyer persona in real-time. This allows for "automatización creativa" to generate content at scale without sacrificing quality, enabling A/B testing and campaigns that evolve based on performance. The aim is for the marketing team to focus on strategy rather than operational execution. AI is also used for "personalización en tiempo real".
- **Predictive Analytics:** Implement "análisis predictivo y decisiones basadas en en datos" to anticipate enrolments, dropouts, or changes in trends, allowing for proactive interventions. This aims for "dashboards más inteligentes con acciones sugeridas" to take "decisiones en tiempo real y no reactivos".
- **Market Intelligence:** Conduct "un ejercicio de inteligencia de mercados para para llegar a las organizaciones que todavía no llegamos con precisamente ese portafolio ordenado para las empresas". This involves understanding "quién necesita educación, cómo la está buscando, qué lo motiva, cómo prefiere aprender".
- **Digital Ambassadors Program:** Develop a "programa de embajadores digitales, que nos permita crear una red que voceros orgánicos en nuestros diferentes canales de digitales".
- **Digital Playbook:** Create a "playbook digital" to "alinear procesos, lineamientos y tener una estrategia mucho más práctica de cómo trabaja el equipo".

### 4. Technology and Infrastructure Costs

**Overall Strategy:** Technology is viewed as a critical enabler for efficiency and a "músculo operativo" for talisis. The goal is to move beyond manual processes and Excel-based operations towards automated, modern, and real-time digital tools. AI and cloud technology are central to this transformation, aiming to "potenciar" human capabilities rather than replace them, fostering "humanos súper humanos". This requires a significant investment and a strategy to manage associated costs while gaining efficiency.

**Key Projects & Initiatives:**

- **AI-Driven Automation of Core Processes:** Implement AI for "forecast y presupuesto" to achieve greater precision. AI will also aid in "evaluación de proyectos y evaluación de empresas" and "fusiones de adquisiciones" by helping to "targetear" potential acquisitions. AI is expected to "simplificar los pasos" in daily activities, from reconciliations to financial analysis.
- **Cloud Migration and Asynchronous Collaboration:** Migrating to the cloud is underway, which brings "costo" but enables "trabajar de manera asíncrona" and boosts efficiency. The security of cloud services is also a recognised concern that needs protection.
- **Data Architecture and Analytics:** A priority project is to "construir esta arquitectura de datos" to collect comprehensive information on students, faculty, and administrative staff. This aims to provide a "visibilidad organizacional completa, una vista 360 de nuestros clientes" to understand their needs and offer personalised support. This includes creating "dashboards de indicadores clave" and moving from "reportes que hoy en día existen que podamos reducirlos a unos tableros dinámicos con mayor frecuencia de actualización".
- **Integrated Systems:** A major challenge is the "fragmentación" and "lack of interface" between existing systems like SAP and the core student banner system, leading to "open controls" and "discontrol". A key initiative is to "consolidar, este, todos los ecosistemas en plataformas interconectadas", envisioned as "Arquitectura Tecnológica IA: La mente TALISIS conectando todo". This aims to overcome "inconsistencies de datos" due to "demasiados sistemas que trabajan en aislamiento".
- **Chatbots and AI Assistants:** Projects include "Chatbots Educativos" and an "Asistente Virtual Administrativo (proyecto Mazinger Z)," which has already "reduced both financial and personnel resources" in content creation. There are also plans for "tutorías y mentorías personalizadas apoyadas en IA" for students and collaborators.
- **Standardisation of Processes:** Acknowledging that currently "trabajamos con tareas y estas tareas están asignadas a personas," there is a need to move towards "flujos definidos y automatizados" to achieve "muchísima velocidad" in service resolution. This includes efforts to standardise and document processes.
- **Budget Optimisation through Algorithms:** A specific project is proposed to "optimice el presupuesto disponible basado en las necesidades reales... por medio de un algoritmo," to allocate resources more agilely and align with organisational objectives.

### 5. Strategic Investments and Expansion (CAPEX/OPEX)

**Overall Strategy:** Investment decisions are strategically planned to align with market trends and support long-term objectives. This involves efficient administration of "deuda y capital" and constant communication with all areas to evaluate new projects. The goal is to find financially viable expansion models that are replicable.

**Key Projects & Initiatives:**

- **Promecap Exit Strategy:** A long-term priority is to "encontrar la mejor salida para Promecap" by generating "suficiente caja y el generar suficiente EBITDA" to manage debt and ensure a healthy balance sheet. This indicates a strategic financial management of a specific asset.
- **Multibrand Presence Optimisation:** The project focuses on "cómo utilizamos de manera más eficiente toda la presencia que tenemos tanto en en UR, como en Harmon Hall, como en Unit," aiming for a "tema multimarca o tema consolidado". This implies optimising the combined operations for greater efficiency and scale. It also involves "escalabilidad de costos para tener escalabilidad de precios" to make products more economical and reach a wider audience.
- **U-ERRE Regional Expansion:** Explore "la expansión de URL" to become a "fortaleza regional" outside of Monterrey. The primary challenge for this expansion is economic, requiring "dinero".
- **Mergers and Acquisitions (M&A):** A long-term project involves "empezar a ver este, a quién podemos comprar, con quién nos podemos fusionar". This also presents an "economic" challenge related to "levantar capital o... levantar deuda". IA is envisioned to play a key role in "targetear" potential companies for M&A, providing precision in identifying and evaluating opportunities.
- **New Learning Centres/Portfolio Expansion:** Priorities include "la apertura de nuevos centros de aprendizaje" and "la apertura de nuevo portafolio que de acuerdo a las necesidades del mercado". This also extends to "expandir con nuevos modelos," such as "hubs, Talysis, un estudio, un piloto, o modelos de de franquicias, o o de operaciones propias en ciudades estratégicas" that require "menos inversión que un campus completo". These models aim to be "más viables financieramente" and foster interaction with students in strategic cities, while also driving sales and brand positioning.

talisis's approach to cost management is strategic, integrated, and forward-looking. It combines meticulous financial planning and control with a strong emphasis on leveraging technology (especially AI and cloud) to automate processes, gain real-time insights, and empower human talent. The organisation is actively undertaking various projects to optimise core operational costs, enhance marketing efficiency, and enable sustainable growth through strategic investments and innovative educational models.

To refine these strategies and projects, I recommend conducting a **cost-benefit analysis of specific technology investments** across different departments. This analysis should quantify the expected financial returns (e.g., labour cost savings, increased productivity, improved retention, higher conversion rates) against the investment in new systems, AI tools, and training programs. This would help prioritise technology initiatives that offer the highest tangible benefits and ensure that technology spend is directly correlated with a positive impact on the organisation's "salud financiera".

o   ¿Está claro para la organización cómo contribuye cada una de las áreas y puestos al resultado de negocio?

Tali here, while individual leaders within talisis generally demonstrate a clear understanding of how their specific areas and positions contribute to business results, there is a recurring theme across various interviews indicating that the _inter-departmental clarity, alignment, and integrated understanding_ of contributions are areas targeted for significant improvement.

**Areas Demonstrating Clarity of Contribution:**

Many leaders articulate their area's direct impact and role:

- **Alberto Sánchez (Director de Planeación):** Views his area as ensuring financial structure, economic resources, and a healthy balance sheet, aligning strategic and financial planning with market trends. He primarily interacts with internal clients (academy for costs, operations for budget control, HR for payroll, marketing for income forecasts). His team also aligns with the CEO on strategic direction, new projects, and M&A.
- **Alejandro Madrazo (Director Académico):** Clearly defines his area as the "epicenter of innovation" for educational design, deployment, and evaluation, contributing to talisis's vision of accessible, quality education and rethinking institutional organization. He emphasizes that other areas must understand the importance of academic work.
- **Álvaro García (Innovation and Product Director):** States his corporate sales team aims to be a main partner for organizations, transforming talent through academic programs and anticipating capacitación needs. He sees his area attracting alliances and generating impact, requiring support from operational, academic, and administrative areas.
- **Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director):** Identifies her area's impact as securing the best talent to fulfill talisis's value promise and transform lives. Her team supports leaders in evaluating and developing their teams. She acts as a "glue" between areas, promoting effective communication to resolve challenges.
- **Carlos Granados (CIO):** Aims to create an "intelligent, adaptive, and inclusive educational ecosystem" through AI Agents, improving student experience and operational efficiency, and empowering staff. These agents will facilitate efficient communication and data-driven decisions.
- **Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales):** Directly links his area's contribution to student acquisition and retention, which is crucial for achieving talisis's 2035 growth and accessibility vision. He positions the commercial area as the "growth engine" for the organization.
- **Inge Ploennig (Director de Calidad y Acreditación Académica):** Her area ensures content and processes meet high standards and continuous improvement, seeing accreditation as a motor for real enhancement across the institution, aligned with the institutional mission.
- **Joel Enriquez (CSO):** Sees his role as building a "strategic legacy" and being a "founder of organizational culture," a "motor cultural" by giving relevance and echo to the group's actions.
- **Juan Arenas (COO):** Describes his operations area as "integrative of all ideas, projects, initiatives," acting as "enablers of the operation" by directly interacting with students. He also stresses the importance of accountability for service quality.
- **Juan Mendez (Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación):** Views his department as the "architects of systemic change," focused on designing, activating, and sustaining transformation until it becomes culture, encompassing processes, capabilities, technology, and culture. He aims for "everyone to know why they are doing what they are doing".
- **Juliana Effting (Directora de Educación Online):** Her area directly operates online products, ensuring effective student and teacher follow-up, and agile, reliable service through standardized processes and systems. She believes her team plays a "very relevant role" in advocating for online student needs.
- **Katherine Romero (Senior Marketing Manager):** Her marketing team translates talisis's vision into "positioning and action," building brand identity, and accelerating growth by connecting with real people through omnichannel strategies. She states that every action in marketing has a "direct impact on the student".
- **Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director):** Her area collects digital data, serves as a "digital ear" for new generations, drives omnichannel activations, and scales customer acquisition, playing a crucial role in business growth and educational impact.
- **Luis Ruiz (Gerente de desarrollo de software):** His area constructs integrations between talisis's systems, including AI agents, which is fundamental for the organization's technological vision.
- **Marcela Valdez (Directora de Administración y Finanzas):** Her area contributes by providing financial information and analysis, ensuring responsible resource use, and coaching other areas on productivity and cost-benefit. She sees her area as "enablers" for growth and multi-product strategies through administrative processes.
- **Marcos Samaniego (Director de Operaciones Académicas):** His area implements, monitors, and analyzes academic models, translating company-wide efforts into effective execution at campuses. He also reports on progress towards institutional objectives.
- **Mariel Serrano (Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence):** Her area reinforces service excellence, builds reputation, communicates continuous improvement, and promotes the "talisis Way" culture, aiming for organizational synchronicity and a shared vision to consolidate leadership.
- **Paul Moch (Vice President for Teaching & Learning):** His area designs educational processes, models, and policies, aiming to consolidate a clear educational model and foster competence development in students. He considers his role "central" for innovation.
- **Paulina Adalid (Rector Institucional in UNID):** Her role is to serve as a "bridge of union" between talisis and its learning institutions, communicating the vision and representing talisis to authorities and stakeholders, while valuing the diversity of communities.
- **Román de León (Data Scientist):** His area builds data-driven technological solutions, using AI to personalize learning and assist both internal collaborators and students. He sees his team as key to detecting patterns and supporting decision-making.

**Areas Where Clarity and Alignment Are Sought or Challenged:**

Despite individual clarity, a common thread among leaders is the ongoing effort to enhance inter-area clarity and collaboration:

- **Lack of Integrated Processes and Communication:**
    - **Alejandro Madrazo** points out inefficiencies due to a lack of clear and documented processes, leading to constant emergency interruptions. He also states that all areas need to _understand_ the importance of academic work and time.
    - **Domingo Farias** admits "poor organizational design," "lack of structure," and "lack of alignment" hinder Human Capital's impact on teacher profiles. He calls for "clear communication and documented, respect for processes" as needed support.
    - **Fernando de Río** highlights that "platforms do not converse well," data is "dispersed or unreliable," and automation is hard to scale. He mentions that "here in talisis they don't like to share direction, each one wants their own way," necessitating "strategic collaboration" and "clear governance".
    - **Juan Mendez** emphasizes the challenge of truly instilling the "talisis ADN" into every individual's daily actions. He notes "lack of clarity on the vision and strategy from the high direction" and a need for "alignment" and "communication" from other areas.
    - **Juliana Effting** states that talisis "still has much to do in more strategic terms" regarding its digital identity from high leadership, and that "processes, rules...dominate" over listening to customer needs. She needs "clear communication to all of talisis" from leaders about the digital transformation.
    - **Luis Ruiz** expresses feeling "a little isolated in this collaboration" and desires "more direct interactions and with that unified focus and vision". He also needs "time and clear definitions regarding the processes" to deliver quality work.
    - **Marcela Valdez** notes a "lack of integration between systems" leading to "open controls and risks of descontrol," and the absence of a well-designed master data and periodic closures causes discrepancies with accounting.
    - **Marcos Samaniego** identifies the need for a "centralized document repository of all processes" due to the company's size, to ensure consistent communication and avoid duplications.
    - **Mariel Serrano** highlights the obstacle of "collaborators not understanding" and thus not committing to the transversal talisis Bit project, and the "arduous work" of achieving "100% effective alignment among all areas". She needs "openness and coordination between areas to build aligned messages" and avoid "silos that fragment the institutional narrative".
    - **Paul Moch** hints at a need for greater understanding of education's central role over business and flexibility in processes for innovation.
    - **Román de León** frequently mentions that departments "don't validate with us the solution they want to achieve," and often seek his team's input too late in the process, leading to delays and misalignments. He identifies "lack of clear definition of some of the metrics" and "too many systems that work in an isolated manner" as causes for data inconsistencies. He also needs "much communication between departments" to achieve a "clear vision" for the organization's future.

**Inference from the Information:**

It is evident that talisis is actively working towards greater clarity and alignment regarding each area's contribution to business results. The recurring emphasis on "talisis Way" culture, shared objectives (OKRs/KPIs), and strategic communication (connections, town halls, conventions) points to a top-down effort to foster this understanding. However, the operational reality still presents challenges with fragmented systems, undocumented processes, and a need for deeper, earlier inter-departmental collaboration and a more robust shared understanding of long-term strategic direction. The desire for "co-creation" rather than a client-supplier relationship between internal departments is a key indicator of where current clarity falls short and what is being strived for.

To address the identified gaps in inter-departmental clarity and collaboration, Tali recommends conducting a detailed **Process Mapping and Stakeholder Alignment Workshop** for key cross-functional initiatives. This would involve identifying critical value streams, mapping existing processes end-to-end, identifying points of friction, communication gaps, and data inconsistencies, and collaboratively designing improved workflows with clearly defined roles, responsibilities, and expected contributions for each area. This framework can help transform the desired "orchestrated" collaboration into a tangible operational reality by simplifying complex interdependencies into a more easily understandable system.


o   ¿Están convencidos de que sus actividades y esfuerzos están alineados a contribuir con el resultado de negocio? Y ¿Hasta qué nivel de la organización se permea esa conciencia de afectación al resultado financiero con sus actividades propias?

Based on the detailed insights from the interviews, it is evident that leaders across various departments at talisis exhibit a strong conviction regarding how their specific activities and efforts contribute to overall business results. However, the permeation of this understanding, particularly in terms of its direct impact on _inter-departmental financial efficiency and integrated operational alignment_, presents a more nuanced picture with discernible opportunities for enhancement.

**Conviction of Alignment with Business Results**

A consistent theme across the interviews is the clear articulation by individual leaders of their area's strategic importance and its direct or indirect link to talisis's business outcomes. This conviction is deeply embedded at the leadership level:

- **Strategic & Financial Planning:** Alberto Sánchez (Director de Planeación) explicitly links his area's role to ensuring a "healthy balance sheet," "economic resources," and aligning strategic and financial planning with market trends to achieve the company's objectives over the next decade. He constantly interacts with internal departments (academia for costs, operations for budget control, HR for payroll, marketing for income forecasts) to ensure financial structure and efficient resource allocation.
- **Academic Leadership:** Alejandro Madrazo (Director Académico) positions his area as the "epicentre of innovation" for educational design and deployment, directly contributing to talisis's vision of accessible, quality education. He understands that this academic work is fundamental for the organisation's core value proposition and, implicitly, its market standing.
- **Commercial & Marketing:** Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) directly states that his area is the "growth engine of the organization," crucial for student acquisition and retention, which is vital for achieving talisis's 2035 growth vision. Fernando de Río (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) envisions his area as the "motor that converts strategy into real, sustainable, and people-centered growth," driving market intelligence, brand evolution, and efficient acquisition funnels. Katherine Romero (Senior Marketing Manager) similarly highlights marketing's role in "translating the vision into positioning and action," building brand identity, and accelerating growth by connecting with real people, asserting that every marketing action has a "direct impact on the student". Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director) also directly links her team's efforts to "scaling the business" through customer acquisition strategies.
- **Operations:** Juan Arenas (COO) defines his area as the "integrative of all ideas, projects, initiatives," serving as "enablers of the operation" that directly interact with students to deliver the best service. He emphasizes "accountability" for service quality as fundamental. Marcos Samaniego (Director de Operaciones Académicas) sees his area as the implementer of academic design, ensuring that what is planned actually "succeeds in the campuses," and monitoring progress towards institutional objectives.
- **Human Capital:** Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) states her area's impact is in "securing the best talent" to fulfill the value promise and transform lives, directly supporting leaders to develop their teams. Domingo Farias (Human Capital) refers to his area as the "engine of attitude and energy", attracting talent for a high-performance culture and explicitly linking HR efforts to "company results," "revenue growth," and "profitability".
- **Technology & Data:** Carlos Granados (CIO) aims to create an "intelligent, adaptive, and inclusive educational ecosystem" that improves "operational efficiency". Luis Ruiz (Gerente de desarrollo de software) sees his work on system integrations and AI agents as fundamental for making work more efficient for all users. Román de León (Data Scientist) focuses on building data-driven solutions and applying AI for personalised learning and strategic decision-making, which he sees as crucial for talisis to become a national and international educational leader.
- **Quality & Transformation:** Inge Ploennig (Director de Calidad y Acreditación Académica) frames accreditation as a "motor for real enhancement" across the institution, aligning with the mission. Juan Mendez (Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación) views his department as "architects of systemic change" focusing on design, activation, and sustaining transformation across processes, capabilities, technology, and culture, aiming for "everyone to know why they are doing what they are doing".
- **Leadership & Culture:** Joel Enriquez (CSO) focuses on building a "strategic legacy" and being a "founder of organizational culture," giving "relevance and echo to what we do as a group". Mariel Serrano (Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence) works to reinforce service excellence, build reputation, and promote the "talisis Way" culture, emphasising "organisational synchronicity" and a "shared vision" to consolidate leadership.

This strong conviction among leaders is further supported by the "Reporte_Nicho.pdf," which outlines "Iniciativas estratégicas interconectadas que materializan la visión mediante cultura de alto desempeño, tecnología habilitadora y modelos educativos innovadores". It specifically mentions "Proyectos de alineación cultural," "arquitectura tecnológica IA," "perfilamiento docente," "vinculación productiva," "omnicanalidad," and "business management integrado," all with "métricas claras" like "empleabilidad," "NPS," "retención," and "impacto comunitario medible".
