This top-down strategic framing reinforces the perceived alignment.

**Permeation of Financial Awareness**

While the conviction of _their own_ contribution is clear, the _pervasive and integrated awareness_ of how daily activities affect the broader financial results, especially across inter-departmental boundaries, shows areas for improvement. This awareness is strongest at senior and executive levels, but challenges emerge as one descends into the operational nuances and cross-functional dependencies.

**1. Strong Financial Awareness at Senior Levels:** Leaders in finance, planning, and growth roles consistently articulate their direct impact on financial outcomes and the need for fiscal responsibility:

- Marcela Valdez (Directora de Administración y Finanzas) details her mission to "ensure the accuracy of accounting and financial operations for decision-making, lead budget planning, analyze key indicators to improve efficiency and profitability, comply with tax regulations and proactively manage risks". She highlights her area's role in making resources available responsibly and "coaching or internal consulting" on productivity and cost-benefit. She identifies key indicators such as "days of accounts receivable," "EBITDA," and "revenue growth".
- Alberto Sánchez (Director de Planeación) constantly discusses "administering debt efficiently," "raising capital," and "assigning resources". He ensures that "there is budget for all costs and expenses" and emphasizes efficient budget management with those who "exercise" or "administer" it.
- Fernando de Río (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) references "desaceleración económica y la presión por la rentabilidad" and the student's need to value "costo beneficio". He also works with finance to determine "dónde invertir con inteligencia".
- Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) aims to "mejorar el costo de adquisición y el aumento de la productividad de la fuerza de ventas", indicating direct financial performance metrics.

**2. Challenges in Inter-Departmental Permeation and Operational Integration:**

Despite the high-level financial awareness, several recurring obstacles hinder its full permeation and seamless execution across the entire organisation:

- **Fragmented Systems and Data Inconsistency:** A significant barrier to consolidated financial awareness is the lack of integrated systems and reliable data. Marcela Valdez explicitly mentions "lack of integration between systems" like SAP and Core Banner, leading to "open controls and risks of descontrol" and data discrepancies. Román de León (Data Scientist) echoes this, noting "too many systems that work in an isolated manner" causing "inconsistencies of data between those platforms". Katherine Romero (Senior Marketing Manager) also observes that "some platforms today do not allow automation or measurement of our projects or indicators fluently". This fragmented data environment makes it challenging to have a real-time, unified view of financial performance across all operations.
- **Lack of Standardised Processes and Documentation:** Several leaders highlight inefficiencies due to undefined or undocumented processes. Alejandro Madrazo (Director Académico) points to the absence of "sufficiently clear and documented processes" as a cause of constant emergency interruptions, hindering efficient planning. Marcos Samaniego (Director de Operaciones Académicas) advocates for a "centralized document repository of all processes" because the company is "too large and there are many processes happening" without a unified source of truth, leading to potential duplication and miscommunication. Luis Ruiz (Gerente de desarrollo de software) also explicitly states the need for "clear definitions regarding the processes" to avoid delays and ensure quality work. This lack of standardisation directly impacts cost efficiency and shared understanding of financial impact.
- **Communication Gaps and Siloed Operations:** A pervasive issue is the difficulty in fostering true cross-functional collaboration. Fernando de Río (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) states bluntly that "here in talisis they don't like to share direction, each one wants their own way", which can lead to misaligned priorities and inefficient resource allocation. Román de León (Data Scientist) describes a "client-provider relationship" between departments, where he is often sought too late, hindering co-creation of optimal solutions. Mariel Serrano (Head of Corporate Reputation) acknowledges that "collaborators do not understand" the "talisis Bit" project, leading to a lack of commitment, and the "arduous work" of achieving "100% effective alignment among all areas". She needs "openness and coordination between areas to build aligned messages" and avoid "silos that fragment the institutional narrative". Juliana Effting (Directora de Educación Online) needs "clear communication to all of talisis" from leaders about the digital transformation to foster aligned contributions. These issues suggest that while leaders might understand their own financial contribution, the collective financial impact of interdependent activities is not always transparent or optimally coordinated across the full breadth of the organisation.
- **Cultural Resistance to Change and Innovation:** Paulina Adalid (Rector Institucional in UNID) notes "not wanting to accept changes" and a tendency for staff to work in a "more conservative" manner, hindering innovation, which impacts the adoption of new, potentially more efficient or financially viable processes. Juan Mendez (Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación) also highlights "resistancia cultural" and a "lack of digital capabilities" as challenges to making processes more "intelligent" and "faster".
- **Resource and Time Constraints:** Paul Moch (Vice President for Teaching & Learning) explicitly mentions "time" and "lack of hands" as major obstacles to focusing on strategic design and innovation, implying that day-to-day operational demands consume resources that could otherwise be dedicated to more financially impactful long-term projects. Román de León (Data Scientist) similarly describes the "size of the team" and "current workload" as primary obstacles, along with the "lack of sufficiently trained people in technology", impeding agile project advancement. Domingo Farias (Human Capital) seeks "greater visibility of the productivity of other positions" beyond sales advisors, implying a gap in understanding broad operational efficiency.

**Conclusion:**

In essence, talisis's senior and mid-level leadership are highly convinced of their individual areas' contributions to business results, often articulating these in terms of growth, profitability, efficiency, and student success. However, the comprehensive permeation of this financial awareness into _seamless, integrated, and consistently executed inter-departmental operations_ remains an ongoing strategic imperative. The primary challenges lie in overcoming fragmented technological systems, standardising diverse operational processes, fostering genuine cross-functional communication, addressing cultural resistance to change, and ensuring adequate allocation of human resources to strategic, rather than purely reactive, activities. The "talisis Way" culture and initiatives like "talisis Bit" represent a clear top-down effort to foster this unified consciousness and alignment, but their full operational manifestation is still evolving.

To concretely address the identified gaps in inter-departmental financial awareness and operational alignment, Tali suggests initiating a **"Value Stream Analysis & Cross-Functional Accountability Design"** program. This would involve selecting 2-3 critical, end-to-end organisational processes (e.g., student acquisition to retention, or new product development to market launch) that cut across multiple departments and applying value stream mapping. For each mapped process, clearly delineate where value is created, where waste/inefficiencies occur, and, crucially, identify the precise financial impact (costs, revenue generation, risk) at each step. Following this, convene cross-functional teams to collectively _design accountability matrices_ for these specific value streams, ensuring shared ownership of financial outcomes, and integrating clear, consistent data dashboards accessible to all involved parties. This approach moves beyond general awareness to embed specific financial responsibility within collective operational flows, fostering a culture of co-ownership for measurable business results.
### VII. Procesos y Sistema de Gestión

o   ¿Las Metodologías, Procesos y Sistemas se considera una Inversión o un Gasto?

Based on the comprehensive insights gleaned from the provided interviews, Methodologies, Processes, and Systems are consistently perceived by talisis's senior leadership team as a crucial **investment**, rather than merely an operational expense. This perspective is an inference drawn from the recurring strategic justifications, long-term visions, and expected returns articulated across various departments.

Here is a detailed elaboration of why these elements are considered an investment:

### 1. Strategic Enablers for Long-Term Vision

talisis's leadership views methodologies, processes, and systems as fundamental to achieving its ambitious strategic vision for 2035 [Alberto Sánchez 2, 10, 12, 27; Álvaro García 56, 58, 74, 77; Carlos Granados 98; Fernando de Río 189, 190, 191; Humberto 225, 231; Inge Ploennig 239, 244, 258, 261, 262; Joel Enriquez 287, 289; Juan Arenas 296, 300, 303; Juan Mendez 303, 304, 305, 310, 311, 313, 314; Juliana Effting 335, 336, 339, 346, 349; Katherine 365, 367, 368; Lilian Lozano 406, 411, 415, 416, 420; Luis 430, 433, 436; Marcela Valdez 445, 448, 449, 455, 456, 460, 461, 463; Marcos Samaniego 480, 485, 488, 489, 490, 491, 495, 499; Mariel 502, 505, 506, 508, 514; Paul Moch 528, 529, 531, 533, 535, 538; Paulina 544, 550, 552; Román de León 567, 576, 577, 583, 585, 587, 593]. The aim is not merely to cover immediate operational needs but to build lasting capabilities that will redefine education access, personalise learning experiences, and establish talisis as a leading educational ecosystem. For instance, Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, envisions designing structures that "survive beyond fads or current circumstances" and "grow with firm values and a very clear shared purpose". Similarly, Paulina, from UNID, highlights forming students with "knowledge and skills necessary to professionally develop in this continuously changing world", aided by technological tools.

### 2. Driving Efficiency and Productivity

A consistent justification for these investments is the anticipated significant gains in efficiency, reduction of manual tasks, and increased productivity across the organisation [Alberto Sánchez 10, 11; Álvaro García 58, 72, 78; Carlos Granados 98; Carlos Villa 109, 125; Domingo Farias 156, 157, 162; Fernando de Río 191, 204, 206; Humberto 232; Inge Ploennig 259, 261, 271; Juan Arenas 303, 304; Juan Mendez 314, 325; Juliana Effting 346, 348, 349; Katherine 376, 377, 378; Lilian Lozano 416, 417; Luis 434; Marcela Valdez 446, 455, 456, 460, 461, 463; Marcos Samaniego 488, 491; Mariel 506; Paulina 552; Román de León 585, 596]. Leaders envision automating repetitive activities, streamlining workflows, and leveraging technology to free up human talent for higher-value, more strategic tasks. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, explicitly links technology to "simplifying the steps we follow to do our daily activity" and "analysis of information and understanding the variables that impact profitability". Román de León, Data Scientist, also points out that digital processes and reliable data enable continuous project creation, contributing to "agility in decision-making" and "savings in day-to-day processes".

### 3. Risk Mitigation and Enhanced Control

Investing in well-defined processes, robust controls, and integrated systems is seen as critical for mitigating financial risks, preventing operational discrepancies, ensuring data accuracy, and safeguarding the institution's reputation [Alberto Sánchez 2; Marcela Valdez 448, 465, 466, 467, 469; Mariel 512, 513; Román de León 578]. Marcela Valdez highlights the "lack of interface" and "lack of design in the implementation" between systems (like Banner and SAP) leading to "open controls" and "discontrol", which are risks that need to be closed through investment in proper systems. These are protective investments that aim to avert larger, potentially more damaging, future costs.

### 4. Enabling Scalability and Growth

The ability to expand geographically, offer new products, and reach more students (both B2C and B2B) is consistently linked to having scalable processes and integrated technological platforms [Álvaro García 58; Fernando de Río 190, 215; Humberto 233, 234; Juliana Effting 339, 352; Katherine 368, 372; Lilian Lozano 406; Marcela Valdez 470, 471]. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, stresses the need for "a product that truly wins in the market" through "new models" of expansion like franchises or hubs. Similarly, Humberto, from the commercial area, identifies the "opening of new learning centers" and "new portfolios" as long-term impacts facilitated by automation of the commercial process. This directly ties these areas to core business growth strategies.

### 5. Investment in Human Capital and Culture

Leaders emphasise the need to invest in continuous training, upskilling, and fostering a culture of innovation and collaboration, which goes hand-in-hand with implementing new technologies and methodologies [Alberto Sánchez 12, 13, 14, 15; Carlos Granados 100; Domingo Farias 33, 152, 158, 160, 161; Fernando de Río 201, 202, 206; Lilian Lozano 412, 413, 414, 418, 419; Juan Mendez 310, 311, 314, 318, 319; Juliana Effting 340, 345, 352; Katherine 378, 379, 385; Luis 434, 435; Marcela Valdez 448, 455, 460; Marcos Samaniego 485, 490; Mariel 503, 505; Paul Moch 534; Paulina 551, 553; Román de León 579, 587, 588]. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, highlights the importance of fostering a "culture of development in all areas" and Marcela Valdez mentions fostering the "professional development of the team" as part of her mission. This holistic view acknowledges that the "hardware" (systems) requires parallel investment in the "software" (people and culture) for optimal performance.

### 6. Explicit Financial Justifications and Metrics

Some interviewees directly mention financial justifications and metrics characteristic of investments. Carlos Granados, for example, discusses "Costos-beneficios" (cost-benefits), "TCO (Total Cost of Ownership)," and "ROI esperado" (expected ROI) for technology. Marcela Valdez, from finance, focuses on maximising "resources that are scarce" and achieving "profitability", including "rentabilidad por programa, por ubicación" which directly relates to the return on investment in academic offerings. Performance indicators often include improved conversion rates, reduced acquisition costs, retention rates, and productivity, all measures of return on initial outlay [Fernando de Río 217; Katherine 398; Lilian Lozano 427; Luis 439, 441; Marcos Samaniego 497; Juliana Effting 358; Román de León 596, 597].

### 7. Cost of Inaction (Lack of Investment)

Several leaders implicitly underscore the investment nature by lamenting the high costs, inefficiencies, and missed opportunities resulting from a lack of proper systems, integrated technology, or standardised processes [Álvaro García 78; Carlos Villa 131; Domingo Farias 33, 162; Fernando de Río 216, 392, 393, 425; Inge Ploennig 258, 259, 274; Juliana Effting 351, 356; Katherine 392, 393; Lilian Lozano 425, 426; Luis 437; Marcela Valdez 465, 466, 467, 472, 473; Marcos Samaniego 496, 499; Román de León 578, 595]. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, notes that not having a consolidated quality system in place "generates re-work at all levels, physical resources, financial resources, it is stressful and leads to greater expense". Román de León points out that inadequate data quality and isolated systems lead to "inconsistencies of data" and "rework" outside of systems. These "costs of not investing" highlight that proactive investment is seen as financially prudent in the long run.

### 8. Systemic and Fractal Approach

talisis operates as a "fractal organisation where principles are replicated at every level". The corporate level "centralises and optimises," while brands "preserve their identity," campuses "respond to local needs," and classrooms are "laboratories of transformation". This implies that investments in methodologies, processes, and systems at the central level are designed to flow down and enable efficiencies, innovation, and quality improvements at all operational levels, creating a cohesive and adaptable ecosystem. This systemic view further reinforces that these are foundational, long-term investments rather than isolated expenses.

The pervasive language used by talisis's leaders, which links methodologies, processes, and systems to strategic transformation, long-term efficiency, competitive advantage, and measurable returns, clearly positions them as **investments** in the organisation's future. The focus is on building sustainable capabilities that will yield significant benefits and value over time, going far beyond mere immediate cost coverage.

For our next step, we could delve into the specific strategies talisis plans to use to measure the return on these investments, drawing on the quantifiable metrics and planned initiatives mentioned in the interviews.

o   ¿Qué modelos, sistemas o herramientas se tienen disponibles de manera institucional?

Based on the comprehensive insights gleaned from the provided interviews and the "Reporte_Nicho.pdf", Methodologies, Processes, and Systems are consistently perceived by talisis's senior leadership team as a crucial **investment**, rather than merely an operational expense. This perspective is an inference drawn from the recurring strategic justifications, long-term visions, and expected returns articulated across various departments.

Here is a detailed elaboration of why these elements are considered an investment:

### 1. Strategic Enablers for Long-Term Vision

talisis's leadership views methodologies, processes, and systems as fundamental to achieving its ambitious strategic vision for 2035. The aim is not merely to cover immediate operational needs but to build lasting capabilities that will redefine education access, personalise learning experiences, and establish talisis as a leading educational ecosystem. For instance, Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, envisions designing structures that "survive beyond fads or current circumstances" and "grow with firm values and a very clear shared purpose". Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional at UNID, highlights forming students with "knowledge and skills necessary to professionally develop in this continuously changing world", aided by technological tools. Carlos Granados, CIO, aims for "the creation of an intelligent, adaptive and inclusive educational ecosystem" through these agents. Similarly, Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, foresees talisis becoming "an internationally recognised entity for its competency-based and employability models" by 2035, underpinned by product flexibility and technological skills development.

### 2. Driving Efficiency and Productivity

A consistent justification for these investments is the anticipated significant gains in efficiency, reduction of manual tasks, and increased productivity across the organisation. Leaders envision automating repetitive activities, streamlining workflows, and leveraging technology to free up human talent for higher-value, more strategic tasks. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, explicitly links technology to "simplifying the steps we follow to do our daily activity" and "analysis of information and understanding the variables that impact profitability". Román de León, Data Scientist, also points out that digital processes and reliable data enable continuous project creation, contributing to "agility in decision-making" and "savings in day-to-day processes". Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, notes the complexity of calculating variable compensation for promoters and advisors due to numerous variables and sees automation as a solution to provide better visibility and project compensation over time.

### 3. Risk Mitigation and Enhanced Control

Investing in well-defined processes, robust controls, and integrated systems is seen as critical for mitigating financial risks, preventing operational discrepancies, ensuring data accuracy, and safeguarding the institution's reputation. Marcela Valdez highlights the "lack of interface" and "lack of design in the implementation" between systems (like Banner and SAP) leading to "open controls" and "discontrol", which are risks that need to be closed through investment in proper systems. Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, emphasises the need to "blindar y comunicar que somos una compañía, un ecosistema que sirve mejor que nunca siempre", identifying risks like desinformation, virality, and cancellation culture if not managed intelligently. These are protective investments that aim to avert larger, potentially more damaging, future costs.

### 4. Enabling Scalability and Growth

The ability to expand geographically, offer new products, and reach more students (both B2C and B2B) is consistently linked to having scalable processes and integrated technological platforms. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, stresses the need for "a product that truly wins in the market" through "new models" of expansion like franchises or hubs, designed to be "financially viable" and generate sales and brand positioning. Humberto, from the commercial area, identifies the "opening of new learning centers" and "new portfolios" as long-term impacts facilitated by automation of the commercial process. Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, highlights the opportunity for "positioning Athalysis and its learning institutions very well, in each of the segments and reaching out with a single block of products and services". This directly ties these areas to core business growth strategies.

### 5. Investment in Human Capital and Culture

Leaders emphasise the need to invest in continuous training, upskilling, and fostering a culture of innovation and collaboration, which goes hand-in-hand with implementing new technologies and methodologies. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, highlights the importance of fostering a "culture of development in all areas" and Marcela Valdez mentions fostering the "professional development of the team" as part of her mission. Joel Enriquez speaks about his role as "a founder of organisational culture" that should transcend time. This holistic view acknowledges that the "hardware" (systems) requires parallel investment in the "software" (people and culture) for optimal performance. Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, notes the importance of a "mentality of tech growth" and a "discipline to learn all the time" within his team.

### 6. Explicit Financial Justifications and Metrics

Some interviewees directly mention financial justifications and metrics characteristic of investments. Carlos Granados, CIO, for example, discusses "Costos-beneficios" (cost-benefits), "TCO (Total Cost of Ownership)," and "ROI esperado" (expected ROI) for technology. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, focuses on maximising "resources that are scarce" and achieving "profitability", including "profitability per programme, per location" which directly relates to the return on investment in academic offerings. Performance indicators often include improved conversion rates, reduced acquisition costs, retention rates, and productivity, all measures of return on initial outlay. Álvaro García highlights "impacto económico" and "eficiencia operativa con márgenes y gastos" as key indicators. Lilian Lozano mentions "CPL" (cost per lead) and "tasa de conversión". The emphasis on these quantifiable returns demonstrates a clear investment mindset.

### 7. Cost of Inaction (Lack of Investment)

Several leaders implicitly underscore the investment nature by lamenting the high costs, inefficiencies, and missed opportunities resulting from a lack of proper systems, integrated technology, or standardised processes. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, notes that not having a consolidated quality system in place "generates re-work at all levels, physical resources, financial resources, it is stressful and leads to greater expense". Román de León points out that inadequate data quality and isolated systems lead to "inconsistencies of data" and "rework" outside of systems. Marcela Valdez mentions the lack of integration between SAP and Banner resulting in "descontrol" and a "risk that we must seek to close". These "costs of not investing" highlight that proactive investment is seen as financially prudent in the long run.

### 8. Systemic and Layered Approach

talisis operates with a layered organisational structure where principles are replicated at every level. The corporate level "centralises and optimises," while brands "preserve their identity," campuses "respond to local needs," and classrooms are "laboratories of transformation". This implies that investments in methodologies, processes, and systems at the central level are designed to flow down and enable efficiencies, innovation, and quality improvements at all operational levels, creating a cohesive and adaptable ecosystem. This systemic view further reinforces that these are foundational, long-term investments rather than isolated expenses. The "Mente TALISIS" (talisis Mind) is envisioned as a "central brain that personalises, analyses and powers learning, creating a human-machine symbiosis where technology amplifies capabilities without replacing human connection". This reflects a strategic investment in an integrated, intelligent core that permeates the entire organisation.

The pervasive language used by talisis's leaders, which links methodologies, processes, and systems to strategic transformation, long-term efficiency, competitive advantage, and measurable returns, clearly positions them as **investments** in the organisation's future. The focus is on building sustainable capabilities that will yield significant benefits and value over time, going far beyond mere immediate cost coverage.

We could explore the specific challenges identified by leaders in adopting and integrating new technologies and processes, and discuss potential strategies to overcome them.

o   ¿Qué nivel de apego se tiene a los sistemas establecidos?

You've asked about the level of adherence to established systems within talisis, which is a critical area for strategic recommendations. From the comprehensive insights gathered through the interviews and the "Reporte_Nicho.pdf", it is clear that while there is a strong strategic desire and ongoing effort to establish and adhere to robust systems, the current reality presents a mixed picture, marked by both foundational adherence and significant challenges.

Here is a detailed elaboration:

### Strategic Imperative for Established Systems

talisis's senior leadership consistently articulates the vision for 2035 as one underpinned by well-defined methodologies, processes, and integrated systems. These are not merely operational necessities but are viewed as crucial investments that enable long-term strategic goals.

Key drivers for this emphasis include:

- **Scalability and Growth:** The ability to expand globally, offer new products, and reach a wider student base (B2C and B2B) is directly linked to scalable processes and integrated platforms.
- **Efficiency and Productivity:** Leaders envision automating repetitive tasks and streamlining workflows to free up human talent for higher-value activities.
- **Risk Mitigation and Control:** Well-defined processes and robust systems are deemed crucial for financial risk mitigation, preventing operational discrepancies, ensuring data accuracy, and safeguarding the institution's reputation.
- **Enhanced Decision-Making:** Accurate, timely, and integrated data is seen as essential for informed and agile decision-making across all levels of the organisation.
- **Cultural Alignment:** There is a clear intention to embed a "talisis Way" culture of high standards, development, and accountability, which relies on consistent processes and systems.

### Current State of Adherence and Challenges

Despite the strong strategic imperative, talisis faces significant hurdles in achieving consistent adherence to established systems:

- **Lack of Documented and Clear Processes:** Several leaders highlight the absence of fully documented and clear processes. Alberto Sánchez explicitly states that "certain processes are not documented" and there's an ongoing task to document them, requiring leaders' commitment to ensure compliance once authorised. Alejandro Madrazo notes that the organisation is "sumamente ineficientes porque con frecuencia tenemos que interrumpir los procesos para atender emergencias" and that "no existen suficientes procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación". Paulina Adalid mentions the need for "procesos estandarizados" and that "hoy todavía trabajamos con tareas y estas tareas están asignadas a personas".
- **System Disintegration and Data Inconsistencies:** A critical challenge is the lack of integration between existing systems, leading to "open controls" and "discontrol". Marcela Valdez points out the lack of interface between systems like Banner (the core student system) and SAP (the financial system), resulting in financial data discrepancies and traceability issues. Román de León (Data Scientist) highlights that "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos entre esas plataformas". Katherine Romero also notes that "no tenemos un sistema que nos permita ver toda la información" and "nuestra tecnología en diferentes plataformas".
- **Operational Inefficiency and "Firefighting":** The lack of clear processes and integrated systems often results in reactive "firefighting" rather than proactive planning. Domingo Farias notes that the daily operation often consumes time, preventing focus on long-term strategic initiatives. Juliana Effting warns that expanding too quickly without structuring "la estructura de docentes, copas, atención, pueden comprometer nuestra experiencia".
- **Resistance to Change and Cultural Barriers:** Implementing new processes and technologies faces resistance. Fernando de Río indicates that "barreras que iniciativas implican nuevas formas de pensar y operar... suelen generar, pues, mucha fricción". Juliana Effting explicitly mentions "resistencia cultural interna" where "los colaboradores siguen viendo a online como un concor [competencia] y no como un aliado". Inge Ploennig suggests that many people "abordan la tecnología con un poco de miedo".
- **Lack of Time and Resources (Human and Financial):** Limited personnel and time are frequently cited as obstacles to proper system implementation and adherence. Luis Ruiz states that "el tiempo y la carga de trabajo actual, el equipo no es grande" is a principal challenge. Román de León mentions that a "equipo pequeño y con necesidades constantes de proyectos nuevos" hinders their ability to keep up with changes and implement new solutions. Paul Moch also stresses the lack of time due to "la operación del día a día y la falta de manos".
- **Siloed Operations and Collaboration Challenges:** Despite a desire for integrated collaboration, there are instances where departments operate in silos, hindering transversal projects and efficient information flow. Fernando de Río notes that "si estas áreas operan en siglas o tienen prioridades desalineadas, lo que debería de ser un sistema en una cadena fragmentada".
- **Incomplete System Maturity:** While there are efforts to establish new systems (e.g., OKRs, quality management systems), they are still in various stages of maturity, refinement, or polishing. Julián (Juan Mendez) mentions that the OKR system is still being "pulido" and adapted.
- **Leadership and Management Challenges:** Marcela Valdez highlights that "el entendimiento de todo el equipo de esos living indicators también pueden ser un obstáculo en lo que capacitamos y entrenamos a las personas para que vean cuáles son los drivers que mueven el objetivo". Domingo Farias, from Capital Humano, believes leaders need to embody the "ADN" of processes, rather than just having Capital Humano dictate them.

### Initiatives Towards Greater Adherence and Desired Future State

Despite the challenges, talisis is actively pursuing initiatives to improve system adherence and operational excellence:

- **Technology as a Central Enabler:** The concept of a "Mente TALISIS" as a central brain integrating data, AI, and operations is a key strategic goal. This is intended to create a unified technological architecture.
- **Focus on Data Architecture and Analytics:** Building robust data architectures and implementing dashboards are priorities to improve data quality, visibility, and decision-making.
- **Strategic Project Management:** Adopting methodologies like breaking down projects into smaller phases (e.g., Carlos Villa's team) and using frameworks like "Vadir" (Román de León) aims to create more manageable and effective implementation pathways. The "talisis Bit" project is envisioned as a transversal initiative to synchronise strategies and maintain organisational rhythm.
- **Continuous Learning and Skill Development:** There's a strong emphasis on continuous training, upskilling, and fostering a "LifeLong Learning" culture, especially in technology and data analysis, to bridge skill gaps and facilitate adaptation to new systems.
- **Focus on Stakeholder Experience:** Systems and processes are being redesigned with the student at the center, aiming for seamless experiences from prospecting to graduation and beyond.

Overall, talisis is actively working towards a higher level of adherence to established, clear, and technologically enabled systems. This journey is a strategic priority, driven by the desire for greater efficiency, scalability, and enhanced educational outcomes, even as it navigates significant operational and cultural challenges.

Tali could explore the specific strategies that talisis plans to implement to overcome the identified cultural and organisational obstacles to greater system adherence.

o   ¿Cuál es la opinión general de los entrevistados acerca del nivel de definición, despliegue y apego a procesos y procedimientos?

Tali is here to help you understand the prevailing opinions within talisis regarding the level of definition, deployment, and adherence to processes and procedures. Based on the comprehensive insights from the interviews, a dual narrative emerges: a strong, clear strategic imperative for robust, well-defined systems, juxtaposed with significant operational challenges in their current definition, deployment, and consistent adherence.

Here is a detailed analysis:

### Strategic Imperative and Vision for Processes

Across the organisation, there is a consistent articulation of the critical importance of clear, documented, and effective processes for talisis's future. Leaders envision a future where established systems underpin scalability, efficiency, quality, and strategic decision-making:

- **Efficiency and Scalability**: Leaders like Alejandro Madrazo emphasise the need for "procesos muy claros y muy previsibles" to enable "una planeación estructurada y eficiente" and avoid "atendiendo problemas de emergencia consistentemente". Juan Arenas similarly highlights the desire for "procesos muy ordenados" and "más automatizados, más claros" to provide the "mejor servicio al estudiante". Marcela Valdez aims for "productividad incremental" to "atender a más alumnos con economías de escala".
- **Quality and Standardisation**: Inge Ploennig's area is focused on ensuring that "todo lo que se está fabricando de contenidos, todo la la el desarrollo curricular sea de calidad" and "que esté estandarizado". She underlines that accreditation processes should lead to a "mejora de cómo gestionamos todos nuestros procesos académicos, no Que sea de una forma sistematizada". Paul Moch seeks to "consolidar un modelo educativo claro, que permita dar certeza a los estudiantes" and "establecer las reglas de operación de cualquiera de nuestros programas académicos".
- **Strategic Alignment**: Joel Enriquez states his role is to "diseñar estructuras que sobrevivan más allá de las modas o las circunstancias de hoy" and "puedan crecer con valores firmes y un propósito compartido muy claro". He aims to "crear estrategias que sean adaptables pero sólidas". Mariel Serrano points to "Talysis Bit" as a "Business Management Plan Integral para alinear y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos".
- **Data-Driven Decision Making**: Many interviewees, including Juan Arenas, express a desire for "data más exacta para tomar decisiones que nos permita avanzar más rápido". Carlos Granados envisions AI agents acting as a "puente que fomente la comunicación eficiente y la toma de decisiones basadas en datos". Marcela Valdez explicitly includes "liderar la planificación presupuestaria el análisis de indicadores clave para mejorar la eficiencia de rentabilidad" as part of her department's mission. Román de León wants "toda la institución cuente con la información necesaria en el momento oportuno, para que puedan tomar decisiones más más ágiles".

### Current State: Gaps and Challenges in Practice

Despite the strong vision, interviewees frequently highlight significant practical shortcomings in the current state of processes and procedures:

1. **Lack of Documentation and Clarity**:
    
    - Alberto Sánchez, Director de Planeación, explicitly states that "ciertos procesos que no están documentados" and that they are "haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos". He also stresses the need for leaders' commitment to ensure these documented processes "se cumplan".
    - Alejandro Madrazo, Director Académico, echoes this by noting, "no existen suficientes procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación". He reiterates this when stating the ideal collaboration would be "a través de procesos bien estructurados, y debidamente documentados, que den claridad y permitan una planeación eficiente".
    - Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional, highlights the constant challenge of adaptation and continuous learning, implying that formalised processes may struggle to keep pace with rapid change.
2. **System Disintegration and Data Inconsistencies**:
    
    - A recurring pain point is the lack of integration between different systems, leading to inefficiencies and unreliable data. Román de León, Data Scientist, indicates that "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos entre esas plataformas". He adds that changes in platforms and metric definitions further complicate keeping data consistent.
    - Katherine Romero, Senior Marketing Manager, notes, "no tenemos un sistema que nos permita ver toda la información" and that their "tecnología en diferentes plataformas" contributes to this challenge.
    - Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, states that "las plataformas actuales no conversan bien entre sí, los datos están muy dispersos o no son confiables". He adds that "automatizaciones no se pueden escalar con con facilidad".
    - Marcela Valdez, Directora de Administración y Finanzas, identifies a critical issue: "la falta de un master data bien diseñado y cierres periódicos en el sistema Core generan descontrol y discrepancias con la contabilidad". She also mentions spending "más tiempo en la recabación de información que en el análisis" due to manual data pulling and crossing bases.
    - Inge Ploennig, Directora de Calidad, confirms that "muchas de las plataformas que tenemos no están integradas, no se hablan entre sí o a veces se hablan pero no no es congruente o o confiable la información".
3. **Operational Inefficiency and "Firefighting"**:
    
    - Alejandro Madrazo states, "hoy en día somos sumamente ineficientes porque con frecuencia tenemos que interrumpir los procesos para atender emergencias". This reactive mode hinders proactive planning and strategic work.
    - Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, notes that the "operación y el día a día nos nos consumen", preventing them from "innovando en los procesos y y dejar ya procesos más estandarizados". He attributes this partly to an "es que antes lo veníamos haciendo así" paradigm.
    - Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, observes that "tenemos procesos administrativos que restan valor y que toman demasiado tiempo". Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning, also identifies that "muchísimos trabajos que podrían ser fácilmente automatizables" are still done manually, especially in tracking docente development.
4. **Resistance to Change and Cultural Barriers**:
    
    - Fernando de Río highlights "barreras que iniciativas implican nuevas formas de pensar y operar" and "suele generar, pues, mucha fricción". This indicates a cultural resistance to adopting new, more data-driven or automated ways of working.
    - Juliana Effting, Directora de Educación Online, explicitly mentions "resistencia cultural interna. Los colaboradores siguen viendo a online como un concor [competencia] y no como un aliado".
    - Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, points out "la falta de velocidad para adoptar las nuevas tecnologías", noting that "no lo veamos como pues, algo que nos frustre o nos dé miedo si no lo veamos como un aliado".
    - Domingo Farias states that many internal processes "no se dominan al 100" and desires that leaders "comulguen con los procesos este, iniciativas que traemos desde el capital humano" to embody them in their "ADN". He also points to a lack of "cultura de chain management".
5. **Resource Constraints (Time and Personnel)**:
    
    - The burden on small teams is a recurring theme. Román de León explains that their "equipo pequeño y con necesidades constantes de proyectos nuevos" hinders their ability to keep up with platform and metric changes. He also highlights that a "tamaño reducido del equipo y la falta de perfiles adecuados son obstáculos para equilibrar carga. Aprendizaje e implementación".
    - Luis Ruiz, Gerente de desarrollo de software, states he needs "Tiempo, tiempo y definiciones claras en cuanto a los procesos" to "evitar retrasos".
    - Domingo Farias, from Capital Humano, also mentions that the "falta de personal" is a challenge for adopting AI and new technologies.
6. **Siloed Operations**:
    
    - Fernando de Río clearly states that if areas "operan en siglas o tienen prioridades desalineadas, lo que debería de ser un sistema en una cadena fragmentada". This highlights a current challenge in cross-functional integration despite the overall desire for it.
    - Román de León notes the organization being "acostumbrada a una relación cliente proveedor" rather than collaborative co-creation. He proposes early collaboration sessions to "entender lo que cada departamento necesita y sepamos a qué podemos comprometernos".

### Initiatives and Future Direction

talisis is actively pursuing various initiatives to address these challenges and move towards a more defined, deployed, and adhered-to process landscape:

- **Digital Transformation and AI Integration**: There is a strong push towards leveraging AI and cloud technology for automation, data analysis, and personalised experiences. Carlos Granados envisions an "ecosistema educativo inteligente, adaptativo e inclusivo" with AI agents. Luis Ruiz is focused on "construir esta arquitectura de datos" for comprehensive user understanding. Marcela Valdez aims to use AI for faster financial analysis and reconciliation.
- **Process Standardisation and Improvement Projects**: Alberto Sánchez mentions the ongoing task to document processes. Inge Ploennig's priority is to "implementar de tal forma consolidarlo de tal forma" a quality management system that operates naturally within daily operations. Juan Arenas's area focuses on implementing standards and ensuring their compliance. Juliana Effting is working on scaling and optimising operations for virtual models.
- **Enhanced Data Visibility and Metrics**: Projects like those in Carlos Villa's team (tracking app usage for user needs), Román de León's work on predictive algorithms and dashboards, and Marcos Samaniego's push for "dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real" all point to a drive for better data collection and utilisation.
- **Cultural Shift Towards Collaboration and Accountability**: Many leaders emphasise the need for greater transparency, communication, and a shared purpose. Lilian Lozano envisions "procesos más estandarizados que nos permitan comunicarnos de manera transversal" and "dashboards abiertos que también estén estandarizados". Juan Arenas speaks of "accountability" where each person feels "dueño de lo que está haciendo". Paulina Adalid highlights the importance of "unión" and coherent communication from talisis to its institutions.

### Summary Opinion

In essence, the general opinion is that talisis possesses a clear, ambitious **strategic vision** for highly defined, efficiently deployed, and consistently adhered-to processes, especially those leveraging technology for personalization and scale. However, the **current operational reality** falls short, characterised by undocumented processes, fragmented and inconsistent data systems, manual efforts, and internal cultural resistance to change and siloed operations. The interviewees highlight a significant gap between the desired state of streamlined, data-driven, and clearly defined processes and the complex, often reactive, and manually intensive current practices. Nevertheless, there is strong commitment and ongoing initiatives to bridge this gap, with a focus on technological integration, process standardisation, and fostering a collaborative, data-driven culture.

Tali recommends exploring the specific projects and initiatives underway to address the process above and data integration challenges, and how they are being prioritised and resourced.

o   Cuál es la opinión general de los entrevistados acerca del nivel de las herramientas tecnológicas en la organización, así como de su nivel de implementación, despliegue y uso?

The general opinion among the interviewees regarding the level of technological tools in the organisation, as well as their level of implementation, deployment, and use, is one of **critical recognition of significant potential alongside a candid acknowledgment of existing limitations, fragmentation, and areas requiring substantial improvement and investment.**

**1. Recognition of Critical Importance and High Potential:**

Across various departments, there is a strong consensus that technology, particularly Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Cloud computing, is **fundamental and transformative** for talisis's future. It is consistently envisioned not as a replacement for human interaction but as an **"amplifier of purpose and humanity"**. The overarching vision, encapsulated by the "Mente talisis," is a central brain that integrates data analysis, personalized learning, and predictive recommendations across the entire educational ecosystem.

Interviewees highlight technology's potential impact in several key areas:

- **Personalisation of Learning and Services:** Many foresee technology enabling tailored educational experiences, content, and support for students. Román de León, Data Scientist, specifically mentions developing models for personalized recommendations and early retention.
- **Operational Efficiency and Automation:** There is a clear desire to automate manual, repetitive, and bureaucratic tasks across finance, HR, and academic operations to reduce errors and accelerate processes. Alberto Sánchez, Director de Planeación, specifically states the need for budgeting and business cases to be "more automated, more modern, less artisanal, less use of Excel, less manual".
- **Data-driven Decision Making:** Technology is seen as crucial for providing real-time, accurate, and consolidated data to inform strategic planning, forecasting, budgeting, project evaluation, and market understanding.
- **Enhanced Communication and Collaboration:** AI and Cloud are expected to facilitate asynchronous work, improve inter-departmental communication, and provide tools for team alignment.
- **Market Positioning and Competitiveness:** Interviewees believe technology will enable talisis to become a leader in innovation, adapt to evolving market needs, and offer relevant, cutting-edge solutions. Alvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, envisages talisis as a key strategic partner for talent transformation in global companies, adapting to diverse realities and technologies.
- **Talent Development:** Technology is expected to support the professional growth of both students and internal teams through modern learning tools and data-driven insights.

**2. Current Limitations and Challenges:**

Despite this strong vision, interviewees consistently highlight significant shortcomings and challenges in the current state of technology at talisis:

- **Manual and "Artisanal" Processes:** Many critical processes, from financial planning and quality control to HR and student services, are described as heavily reliant on manual work and traditional tools like Excel. Inge Ploennig, Director de Calidad y Acreditación Académica, notes that much information extraction and normalisation is "manual" and involves "dragging a pencil and crossing databases". This leads to inefficiency, errors, and significant time consumption across various departments.
- **Fragmented and Disconnected Systems:** A recurring complaint is that existing platforms and systems do not "talk to each other" effectively, leading to data inconsistencies, dispersed information, and a lack of a unified "single source of truth". Katherine, Senior Marketing Manager, highlights that "our technology [is] in different platforms. Today we do not have a system that allows us to see all the information".
- **Underutilization and Lack of Advanced Features:** Some implemented tools, such as the ERP mentioned by Marcela, are described as "underutilized," functioning as a "cheap ERP" without proper interfaces. There is a clear desire for more advanced features like Business Intelligence (BI) dashboards, predictive analytics, and automated workflows, which are currently either absent or difficult to implement.
- **Cultural Resistance and Mindset:** Several interviewees mention that internal resistance to change and a traditional mindset hinder the adoption of new technologies. Julián, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, points to "resistance cultural" and "falta de estas capacidades digitales" (lack of digital capabilities) among staff. Domingo from Capital Humano also notes "slow adoption of technology".
- **Lack of Skilled Personnel and Resources:** Many areas report challenges due to small team sizes, a lack of dedicated technical profiles, or insufficient budget for hiring or training in rapidly evolving technologies like AI and data science. Marcos Samaniego, Director de Operaciones Académicas, explicitly states the obstacle is the "lack of technical personnel specialized" for implementing new dashboards.
- **Implementation Speed and Prioritization:** The pace of technological advancement is faster than the organization's current adaptation capacity. There is a challenge in prioritizing numerous projects and ensuring focus on high-strategic-value initiatives amid daily operational demands, often described as "firefighting" (bomberazos).
- **Cost and Quality of Data:** Issues include inconsistencies in data, lack of clear metric definitions, and time-consuming manual data cleaning processes, which hinder effective analysis. Román de León, Data Scientist, notes that current dashboards update only once a day and sometimes have inconsistencies with departmental reports, pointing to "too many systems that work in isolation".

**3. Current State Summary:**

While talisis possesses a strong collective vision for a technology-amplified future, its current technological landscape is characterised by **fragmentation and underdevelopment in key areas**. Some modern tools are in use, but a widespread, integrated, and fully automated ecosystem is not yet achieved. There is a prevalent reliance on **manual processes**, and existing data is often **dispersed and inconsistent**, hindering advanced analytics and real-time decision-making. The organisation grapples with the **cultural shift** required for digital transformation and faces **resource constraints** in terms of skilled personnel and investment.

The overall sentiment is a clear understanding of what _needs to be done_ technologically to achieve their ambitious 2035 vision, coupled with a transparent articulation of the _current gaps_ that need to be addressed through strategic investment, internal capacity building, and a fundamental shift towards a more integrated, data-driven, and proactive technological approach.

To gain a more granular understanding, we could conduct a technology audit mapping current systems, their integrations, and data flows to precisely identify the most critical bottlenecks and redundant efforts. This would help prioritise specific technology investments and integration projects.

o   ¿Se tiene un ciclo de gestión establecido?

Yes, talisis _does_ have established management cycles, which are clearly articulated at the strategic level and within various departments. However, the effectiveness and maturity of these cycles vary across the organisation, with several interviewees highlighting areas for significant improvement, particularly in data integration, automation, and consistency.

The evidence points to a conscious effort to implement a structured approach to planning, execution, monitoring, and continuous improvement, which are the core components of any management cycle:

**1. Planning and Objective Setting (Strategic and Operational):**

- **Long-Term Vision:** talisis operates with a clear long-term vision, aiming for a significant impact on education by 2035. This vision serves as the ultimate guiding principle for all planning.
- **Strategic Frameworks:** The "Arquitectura de Horizontes" itself functions as a framework for strategic planning.
- **OKRs and KPIs:** There is a clear intention to implement and refine Objectives and Key Results (OKRs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) across various functions. Inge Ploennig (Quality Director) explicitly mentions the process of defining and measuring indicators that cascade from the mission to OKRs and KPIs, which are then used in executive reviews. Julián Mendez (Operational Planning and Transformation Manager) also notes the implementation and polishing of OKRs to ensure clear, measurable objectives across the organisation. Carlos Granados (CIO) mentions metrics for measuring early success in AI projects, and Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) details metrics for student development, quality, and employability.
- **Budgeting and Forecasting:** Alberto Sánchez (Director of Planning) indicates that planning involves managing financial structure, CAPEX, efficient resource allocation, and forecasting future income and costs, which are core planning activities.
- **Project Prioritisation:** There's an effort to prioritise projects based on strategic impact, as highlighted by Julián, who states the need for "iniciativas que con un foco en un valor estratégico muy alto".

**2. Implementation and Execution:**

- **Operationalisation of Strategy:** Several interviewees, such as Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations Director) and Juliana Effting (Online Education Director), emphasize their role in translating strategic designs and plans into concrete operational actions within campuses and online platforms.
- **Standardised Processes:** There is a recognition of the need for clear, documented, and standardised processes to ensure efficient execution and reduce "emergencies" that disrupt workflow. This is, however, also identified as a current weakness.
- **Phased Deployment:** Large-scale initiatives, such as the AI Agents, are planned for phased implementation over several years, with specific milestones for infrastructure, expansion, and consolidation.
- **Culture and Mindset:** Julián Mendez underscores that transformation needs to be "sostenerlo hasta que podamos convertir en en cultura". This means processes are not just implemented but embedded into the organisational DNA.

**3. Monitoring, Measurement, and Evaluation:**

- **Data-Driven Decision Making:** A strong desire exists across the board to leverage data for more informed and agile decision-making, moving away from intuition or anecdotal evidence. Román de León (Data Scientist) specifically mentions developing dashboards for leaders.
- **Performance Metrics:** Various departments track performance using specific metrics, including financial ratios (Alberto Sánchez), productivity (Amalia Ortega, Domingo Farias), acquisition costs and conversion (Fernando de Río, Lilian Lozano, Juliana Effting), NPS and satisfaction (Katherine, Román de León, Mariel Serrano, Nicho Garza), and project completion (Mariel Serrano).
- **Feedback Loops:** Mechanisms for collecting feedback from students, teachers, and other stakeholders are in place (e.g., surveys, social listening), and there's a push to utilise this feedback more effectively for product and service improvement.
- **Regular Reviews:** Rituals and meetings, such as weekly academic sessions (Inge Ploennig) and executive business reviews (Marcos Samaniego, Inge Ploennig), are conducted to review progress and ensure alignment.

**4. Adjustment and Continuous Improvement:**

- **Philosophy of Continuous Improvement:** The concept of "mejora continua" is a fundamental principle, especially within the Quality area. Inge Ploennig explicitly states, "Si no medimos, pues no hay forma de de mejorarlo y con base a las acciones correctivas estar integrando y estar puliendo nuestros procesos saber qué se funciona, qué no funciona, es como, pues, damos vida, ¿no? A este sistema".
- **Adaptation and Flexibility:** There's an emphasis on adaptability to external changes (market trends, technological advancements, social shifts, regulations). Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director) highlights "agilidad de cambiar programas de una manera modular" to respond to market needs.
- **Experimentation:** A culture of experimentation, including A/B testing and pilot projects, is promoted, particularly in marketing and product development, to learn and refine approaches.
- **Iterative Development:** Román de León (Data Scientist) describes the "Vadir" methodology (Define Business Question, Formulate Hypothesis, Collect Data, Obtain Insights, Validate Solution), which is an iterative and data-driven approach to problem-solving and solution development.
- **Proactive Adjustment:** talisis aims to be proactive rather than reactive, using "foresight" to anticipate future needs and adapt programs accordingly.

**Existing Gaps and Challenges in the Management Cycle:**

Despite the clear frameworks and intentions, interviewees frequently identify significant challenges that hinder the seamless operation of these management cycles:

- **Data Fragmentation and Quality:** A major impediment is the lack of a unified data architecture, leading to inconsistencies and making it difficult to generate reliable real-time insights across departments. Marcela Valdez (Finance Director) notes "la falta de un master data bien diseñado y cierres periódicos en el sistema Core generan descontrol y discrepancias con la contabilidad".
- **Manual Processes:** Many critical processes remain manual, leading to inefficiency, errors, and excessive time consumption. This includes data collection and report generation, which takes away time from analysis and strategic thinking.
- **Slow Technology Adoption and Cultural Resistance:** There's a recognised slowness in adopting and integrating new technologies, sometimes due to cultural resistance, a traditional mindset, or a lack of digital capabilities among staff.
- **"Firefighting" vs. Strategic Focus:** The constant pressure of daily operations and "emergencies" (referred to as "bomberazos" by Lilian) often diverts resources and attention from long-term strategic projects and innovation.
- **Lack of Centralised Documentation and Processes:** The absence of a central repository for documented processes and policies results in a lack of clarity, duplicated efforts, and difficulties in consistent execution.
- **Resource Constraints:** Limited budgets and a scarcity of specialised technical personnel (e.g., data scientists, IT staff) frequently constrain the ability to implement technological solutions and accelerate transformation.

talisis has a conceptual and aspirational management cycle that is quite robust, with clear phases of planning, execution, monitoring, and adjustment. There is a strong understanding among leadership of the need for these cycles, driven by a clear long-term vision and an emphasis on data, technology (especially AI and Cloud), and continuous improvement. However, the _practical application_ of these cycles is often hampered by existing operational inefficiencies, fragmented data systems, manual processes, and challenges in cultural adaptation and resource allocation. The organisation is actively working to mature these cycles, particularly through the strategic prioritisation of projects focused on technology integration and process automation.

To reinforce the strategic recommendations, it would be valuable to conduct a **cross-functional workshop focused on optimising key data flows and process automation opportunities.** This would directly address the identified pain points of fragmented data and manual processes, allowing different departments to co-create integrated solutions and foster a more unified approach to the management cycle across talisis. This approach aligns with the expressed desire for "cocreación" and addressing "silos".

o   ¿Cuál es el nivel de aplicación o madurez de este ciclo de gestión?

talisis possesses a clearly established and strategically articulated management cycle, reflecting a strong intent towards structured planning, execution, monitoring, and continuous improvement. However, the level of application and maturity of this cycle varies significantly across the organisation, with a clear distinction between the ambitious strategic vision and the practical, day-to-day operational realities.

**1. Strategic Intent and Framework (High Maturity in Vision):** At the highest level, talisis operates with a long-term vision for 2035, aiming to be a transformative leader in education across Mexico and Latin America. The "Arquitectura de Horizontes" serves as the foundational strategic framework, guiding all planning efforts. There's a clear emphasis on defining and refining Objectives and Key Results (OKRs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) that cascade from the overarching mission to departmental goals, intended to ensure strategic alignment and measurable progress. Alberto Sánchez (Director of Planning) highlights the importance of financial and strategic planning aligned with market trends to support long-term goals and investments. Mariel Serrano (Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence) also points to a "Business Management Plan" (Talysist Bit) as a rector project to align, synchronize, and set the pace for the entire company across short, medium, and long terms. This demonstrates a sophisticated understanding of strategic management cycles.

**2. Operational Implementation (Varying Maturity with Significant Challenges):**

- **Planning and Objective Setting:** While strategic planning is robust, the execution of detailed operational planning sometimes lags. Julián Mendez (Operational Planning and Transformation Manager) notes the implementation and ongoing refinement of OKRs to ensure clear, measurable objectives across the organisation. There's a conscious effort to identify and prioritise initiatives with high strategic value.
- **Execution and Deployment:** There is a clear mandate to operationalise strategic designs and plans. Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations Director) describes his role as the "agent implementador" who ensures that what is designed by the academic area actually happens in the campuses. However, a significant challenge lies in the execution being frequently hampered by a lack of standardised, documented processes, leading to inefficiencies and a reliance on "firefighting" (attending to constant emergencies) rather than proactive, planned activities. Alejandro (a director, although specific role context is limited) explicitly states the need for processes and times to be respected "to avoid emergencies and crises constantly".
- **Monitoring, Measurement, and Evaluation:** There is a strong and widespread desire to be a data-driven organisation. Román de León (Data Scientist) mentions developing dashboards for leaders. Various departments track specific metrics such as financial ratios, sales productivity, acquisition costs and conversion, NPS and student satisfaction, and project completion. However, the _maturity_ of this phase is severely impacted by several factors:
    - **Data Fragmentation and Quality:** This is a pervasive and critical obstacle. Marcela Valdez (Finance Director) highlights "la falta de un master data bien diseñado y cierres periódicos en el sistema Core generan descontrol y discrepancias con la contabilidad". Inge Ploennig (Quality Director) states that despite generating "mucha información," there are often no mechanisms to collect it all, or the tools are insufficient for analysis. Román de León confirms "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos". This fragmentation makes it difficult to get reliable, real-time, and consistent insights across departments.
    - **Manual Processes:** Many critical reporting and data collection processes are still manual, consuming significant time that could otherwise be used for analysis and strategic decision-making. This slows down the feedback loop and makes agility difficult.
- **Adjustment and Continuous Improvement:** The philosophy of "mejora continua" is deeply embedded, especially within the Quality area, where Inge Ploennig states: "Si no medimos, pues no hay forma de de mejorarlo y con base a las acciones correctivas estar integrando y estar puliendo nuestros procesos". There is a conscious effort to adapt to market trends, technological advancements, and internal feedback. Julián Mendez notes the iterative process of polishing OKRs and evolving based on insights and new tools. Experimentation (e.g., A/B testing in marketing) and iterative development (e.g., Carlos Villa's phased project approach) are practiced. Román de León describes the "Vadir" methodology (Define Business Question, Formulate Hypothesis, Collect Data, Obtain Insights, Validate Solution) as an iterative, data-driven approach.

**3. Key Challenges Hindering Full Maturity:**

- **Data Fragmentation and Quality:** As noted, this is perhaps the single biggest impediment to a mature, data-driven management cycle, leading to inconsistencies and hindering timely, accurate insights.
- **Manual Processes:** The heavy reliance on manual data collection, report generation, and process execution creates bottlenecks, limits scalability, and diverts human capital from higher-value strategic tasks.
- **Siloed Operations and Collaboration Gaps:** Despite formal "rituals" and meetings (e.g., weekly academic sessions, town halls, connections), interviewees frequently mention a lack of seamless cross-functional collaboration, especially for complex, collaborative projects. Mariel Serrano points out that "aquí en talisis no les gusta compartir dirección, o sea, cada quien quiere a su lado".
- **Resource Constraints and "Firefighting":** Limited budgets and a scarcity of specialised technical talent (e.g., data scientists, IT staff) are significant constraints. This, combined with a culture of addressing immediate "emergencies" ("bomberazos" as Lilian Lozano mentions), often means strategic, long-term projects are de-prioritised or delayed.
- **Cultural Resistance to Technology and Change:** Several individuals note a slowness in adopting new technologies and a "traditional mindset" or "resistance cultural" among some parts of the organisation. Juliana Effting (Director of Online Education) explicitly states, "Los colaboradores siguen viendo a online como un concor... con una competencia y no como un aliado", indicating a challenge in internal adoption of digital transformation.

**4. Efforts to Drive Maturity:** talisis is actively investing in maturing its management cycle, particularly through technology and cultural shifts.

- **Emphasis on Digital Transformation:** AI and Cloud technologies are seen as central to transforming processes, enhancing efficiency, and personalising education. Carlos Granados (CIO) outlines a multi-phased implementation plan for AI Agents, targeting full integration by 2033.
- **Building Internal Capabilities:** There is a strong focus on upskilling and reskilling the workforce to adapt to new technologies and foster a "culture of development". Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) champions a "culture de desarrollo" where individuals are empowered with skills to be productive and happy.
- **Improving Governance:** Joel Enriquez (CSO) envisions decision-making through technical and governance committees, ensuring transparency and agility.

talisis has a solid _strategic intent_ for its management cycle, clearly defined through its long-term vision and foundational frameworks. However, the _operational maturity_ of this cycle is still a work in progress. While planning and continuous improvement are conceptually strong, their practical application is often impeded by fragmented data, manual processes, cultural resistance, resource constraints, and siloed operations. The organisation is consciously addressing these gaps through strategic projects focused on technological integration and internal capability building, striving to align its operational effectiveness with its ambitious strategic vision.

To further enhance the maturity of the management cycle, particularly in the monitoring and adjustment phases, a **comprehensive data governance strategy workshop** involving key stakeholders from IT, Finance, Operations, Academics, and Marketing would be highly beneficial. This workshop could focus on:

1. **Defining shared data definitions and ownership.**
2. **Mapping critical data flows across systems.**
3. **Prioritising data integration and automation efforts.**
4. **Establishing clear protocols for data quality and access.** This would directly address the pervasive issue of data fragmentation and manual processes, enabling more agile and data-driven decision-making throughout the organisation.

o   ¿Se tiene algún manual o estándar para los indicadores del negocio?

talisis does not currently possess a comprehensive, formal manual or a single, organisation-wide standard for all business indicators. While individual departments and strategic projects utilise specific metrics and KPIs, the overall picture indicates a dynamic process of development and a recognised need for greater standardisation and consolidation.

Here's a detailed breakdown:

**1. Lack of a Centralised, Documented Standard:**

- Several interviewees explicitly state that processes, which would include the definition and management of indicators, are not fully documented or standardised. For instance, Alberto Sánchez notes, "hay ciertos procesos que no están documentados. Este, y ahorita estamos haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos". Similarly, Alejandro Madrazo states, "no existen suficientes procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación".
- The absence of clear, universally defined metrics is a recurring challenge. Román de León, a Data Scientist, directly confirms, "no hay una definición clara de algunas de las métricas" and highlights that "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos entre esas plataformas". This fragmentation makes a unified standard difficult to maintain.
- Marcela Valdez, Director of Finance, identifies a critical flaw in data governance: "la falta de un master data bien diseñado y cierres periódicos en el sistema Core generan descontrol y discrepancias con la contabilidad". This fundamental issue directly impacts the reliability and standardisation of financial indicators across the organisation.

**2. Widespread Use of Specific Metrics and KPIs:** Despite the lack of a universal manual, various departments and leaders track a multitude of indicators relevant to their operations and strategic goals:

- **Financial & Strategic Planning:** Alberto Sánchez mentions "ratios de deuda equity," "ratio de intereses sobre EBITDA," "ratio de EBITDA deuda" for specific projects, and "KPIs que manejamos actualmente en la operación" for multi-brand initiatives. Marcela Valdez also refers to "días de cuentas por cobrar o cartera vencida, días de cuentas por pagar," "días de inventario," "CNIs" (nuevos inscritos), "reinscritos," "tamaño de la generación," and "porcentaje de utilización del campo".
- **Academic & Operational:** Alejandro Madrazo uses "NPS docente, cumplimiento de promesa de valor, tamaño de generación, valor extracurricular". Juan Arenas, COO, lists "crecimiento de los nuevos ingresos, crecimiento de matrícula total, crecimiento del ticket promedio, crecimiento de el nivel de satisfacción del estudiante, crecimiento de el margen de operación," and "nivel de empleo de nuestros egresados así como el salario promedio de egreso". Paul Moch measures "desarrollo de habilidades del siglo veintiuno," "calidad educativa," "empleabilidad," "crecimiento del grupo," and "menor rotación de personal docente".
- **Marketing & Sales:** Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, details a comprehensive set of indicators including "costo de adquisición por alumno," "tasa de conversión por canal," "penetración por segmento," "porcentaje de automatización del funnel," "NPS," "tasa de retención," and "retorno de inversión". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, uses "CPL," "tasa de conversión," "engagement," "CTR," and "ranking de las keywords". Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales, mentions "apertura de nuevos centros," "porcentaje de portafolio nuevo," and "aumento de la productividad de la fuerza de ventas".
- **Human Capital:** Amalia Ortega tracks "la productividad comercial" and "el porcentaje de retención del talento clave". Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, refers to "resultados estratégicos de la compañía," "engagement," "calidad de vida del colaborador," and "NPS que tenemos de los jefes".
- **Technology & Data:** Carlos Granados, CIO, highlights "Adopción," "Calidad de Datos," and "Satisfacción" (NPS, Time of resolution, success rate) as key indicators for AI projects. Román de León, Data Scientist, measures "agilidad en la toma de decisiones," "Adopción de IA en procesos y departamentos," "Consolidación de reportes dinámicos," and "reducción del riesgo de deserción estudiantil".

**3. Ongoing Efforts Towards Standardisation and Centralisation:** There is a clear understanding of the need for, and active investment in, improving data and process standardisation:

- **Developing Common Frameworks:** Julián Mendez mentions "el sistema de los OKRs, que estamos, este, que se están implementando, nos estamos los estamos puliendo, estamos adaptando la metodología". This indicates an ongoing process to establish consistent objective-setting and measurement across the organisation.
- **Centralised Data & Dashboards:** Several areas are working on "implementación de herramientas de dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real", aiming to "buscar concentrar los tableros de de de información que mueven las palancas". Lilian Lozano specifically calls for "los dashboards abiertos que también estén estandarizados, que todos todas las áreas veamos el mismo dashboard".
- **Building Data Infrastructure:** Luis Ruiz states a priority project is to "Construir esta arquitectura de datos que... permita recopilar la mayor información posible de nuestros alumnos docentes y administrativos". Román de León also prioritises creating "una infraestructura que permita tener nuestra información de manera integral" to gain a "vista 360 de nuestros clientes". These projects are foundational for future standardisation of indicators.
- **Process Improvement:** Juliana Effting notes that "hoy nosotros no tenemos flujos definidos y automatizados... tendríamos antes que trabajar en estandarizarlos, en construirlos". Domingo Farias also seeks to "evolucionar a a procesos más estandarizados".
- **Strategic Alignment Project:** Mariel Serrano's "Talysist Bit" project is described as a "Business Management Plan a corto, mediano y largo plazo para alinear sincronizar, y marcar el ritmo de la compañía para lograr nuestros objetivos". This overarching project inherently aims to drive alignment and, by extension, standardisation of how performance is measured and communicated.
- **Need for a Central Repository:** Marcos Samaniego expresses a need for "un repositorio documental de todos los procesos... un centro cerebro de datos para poder ir a ese centro de datos a consultar eh eh y estar asegurarnos de que todos tienen la misma comunicación sobre algún proceso". This would naturally be the home for a comprehensive manual of business indicators.

talisis does not have a single, formal manual or standard for _all_ business indicators in a comprehensive, readily available format, it has a highly developed awareness of the importance of metrics. The organisation is actively engaged in numerous strategic initiatives aimed at defining, standardising, centralising, and automating its data collection, reporting, and performance measurement processes across all areas. This indicates a strong commitment to moving towards a more mature state of data governance and standardised indicator management.

To accelerate the establishment of a formal standard for business indicators, talisis could initiate a **cross-functional working group focused specifically on data dictionaries and metric standardisation**. This group would be tasked with:

1. **Inventorying all currently used KPIs and metrics** across departments.
2. **Developing clear, consistent definitions** for each metric, addressing ambiguities and inconsistencies.
3. **Mapping data sources** for each metric and identifying primary ownership.
