4. **Prioritising metrics for initial standardisation** based on strategic importance and current data availability/quality. This would lay the groundwork for a comprehensive manual of business indicators and facilitate more reliable, comparable, and actionable insights across the entire organisation.

o   ¿En qué nivel está el apego a la medición, revisión y mejora de los indicadores del negocio?

talisis demonstrates a **developing and transitional level of adherence** to the measurement, review, and improvement of business indicators. While there is a strong strategic intent and a clear understanding of the importance of data-driven decision-making, the organisation currently faces significant systemic and operational challenges that limit consistent and efficient adherence across all areas.

Here's a detailed breakdown:

**1. Strategic Intent and High Awareness of Measurement Importance:** Senior leadership and various departmental heads universally acknowledge the critical role of metrics and data in achieving talisis's strategic objectives and long-term vision.

- Nicho Garza, CEO, states: "Cada proyecto tiene métricas claras: desde empleabilidad hasta NPS, desde retención hasta impacto comunitario medible. No dejamos nada al azar." This highlights a foundational commitment to measurable outcomes.
- Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Accreditation, firmly believes: "Si no medimos, pues no hay forma de de mejorarlo". This sentiment is echoed across departments, indicating a pervasive understanding of the necessity of measurement for improvement.
- Juan Arenas, COO, emphasises the need for "data más exacta para tomar decisiones que nos permita avanzar más rápido".

**2. Widespread, but Fragmented, Measurement of Indicators:** Individual departments and leaders actively define and track a broad range of specific KPIs relevant to their functions, showing that measurement is widely practiced:

- **Financial & Operational:** Alberto Sánchez (Planning) monitors "ratios de deuda equity," "ratio de intereses sobre EBITDA," and "ratio de EBITDA deuda" for specific projects, alongside "KPIs que manejamos actualmente en la operación" such as "ingresos de Harmon Hall". Marcela Valdez (Finance) tracks "días de cuentas por cobrar o cartera vencida, días de cuentas por pagar, días de inventario," "nuevos inscritos (NI), reinscritos," "tamaño de la generación," and "porcentaje de utilización del campo". Juan Arenas (COO) measures "crecimiento de los nuevos ingresos, crecimiento de matrícula total, crecimiento del ticket promedio, crecimiento de el nivel de satisfacción del estudiante, crecimiento de el margen de operación," "número de alumnos online o el número de alumnos híbridos," "número de ventas por asesor," and "nivel de empleo de nuestros egresados así como el salario promedio de egreso".
- **Academic & Student Experience:** Alejandro Madrazo (Academic Innovation) uses "NPS docente, cumplimiento de promesa de valor, tamaño de generación, valor extracurricular". Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) measures "desarrollo de habilidades del siglo veintiuno," "calidad educativa," "empleabilidad," "crecimiento del grupo," and "menor rotación de personal docente". Paulina (UNID) notes "qué impacto estamos teniendo en nuestros estudiantes," "crecimiento de nuestras instituciones," and "porcentajes de empleabilidad".
- **Marketing & Sales:** Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) provides a comprehensive list, including "costo de adquisición por alumno," "tasa de conversión por canal," "penetración por segmento," "porcentaje de automatización del funnel," "NPS," "tasa de retención," and "retorno de inversión". Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director) measures "CPL, tasa de conversión, engagement, CTR," and "ranking de las keywords". Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) tracks "apertura de nuevos centros," "porcentaje de portafolio nuevo," and "aumento de la productividad de la fuerza de ventas".
- **Human Capital:** Amalia Ortega (HRBP) measures "la productividad comercial" and "el porcentaje de retención del talento clave". Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) monitors "resultados estratégicos de la compañía," "engagement," "calidad de vida del colaborador," and "NPS que tenemos de los jefes".
- **Technology & Data:** Angel Casan / Carlos Granados (CIO) define indicators for AI projects such as "Adopción (% de usuarios activos, Frecuencia de uso, Retención de usuarios)," "Calidad de Datos (Datos de perfil completos, Precisión de datos, Tasa de actualización)," and "Satisfacción (NPS por solución, Tiempo de resolución, Tasa de éxito)". Román de León (Data Scientist) focuses on "agilidad en la toma de decisiones," "Adopción de IA en procesos y departamentos," "Consolidación de reportes dinámicos," and "reducción del riesgo de deserción estudiantil".

**3. Significant Challenges and Gaps in Current Adherence:** Despite widespread measurement, several critical issues hinder consistent and efficient adherence to indicator management:

- **Lack of Standardisation and Clear Metric Definitions:** A recurring problem is the absence of clear, universally defined metrics. Román de León (Data Scientist) explicitly states: "no hay una definición clara de algunas de las métricas". Alejandro Madrazo (Academic Innovation) desires "procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación".
- **Data Fragmentation and Inconsistency:** Multiple interviewees highlight that "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos entre esas plataformas". This leads to a fragmented view of information. Marcela Valdez (Finance) notes that the "falta de un master data bien diseñado y cierres periódicos en el sistema Core generan descontrol y discrepancias con la contabilidad".
- **Manual Processes and Lack of Automation:** Much of the data collection, consolidation, and reporting remains manual, which is time-consuming and prone to delays. Inge Ploennig (Quality & Accreditation) states, "mucha de ello se hace manual y y pues eso a la gente que lo genera les les da mucho pues te quita mucho tiempo".
- **Limited Centralised Reporting and Business Intelligence (BI):** While there's a push for dashboards, current implementation is often insufficient. Fernando de Río (Marketing) admits, "no tenemos buenos dashboards". Inge Ploennig (Quality & Accreditation) adds that even when data is integrated, it often produces "nada más reportes, o sea no analiza la información, no hay dashboard no hay un BI". Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations) is working on "dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real", indicating a current gap.
- **Challenges in Real-time Visibility and Agility:** The desire for "información visual para todos" in "tiempo real o casi" is a stated need, implying that current reporting often has "un desfase ligero" or updates only "una vez al día". This impacts the agility needed for rapid decision-making.
- **Cultural and Operational Resistance:** Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) mentions that "no nos permite a a a ir innovando en los procesos y y dejar ya procesos más estandarizados, por por el, no no no no te pusiste por la decidida, sino por es que antes lo veníamos haciendo así, y ese es el tipo paradigma". Juliana Effting (Online Education) highlights "la resistencia cultural interna".
- **Resource Constraints:** Lack of adequate technical personnel and data specialists is cited as a key obstacle to advancing data infrastructure and analytics.

**4. Ongoing Efforts Towards Improvement and Greater Adherence:** talisis is aware of these challenges and is actively investing in initiatives to improve indicator management:

- **OKR Implementation:** Julián Mendez (Operational Planning & Transformation) notes: "el sistema de los OKRs, que estamos, este, que se están implementando, nos estamos los estamos puliendo, estamos adaptando la metodología". This is a direct effort to establish clear, measurable objectives across the organisation.
- **Centralised Data Infrastructure:** Luis Ruiz (Software Development) prioritises to "Construir esta arquitectura de datos que... permita recopilar la mayor información posible de nuestros alumnos docentes y administrativos". Román de León (Data Scientist) is also focused on creating "una infraestructura que permita tener nuestra información de manera integral" to gain a "vista 360 de nuestros clientes".
- **Process Standardisation and Documentation:** Alberto Sánchez (Planning) mentions: "hay ciertos procesos que no están documentados. Este, y ahorita estamos haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos". Juliana Effting (Online Education) acknowledges, "hoy nosotros no tenemos flujos definidos y automatizados... tendríamos antes que trabajar en estandarizarlos, en construirlos".
- **Strategic Alignment Project (Talysist Bit):** Mariel Serrano describes the "Talysist Bit" project as a "Business Management Plan a corto, mediano y largo plazo para alinear sincronizar, y marcar el ritmo de la compañía para lograr nuestros objetivos". This project implicitly aims to standardise how performance is measured and communicated to ensure alignment.
- **Focus on Data Quality and Use:** Marcela Valdez (Finance) seeks "información financiera con mayor oportunidad, dar visibilidad con antelación", and Carlos Granados (CIO) is implementing a tool to "trackear pantallas y botones más utilizadas o o interactuadas" to understand user behaviour and improve functionalities.

**Conclusion on Adherence Level:**

The level of adherence to the measurement, review, and improvement of business indicators at talisis is **aspirational and in active development**. While there is a strong culture that values metrics and accountability, and many departments are actively measuring a wide array of indicators, the organisation has not yet fully achieved comprehensive, unified, and automated systems for data collection, standardisation, and analysis across all its functions. The current state is characterised by a recognition of these gaps and a concerted effort, especially through strategic projects and technological investments, to move towards a more integrated, real-time, and data-driven operational model.

To accelerate the maturation of indicator adherence, talisis should consider establishing a **cross-functional "Performance Metrics Steering Committee"**. This committee, reporting directly to senior leadership, would be responsible for:

1. **Developing a universal data dictionary and a consolidated KPI framework** for the entire organisation, ensuring consistent definitions and reporting standards.
2. **Overseeing the integration of disparate data sources** into a centralised data warehouse, prioritising the most critical systems for immediate impact.
3. **Mandating and supporting the adoption of Business Intelligence (BI) tools and automated dashboards** across all relevant departments, along with providing the necessary training to empower teams in data analysis. This structured approach would help transform the current fragmented efforts into a cohesive, highly adherent, and truly data-driven ecosystem, enabling more precise review and continuous improvement of all business indicators.

o   ¿Se tiene definido el “qué, cómo y quién” para la toma de decisiones?

talisis has a defined, though still evolving and, at times, fragmented, approach to decision-making, which encompasses the "what, how, and who" for these processes. The organisation demonstrates a strong intent to move towards a more systematic, data-driven, and collaborative decision-making culture.

**1. The "What" for Decision-Making: Information and Criteria**

talisis's decisions are primarily guided by strategic objectives, market dynamics, and a strong emphasis on data.

- **Strategic Alignment and Vision:** Decisions are fundamentally linked to talisis's long-term vision, particularly the "architecture of horizons" leading to 2035. Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, stresses that financial and strategic planning must align with market trends and CAPEX needs to achieve long-term goals. Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, highlights the "Talysist Bit" project as a "Business Management Plan" to align and synchronise the company's rhythm towards its objectives across short, medium, and long terms.
- **Data and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs):** There is a pervasive recognition that decisions should be "data más exacta" and "basadas en evidencia".
    - **Financial Indicators:** Alberto Sánchez monitors "ratios de deuda equity," "ratio de intereses sobre EBITDA," and "ratio de EBITDA deuda" for projects. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, tracks "días de cuentas por cobrar o cartera vencida, días de cuentas por pagar, días de inventario," "nuevos inscritos (NI), reinscritos," and "tamaño de la generación". She also seeks "información financiera con mayor oportunidad" and "rentabilidad por programa, por ubicación".
    - **Operational & Growth Metrics:** Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, details a comprehensive set including "costo de adquisición por alumno," "tasa de conversión por canal," "penetración por segmento," "porcentaje de automatización del funnel," "NPS," "tasa de retención," and "retorno de inversión". Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales, tracks "apertura de nuevos centros," "porcentaje de portafolio nuevo," and "aumento de la productividad de la fuerza de ventas".
    - **Academic & Student Experience:** Alejandro Madrazo, Academic Director, uses "NPS docente, cumplimiento de promesa de valor, tamaño de generación". Paul Moch, VP Teaching & Learning, measures "desarrollo de habilidades del siglo veintiuno," "calidad educativa," "empleabilidad," "crecimiento del grupo," and "menor rotación de personal docente". Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Accreditation, emphasizes objective measurement against mission and vision using KPIs. Carlos Granados, CIO, defines success for AI projects by "Adopción," "Calidad de Datos," and "Satisfacción" (NPS).
    - **Human Capital:** Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, measures "la productividad comercial" and "el porcentaje de retención del talento clave". Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, monitors "resultados estratégicos de la compañía," "engagement," "calidad de vida del colaborador," and "NPS que tenemos de los jefes".
    - **Technological & Data Metrics:** Román de León, Data Scientist, aims to measure "agilidad en la toma de decisiones," "Adopción de IA en procesos y departamentos," "Consolidación de reportes dinámicos," and "reducción del riesgo de deserción estudiantil".
- **Market and Customer Insights:** Decisions are informed by market trends, competitor movements, and direct feedback from students. Carlos Granados (Mobile Dev Lead) specifically seeks to know "qué es lo que le duele al alumno o qué le gustaría ver como nueva funcionalidad" beyond internal assumptions.

**2. The "How" Decisions are Made: Processes and Mechanisms**

talisis employs a combination of formal structures and a growing reliance on technology, while actively seeking to streamline and integrate its processes.

- **Formal Governance Structures:** Carlos Granados, CIO, mentions that "decisiones clave se tomarán a través de comités técnicos y de gobernanza," outlining a tiered decision-making process with "Estratégico" (C-Level + Directors, monthly), "Táctico" (Project Leaders, fortnightly), and "Operativo" (Technical teams, weekly) levels. This framework aims for strategic alignment, agility, and transparency.
- **Regular Review & Rituals:** Monthly business review meetings and established "rituales semanales" for academic areas, including brainstorming sessions, are in place. Information is cascaded from top management (C-level) through "connections," "conventions," and "town halls" to ensure clarity and alignment.
- **Process Standardisation and Documentation:** Several leaders highlight the need for clearer and more documented processes to enable efficient planning and reduce emergencies. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, states: "hoy nosotros no tenemos flujos definidos y automatizados... tendríamos antes que trabajar en estandarizarlos, en construirlos". Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, aims for a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos".
- **Technological Enablement:**
    - **Automation:** There is a strong push to automate manual tasks to save time and reduce errors, particularly in areas like budgeting, business case evaluation, financial reconciliation, and commercial compensation calculation.
    - **Integrated Data Infrastructure:** A key strategic project is to "Construir esta arquitectura de datos que... permita recopilar la mayor información posible" for a "vista 360 de nuestros clientes". This is intended to overcome current data fragmentation and inconsistencies that hinder timely and reliable decision-making.
    - **Business Intelligence (BI) Tools and Dashboards:** Leaders express a desire for "información visual para todos" in "tiempo real o casi", with Marcos Samaniego actively implementing "dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real". Fernando de Río, however, admits, "no tenemos buenos dashboards", indicating ongoing challenges.
    - **Artificial Intelligence (AI) and Machine Learning (ML):** AI is seen as a "gran aliado" for more precise forecasting, budgeting, and project evaluation. Román de León proposes AI for predictive retention models, optimising academic programming, and personalising content. Carlos Granados envisions AI-powered "tutorías" and streaming content. Fernando de Río highlights AI for "segmentación hiper personalizada," "análisis predictivo," and "automatización creativa" in marketing. Paulina Adalid, Rector, mentions using AI tools for "guiando hacia hacer las cosas correctamente" and being "a la vanguardia".
- **Collaborative and Empathetic Approaches:** There's a strong emphasis on fostering a culture of "cocreación" and moving away from a client-provider dynamic towards "socio estratégico". Julián Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, advocates for "empoderamiento real de los equipos" and autonomy to counter micromanagement. Leaders also emphasize maintaining a "trato humano cercano" and "empatía" despite technological advancements, seeing technology as an amplifier, not a replacement, for human connection.

**3. The "Who" for Decision-Making: Involved Parties**

Decision-making involves a multi-layered structure, from the highest leadership to individual contributors, with a strong focus on cross-functional collaboration and clear responsibilities.

- **Senior Leadership (C-Level and Directors):**
    - **Vision and Strategy:** The CEO (Nicho) and other C-level executives set the overarching vision and strategic direction. Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, sees his role as building "un legado estratégico" and acting as a "fundador de cultura organizacional".
    - **Governance and Oversight:** Strategic committees involving C-level and Directors are designated for key decisions. They also approve documented processes and procedures.
- **Department Heads and Directors:**
    - **Implementation and Operationalisation:** Leaders like Juan Arenas (COO) are responsible for "haciendo realidad las cosas" and delivering services to students. Alberto Sánchez (Planning) manages financial and strategic planning and interacts with internal clients across departments.
    - **Team Development:** Department heads are responsible for identifying, evaluating, and developing their teams' skills and competencies.
    - **Cross-Functional Collaboration:** Directors are key facilitators and participants in inter-departmental collaboration, aiming to break down silos.
- **Teams and Individual Contributors:**
    - **Execution and Feedback:** Teams are responsible for executing tasks and providing crucial feedback from the ground level to inform improvements. Carlos Granados (Mobile Dev Lead) emphasizes the need for user feedback to guide development.
    - **Innovation and Adaptation:** Employees are encouraged to adopt new technologies, experiment, and propose innovative ideas.
    - **Communication:** Effective and clear communication is highlighted as a fundamental need across all levels to reduce friction and ensure alignment.
    - **Students:** While not direct decision-makers, students are positioned at the "centro de todo lo que hacemos", and their needs, feedback, and experience are crucial inputs for decision-making.

talisis has a robust conceptualisation of "what" to decide (strategic, data-driven, customer-centric), is actively evolving "how" to decide (moving towards automated, integrated, and collaborative processes), and has a multi-layered "who" involved in decisions. However, the consistent theme of challenges—such as data fragmentation, manual processes, lack of clear metric definitions, and the need for greater cross-functional alignment and technological capabilities—indicates that while the "what, how, and who" are largely defined, their full and seamless implementation is still a work in progress.

**Suggestion:**

To strengthen the "how" and "who" aspects of decision-making, I recommend establishing a **"Strategic Data Council"** comprising key leaders from Planning, Finance, IT, Data Science, Marketing, and Operations. This council would be tasked with:

1. **Standardising Data Governance:** Defining universal metrics, data ownership, and quality standards across all business units.
2. **Prioritising Technology Investments:** Collaboratively identifying and funding the most impactful technology and data infrastructure projects (e.g., centralised data lake, integrated BI dashboards) that directly enable faster, more accurate decision-making.
3. **Fostering Data Literacy:** Overseeing the creation and implementation of training programmes to empower all employees to understand and utilise the newly available data and tools.

This approach would centralise efforts, break down data silos, and ensure that decision-making processes are uniformly supported by high-quality, accessible data, enabling talisis to achieve its strategic objectives with greater agility.

o   ¿En dónde se documentan y cómo se despliegan las decisiones tomadas o los nuevos estándares una vez definidos?

talisis has a multifaceted approach to documenting and deploying decisions and new standards, although several leaders indicate that this process is still evolving and requires further systematisation and technological enhancement.

**I. Documentation of Decisions and New Standards**

Decisions and new standards within talisis are documented through a combination of formal processes, strategic initiatives, and increasingly, through digital platforms and data repositories:

- **Formal Process Documentation:** There is a clear recognition of the need for formal documentation. Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, highlights the importance of "políticas o procedimientos que vamos a en los que estamos trabajando" to ensure efficient budgeting and project evaluation. Alejandro Madrazo, Academic Director, explicitly states the ambition to create a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos" to enable structured and efficient long-term planning, thereby reducing the need for constant emergency responses. Julián Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, echoes this sentiment, desiring a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos" as a central "cerebro de datos" for consolidated knowledge and consistent communication. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, also underscores the importance of maintaining "controles internos robustos" within her mission, which implicitly requires documented procedures.
    
- **Strategic Planning Documents:** High-level strategic decisions are enshrined in overarching plans, such as the "arquitectura de Horizontes". A significant initiative, "Talysist Bit" (or "talisis Bit"), led by Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, is described as a "Business Management Plan" that defines the rhythm, communication, and actions of the entire organisation towards its strategic objectives. This plan outlines phases for conceptualisation, modelling, planning, deployment, and execution, indicating a structured documentation of strategic decisions.
    
- **Meeting Outputs and Performance Metrics (OKRs/KPIs):** Decisions are regularly made and documented during various meetings. Carlos Granados, CIO, specifies that "decisiones clave se tomarán a través de comités técnicos y de gobernanza," operating at strategic (monthly), tactical (fortnightly), and operational (weekly) levels. These forums serve as points for formalising decisions. The organisation also uses OKRs (Objectives and Key Results) and KPIs (Key Performance Indicators) to define and track objectives, providing a documented framework for performance and strategic alignment. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Accreditation, describes a "matriz de congruencia" with 14 key indicators linked to the institutional mission, reviewed quarterly, which serves as a documented measure of compliance.
    
- **Digital Platforms and Dashboards (Aspirational/Developing):** A major aspiration across various departments is to centralise and visualise data to support rapid decision-making. Alberto Sánchez desires "información visual para todos" in "tiempo real o casi" to replace dispersed Excel files and static presentations. Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, is actively implementing "dashboards centralizados y mediciones automáticas o en tiempo real" to monitor operational processes. Marcela Valdez also aims to "concentrar los tableros de de de información que mueven las palancas". Román de León, Data Scientist, seeks to "reducir los reportes... a unos tableros dinámicos con mayor frecuencia de actualización". Carlos Granados mentions an "informe estratégico que puede incluir dashboards y gráficas para facilitar la toma de decisiones" based on interview data. The "Reporte Nicho" corroborates this vision, highlighting "Plataforma talisis.com, analítica predictiva para reducir deserción, IA para personalización, y arquitectura tecnológica unificada que conecta todas las operaciones" as a systemic manifestation, aiming for a "mente TALISIS" that conceptualises, guides, and recommends. Luis Ruiz also lists "Construir esta arquitectura de datos" as a priority project to gather comprehensive information about users.
    

**II. Deployment of Decisions and New Standards**

The deployment of decisions and new standards in talisis relies on a combination of formal communication channels, defined governance structures, and ongoing efforts to leverage technology and foster a supportive culture:

- **Formal Communication Channels and Organisational Rituals:**
    
    - **Company-Wide Events:** talisis employs large-scale "rituales" such as "connections," "conventions," and "town halls" to cascade strategic information and decisions from top management (C-level) throughout the organisation. Inge Ploennig commends the improved format of town halls for effectively communicating the institutional vision and context. Mariel Serrano's area, Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence, is responsible for a "estrategia de comunicación transversal" that ensures consistent messaging and supports all business areas.
    - **Regular Meetings and Feedback Loops:** Within departments, "rituales semanales" like brainstorming sessions are used to discuss and disseminate new ideas and operational adjustments. Juan Arenas, COO, emphasises his role in "retroalimentar sobre los procesos diseñados" to ensure their practical applicability in the field. Carlos Granados also describes a system for collecting user feedback directly through applications, where comments can inform future developments and directly influence the deployment of new functionalities.
- **Governance Structures:** The multi-tiered committee system (Strategic, Tactical, Operational) described by Carlos Granados is central to deploying decisions. Strategic directives from the highest level are broken down and implemented by project leaders and technical teams, ensuring alignment and accountability. Marcos Samaniego also participates in "comités" where alliances and strategies are discussed before being deployed to campuses.
    
- **Technological Enablement (Current and Future State):**
    
    - **Unified Data Architecture:** A critical goal is to overcome current data fragmentation and manual processes. The vision is to build an "arquitectura tecnológica unificada" or "cerebro digital" that can automatically collect, process, and disseminate information across all platforms, enabling faster and more informed decisions. This centralisation is expected to facilitate the rapid deployment of new standards and insights.
    - **Automation:** The automation of administrative and operational processes is a significant focus, as it can embed new standards directly into workflows, reducing manual effort, errors, and speeding up execution. Juliana Effting explicitly states the need to "estandarizarlos, en construirlos" before leveraging cloud technology for automated flows. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, desires to "dejar a un lado procesos manuales, y burocráticos, para evolucionar a a procesos más estandarizados".
    - **AI for Personalisation and Support:** The use of AI is envisioned to personalise learning experiences and provide timely support, effectively deploying tailored educational approaches at scale. This includes AI-powered "tutorías" and predictive models for student retention, directly influencing how new pedagogical standards are deployed and experienced by students.
- **Leadership and Culture of Accountability:**
    
    - **Clarity and Compliance:** Alberto Sánchez stresses that once policies are "autorizados por ellos estos estas políticas o procedimientos... que se cumplan". This indicates that leaders are expected to ensure adherence to new standards. Domingo Farias also pushes for departments to have "mayor claridad de qué es lo que que necesitamos cumplir en este año".
    - **Collaborative Culture:** There's a strong emphasis on fostering a culture of "cocreación", "corresponsabilidad", and "empoderamiento real de los equipos". Román de León desires that leaders and colleagues "se involucren de manera temprana" in new solutions, moving away from a client-provider dynamic. This implies that the deployment of decisions is not merely a top-down mandate but involves active participation and buy-in from all levels. Joel Enriquez highlights the "Talysist Bit" project as a cultural endeavour to ensure "más de 1500 personas trabajen con foco ritmo, y sentido común", thereby embedding the strategic rhythm into the organisation's core.

talisis's strategy for documenting and deploying decisions and standards is moving towards a more integrated, data-driven, and collaborative model. While formal structures and communication channels are in place, the future vision involves significant technological advancements to centralise data and automate processes, complemented by a culture that values shared purpose, collaboration, and continuous adaptation.

To accelerate the transition to a more integrated and data-driven documentation and deployment system, I recommend establishing a **"Cross-Functional Data & Process Harmonisation Task Force."** This task force, comprising representatives from IT, Data Science, Operations, Finance, Academic Affairs, and HR, would be responsible for:

1. **Auditing Existing Documentation & Data Flows:** Identifying all current documentation repositories, data sources, and information flow processes (manual and automated) across the organisation.
2. **Defining Standard Data Models & Metric Definitions:** Collaboratively establishing a universal language for key business metrics and data elements to resolve inconsistencies and fragmentation.
3. **Prioritising Automation & Integration Projects:** Based on the audit and standardised definitions, creating a prioritised roadmap for integrating disparate systems and automating manual data collection and reporting, directly supporting the development of centralised dashboards and a unified data lake.

This task force would address the frequently mentioned challenges of data fragmentation, manual processes, and lack of clarity, providing a foundational structure upon which more efficient decision deployment can be built.

o   ¿Cómo se escalan los problemas?

talisis addresses challenges and issues through a multi-layered approach that encompasses formal governance structures, feedback mechanisms, technological solutions, and a strong push for cultural and process standardisation. While some problem-solving currently relies on reactive and manual efforts, the strategic direction is clearly towards more proactive, data-driven, and automated systems for problem identification and resolution.

**I. Problem Identification and Feedback Mechanisms:**

talisis gathers information on problems through various channels:

- **Direct Stakeholder Feedback:** The organisation actively collects feedback from students, teachers, and staff. This includes formal surveys, "voice of the customer" mechanisms, and analysis of open-ended questions in Net Promoter Score (NPS) surveys. Carlos Granados, CIO, is implementing an in-app rating component that directly solicits user comments, feedback, and complaints, with a system for following up on negative reviews to gather more detail. Juan Arenas, COO, similarly engages in constant dialogue with students, teachers, and staff to understand their "pains" and areas for improvement.
- **Data Analysis and Monitoring:** There is a significant emphasis on leveraging data for early problem detection. Carlos Granados's team uses tools like "Centric" for proactive error detection in applications, allowing them to address issues "before the user or student raises their hand". Marcos Samaniego's area conducts measurements and analyses of operational results to determine if processes are functioning as designed or require adjustments, providing feedback to process designers. Marcela Valdez aims to use data to understand profitability per programme and location, identifying root causes of underperformance. Román de León, Data Scientist, focuses on building robust data architectures and dashboards for continuous monitoring of key institutional indicators. Amalia, Director of Talent & Culture, uses AI for "analysis, understanding of certain pain points" to establish strategic actions.
- **Proactive Risk Management:** Leaders are tasked with anticipating external challenges. Joel Enriquez, CSO, views his role as "reading the context" of a world "full of tensions" to design adaptable strategies. Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, highlights the need for "reputational intelligence capable of reading and anticipating social movements" to mitigate risks like misinformation or reputational crises. Carlos Granados also envisions using AI to proactively identify students at risk of not graduating on time, to prevent negative brand perception.

**II. Communication and Escalation Channels:**

Once problems are identified, talisis employs established communication and escalation pathways:

- **Multi-tiered Governance Committees:** Critical decisions, particularly those concerning significant problems or strategic challenges, are addressed through a structured committee system. This framework ensures problems are handled at the appropriate level and escalated when necessary:
    - **Strategic Level:** C-level executives and Directors convene monthly to define vision and direction. This is the forum for escalating major, high-impact problems requiring top-level strategic decisions.
    - **Tactical Level:** Project leaders meet fortnightly to address implementation-specific issues.
    - **Operational Level:** Technical teams hold weekly meetings to resolve day-to-day execution problems.
- **Formal Organisational Rituals:** Company-wide events such as "connections," "conventions," and "town halls" serve as key channels for cascading strategic information and addressing overarching challenges from top management down through the organisation. Inge Ploennig praises the improved format of these town halls for their clarity in communicating the institutional vision.
- **Cross-Functional Feedback Loops:** Juan Arenas, COO, describes his role as providing direct "feedback on designed processes" to ensure their practical applicability and identify areas where they are not "really happening as planned". Marcos Samaniego's team similarly provides feedback to academic process designers based on operational results. Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, actively fosters conversations across departments to overcome "obstacles and dynamics" and ensure inter-departmental understanding.
- **Internal Liaison Roles:** Amalia's team functions as "the glue" between different areas, facilitating communication and fostering agreements to "fix situations" and resolve inter-departmental issues. Julián Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, advocates for "well-designed collaborative spaces" to "resolve among all the different circumstances".
- **Developing Digital Communication:** The long-term vision includes implementing automated alerts and centralised dashboards to provide real-time visibility into emerging issues. This would significantly streamline problem reporting and allow for immediate notification of relevant stakeholders. Carlos Granados specifically mentions a cloud service that can process negative feedback events and trigger automated, personalised email responses to users, serving as an automated initial escalation and response system.

**III. Problem Resolution and Improvement Approaches:**

talisis employs various strategies to resolve identified problems:

- **Proactive Prevention:** Leaders aim to prevent problems before they escalate. Carlos Granados suggests using AI to send personalised reminders for graduation requirements, preventing delays and reputational damage. Domingo Farias's goal of a "Human Engine for high performance" and improving talent attraction aims to prevent productivity and retention issues.
- **Structured Problem-Solving Methodologies:** Román de León, Data Scientist, describes the "Vadir methodology" – defining a business question, formulating a hypothesis, collecting data, generating insights, and validating the solution with the user – as a structured framework for problem-solving.
- **Process Improvement and Automation:** A consistent theme is the drive to transition from "manual and bureaucratic processes" to "standardised and faster processes" through automation and technology. This is viewed as a fundamental way to resolve inefficiencies, reduce errors, and accelerate operations. Juliana Effting explicitly states the "super challenge" of standardising processes before automation can truly be effective.
- **Cultural Alignment and Change Management:** Several leaders recognise that problem resolution often requires cultural shifts. Domingo Farias promotes integrating processes and a "high-performance culture" into the "DNA of each leader" to foster shared understanding and accountability. Mariel Serrano's "Talysist Bit" project directly tackles cultural alignment and synchronisation across the organisation to overcome challenges related to commitment and consistency. Paulina, Director of UNID, acknowledges that resistance to change and a conservative mindset within the workforce are significant obstacles.
- **Data-Driven Decision-Making:** The push for centralised, real-time dashboards and robust data architectures is designed to enable "faster decision-making", allowing for rapid and informed responses to identified issues.
- **Resource and Capability Development:** Addressing problems such as limited time, small team size, or lack of specialised personnel involves advocating for adequate resources, fostering continuous learning and training, and exploring strategic partnerships with external technology providers to bring in necessary expertise and accelerate progress.

talisis's approach to escalating and solving problems is evolving towards a more integrated and proactive model. While existing structures handle day-to-day and tactical issues, there's a collective aspiration to leverage technology and cultural transformation to address systemic challenges, enabling faster, more informed decision-making and continuous improvement across all levels of the organisation.

To further streamline problem escalation and resolution, particularly across disparate systems and departments, I recommend initiating a **"Cross-Functional Process Mapping and Automation Initiative."** This initiative would involve:

1. **Selecting 2-3 high-friction, inter-departmental processes** (e.g., student enrolment and onboarding, content creation and deployment, or internal budget approval workflows) that are currently highly manual or fragmented, as highlighted by several leaders.
2. **Mapping these processes end-to-end** with representatives from all involved departments, clearly identifying hand-offs, bottlenecks, data discrepancies, and "pain points."
3. **Designing a future-state process** that incorporates standardisation, automation where feasible (leveraging existing or proposed technologies like AI and cloud), and clearer communication protocols.
4. **Developing a pilot for one of these re-designed processes,** with clear metrics for efficiency and error reduction.

This approach directly addresses the pervasive issues of manual processes, data fragmentation, and inter-area communication challenges, providing concrete improvements that would inherently simplify problem identification, communication, and resolution within those specific workflows.

o   ¿Cómo se pide ayuda?

Within talisis, the process of identifying challenges and consequently, how help is sought and provided, is multifaceted, drawing on a blend of formal mechanisms, cultural expectations, and direct appeals from leaders. It is often a reactive process triggered by identified gaps or inefficiencies, but there is a clear aspiration for more proactive, structured support.

Here's a breakdown of how help is requested and the types of support needed, based on the insights from various leaders:

**I. Direct Appeals for Support and Resources:**

Leaders explicitly state their needs for specific resources and capabilities:

- **Personnel and Budget:** Several leaders highlight the constraint of limited team size and the need for additional personnel to manage workloads and accelerate projects. Román de León, Data Scientist, directly requests "the hiring of one or two permanent persons" or "a budget to have one or two permanent people" to advance projects more agilely and prevent overloads. Luis Ruiz, Software Development Manager, also identifies "team size and the lack of trained personnel" as major challenges, implying a need for more resources. Similarly, Alejandro Madrazo, Academic Director, points to "limited budget, absence of full-time teaching leadership, and challenges in hiring leadership for laboratories", indicating a need for more funding and key hires.
- **Specific Technological Tools & Infrastructure:** The need for better digital tools and integrated systems is a recurring theme. Alberto Sánchez, Planning Director, explicitly states, "we need digital tools to be able to do it [automate budget and business cases]". Carlos Granados, CIO, seeks "a clear channel to know what students really need or want" and highlights the value of AI agents for scaling customer interaction. Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales, mentions the need for "the necessary technological tools" to adapt to market changes. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, identifies "technology" as a significant obstacle, specifically the lack of "integrated systems" and the inability to "analyse information" beyond mere reports. Her team needs a "system that truly stores information and then analyses it" to avoid manual data integration. Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, echoes this, stating the need for "support from a central area to create a repository of all processes" and "a central data brain" to ensure consistent communication and prevent redundant efforts. Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, also requests "agile access to data strategic agendas, institutional priorities, and real reputational challenges".
- **Defined Processes and Clear Communication:** There is a strong call for clarity and structure in processes across the organisation. Alberto Sánchez asks for "support... for these policies or procedures that we are working on to be complied with" by leaders once authorised. Alejandro Madrazo stresses the need for "clear and documented communication" and "respect for processes" to avoid constant emergencies. Juan Arenas, COO, similarly requires "clear processes... openness, listening, enablers, allow those processes to function well, and a structure in time for everything that is done". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, seeks "communication, alignment, teamwork" from leaders and colleagues.

**II. Implicit Requests Arising from Identified Challenges:**

Help is often implicitly requested when leaders describe obstacles, inefficiencies, or areas for improvement within their domains:

- **Process Inefficiencies and Manual Work:** Many leaders lament the reliance on "manual and bureaucratic processes", leading to time consumption and errors. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, notes that the lack of integration between systems (like SAP and Core Banner) creates "open controls and risks of discontrol", indicating a need for robust system integration and design. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, desires to "leave aside manual and bureaucratic processes" for "standardised and faster processes".
- **Inter-Departmental Silos and Lack of Collaboration:** A pervasive challenge is the "disarticulation between key areas" and the difficulty in fostering "global or collaborative projects". Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, notes the struggle to maintain collaboration with the sales team, and requests "leaders of other areas willing to work with a shared vision". Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, explicitly calls for "openness and coordination between areas to build aligned messages, share relevant information, and avoid silos that fragment the institutional narrative". Román de León describes an environment where departments "do not validate the solution they want to achieve" with his team, seeking only project delivery, which leads to inefficiencies. Julián Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, highlights the need for "well-designed collaborative spaces... to resolve among all the different circumstances".
- **Cultural Resistance to Change:** Paulina Adalid, Institutional Rector, points out the challenge of students arriving with "very precarious knowledge" and "emotional and affective situations" post-pandemic, which requires teachers to "accept that challenge of continuing to train". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, notes the "lack of speed to adopt new technologies" due to fear, implying a need for cultural support for technological adoption. Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, and Domingo Farias both emphasise the need for leaders to be "committed with the organisation" and to "lead by example" to drive the desired culture. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, highlights "internal cultural resistance" where online education is seen as competition rather than an ally.
- **Need for Strategic Clarity and Focus:** Domingo Farias points to a "lack of prioritisation and focus" as a key challenge, indicating a need for clearer strategic direction from senior leadership. Inge Ploennig stresses the importance of having "a very clear objective" and focusing efforts to avoid being "good at nothing".
- **Talent Management and Development:** Domingo Farias reveals high turnover in sales advisors and the lengthy hiring process, signaling a need for HR support to streamline talent acquisition and retention. Alejandro Madrazo highlights the need for "much better teacher training".

**III. Channels and Methods for Requesting Help:**

While not always explicitly detailed, the interviews suggest various channels for requesting and offering help:

- **Formal Governance Committees:** Critical issues and strategic challenges are addressed in multi-tiered committees (strategic, tactical, operational). This is where major problems are escalated for top-level decisions.
- **Inter-Departmental Meetings and Rituals:** Regular meetings and "rituals" are mentioned as forums for collaboration, idea generation, and information sharing, where challenges are likely surfaced. Marcos Samaniego and Inge Ploennig both mention regular meetings to "give feedback" on operational results to process designers.
- **Direct Feedback and Dialogue:** Juan Arenas, COO, actively engages in "constant conversation with teachers, students, and collaborators" to understand their "pains" and areas for improvement. Carlos Granados is implementing an in-app rating component to solicit direct user feedback and complaints.
- **Liaison Roles:** Amalia Ortega's team (HRBP) functions as "the glue" between different areas, facilitating communication and helping "fix situations".
- **Proactive Analysis and Monitoring:** Román de León, Data Scientist, aims to build robust data architectures and dashboards for continuous monitoring of key indicators, which would proactively identify issues before they escalate. This implicitly serves as a way to "ask for help" by highlighting problems through data.

talisis seeks help through direct requests for resources and transparent processes, and implicitly through the identification of inefficiencies, cultural barriers, and technological gaps. The desired support encompasses additional personnel and budget, as well as integrated systems, clear communication, cross-functional collaboration, and a leadership culture that fosters autonomy and a shared purpose.

To address the recurring theme of **fragmented information and lack of integrated data systems** as a core barrier to effective problem-solving and decision-making, I recommend establishing a **"Centralised Data Governance and Integration Task Force."** This task force should:

1. **Map existing data sources and systems** across key departments (e.g., academic operations, finance, marketing, sales, HR) to identify current gaps, overlaps, and inconsistencies.
2. **Define a unified data dictionary and standard operating procedures** for data collection, storage, and access, ensuring data quality and reliability.
3. **Prioritise 2-3 critical cross-functional dashboards/reports** (e.g., student lifecycle, program profitability by location, talent pipeline) that provide real-time, actionable insights for senior leadership and operational teams.
4. **Pilot the integration of key systems** (e.g., SAP with Core Banner, CRM with academic platforms) to demonstrate tangible benefits in efficiency, error reduction, and informed decision-making.

This initiative would directly respond to explicit requests for better data and address the underlying causes of many operational and strategic challenges faced by various departments. It would simplify how problems are identified (through readily available data) and allow for more proactive and data-driven solutions across the organisation.

o   ¿Se aplica alguna metodología para el análisis y solución de problemas?

Yes, talisis explicitly and implicitly applies various methodologies for problem analysis and solution, ranging from structured frameworks to emergent, data-driven approaches. These methodologies are crucial for achieving efficiency, fostering innovation, and addressing organisational challenges.

Here's a detailed breakdown:

**I. Explicitly Applied Methodologies for Analysis and Solution:**

1. **Vadir Methodology:** Román de León, Data Scientist, explicitly states that his team uses the **Vadir methodology**. This structured problem-solving approach involves several key steps:
    
    - **V (Visualise/Pregunta de Negocio):** Generating a business question and identifying the true actionable question they seek to resolve.
    - **A (Analyze/Hipótesis y Plan de Análisis):** Formulating a hypothesis and an analysis plan to gain a clear, data-driven vision of what they intend to build.
    - **D (Data Collection/Recolección de Datos):** Collecting the necessary data to execute the plan.
    - **I (Insights/Obtención de Insights):** Obtaining insights through statistics or machine learning.
    - **R (Resolution/Solución y Validación):** Finally obtaining the solution or constructing what was intended and validating it with the user. This methodology is used to guide projects from the initial question to user validation.
2. **OKR/KPI Frameworks for Performance Management and Problem Identification:** Multiple leaders refer to formal frameworks for setting objectives and measuring performance:
    
    - Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, details a "cascading" process where objectives are derived directly from the institutional mission and flow down to **OKRs and KPIs**. These are regularly reviewed in "rituals" (meetings) to measure progress and identify areas for improvement, emphasizing constant measurement for continuous betterment.
    - Julián Mendez, Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation, mentions that the **OKR system** is being implemented and polished within talisis, aiming for clear, measurable objectives across the organisation.
    - Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, also refers to **OKRs** for sharing objectives and ensuring all areas are aligned towards the same direction. These frameworks help in identifying deviations from goals (problems) and tracking the effectiveness of solutions.
3. **Continuous Improvement Cycles:** There's a strong emphasis on iterative enhancement:
    
    - Inge Ploennig outlines a cycle of "constantly measuring" and taking "corrective actions" to "integrate and polish our processes," which allows them to understand "what works, what doesn't".
    - Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, describes monitoring and analysing results to adjust and continuously improve the academic model.
    - Juan Arenas, COO, also highlights collaboration for "designing future initiatives that allow us to keep improving and innovating processes and services". This indicates an ongoing, systematic approach to refining operations and offerings.
4. **Agile/Iterative Development:**
    
    - Carlos Granados, Software Development Manager, explains that his team divides projects into "small phases" to deliver "continuous value" and allows for "quick adjustments" if needed, avoiding long delays.
    - The "Mazinger Z" project, which involved AI for content creation, underwent "many iterations" to refine its outputs. This methodology allows for flexibility and responsiveness in developing solutions.
5. **Quality Assurance and Testing Methodologies:**
    
    - Inge Ploennig's area functions as a "filter" to ensure content quality, aligning "standards and criteria in our testing matrix". This ensures that new content and processes meet defined quality benchmarks before being released.
6. **Human-in-the-Loop AI Implementation:**
    
    - Román de León details the use of "Human in the Top Dashboards" where "the algorithm suggests, but the teacher values and decides". This methodology ensures that AI recommendations are reviewed and approved by human experts, blending technological efficiency with human judgment, especially in sensitive areas like education. They also provide "explanations of models with natural language" to enhance understanding and trust among users.
7. **Strategic Foresight and Scenario Planning:**
    
    - Inge Ploennig identifies the need for "a study more in the medium and long term" for curriculum relevance.
    - Joel Enriquez, CSO, describes his role as "reading the context" like "reading the wind before sailing," which involves designing strategies that are "adaptable but solid". This proactive approach helps talisis anticipate future challenges and opportunities.
8. **Process Standardisation and Documentation:**
    
    - Alejandro Madrazo, Academic Director, strongly advocates for "very clear and predictable processes" and "clear and documented communication" to avoid constant emergencies.
    - Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, emphasises the need for a "centralised documentary repository of all processes" to ensure consistent communication and prevent duplication of efforts.
    - Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, highlights the "super challenge of having standardised processes" and "defined and automated flows" for case resolution. These efforts aim to create repeatable, efficient, and transparent operational methodologies.

**II. Implicit and Emerging Methodologies/Approaches:**

1. **Data-Driven Decision Making:** This is a pervasive aspiration and an emerging methodology across many areas:
    
    - Alberto Sánchez, Planning Director, needs "digital tools" for "dynamic information" to enable "faster decision-making".
    - Carlos Granados seeks "a clear channel to know what students really need or want" to create "truly useful solutions". He also uses tools for error detection and agile adjustments in production environments.
    - Ángel Casan, Rector, expects AI agents to facilitate "data-driven decision-making".
    - Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, states that "decisions are made based on data".
    - Many leaders express the need for integrated dashboards, predictive analytics, and real-time insights to inform strategic and operational choices. The "Mente TALISIS" concept in the summary report encapsulates this vision of a central analytical brain.
    - Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, aims to "learn from our data" to understand program profitability and allocate resources more efficiently. This shows a strong move towards evidence-based problem identification and solution validation.
2. **Customer-Centric Feedback Loops and Design:**
    
    - Juan Arenas, COO, actively engages in "constant conversation with teachers, students, and collaborators" to understand their "pains" and areas for improvement, aiming to "advance in solving the pains" and "strengthening what they are doing very well".
    - Juliana Effting stresses the need to "survey, know, ask," and "do Focus Groups" to truly understand the student's voice and structure operations around them.
    - Katherine, Marketing Director, focuses on "listening to students through different aspects" like social listening to identify effective strategies and messages. This indicates a systematic approach to identifying problems and validating solutions from the user's perspective.
3. **Cross-Functional Collaboration for Problem-Solving:** Many leaders identify the need to break down "silos" and improve inter-departmental communication and coordination to address complex issues:
    
    - Fernando de Río notes that "various projects depend on real collaboration between the commercial team, IT, CX, and academia" and that "if these areas operate in silos or have misaligned priorities," it fragments the system.
    - Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, highlights the need for "openness and coordination between areas to build aligned messages" and avoid fragmentation.
    - Julián Mendez stresses the importance of "well-designed collaborative spaces... to resolve among all the different circumstances".
    - Román de León advocates for early collaboration sessions to define commitments and manage expectations. This collaborative spirit is seen as a key problem-solving mechanism, ensuring that solutions are holistic and integrated.
4. **Experimentation and Prototyping:**
    
    - Fernando de Río desires "confidence to experiment and autonomy to decide".
    - Paul Moch discusses "controlled experimentation" and "tolerance for constructive failure".
    - Carlos Granados uses open-source tools like GrowthBook for A/B testing.
    - Luis Ruiz suggests "implementing new technologies earlier, perhaps for proofs of concept, that eventually become robust solutions". This indicates an agile, learn-by-doing approach to discovering and validating solutions.

**III. Challenges in Applying Methodologies:**

Despite the adoption of these methodologies, several leaders point to obstacles that hinder their full and effective application:

- **Lack of Clear, Documented Processes:** Many processes are still manual, undocumented, or fragmented, leading to inefficiencies and "emergencies".
- **Data Fragmentation and Quality Issues:** Information is often dispersed across various unintegrated systems, leading to inconsistencies, unreliability, and a heavy reliance on manual data collection for analysis, which consumes valuable time.
- **Resource Constraints (Time, Budget, Talent):** Limited team sizes and constant operational demands ("firefighting") prevent dedicating sufficient time to strategic design, long-term projects, and skill development. There's a particular lack of technically skilled personnel for data-related initiatives.
- **Cultural Resistance to Change:** Some individuals or departments are reluctant to adopt new technologies or different ways of working, preferring traditional methods. Mariel Serrano mentions the challenge of ensuring collaborators "understand" and "commit" to new initiatives like "talisis Bit".
- **Lack of Transversal Governance and Shared Vision:** The "disarticulation between key areas" and misaligned priorities can impede global or collaborative projects. Fernando de Río highlights the absence of "clear governance" and "transversal leaders" to ensure a shared narrative.

talisis is actively working towards systematising its problem analysis and solution efforts through various methodologies, with a strong lean towards data-driven, technology-enabled, and agile approaches. However, overcoming internal challenges related to data infrastructure, cultural change, and resource allocation will be critical for these methodologies to reach their full potential and consistently drive the organisation's strategic goals.

Given the repeated emphasis on the need for clearer processes, improved data integration, and enhanced cross-functional collaboration, I recommend exploring the implementation of a **Process Mining initiative**. This would involve:

1. **Automated Process Discovery:** Using event logs from existing systems (even fragmented ones) to automatically map actual process flows as they occur in real-time, highlighting deviations from ideal paths, bottlenecks, and manual workarounds.
2. **Conformance Checking:** Comparing discovered processes against defined "ideal" processes (where they exist) or desired future states, immediately identifying non-compliance and areas for re-engineering.
3. **Performance Analysis:** Quantifying process metrics (e.g., cycle time, rework rates, resource utilisation) to pinpoint the most impactful areas for optimisation and automation, directly addressing concerns about efficiency and resource allocation.

This approach would provide an evidence-based, objective view of how problems manifest within operational flows, offering a concrete starting point for targeted solutions that align with the desire for automation, data-driven decisions, and reduced manual effort mentioned by multiple leaders. It would move beyond "believing" problems exist to "knowing" exactly where and how they occur.

o   ¿Se tiene algún sistema para fomentar ideas de mejora y su reconocimiento?

Based on the information provided in the sources, talisis does not explicitly detail one single, formal "suggestion box" system with a defined recognition program for all improvement ideas across the entire organisation [All sources]. However, the interviews collectively reveal a multifaceted approach and a strong cultural emphasis that actively fosters and, in some cases, implicitly or explicitly, recognises ideas for improvement.

Here's a detailed breakdown:

**1. Cultural Emphasis on Innovation and Continuous Improvement:** Many leaders highlight a strong organisational drive towards modernisation, efficiency, and data-driven decision-making, which inherently fosters an environment receptive to new ideas.

- **Innovation as a Habit:** Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, articulates a core strategy of "cultivating a mindset of permanent innovation at every point of contact" and aims to make "innovation a habit" through "constant A/B testing, pilots, and new tools". This demonstrates a systemic approach to continuous experimentation and refinement.
- **High-Performance Culture:** Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, and Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, champion a "High-Performance Culture" and see themselves as "founders of organizational culture". This culture promotes a mindset of continuous development and an active search for improvement.
- **Constant Learning and Self-Improvement:** Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional en UNID, emphasises a "constant challenge to surpass ourselves, to acquire new knowledge". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, promotes "lifelong learning" and an "experimentation mindset" within her team.

**2. Structured and Collaborative Spaces for Idea Generation and Refinement:** Several formal and informal mechanisms exist within different areas for generating and discussing ideas for improvement:

- **Brainstorming and Ideation Sessions:** Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, mentions weekly "lluvia de ideas" (brainstorming) sessions within her academic area, specifically designed for reflection and generating new ideas for strategic projects. Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning, also desires "more intentional spaces for design and ideation" for his team.
- **Co-creation and Feedback Loops:**
    - **Cross-Departmental Co-creation:** Román de León, Data Scientist, strongly advocates for early involvement and "co-creation" with other departments rather than a simple client-provider dynamic. He actively engages in "bi-monthly feedback sessions" with teachers to improve tools and solutions.
    - **User-Centric Co-creation:** Carlos Villa, Mobile Dev Lead, is developing a tool to capture direct user feedback on application usage (screens and buttons) and sentiments, aiming to inform future functionalities. Katherine Romero, Senior Marketing Manager, plans to "scale this relationship towards a continuous co-creation model" with teachers, students, and allies for designing educational solutions and campaigns. Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, stresses the need to "survey, know, ask, and hold Focus Groups" with students to structure operations around their needs.
    - **Collaborative Spaces:** Juan Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, values "well-designed collaborative spaces to think as a team" and "quality time to align and co-design".
- **Strategic Committees:** Carlos Granados, CIO, indicates that key decisions are made through "technical and governance committees", which serve as forums where strategic ideas and improvements are presented and evaluated for implementation. Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, also notes participation in committees for maturing alliances and translating them into actionable plans.

**3. Data-Driven Identification of Improvement Areas:** The organisation is increasingly relying on data and technology to identify areas for improvement:

- **Data Architecture and Predictive Analytics:** Luis Ruiz, Gerente de desarrollo de software, and Román de León, Data Scientist, highlight the priority of building a robust data architecture to collect comprehensive information (economic, academic performance, social context) about students, teachers, and administrators. This data then fuels the development of predictive models (e.g., for student retention) and personalised solutions.
- **Automated Analysis and Dashboards:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finanzas, seeks to improve the management of financial information for more agile decision-making. Many interviewees express a desire for "more exact data to make decisions" through "intelligent dashboards", automating manual processes, and reducing discrepancies. This data-centric approach aims to systematically identify what needs improvement.

**4. Implicit and Emerging Recognition of Ideas:** While a formal reward system for all ideas is not evident, recognition primarily occurs through:

- **Implementation and Impact:** Ideas that are integrated into major strategic projects, like the "talisis Beat" (Mariel Serrano, Joel Enriquez), gain visibility and recognition through their successful execution and measurable impact on organisational rhythm, communication, and reputation.
- **Empowerment and Autonomy:** Román de León explicitly desires for his team to have "autonomy to propose their own projects that they believe can generate an impact". This empowerment to lead and implement ideas serves as a significant form of recognition.
- **Leadership and Mentorship:** Leaders like Fernando de Río and Lilian Lozano express a personal purpose of inspiring and fostering the growth of their teams. This supportive environment, combined with constructive feedback (as mentioned by Carlos Villa), helps to value and guide contributions.

talisis is actively fostering a culture of innovation and continuous improvement through various collaborative mechanisms and a strong reliance on data analytics. While a formal, company-wide "suggestion box" with explicit recognition isn't described, the emphasis on co-creation, data-driven insights, and empowered teams suggests that ideas are encouraged, evaluated, and recognised through their successful implementation and contribution to the organisation's strategic goals and ongoing transformation.

Given the emphasis on "constant learning" and "experimentation mindset" within talisis, we could explore the specific challenges and successes encountered in translating these cultural aspirations into concrete, repeatable processes for innovation and improvement across all departments.

o   ¿Existe algún área para la administración de la mejora de procesos, procedimientos y sistemas’

Based on the information available in the sources and our conversation history, talisis does not appear to have one single, formally designated "area for the administration of process, procedures, and systems improvement" that centralises all such activities under one name [Query, general absence of a single explicit mention]. Instead, the function of driving and administering process, procedure, and system improvement is a distributed responsibility, evident in the mandates and ongoing efforts of several key departments and overarching strategic initiatives within the organisation.

Here's a detailed elaboration:

**1. Dedicated Areas for Transformation and Quality:** While not named generically as "Process Improvement Administration," certain areas have explicit mandates that encompass these functions:

- **Gerencia de Planeación Operativa y Transformación (Juan Mendez):** This area directly aligns with the query. Juan Mendez states that his mission is not just to "operate the change, but to design it and activate it," and crucially, to "sustain it until we can convert it into culture". He views his team as "arquitectos de este cambio sistémico", responsible for making the vision a reality through processes, capabilities, technology, and culture. This clearly positions his area as a key administrator of systemic change and process transformation.
- **Dirección de Calidad y Acreditación Académica (Inge Ploennig):** Inge's area plays a critical role in administering and ensuring the _quality_ of academic processes, procedures, and content. She explicitly focuses on "el sistema de calidad, poderlo implementar de tal forma consolidarlo de tal forma, que independientemente si toca una acreditación o no, ya esté todo dado". This involves strengthening existing frameworks, integrating rituals, clear processes, dashboards, and KPIs/OKRs to ensure continuous quality and systematic management of academic processes. She also adapted quality validation processes for content production using AI.

**2. Strategic Initiatives Driving Systemic Improvement:** Broader organisational projects are also designed to drive process and system improvement across departments:

- **Talysist Bit (Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, and Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation):** This initiative is described as a "Business Management Plan Integral para alinear y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos" and a "sistema organizacional que nos permita que más de 1500 personas trabajen con foco ritmo, y sentido común". It aims to "marca el ritmo de talisis cómo nos comunicamos, cómo accionamos, cómo actuamos y cómo nos conectamos como organización". By fostering synchronisation and a common purpose, Talysist Bit inherently pushes for aligned and improved processes across the entire company.

**3. Technology and Data as Enablers and Drivers:** The IT and data science departments are seen as crucial for enabling and driving process and system improvements:

- **CIO (Carlos Granados):** Carlos envisions AI agents contributing to "automatización inteligente" and "decisiones basadas en datos precisos y en tiempo real" to reduce bureaucracy and make operations more efficient. He mentions "reingeniería ágil" as a mitigation strategy for "procesos incompletos". Decisions on key projects are made through "comités técnicos y de gobernanza".
- **Software Development (Luis Ruiz):** Luis's area is responsible for "construir varias de las integraciones entre nuestros diferentes sistemas", including the incorporation of AI agents to "eficientar los procesos". A priority project is to build a "data architecture" to collect comprehensive information for generating solutions.
- **Data Science (Román de León):** Román's team focuses on designing and implementing a data architecture to understand the industry and student development, providing strategic visibility. He applies "algoritmos de machine learning para detectar patrones" and seeks to optimise processes like "programación académica" and content personalisation. He also advocates for a long-term "partner tecnológico" to "rediseñar la arquitectura tecnológica" and ensure processes function optimally.

**4. Operational Feedback and Identified Needs:** Operational and administrative areas, while not primarily "administrators of improvement," actively identify needs and provide feedback for process and system enhancements:

- **Chief Operations Officer (Juan Arenas):** His area integrates ideas and projects that "se convierten en habilitadores de la operación," and he is responsible for "retroalimentar sobre los procesos diseñados" to ensure they are "realmente ejecutables". This highlights a feedback loop crucial for process improvement.
- **Director of Administration and Finanzas (Marcela Valdez):** Her department identifies the need to "mejorar la gestión de la información" for more agile decision-making and addresses the "falta de integración entre sistemas" and the absence of a "master data bien diseñado" which create "descontrol y discrepancias". She also aims for "automatizar medios de pago y procesos de alta baja".
- **Director Académico (Alejandro Madrazo):** He consistently highlights the "fundamental need for 'procesos muy claros y muy previsibles'" to avoid interruptions and allow focus on innovation.
- **HRBP Director (Amalia Ortega):** Her area is "haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos" and she acts as a "pegamento de muchas de las áreas," facilitating communication to resolve challenges.

**Challenges and Ongoing Development:** Despite these distributed efforts, several interviewees acknowledge that the organisation is still on a journey towards fully mature and integrated process and system management:

- **Lack of Documentation and Clarity:** Explicitly stated that "certain processes are not documented" and that existing processes are often not "suficientemente claros y documentados".
- **System Disintegration and Data Inconsistencies:** A recurring theme is that "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos". There is a recognised need for a "cerebro de datos" or "repositorio documental de todos los procesos".
- **Operational Inefficiency and "Firefighting":** Many lament that daily operations consume time, leading to a reactive approach rather than proactive process standardisation and innovation.
- **Cultural Resistance:** There are noted "barreras que iniciativas implican nuevas formas de pensar y operar" and "resistencia cultural interna".
- **Resource Constraints:** Limited personnel and time often hinder the full implementation of process improvements.

While talisis does not centralise process, procedure, and system improvement under one specific "department of improvement," these functions are clearly integrated into the roles of the "Gerencia de Planeación Operativa y Transformación," "Dirección de Calidad y Acreditación Académica," and are a core objective of strategic initiatives like "Talysist Bit." Furthermore, technology and data science departments are instrumental in designing and implementing these improvements, while operational areas provide critical feedback. The organisation is actively working to overcome challenges related to documentation, system integration, and cultural adoption to achieve a more cohesive and efficient operational model.

Given the recurring challenge of cultural resistance to change and new ways of working, we could discuss specific strategies talisis is employing or could employ to foster a stronger culture of adaptation and proactive process improvement, rather than a reactive "firefighting" mentality.

### VIII. Transformación y Gestión del Cambio

o   ¿Qué Procesos se quieren transformar?

talisis is actively engaged in a comprehensive transformation of its educational model, driven by its "Architecture of Horizons" vision for 2035. This ongoing evolution aims to enhance quality, efficiency, and relevance across the organisation. The transformation of processes is a central theme, encompassing both specific departmental operations and broader systemic changes, with a strong emphasis on leveraging technology and data for continuous improvement.

The processes talisis seeks to transform can be broadly categorised as follows:

**1. Core Academic and Curricular Processes:**

- **Content Production and Quality Assurance:** A primary focus is on ensuring that all academic content and curricular development are of high quality and standardised. This includes strengthening quality frameworks and integrating clear processes and KPIs/OKRs for continuous quality assurance. There has been a significant adjustment in quality validation for AI-produced content over the last 18 months, requiring alignment with new standards.
