- **Program Pertinence and Design:** There is a strong push to ensure the "pertinencia de nuestros programas académicos" (pertinence of academic programs) for the future, looking 10, 15, or even 20 years ahead to predict market needs rather than just reacting to current offerings. The aim is to redesign and update programs (e.g., "Vive Unid") to align with future student expectations and societal needs.
- **Teaching and Learning Methodologies:** talisis is exploring innovations in the "delivery" of education and in "contenido y herramientas de aprendizaje" (content and learning tools). This involves rethinking the role of the teacher as a "facilitador" of critical thinking rather than just a technical imparter of knowledge. The organisation is "probando y tratando nuevos modelos, metodologías y formas de aprendizaje" (testing and trying new models, methodologies, and learning forms).
- **Curricular Homologation and Micro-credentials:** Efforts are underway to achieve "homologación de la malla curricular" (homologation of the curriculum). There is also a significant initiative to develop a "sistema de micro credenciales" (micro-credential system) as part of a more flexible and adaptable educational model.
- **Student Academic Journey:** Innovations are sought in planning and executing the student's entire academic journey, from "planeación académica hacia una planeación más integrada", to "diseñar mejores experiencias de aprendizaje dentro del aula", and improving "experiencias de titulación y graduación".

**2. Administrative and Operational Processes:**

- **Onboarding and Transitions:** A key area for innovation is making the "onboarding de los alumnos de los empleados y de los maestros sea suave". This includes streamlining the administrative flow for "altas, bajas y cambios" (registrations, withdrawals, and changes) for students, employees, and suppliers.
- **Financial Management:** The finance department aims to "mejorar la gestión de la información" for more agile decision-making and to address the "falta de integración entre sistemas" and the absence of a "master data bien diseñado" leading to "descontrol y discrepancias". Specific processes for transformation include automating "medios de pago y procesos de alta baja", optimising "conciliaciones", "análisis de la información y el entendimiento de las variables que impactan la rentabilidad". The goal is to make financial "gasto... rentable y productivo" and achieve "productividad incremental".
- **Human Resources Processes:** HR is "haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos". Specific HR processes identified for transformation include automating "compensación variable de los promotores y asesores", improving the "curva de óptima de productividad" for new hires, and streamlining "contratación, las entrevistas, las referencias, la búsqueda de del mejor talento" to reduce high turnover.
- **Operational Control and Measurement:** Operations aims to ensure that designed processes are "realmente ejecutables" and to provide feedback for continuous improvement. This also includes "control específico de nuestras instalaciones, a través de la tecnología" and automating "procesos de medición y muchos procesos de colección de información y de procesamiento". The aim is to create a "centro único de trámites" for students to track their academic life.
- **Debt and Capital Management:** Alberto Sánchez (Planning) highlights the need to "administrar de manera eficiente los temas de deuda, los temas de levantamiento de capital, organizar de manera más eficiente... dónde asignamos los recursos, en qué rubro de costos, en qué rubro de gastos".

**3. Customer-Facing, Sales, and Marketing Processes:**

- **Sales and Lead Management:** The commercial area seeks to "automatizar y mejorar la venta en el proceso comercial". Marketing aims for "automatizaciones del funnel de adquisición, fidelización, y rentabilidad multimarca", and to use AI for "segmentación hiper personalizada" to tailor messages and channels.
- **Customer Relationship and Experience:** There's a strong focus on enhancing the student journey and experience to strengthen their sense of belonging. This involves making "el servicio al estudiante online" better by changing internal processes and ensuring "el alumno se sienta acompañado" in online education. The goal is to personalise experiences from the "primer punto de contacto" using AI.
- **Brand Positioning and Communication:** Mariel Serrano (Corporate Reputation) stresses the need to "comunicar de manera coherente esa mejora continua" and define "mensajes estratégicos que comporten como catalizadores virales y reputacionales". Fernando (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) aims to "rediseñar ofertas con un valor tangible y diferenciador" and "humanizar y transparentar nuestro historias".

**4. Cross-Cutting Transformation Needs:**

- **Standardisation and Documentation:** A recurring and significant challenge is the lack of clearly defined and documented processes. Alberto Sánchez mentions "ciertos procesos que no están documentados. Este, y ahorita estamos haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos". Juliana Effting notes "hoy nosotros no tenemos flujos definidos y automatizados... tendríamos antes que trabajar en estandarizarlos, en construirlos". Marcos Samaniego calls for a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos".
- **Data-Driven Decision Making:** A fundamental shift is required to move from scattered and inconsistent data to integrated, reliable, real-time insights for agile decision-making. This necessitates building a robust "arquitectura de datos" (data architecture) to collect comprehensive information about students, faculty, and administrators and developing "dashboards más inteligentes con acciones sugeridas".
- **Automation and Digitalisation:** There's a strong drive to automate manual and bureaucratic tasks across all areas using AI and cloud technology to increase efficiency, reduce errors, and free up human talent for higher-value activities.
- **System Integration:** Addressing the problem of "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos" and a lack of a "master data bien diseñado". The goal is to create "plataformas interconectadas" and "ecosistemas integrados".
- **Efficiency and Agility:** The underlying goal of many transformations is to reduce "burocracia" and "ineficiencia", increase the "rapidez y sentido de cambio", and enable faster decision-making.
- **OKR Implementation:** The implementation of OKRs (Objectives and Key Results) is a key process transformation to establish clear, measurable objectives and provide continuous feedback across the organisation.
- **Change Management and Cultural Adoption:** Acknowledged as a significant challenge, overcoming "resistencia al cambio" (resistance to change) and fostering a culture that embraces new ways of working, particularly with technology, is crucial. Joel Enriquez's "Talysist Bit" project is a "Business Management Plan Integral para alinear y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos", aiming to ensure that "más de 1500 personas trabajen con foco ritmo, y sentido común".

talisis is embarking on a holistic process transformation journey that touches every facet of its operations, from how it produces content and manages finances to how it interacts with students and organises its talent. The common thread across these transformations is a move towards greater standardisation, data-driven insights, automation, and integration, all while maintaining a human-centric approach to education.

Given the critical and recurring challenge of data inconsistency and lack of a unified data architecture, we could delve deeper into the specific strategies and investments talisis plans to make in this area.

o   ¿Se aplica alguna metodología para la Gestión del Cambio?

Based on the provided sources and our conversation history, talisis demonstrates an **emerging and evolving approach to change management**, rather than strictly adhering to a single, formally named methodology. While the term "gestión del cambio" (change management) is explicitly mentioned, particularly by Carlos Granados, the broader discourse reflects a proactive, adaptive, and iterative philosophy that seeks to embed change within the organisational culture and processes.

Here's a detailed breakdown of how change management is (or is intended to be) applied within talisis:

**1. Explicit Recognition and Strategic Intent:**

- **A Core Competency:** Carlos Granados, CIO, explicitly lists "Gestión del Cambio" as a crucial transversal competency required for the team to implement and manage the AI Agents infrastructure effectively. This indicates a recognition at the CIO level that change management is a distinct and necessary skill set for successful technological transformation.
- **Addressing Resistance:** Carlos Granados also identifies "Resistencia al cambio" (resistance to change) as a high-impact, high-probability risk for initial projects and proposes "Programa de gestión del cambio" (change management program) as a mitigation strategy. This suggests an intention to implement structured programs to address this common challenge.
- **Cultural Focus:** Julián Mendez (Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación) explicitly states that his area's mission is not just to operate change, but to design and activate it, and most importantly, **sustain it until it becomes culture**. He also highlights the "cultura de chain management" as something that talisis has "carecido mucho" and that changes are often "aventamos sin tener un change correcto". This points to a strong awareness of the need for structured change management and a desire to formalise it.

**2. Philosophy of Continuous Improvement and Adaptation:**

- **Mejora Continua (Continuous Improvement):** The concept of "mejora continua" is a fundamental principle, especially within the Quality area. Inge Ploennig (Director de Calidad) explicitly states, "Si no medimos, pues no hay forma de de mejorarlo y con base a las acciones correctivas estar integrando y estar puliendo nuestros procesos saber qué se funciona, qué no funciona, es como, pues, damos vida, ¿no? A este sistema". This systematic approach to measurement, feedback, and corrective actions is a cornerstone of iterative change.
- **Adaptability and Flexibility:** There is a strong emphasis on adaptability to external changes like market trends, technological advancements, social shifts, and regulations. Lilian Lozano (Digital Marketing Director) highlights "agilidad de cambiar programas de una manera modular" to respond to market needs, which implies a flexible approach to implementing changes in educational offerings. Juan Arenas (COO) also mentions adapting to shifts towards more hybrid and personalised education models.
- **Proactive Adjustment:** talisis aims to be proactive rather than reactive, using "foresight" to anticipate future needs and adapt programs accordingly. Humberto (Commercial Director) mentions the need to seek "nuevas tendencias que vayan evolucionando y ver cómo las podemos implementar" rather than just reacting to the market.

**3. Iterative and Experimental Approaches:**

- **Experimentation:** A culture of experimentation, including A/B testing and pilot projects, is promoted, particularly in marketing and product development, to learn and refine approaches. Fernando de Río (Chief Growth and Marketing Officer) states, "haremos de la innovación un hábito, no solamente una campaña busca un testeo constante de AB tests, pilotos".
- **Iterative Development (Vadir Methodology):** Román de León (Data Scientist) describes the "Vadir" methodology (Define Business Question, Formulate Hypothesis, Collect Data, Obtain Insights, Validate Solution), which is an iterative and data-driven approach to problem-solving and solution development. This systematic framework guides how his team approaches new solutions, inherently managing the change process for data-driven initiatives.
- **Phased Project Implementation:** Carlos Villa (Mobile Dev Lead) highlights a strategy of implementing projects in "fases pequeñas" (small phases) to allow for re-adjustment and flexibility if changes are needed, ensuring continuous progress and deliverables. This is a practical approach to managing large-scale transformations.

**4. Challenges in Current Implementation (and drivers for change management needs):**

- **Lack of Documented Processes:** A significant and recurring theme is the absence of clearly defined and documented processes. Alberto Sánchez (Director de Planeación) states, "ciertos procesos que no están documentados. Este, y ahorita estamos haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos". Alejandro Madrazo (Director Académico) highlights the current inefficiency due to frequent interruptions to "atender emergencias" because "no existen suficientes procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación". Marcos Samaniego (Director de Operaciones Académicas) also calls for a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos". The very act of documenting these processes is a foundational change management effort.
- **System Integration Issues:** Multiple leaders point to "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos". The lack of a "master data bien diseñado" leads to "descontrol y discrepancias". This technological fragmentation necessitates a significant change in how data is managed and integrated.
- **Cultural Resistance to Change:** Despite the aspirational commitment to innovation, the "resistencia cultural interna" is acknowledged as a challenge, especially regarding the adoption of online education. Paulina (Director UNID) notes the difficulty in "no querer aceptar los cambios". Inge Ploennig (Quality Director) observes that "mucha gente lo ha acordado de miedo" when it comes to technology adoption.
- **Communication Gaps and Misalignment:** Fernando de Río highlights the "desarticulación entre áreas clave" and misaligned priorities. Román de León notes, "falta mucha comunicación entre departamentos". Mariel Serrano (Corporate Reputation) mentions the challenge of achieving 100% alignment for annual objectives. The need for "gobernanza clara" and "líderes transversales" is underscored.
- **Time and Resource Constraints:** Román de León (Data Scientist) and Alberto Sánchez (Planning Director) highlight that a small team and constant project demands make it difficult to keep up with technological advancements and process standardisation. This impacts the capacity to proactively manage change.

**5. Emerging Methodologies and Tools as Change Enablers:**

- **OKR Implementation:** Julián Mendez indicates that the implementation of OKRs (Objectives and Key Results) is an ongoing process of "pulido" and "adaptación de la metodología". OKRs, by their nature, are a change management tool for aligning objectives and driving measurable results across the organisation.
- **Talysist Bit Project:** Joel Enriquez (CSO) describes "Talysist Bit" as a "Business Management Plan Integral para alinear y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos" and to ensure "más de 1500 personas trabajen con foco ritmo, y sentido común". This project, driven by technology, aims to create a shared "nervous system" for the organisation, fundamentally shaping how change is orchestrated and adopted.
- **Technology as an Enabler:** The use of AI, Cloud, and data analytics is seen as a key enabler for transforming processes, from automating manual tasks and improving decision-making to personalising the student experience and managing financial flows. These technological shifts inherently require substantial change management efforts.

While talisis does not appear to follow a rigid, single change management methodology like ADKAR or Kotter's 8-Step Process explicitly named by its interviewees, it is actively engaged in a strategic and multifaceted transformation. This transformation inherently involves extensive change management, characterised by a strong philosophy of continuous improvement, iterative development, a growing reliance on data and technology as enablers, and a clear awareness of the cultural and operational challenges that need to be addressed through a more formalised and integrated approach in the future. The organisation is "doing the work" of change management, even if the formal methodology is still being consolidated.

Given the critical and recurring challenge of data fragmentation and the desire for "una arquitectura de datos" and "un solo dato para la toma de decisiones", we could further analyse the specific investments, projects, and expected outcomes related to building a unified data architecture and how this will support broader organisational change.

o   ¿Qué presupuesto se tiene disponible para los esfuerzos de transformación?

Based on the provided sources and our conversation history, there is **no specific, quantifiable budget explicitly stated as available for "transformation efforts"** within talisis. The interviews frequently highlight the _need_ for investment and discuss resource constraints, rather than detailing a dedicated financial allocation for these efforts.

Here's a breakdown of what the sources do indicate regarding the financial aspects of transformation:

1. **Investment as a Strategic Imperative, not a Defined Budget:**
    
    - Many leaders identify the need for significant investment in technology and data infrastructure to achieve their long-term vision. Fernando de Río, for instance, explicitly states that resolving current technological limitations (fragmented platforms, dispersed data) "implies a strong investment and very capable people in data". Katherine, from marketing, also echoes the need for "tenerlas herramientas tecnológicas necesarias" and "una fuerte inversión" to address technology gaps.
    - The overall approach to systems, methodologies, and processes is consistently perceived as a "crucial investment" for talisis's future.
2. **Resource Constraints as an Obstacle:**
    
    - While financial budget for "transformation" is not specified, various interviewees point to **limited resources** – particularly in terms of _personnel_ and _time_ – as significant obstacles to advancing transformation projects.
    - Domingo Farias, from Capital Humano, identifies "recursos limitados" not primarily as economic, but in terms of "gente, hablo de tiempos, hablo de de de, o sea, de muchas cosas". He emphasises a "culture of doing more with less" and the challenge of how to achieve goals "con o sin recursos".
    - Similarly, Luis Ruiz, Manager of Software Development, explicitly states that "the time and current workload, the team is not large" is one of the main challenges, along with the "lack of trained personnel in technology". Paul Moch also highlights "limited time" and "lack of hands" to dedicate to design and strategy due to daily operational demands. Román de León, Data Scientist, notes that his small team struggles to keep up with constant project demands and new technology adoption.
    - Juliana Effting, Director of Online Education, lists "recursos y de estructura. Tanto recursos humanos como presupuesto, estructura organizacional" as obstacles.
3. **Explicit Requests for Budget or Resources:**
    
    - Román de León, Data Scientist, is one of the few who directly articulates a need for a specific budget allocation, stating: "I would like to have a budget for experimentation" and "a larger team since I only have one person under my charge". He further clarifies this, requesting "a budget to have one or two permanent people who could help us advance projects more agilely". This indicates that such a dedicated budget for his area's transformation-related efforts (experimentation, team expansion) is _not currently available_ or sufficient.
4. **Cost Considerations and Financial Health:**
    
    - The organisation is aware of the costs associated with technological shifts. Carlos Villa, Mobile Dev Lead, notes that migrating to the cloud "generates cost" and provides specific examples of monthly server costs, indicating a need to manage these expenses efficiently.
    - Alberto Sánchez's area focuses on ensuring that "the financial part is structured in a way that supports all internal and external needs. This includes CAPEX needs". He also seeks to manage debt and capital raising efficiently to align financial and strategic planning with market trends.
    - Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, prioritises "vigilar y propiciar que el flujo de efectivo mínimo se cubra", which implies a focus on short-term financial stability that might influence investment decisions for long-term transformation projects. She also highlights critical issues like the "lack of integration between systems" and the absence of a "master data well designed" as risks that imply a need for substantial investment to resolve.
5. **Efficiency and Cost Reduction through Technology:**
    
    - Paradoxically, technology is also seen as a means to _reduce_ costs and increase efficiency, rather than solely an expense. Inge Ploennig mentions using AI to produce content with "fewer resources, both financial and human". Álvaro García believes technology can "lower many training costs".

talisis deeply understands the strategic importance and necessity of investing in transformation (especially through technology and data infrastructure), the provided information does not disclose a specific budget allocated for these overarching efforts. Instead, it points to significant existing resource constraints (people, time), a recognition of the need for substantial future investment, and ongoing efforts to manage costs and seek funding for specific, high-impact projects.

Given the recurring theme of resource constraints, particularly in terms of personnel for key transformation projects, we could explore in more detail how talisis plans to address these staffing challenges. For example, we could look into whether there are plans for internal talent development, external recruitment strategies, or increased reliance on external consultants for these initiatives.

o   ¿Quién es el dueño de este presupuesto?

Based on the provided sources and our conversation history, the information does **not explicitly state who the specific owner is for a "transformation budget"**. While the question "Who is the owner of this budget?" is listed in the provided excerpts under the "Transformation and Change Management" section, no direct answer is supplied for this query.

However, the interviews offer insights into how financial resources are managed and allocated, which can be inferred to cover various initiatives, including transformation efforts:

1. **Distributed Financial Oversight:**
    
    - **Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance**, plays a central role in managing the company's financial health. Her responsibilities include "asegurar la precisión de las operaciones contables y financieras para la toma de decisiones, liderar la planificación presupuestaria el análisis de indicadores clave para mejorar la eficiencia de rentabilidad, cumplir con las regulaciones fiscales y gestionar riesgos proactivamente, manteniendo controles internos robustos, fomentar el desarrollo profesional del equipo, y promover la cultura talisis". She explicitly states her area "contribuye buscando que el gasto sea rentable y productivo y busca maximizar los recursos que son escasos para para lograr este sueño". She also highlights the need to "vigilar y propiciar que el flujo de efectivo mínimo se cubra" and manage the company's debt and capital raising. While her role is critical in financial planning and resource allocation, the sources do not designate her as the sole "owner" of a dedicated transformation budget.
    - **Alberto Sánchez, Director de Planeación**, is also deeply involved in "planeación estratégica y financiera". His role includes "organizar de manera más eficiente el los temas hacia dónde asignamos los recursos, en qué rubro de costos, en qué rubro de gastos". He notes the importance of "colaboración constante con las áreas es clave para evaluar y administrar proyectos" and "mantener alineación directa con el CEO para asegurar coherencia estratégica" regarding financial aspects. This indicates that financial allocation for strategic initiatives, including those related to transformation, is a collaborative and high-level executive decision.
    - **Carlos Granados, CIO**, mentions that "decisiones clave se tomarán a través de comités técnicos y de gobernanza," which operate at strategic (monthly), tactical (fortnightly), and operational (weekly) levels, involving "C-Level + Directores" for strategic decisions. This suggests a collective approach to major investment and project decisions, rather than a single budget owner.
2. **Focus on Resource Constraints Beyond Purely Financial Budget:**
    
    - Several interviewees highlight that the limitations affecting transformation efforts are often related to **resources beyond just money**. Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, explicitly states that when he refers to "recursos limitados," he means "no solamente hablo de económicos, hablo de gente, hablo de tiempos, hablo de de de, o sea, de muchas cosas". He notes a "culture of doing more with less".
    - Similarly, Luis Ruiz, Gerente de desarrollo de software, identifies "el tiempo y la carga de trabajo actual, el equipo no es grande" as a primary obstacle, along with "no tener dentro de la organización suficientes personas capacitadas en en tecnología". Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning, also mentions "tiempo, no cuento con el tiempo necesario para poder centrarme en espacios de diseño... y la falta de manos". This suggests that while financial considerations are present, the challenge of securing and allocating human capital and time is equally, if not more, pressing in the context of transformation.
3. **Specific Budget Requests but No Overarching Fund:**
    
    - Román de León, Data Scientist, is one of the few who articulates a direct need for a specific budget, stating: "quisiera tener un presupuesto para experimentación" and "un presupuesto para tener una o 2 personas de planta que nos pudieran ayudar a avanzar de manera más ágil en los proyectos". This direct request implies that such dedicated and independently managed budgets for _his_ specific transformation-related initiatives are not readily available or are insufficient, necessitating explicit allocation.

talisis clearly recognises the need for significant investment to drive transformation, particularly in technology and data infrastructure, the sources do not identify a single "owner" of a dedicated "transformation budget." Instead, financial oversight and resource allocation appear to be integrated into broader strategic and operational planning, managed collaboratively by various leadership roles within Finance, Planning, and executive committees. The challenges faced often relate more to the availability of time, skilled personnel, and process clarity than solely to a lack of earmarked financial funds for transformation.

Given the recurring theme of shared responsibility and the challenges in aligning priorities across departments, a deeper analysis into talisis's current governance structure for cross-functional strategic projects might be beneficial. This could explore the effectiveness of existing committees, communication protocols, and accountability frameworks in enabling smooth execution of transformation initiatives.

o   ¿Qué porcentaje de los ejecutivos consideran conveniente entrar a un proceso de transformación en la organización y de qué niveles son?

Based on the provided sources and our conversation history, it is evident that a remarkably high percentage of the interviewed executives consider it not merely convenient, but **essential and imperative** to engage in a comprehensive transformation process within talisis. The discussions from nearly all interviewees, spanning various levels and departments, underscore a deep-seated belief in the necessity of transformation for the organisation's future, competitiveness, and mission fulfillment.

While no explicit numerical percentage is provided in the sources stating how many executives consider transformation "convenient," the collective sentiment and detailed strategic plans articulated by 19 out of 20 interviewed leaders (Angel Casan's section states "No se cuenta con información") strongly suggest that **virtually 100% of the interviewed executives** view transformation as critical.

The executives discussing and leading these transformation efforts are from various levels of the organisation, predominantly in strategic and senior management roles:

**I. Executive and C-Level Leadership:**

- **Alberto Sánchez, Director de Planeación**: Actively seeks to modernise and automate financial planning and project management, moving away from manual, artisanal processes through digital tools. His role involves aligning strategic and financial planning for the organisation's future.
- **Alejandro Madrazo, Director Académico**: Views his area as the "epicenter of innovation" for educational design and implementation, aimed at rethinking and reimagining the institutional organisation of education. He explicitly states talisis seeks to "repensar y re imaginar las formas de organización institucional de la educación en México y en el mundo".
- **Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director**: Foresees talisis in 2035 being "muy distinto" from its current state, with a profound evolution in products, methods, and organisation, driven by AI and adaptive learning processes. His team focuses on transforming talent in organisations.
- **Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director**: Stresses her area's role in helping leaders "evaluar, identificar y desarrollar a sus equipos," which is fundamental for talent transformation and contributes to "transformar la vida de las personas".
- **Carlos Granados, CIO**: Explicitly states that the project to implement AI agents "representa una transformación fundamental en el modelo educativo de talisis" with the goal of creating an "ecosistema educativo inteligente, adaptativo e inclusivo".
- **Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff**: Emphasises fostering a "cultura de desarrollo" and a "cultura con una disciplina de altos altas estándares". He highlights the need to "adoptar mejor la tecnología y los avances tecnológicos inteligencia artificial" and addresses the need for "change management".
- **Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer**: Articulates a vision where talisis redefines access, quality, and personalisation of learning through a "estrategia de transformación que combine todo el tema de agilidad operativa, inteligencia de mercado, innovación". He explicitly states his team must "transformarse" to keep pace with industry changes.
- **Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales**: Aims for talisis to be "el grupo educativo de mayor alcance y accesibilidad en México," which requires significant expansion and process improvement, including sales automation.
- **Inge Ploennig, Directora de Calidad y Acreditación Académica**: Her area focuses on continuous improvement and adapting to new technologies like AI for content creation. She notes that "talisis nada más va caminando en este proceso de transformación" and that failing to integrate technology would mean "nos quedamos atrás".
- **Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer (CSO) y Director de Asuntos Estratégicos y Corporativos**: His work is centered on "construir un legado estratégico" and he describes himself as a "fundador de cultura organizacional," leading "programas de transformación estratégica".
- **Juan Arenas, Chief Operations Officer**: His area's core contribution is to "hacer que sucedan las cosas", continuously "mejorando e innovando los procesos y servicios", and planning for a migration towards online education.
- **Juliana Effting, Directora de Educación Online**: Identifies her area as responsible for the core operation of online products, needing "las personas, las herramientas, los procesos, los sistemas, todos muy homologados y muy listos para garantizar la entrega". She explicitly states talisis is "caminando en este proceso de transformación" and highlights the need for leaders to communicate clearly about the "transformación digital que estamos haciendo y que sí o sí vamos a hacer".
- **Katherine Romero, Chief Marketing Officer**: Views marketing as "una pieza clave para materializar la visión de talisis hacia el 2035," translating vision into "posicionamiento y acción". She explicitly highlights "transformación de competencias" as a key trend and concludes her section by stating, "El marketing de talisis está listo para ser ese motor de de transformación".
- **Lilian Adalid, Chief Marketing Officer**: Is inspired by talisis's purpose to "transformar comunidades a través de las personas". She actively discusses the impact of AI and automation in making processes more efficient and strategic.
- **Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration & Finance**: Aims for financial decisions to "habilitar el crecimiento de los alumnos" and maximise "recursos que son escasos". Her area acts as an "Enabler" for "multicanal y multiproducto" growth through administrative processes and financial support.
- **Marcos Samaniego, Director de Operaciones Académicas**: Aims to "consolidar un modelo educativo claro" and "aumentar la calidad educativa". He is also focused on adapting to "personalización de contenidos a través de la inteligencia artificial" and implementing solutions more rapidly.
- **Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, Strategic Communication & Business Intelligence**: Seeks to position talisis as a "ecosistema educativo de vanguardia" and reflects on its mission to "transformar vidas". She describes "Talysist Bit" as a "proyecto transversal" and a "Business Management Plan Integral para alinear y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos".
- **Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning**: His role is to design "procesos, modelos, [y] políticas" to consolidate a clear and high-quality educational model. He discusses "repensar profundamente el modelo educativo" and adapting to new trends like microcredentials and hybrid models.
- **Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional en Universidad Interamericana para el Desarrollo**: Focuses on "formando estudiantes que tengan el conocimiento y las habilidades necesarias para desenvolverse profesionalmente en este mundo que es continuamente cambiando," which requires continuous adaptation and new teaching methodologies. She also mentions the need for constant training and new learning for her team to adapt to globalised needs.

**II. Manager and Specialist Level:**

- **Juan Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación**: Explicitly states that his area's mission is to "diseñar y activar" change and "sostenerlo hasta que podamos convertir en en cultura". He sees technology as a "catalizador de transformación digital" and talks about how the organisation has "madurado" significantly in its data-driven approach.
- **Luis Ruiz, Gerente de desarrollo de software**: Prioritises building a robust data architecture and implementing AI solutions to "transformarán tus procesos y responsabilidades" and improve educational quality.
- **Román de León, Data Scientist**: His area aims to "transformar la manera en la que opera el negocio" by providing innovative solutions and insights. He seeks a budget for "experimentación" and a larger team to "avanzar de manera más ágil en los proyectos" related to transformation.

The overwhelming evidence from the interviews indicates that the notion of "transformation" is deeply embedded in the strategic thinking and daily operations of talisis's leadership. It is not a matter of whether it is "convenient" to enter a transformation process, but rather a universal recognition of its necessity. Nearly every interviewed executive, from the C-suite to key management and specialist roles, articulates initiatives, challenges, and aspirations directly related to organisational, technological, academic, and cultural transformation.

Therefore, it can be concluded that **virtually 100% of the interviewed executives across all strategic and operational levels demonstrate a clear conviction and commitment to the ongoing transformation process** within talisis. They perceive it as fundamental for ensuring future growth, efficiency, and the fulfillment of the company's core mission to democratise and improve education.

Given this pervasive understanding and commitment to transformation, the next logical area of analysis could be to delve into the _specific challenges_ these executives foresee or are currently experiencing in executing these transformation initiatives, particularly focusing on how these challenges differ or overlap across various departments and levels. This could inform a more targeted approach to resource allocation and strategic support.
### IX. Gestión de la Capacidad y el Crecimiento

o   ¿Se sigue algún proceso de Planeación Estratégica?
Yes, talisis follows a comprehensive strategic planning process. This process is multi-faceted, highly integrated, and deeply rooted in the organisation's overarching strategic vision, known as the "Architecture of Horizons". It involves a continuous cycle of strategic foresight, market analysis, cultural alignment, and iterative measurement, underpinned by a commitment to data-driven decision-making and technological enablement.

Here is a detailed breakdown of the strategic planning process at talisis:

**I. Overarching Strategic Framework: The "Architecture of Horizons" (2025-2035)** The entire strategic planning at talisis is anchored by a clear, long-term vision to achieve significant impact in education by 2035. This "Architecture of Horizons" serves as the ultimate guiding principle for all planning and deployment efforts, ensuring that high-level strategic aspirations are cohesive and directed towards a common purpose.

**II. Strategic Planning and Objective Setting**

1. **Market Intelligence and Foresight:**
    
    - Strategic planning is heavily "centrada en en lo que el mercado requiere en las tendencias de mercado". This involves meticulous internal analysis to identify "qué programas son los que se están buscando o cursos los que están buscando, qué modalidades son las que está buscando el mercado, [y] por medio de qué canales de venta".
    - External monitoring is also crucial, including keeping an eye on "oportunidades que hay en el mercado" such as potential mergers and acquisitions.
    - Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, emphasizes "impulsando una visión clara del mercado, del estudiante del futuro", indicating a proactive approach to understanding evolving demands. Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, explicitly anticipates that talisis in 2035 "va a ser muy distinto" in terms of products, methods, and organisation, driven by AI and adaptive learning processes, showcasing a strong foresight component in planning.
2. **Leadership Involvement and Vision Setting:**
    
    - Strategic initiatives, such as the implementation of AI agents, are "promovido desde la dirección general y manejado como un proyecto institucional, para que esté apalancado por todos los directivos de la compañía". This top-down promotion ensures broad buy-in and alignment.
    - Joel Enriquez, Chief Strategy Officer, describes his role as central to "construir un legado estratégico," designing "estructuras que sobrevivan más allá de las modas o las circunstancias de hoy". He views his area as a catalyst for "programas de transformación estratégica".
    - Paul Moch, Vice President for Teaching & Learning, focuses on designing "procesos, modelos, [y] políticas" to "consolidar un modelo educativo claro" and "aumentar la calidad educativa".
3. **Objective and Key Results (OKRs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs):**
    
    - talisis has a clear intention to implement and refine OKRs and KPIs across various functions to translate strategic vision into measurable outcomes.
    - Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, details how the "talisis Way" incorporates "13 strategic axes" that "se desprenden directamente de la misión," leading to strategic projects and plans executed at the campus level, all measured by OKRs and KPIs.
    - Julián Mendez, Gerente de Planeación Operativa y Transformación, confirms that "el sistema de los OKRs... se están implementando, nos estamos los estamos puliendo, estamos adaptando la metodología" to ensure clear, measurable objectives across the organisation.
    - Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, measures the success of strategic initiatives through "resultados estratégicos de la compañía," including "el pilar de crecimiento, en el pilar de de vida estudiantil, de de administración eficiente," along with "engagement" and "calidad de vida del colaborador".
4. **Budgeting and Investment Justification:**
    
    - Alberto Sánchez, Director de Planeación, details how financial planning involves structuring resources, managing CAPEX, and efficiently allocating funds to align with strategic goals.
    - Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration & Finance, includes "liderar la planificación presupuestaria el análisis de indicadores clave para mejorar la eficiencia de rentabilidad" as a core part of her department's mission.
    - Investments are justified through rigorous "business cases" and "análisis de productividad, costo beneficio".

**III. Deployment and Alignment of Objectives**

1. **Formal Governance Structures:**
    
    - Carlos Granados, CIO, explicitly states that "decisiones clave se tomarán a través de comités técnicos y de gobernanza," structured into strategic (C-Level, monthly), tactical (Project Leaders, fortnightly), and operational (Technical teams, weekly) levels. This tiered approach ensures strategic alignment, agility, and transparency.
    - Marcos Samaniego, Director of Academic Operations, describes participation in committees to understand the origin and maturation of alliances, ensuring their effective implementation in campuses.
2. **Regular Review and Communication Rituals:**
    
    - Information is systematically cascaded from top management (C-level) through various "rituales," including "connections," "conventions," and "town halls," to ensure clarity and alignment across the organisation.
    - Mariel Serrano's "Talysist Bit" project serves as a "Business Management Plan Integral para alinear y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos," acting as a rhythm for the entire company's communication and actions.
3. **Process Standardisation and Documentation:**
    
    - There is a recognized need to formalise and document processes. Alberto Sánchez notes that "ciertos procesos que no están documentados" are currently being documented, with an emphasis on leaders ensuring their compliance.
    - Alejandro Madrazo, Director Académico, stresses the importance of "procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación" and avoid emergencies.
    - Marcos Samaniego calls for a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos" to centralise knowledge and ensure consistent communication.

**IV. Cultural Integration and Continuous Improvement**

1. **"talisis Way" as a Cultural Driver:**
    
    - The "talisis Way" is a foundational cultural framework that guides the organisation's strategic direction and operational methodology. It is viewed as integral to fostering a "High-Performance Culture," where leaders embody and instil desired attitudes and behaviours, aiming for "Alineación Cultural Total" where "Cada colaborador viviendo los principios TALISIS".
    - Julián Mendez stresses making people "vivir" the "cultural ADN" of talisis, embracing a data-driven approach and continuous evolution.
2. **Philosophy of Continuous Improvement and Adaptation:**
    
    - "Mejora continua" is a fundamental principle. Inge Ploennig states, "Si no medimos, pues no hay forma de de mejorarlo y con base a las acciones correctivas estar integrando y estar puliendo nuestros procesos".
    - There is a strong emphasis on adaptability to external changes, including market trends, technological advancements, social shifts, and regulations. Lilian Adalid highlights the "agilidad de cambiar programas de una manera modular" to respond swiftly to market needs.
    - Experimentation, including A/B testing and pilot projects (e.g., chatbots), is promoted in areas like marketing and product development to learn and refine approaches. Román de León's team actively uses the "Vadir" methodology for iterative and data-driven problem-solving and solution development, from defining a business question to validating solutions with users.

talisis clearly has a defined strategic planning process, which is comprehensive and deeply integrated into its vision, culture, and operations. While there are ongoing efforts to refine and mature its application across all levels, the strategic intent and foundational elements are well-established.

To further enhance the understanding of this process, it would be beneficial to investigate how talisis assesses the _effectiveness_ of its strategic deployment. This could involve exploring the mechanisms in place for capturing feedback on strategic initiatives from operational teams, and how this feedback loop directly influences future adjustments to strategic plans and objectives.

o   ¿Se tiene alguna función de Performance Management?

Based on the provided sources, talisis does not explicitly state that it has a singular, formally designated "Performance Management function" as a standalone department or operational unit [All sources]. However, it is abundantly clear that the principles and practices of performance management are deeply embedded and actively pursued across various strategic, operational, and human capital dimensions of the organisation, constituting a robust, albeit evolving, system of performance management.

Here's a detailed breakdown of how performance management is conducted within talisis:

**I. Strategic Framework and Objective Setting (The 'What')**

1. **Strategic Alignment via "Architecture of Horizons" and "talisis Way"**: The entire organisation's efforts are guided by a long-term vision, the "Architecture of Horizons" (2025-2035). This overarching vision is translated through the "talisis Way," which defines the company's core principles and identity, serving as a foundational framework for strategic direction and operational methodology. This ensures that individual and team performance aligns with broader organisational goals.
2. **OKR and KPI Implementation and Refinement**: talisis is actively implementing and refining its Objectives and Key Results (OKRs) and Key Performance Indicators (KPIs) methodology.
    - **Cascading Objectives**: Strategic axes derived directly from the mission are cascaded down, leading to strategic projects and plans executed at the campus level, all measured by OKRs and KPIs.
    - **Continuous Refinement**: Julián Mendez (Manager of Operational Planning and Transformation) confirms that the OKR system is "being implemented, we are polishing it, we are adapting the methodology" to ensure clear, measurable objectives across the organisation. This refinement includes ensuring clear, measurable objectives and facilitating continuous feedback.
    - **Specific Indicators**: Various leaders articulate specific performance indicators for their areas:
        - **Financial**: Marcela Valdez (Director of Administration & Finance) focuses on "efficiency and profitability", using indicators like "days of accounts receivable," "newly enrolled students (NIs)," and "re-enrolled NIs". Alberto Sánchez (Director of Planning) monitors debt, capital raising, and efficient resource allocation.
        - **Growth & Marketing**: Fernando de Río (Chief Growth & Marketing Officer) uses a comprehensive set including "cost of acquisition per student," "conversion rate per channel," "NPS," and "retention rate". Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) tracks new center openings, portfolio growth, sales, and sales force productivity. Lilian Adalid (Chief Marketing Officer) also mentions CPL, conversion rate, engagement, and CTR.
        - **Academic & Student Experience**: Inge Ploennig (Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation) links performance to institutional mission, regularly reviewing 14 key indicators. Alejandro Madrazo (Academic Director) uses "NPS docente, cumplimiento de promesa de valor, tamaño de generación". Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) measures "development of 21st-century skills," "educational quality," and "student employability". Marcos Samaniego (Director of Academic Operations) implements dashboards for automatic measurements of key operational processes.
        - **Human Capital**: Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) measures success through "strategic results of the company" across pillars like growth, student life, and efficient administration, alongside "engagement," "quality of life of the collaborator," and "NPS of managers". Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) focuses on "commercial productivity" and "percentage of retention of key talent".
        - **Technology & Data**: Carlos Granados (CIO) measures adoption, data quality, and satisfaction (NPS) for AI projects. Román de León (Data Scientist) tracks "agility in decision-making," "AI adoption in processes," and "reduction of student desertion risk".

**II. Performance Monitoring and Review (The 'How')**

1. **Regular Review Rituals**: talisis uses structured "rituals" for communication and review. These include "connections," "conventions," and "town halls" that cascade information from top management (C-level) downwards, ensuring clarity and alignment.
2. **Tiered Governance Committees**: Key decisions are made through technical and governance committees structured at strategic (monthly), tactical (fortnightly), and operational (weekly) levels. These forums formalise decisions and review progress. Marcos Samaniego also describes participation in committees to understand alliances and ensure their effective implementation, including measuring results.
3. **Data-Driven Decision Making**: There is a strong aspiration and ongoing effort to shift towards data-driven decision-making. Many interviewees express a desire for "more accurate data for faster decision-making". Initiatives include developing centralised dashboards and automatic, real-time measurements. Román de León's team designs predictive algorithms and dashboards to support decision-making. Carlos Granados is implementing a system to track app usage and collect user ratings and comments to analyse sentiment and improve user experience.
4. **Continuous Improvement Cycles**: Inge Ploennig explicitly states that "if we don't measure, there's no way to improve it," and emphasizes "constantly measuring" to integrate corrective actions and refine processes. This reflects a commitment to continuous improvement as a core part of performance management.

**III. Talent Development and Culture (The 'Who')**

1. **High-Performance Culture**: Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) champions a "High-Performance Culture" as a primary strategic initiative. This involves setting high standards, rigorously attracting and retaining the "best fit" talent, and embedding a culture of continuous development into every leader's DNA.
2. **Professional Development**: talisis places a significant emphasis on the continuous professional and personal development of its employees.
    - **Identifying Opportunities**: Leaders like Humberto Salazar (Head of Sales) focus on identifying talent, their strengths and weaknesses, and the competencies needed for their next level. Domingo Farias aims to create a "map" of talent to strategically place top performers in key projects.
    - **Formal and Informal Training**: The organisation fosters a culture of ongoing learning, from adopting new technologies and methodologies to providing feedback and coaching. Lilian Adalid emphasizes "LifeLong Learning".
    - **Succession Planning**: Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) explicitly mentions the development of "key talent" and "replacement cards for our executives" as a long-term project.
3. **Managerial Accountability**: Leaders are expected to embody and instil desired attitudes and behaviours, and to manage their teams with clarity and support. Juan Arenas (Chief Operations Officer) highlights his role in motivating and inspiring his team to achieve objectives.
4. **Feedback and Communication**: Feedback is seen as crucial for growth and alignment. Carlos Granados actively gives constructive feedback to his team. Mariel Serrano promotes "clear, open, and empathetic communication" and "constructive honesty" (candor) to resolve conflicts and foster alignment.

**IV. Challenges and Areas for Improvement**

Despite these efforts, interviewees highlight several areas for enhancement:

- **Process Standardisation and Documentation**: Many processes are not yet fully documented, leading to inefficiencies and a lack of consistency. There is a desire for a central repository of documented processes.
- **System Integration**: Lack of integration between different platforms (e.g., SAP and Banner) leads to data inconsistencies, manual workarounds, and limits the ability to gain a holistic view of performance and operations.
- **Transversal Governance and Collaboration**: Some leaders note a "disarticulation between key areas" and a lack of clear governance for transversal projects, which can impede collaboration and shared purpose.
- **Data Quality and Accessibility**: While the importance of data is recognised, challenges remain in collecting high-quality, real-time data and making it easily accessible for all decision-makers.
- **Cultural Adaptation to Technology**: There is a need to overcome resistance or fear towards new technologies, fostering an agile and experimental mindset across the organisation.

talisis may not have a dedicated "Performance Management function" as a separate entity, it operates with a comprehensive and intentionally designed performance management _system_. This system integrates strategic planning, objective setting (OKRs/KPIs), regular performance monitoring and review, a strong focus on talent development and a high-performance culture, and a commitment to continuous improvement. The organisation is actively working to mature and formalise these processes, particularly through increased standardisation, system integration, and data-driven approaches.

Nonetheless, to further understand the maturity of performance management at talisis, it would be beneficial to investigate the specific tools or platforms used for performance reviews, goal tracking, and employee development plans. This could reveal the level of automation and integration supporting these processes beyond general discussions of OKRs and data.

o   ¿Se tiene alguna metodología para la Planeación de la Capacidad?

talisis does not explicitly state that it has a formal, defined "methodology for Capacity Planning" within the provided sources. The query regarding this specific methodology is listed in the general Tali responses document, but no corresponding answer is provided.

However, the interviews reveal a strong underlying focus on various aspects of capacity management, resource optimisation, and strategic planning that implicitly address capacity. There is a clear recognition of existing challenges and aspirations to develop more sophisticated, data-driven approaches to manage the organisation's capacity across its different dimensions:

**1. Recognition of Capacity-Related Challenges:**

- **Human Capital:** Several leaders highlight constraints related to the availability and allocation of personnel. Challenges include a "lack of sufficient staff", difficulties in "recruiting talent" with recruitment processes taking "50 or 40-odd days" from request to hiring, and the burden of small team sizes coupled with high workloads. The high rotation rate of advisors is also noted as an area for improvement.
- **Time and Resources:** There is a common sentiment that time and various resources (beyond just financial) are limited, hindering strategic design and project implementation.
- **Technological Infrastructure:** Limitations in integrated systems and data architecture are identified as significant obstacles to efficient management and analysis, which are foundational for effective capacity planning. Overburdened operational teams due to rapid expansion without proper structuring of staff and attention systems are also a concern.

**2. Strategic Focus on Efficiency and Optimisation:**

- **Resource Allocation:** Leaders, such as Alberto Sánchez (Planning Director), emphasize the need to "efficiently manage debt, capital raising, and allocate resources more efficiently" and "optimise the efficient distribution of costs and expenses using technology". Marcela Valdez (Administration & Finance Director) also highlights "liderar la planificación presupuestaria el análisis de indicadores clave para mejorar la eficiencia de rentabilidad" as part of her department's mission.
- **Automation:** A recurring theme is the desire and ongoing effort to automate manual processes to free up human capacity for higher-value, strategic tasks. Julián Mendez (Operational Planning & Transformation) notes that "certain processes that are very manual... should already be automated".
- **Economies of Scale:** Marcela Valdez explicitly aims for "incremental productivity" to "serve more students with economies of scale", indicating a goal to maximise output from existing or strategically expanded resources.

**3. Data-Driven Decision-Making as a Key Enabler:**

- A pervasive need for more accurate, real-time, and integrated data is expressed across various departments. This is crucial for "faster decision-making", which directly impacts the agility of capacity adjustments and planning. Carlos Granados (CIO) envisions AI agents as a "bridge that promotes efficient communication and data-driven decision-making".
- There's an aspiration to shift from merely collecting information to effectively analysing it to inform decisions. Inge Ploennig (Quality and Accreditation) points out that they "spend more time collecting information than analysing it", and hopes technology will reverse this.

**4. Specific Initiatives and Aspirations Related to Capacity:**

- **Student and Academic Operations Capacity:**
    - Expansion plans are a direct form of capacity increase, such as "expanding URL regionally" and "opening new learning centres" and "new portfolios". Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations Director) mentions "ampliar mucho más la cobertura".
    - There is a focus on managing "cohort size" ("tamaño de generación") as a key indicator.
    - Román de León (Data Scientist) outlines a project idea to "dimension teachers, classrooms, and schedules based on the probable number of students who will enrol, based on demand and the availability of physical infrastructure" using an algorithm. This is the most direct articulation of an **algorithmic approach to capacity planning** for academic resources.
    - Implementing a "unique centre for procedures" for students to track their academic life aims to streamline processes and improve operational capacity for student support.
- **Human Capital Capacity:**
    - Domingo Farias (Chief of Staff) describes efforts to "identify and attract the best talent to have a high-performance culture", including developing a "talent map" to strategically place top performers in key projects.
    - Amalia Ortega (HRBP Director) focuses on "commercial productivity" and "retention of key talent" as long-term projects, including "replacement cards for our executives".
    - The goal is to free up human capacity from "manual processes" so that it can be redirected to "culture, strategy redesign, productivity results and motivating teams".
    - AI is envisioned to accelerate sales force productivity by answering daily doubts and managing high-rotation positions like sales advisors by automating recruitment processes.
- **Technological Capacity:**
    - AI and cloud technology are seen as crucial for scaling operations and services, with an AI agent potentially handling "several prospects at once" to increase sales capacity.
    - Paul Moch (VP Teaching & Learning) highlights technology's role in "increasing and enhancing both learning and teaching in both spaces", and Marcos Samaniego (Academic Operations Director) expects technology to automate measurements and information collection to turn roles into "mentors" and "managers".
    - Building a "data architecture" to collect comprehensive information about students, teachers, and administrators is a priority project.
    - There is an aim to have a "digital brain" or "talisis Mind" that "integrates" data analysis, algorithmic personalisation, predictive recommendations, and intelligent coordination across all 190 educational centres.

talisis does not explicitly reference a single, formal "methodology for Capacity Planning," it is actively engaged in numerous initiatives that constitute a robust, albeit evolving, system for managing and optimising its human, financial, operational, and technological capacities. These efforts are heavily reliant on leveraging technology (especially AI and Cloud) and data-driven insights to achieve greater efficiency, scalability, and strategic alignment in its educational mission. The organisation is moving towards a more automated and integrated approach to understand demand, allocate resources, and measure performance across all its operations.

To further understand how capacity is managed, it would be beneficial to investigate if talisis utilises specific software tools or dashboards for real-time monitoring of key operational capacities (e.g., student-teacher ratios, classroom utilisation, platform scalability metrics) and how these insights directly translate into actionable capacity adjustment plans beyond aspirational goals.

o   ¿Cómo se lleva a cabo el ejercicio de presupuesto para el Capex y el Opex?

While the provided sources do not explicitly detail a formal, step-by-step methodology for how talisis carries out its Capex and Opex budgeting exercise, various interviews offer insights into the financial planning, resource allocation, and investment justification processes.

**Overall Approach to Financial Planning and Resource Allocation:**

talisis approaches financial planning and resource allocation with a strong focus on aligning with market trends and strategic objectives. The Planning and Finance areas are central to this. Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, highlights his area's role in structuring finances, ensuring economic resources, maintaining a healthy balance sheet and cash flow, and efficiently managing debt and capital raising. Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, underscores her department's mission to "ensure the accuracy of accounting and financial operations for decision-making, lead budget planning, [and] analyze key indicators to improve efficiency and profitability". Her area actively contributes by providing financial information and analysis, ensuring responsible use of economic resources, and offering internal "coaching or consulting" on productivity and cost-benefit analysis for organisational decisions.

**Budgeting and Forecasting:**

The budgeting process involves close collaboration and ongoing communication with internal stakeholders. Alberto Sánchez indicates a daily interaction with operations for "budget control" and "when we make the budget and when we make the forecast". His team also collaborates with Human Resources for payroll costs, and with Marketing and Sales to forecast income, costs, and expenses, assessing the ratio of marketing and sales spending against new income. This suggests a continuous and cross-functional effort in preparing and managing the budget.

**Investment Justification (Capex):**

For investments, particularly those related to Capex (capital expenditure), there is an emphasis on project evaluation. Alberto Sánchez notes that communication and collaboration with all areas are "constant" because "they are the ones who know what projects they have in mind, what's coming, and we need to manage all the funds, we need to do the project evaluation, we need to present it". This implies a process where proposed projects from various departments are assessed financially before approval and allocation of funds. For technology-related investments, Carlos Granados, CIO, specifies that decisions to integrate new technologies are based on criteria such as "viability técnica, compatibilidad con infraestructura existente y costos-beneficios". He explicitly mentions "TCO (Costo Total de Propiedad)" and "ROI esperado" as key elements in the "Análisis Económico" for these evaluations.

**Opex Management and Efficiency:**

Beyond just budgeting, there is a strong drive towards optimising operational expenses. Alberto Sánchez's area aims to "efficientar los costos y gastos lo más posible" and specifically to "optimizar la distribución eficiente de costos y gastos usando tecnología, más que solo reducirlos". Marcela Valdez's mission also involves improving "efficiency and profitability". This suggests that Opex management is not merely about cost cutting but about strategic allocation to maximise value and achieve economies of scale, such as her goal to serve "more students with economies of scale".

**Role of Data and Technology:**

There is a clear aspiration to leverage technology and data for more agile and precise financial management. Román de León, Data Scientist, proposes a project to "optimizar el presupuesto disponible" using an "algoritmo" based on "necesidades reales" and "retroalimentación" from students, aiming to "asignar el presupuesto de manera más ágil". This indicates a move towards a data-driven, potentially automated, approach to budget allocation. Julián Mendez mentions that "todo el tema de de presupuesto, todo el tema de business cases, es decir, de proyectos, este, que estuviera un poco más automatizado, más moderno, menos artesanal, menos uso de Excel, menos manual". Marcela Valdez also anticipates AI will "simplify the steps we follow to do our daily activity, from reconciliations... to the analysis of information and the understanding of the variables that impact the profitability of educational institutions". Carlos Granados envisions AI as an ally for improving forecasts and budgets.

**Challenges and Considerations:**

Several challenges hinder a perfectly streamlined budgeting and investment process:

- **Resource Constraints:** Leaders across the organisation, including Alberto Sánchez, acknowledge "recursos limitados" that encompass not just financial resources but also "gente, ... tiempos, ... procesos, recurso en herramientas". Luis Ruiz, for example, points to "el tiempo y la carga de trabajo actual" and the "falta de personal capacitado" as major obstacles.
- **Short-term vs. Long-term Focus:** Marcela Valdez highlights the critical short-term challenge of managing cash flow and accounts receivable, which can necessitate choosing immediate financial stability over potentially prosperous long-term projects.
- **Data and System Integration:** A recurring issue is the lack of integrated systems and unreliable data. Marcela Valdez mentions "la falta de integración entre sistemas, como el SAP y el Core Banner, genera controles abiertos y riesgos de descontrol", hindering accurate financial information. Inge Ploennig also states that they "spend more time collecting information than analysing it". Román de León also points out "inconsistencias de datos" due to "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada".
- **Documentation and Clarity:** Alberto Sánchez explicitly states that "ciertos procesos que no están documentados" are currently being addressed through documentation efforts. Alejandro Madrazo also points out the absence of "suficientes procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación".

While a prescriptive methodology for Capex and Opex budgeting is not explicitly detailed, talisis employs a strategic, cross-functional approach involving financial planning, ongoing budget control, and project-based investment evaluation. The organisation is actively seeking to enhance these processes through technology and data-driven insights, despite facing challenges related to resource limitations, data integration, and the balance between short-term demands and long-term strategic investments.

To gain a clearer understanding of the budgeting process, it would be beneficial to inquire if talisis uses a specific annual or semi-annual budgeting cycle, and what formal approval stages (e.g., departmental, executive, board) are required for Capex and Opex proposals once they have been evaluated.

o   ¿Cómo se justifican las inversiones que se quieren realizar? (Business Case)

talisis justifies its investments through a multi-faceted approach that combines strategic alignment, rigorous financial analysis, cross-functional collaboration, and an increasing drive towards data-driven and automated evaluation processes. The organisation views methodologies, processes, and systems as crucial investments rather than mere expenses, often justifying them by highlighting the high costs and inefficiencies incurred from a lack of proper systems or standardised procedures.

Here's a detailed breakdown of how investments are justified:

1. **Strategic Alignment and Market Focus:** Investments are primarily justified by their alignment with talisis's strategic objectives and market trends. Alberto Sánchez, Director of Planning, states that financial planning must be "centrada en lo que el mercado requiere en las tendencias de mercado" and structured to support all CAPEX needs to achieve long-term objectives. This ensures that resource allocation is in line with the company's strategic direction. Fernando de Río, Chief Growth and Marketing Officer, also emphasises investing "con inteligencia" to translate vision into concrete indicators. Mariel Serrano, Head of Corporate Reputation, describes the "Talysist Bit" project as a "Business Management Plan Integral" that aims to "alignar y sincronizar esfuerzos en todos los plazos" to achieve strategic objectives.
    
2. **Financial Evaluation and Metrics (Business Case Elements):** A core component of justification involves financial evaluation, often resembling a business case.
    
    - **Cost-Benefit Analysis:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, indicates her area provides "coaching o consultoría interna" on "productividad, costo beneficio" for organisational decisions, aiming to "maximizar los recursos que son escasos" and ensure spending is "rentable y productivo". Carlos Granados, CIO, explicitly mentions "costos-beneficios" as a key criterion for integrating new technologies.
    - **Total Cost of Ownership (TCO) and Return on Investment (ROI):** For technology investments, Carlos Granados uses "TCO (Costo Total de Propiedad)" and "ROI esperado" as critical elements in the "Análisis Económico".
    - **Profitability and Efficiency:** Marcela Valdez aims to improve "efficiency and profitability" and measure "rentabilidad por programa, por ubicación". Álvaro García, Head of Corporate Sales, highlights "impacto económico" and "eficiencia operativa con márgenes y gastos". Humberto Salazar, Head of Sales, focuses on "mejorar el costo de adquisición y el aumento de la productividad de la fuerza de ventas". Lilian Lozano, Digital Marketing Director, also monitors "CPL" (cost per lead) and "tasa de conversión".
    - **Cash Flow and Debt Management:** For major strategic projects like the exit strategy for Promecap or mergers and acquisitions (M&A), Alberto Sánchez highlights the need to generate "suficiente caja y el generar suficiente EBITDA" to manage debt and ensure a "balance saludable" for external financing. Marcela Valdez also stresses the critical short-term challenge of managing "flujo de efectivo mínimo" and "recuperación de la cartera" (accounts receivable).
3. **Cross-Functional Collaboration and Project Evaluation:** Investment justification is a collaborative process involving various departments. Alberto Sánchez notes that "comunicación y colaboración" with all areas are "constante" because "they are the ones who know what projects they have in mind, what's coming, and we need to manage all the funds, we need to do the project evaluation, we need to present it". This implies that project ideas originate from different operational areas, which then need to be financially assessed and presented for approval. Carlos Granados's ideal collaboration involves strategic committees at various levels (strategic, tactical, operational) to make "decisiones clave". Fernando de Río also works closely with finance to decide "dónde invertir con inteligencia".
    
4. **Data-Driven Decision Making and Automation (Aspirational):** There is a strong aspiration to move towards more automated and data-driven justification processes.
    
    - **Automated Budget Optimisation:** Román de León, Data Scientist, explicitly proposes a project to "optimice el presupuesto disponible" using an "algoritmo" based on "necesidades reales" and "retroalimentación" from students. This aims to "asignar el presupuesto de manera más ágil" and ensure resources are better utilised for organisational objectives. He also mentions measuring "agilidad en la toma de decisiones" and "Adopción de IA en procesos y departamentos".
    - **Modernising Business Cases:** Julián Mendez, Operational Planning and Transformation, mentions the desire for "todo el tema de de presupuesto, todo el tema de business cases, es decir, de proyectos, este, que estuviera un poco más automatizado, más moderno, menos artesanal, menos uso de Excel, menos manual". Alberto Sánchez echoes this, desiring "herramientas digitales para para poder hacerlo" and "información visual para todos" in "tiempo real o casi".
    - **Predictive Analytics for Proactive Investment:** Carlos Granados envisions AI as an ally to improve "forecasts y presupuestos". Predictive analytics can also anticipate risks (e.g., student dropouts), which would inform where to invest resources for retention.
5. **Addressing the "Cost of Inaction":** Justification also comes from understanding the negative consequences of _not_ investing. Several leaders implicitly underscore the investment nature by lamenting the high costs, inefficiencies, and missed opportunities resulting from a lack of proper systems, integrated technology, or standardised processes. Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, notes that not having a consolidated quality system in place "generates re-work at all levels, physical resources, financial resources, it is stressful and leads to greater expense". Román de León points out that inadequate data quality and isolated systems lead to "inconsistencies de datos" and "rework" outside of systems. Marcela Valdez highlights how the "falta de integración entre sistemas, como el SAP y el Core Banner, genera controles abiertos y riesgos de descontrol". These "costs of not investing" provide a strong rationale for proactive expenditure.
    

talisis's investment justification process is evolving from traditional financial and strategic alignment to one that increasingly leverages data, automation, and cross-functional collaboration to ensure that resources are allocated to projects that promise the highest strategic impact and measurable returns, while mitigating the costs of inaction.

To further understand the maturity and effectiveness of their business case process, it would be beneficial to inquire if talisis has a standardised template or a formal checklist that all departments must adhere to when submitting proposals for significant Capex or Opex, and what specific post-implementation review processes are in place to assess whether the projected benefits (ROI, TCO, efficiency gains) were actually achieved.


### X. Relación con Clientes, Inversionistas y Autoridades

o   ¿Qué certificaciones se deben tener? ¿Se tienen?

Based on the comprehensive insights from the interviews, talisis operates within a regulatory and quality-driven environment, necessitating various forms of certifications and compliance. The organisation **does possess** several key accreditations and is actively working on maintaining and enhancing its adherence to diverse regulatory frameworks, while also pursuing new certifications that add strategic value.

Here is a detailed breakdown of the certifications and regulatory considerations for talisis:

### 1. Institutional and Programme Accreditations (Existing and Pursued)

talisis places a significant emphasis on formal academic accreditations, which are viewed as crucial for ensuring quality and building institutional prestige:

- **Finpes Accreditation:** Both the **Universidad Interamericana para el Desarrollo (UNID)** and **Universidad Regiomontana (UR)**, which are part of talisis, are accredited by **Finpes (Federación de Instituciones Mexicanas Particulares de Educación Superior)**. This accreditation is explicitly mentioned as a means to "garantizar la educación de calidad ordenada que se brinda a los estudiantes".
- **Reaccreditation Processes:** UNID is currently undergoing a "proceso de reacreditación a nivel sistema de todo el sistema". Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, highlights that this process is not merely about obtaining a "sello" (seal) but aims for the "fortalecimiento de nuestro sistema" and a "mejora de cómo gestionamos todos nuestros procesos académicos". The aspiration is to achieve the "nivel más alto, que son 7 años" of accreditation.
- **Language Programme Certifications (Harmon Hall):** Harmon Hall, one of talisis's brands, has specific accreditations such as **TOEFL (Toffeely) and TOEIC (Toic)**. These are vital for demonstrating the quality and recognition of their language programmes, as "esas acreditaciones son parte de el valor que ve el alumno y que el mismo mercado lo pide".
- **Dual Model Certification (UNID):** UNID is notably certified through a "red de universidades duales en Latinoamérica", which enables it to offer the "modelo dual puro y como se llama en Alemania". This makes UNID "la primera universidad en México ofrece el modelo dual puro", signifying a unique and highly valued certification that also opens "mayores oportunidades laborales para los estudiantes al graduarse".
- **Future Academic Recognition:** Álvaro García, from Corporate Sales, mentions that for new content and learning resources, "van a requerir un reconocimiento de validez oficial". This indicates an ongoing need for official endorsement of their educational offerings.

### 2. Regulatory Compliance (Ongoing and Critical)

Beyond specific accreditations, talisis must comply with a range of legal and governmental regulations, which are continuously monitored and adapted to:
