- **Fiscal and Financial Regulations:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, explicitly states that part of her department's mission is to "cumplir con las regulaciones fiscales". Her interactions involve "autoridades gubernamentales como son la Secretaría de Hacienda y Crédito Público la Comisión Nacional Bancaria de Valores, Economía, y y algunas otras", underscoring the critical nature of financial and banking compliance.
- **Labour Legislation:** Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, highlights the importance of staying informed about "reformas en el ámbito legislativo laboral" and working closely with labour advisors to "mantener cumplimiento normativo". Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, also notes that "temas sindicales" and the broader "sociopolítico" environment in Mexico can "afectar un poco" their operations due to their impact on organisational culture and productivity.
- **Data Privacy and Educational Norms:** Carlos Granados, CIO, stresses the importance of "cumplimiento de regulaciones internacionales" such as **GDPR/LGPD** and "Normativas educativas" when designing their AI and technological infrastructure. This indicates a proactive approach to data security and ethical AI use in education. Román de León, Data Scientist, further reinforces this by identifying "la regulación de datos educativos en OM-C37" as a critical external trend that influences his work.
- **Governmental Alignment:** Juan Arenas, COO, points to the necessity of allying with government institutions "para saber qué es lo que están haciendo y, por lo tanto, sumarnos a los proyectos estratégicos gubernamentales que nos permitan alinear nuestra oferta educativa". This proactive engagement ensures their programmes remain relevant and contribute to national educational goals. Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional, serves as a key figure representing talisis "ante nuestras autoridades ya sea autoridades educativas, autoridades gubernamentales, eclesiásticas, empresarios", further ensuring strong relationships and compliance.

### 3. Skill-Based and Micro-Certifications (Emerging Opportunities)

While not explicitly stated as having a large portfolio of _current_ skill-based certifications, the organisation recognises their growing importance and the opportunity to develop them:

- **Co-creation with Industry:** Fernando de Río, Chief Growth & Marketing Officer, mentions collaborating with the productive sector to "cocrear contenidos, certificar a las habilidades". This suggests an intention to develop and offer industry-recognised skill certifications, aligning education with employability needs.
- **Microcredentials and Upskilling:** The concept of "microcredenciales" and "cursos de educación continua" are discussed as flexible learning models to adapt to future job market needs. Román de León's insights also highlight the "demanda de UPSK" (upskilling) as an opportunity to "reciclar nuestros contenidos académicos de microlearning para empresas", implying that these micro-learning modules could lead to specific skill certifications.

### Perception and Strategic Value of Certifications

It's clear that certifications are not merely seen as bureaucratic requirements but as strategic assets:

- **Quality Assurance:** Inge Ploennig's perspective is that accreditation "asegura la calidad de el sistema educativo", albeit her personal view is that true quality "va más allá". The goal is for the accreditation process to genuinely lead to "mejoras" and a "fortalecimiento" of their systems.
- **Market Demand and Prestige:** Multiple leaders acknowledge that certifications (like those for Harmon Hall) are valued by students and "el mismo mercado lo pide". Accreditation also contributes to "prestigio" and positions talisis's institutions within a "grupo selecto de universidades".
- **Future-Proofing:** The continuous pursuit of new accreditations and compliance (e.g., with evolving data regulations, dual models) is part of talisis's strategy to stay "vigentes", "a la vanguardia", and responsive to changing market and societal needs.

talisis has a solid foundation of existing accreditations for its university programmes and is diligent in managing its regulatory compliance across various domains. There is a clear strategic intent to not only maintain these but also to actively pursue new forms of certifications, particularly in skill-based and micro-credential areas, to meet evolving market demands and solidify its position as a leader in educational innovation.

**Next Step Suggestion:** To further understand the effectiveness of talisis's certification strategy, it would be beneficial to explore how they communicate the value of these certifications and accreditations to prospective students and employers, and what mechanisms are in place for tracking the impact of these certifications on student employability and career progression.

o   ¿Se tiene algún trámite o permiso pendiente ante las autoridades?
Based on the comprehensive information from the provided sources, there is **no explicit mention** of any specific "trámites o permisos pendientes" (pending procedures or permits) with authorities for talisis.

However, the interviews provide extensive insights into talisis's ongoing engagement with regulatory bodies, its commitment to various forms of compliance, and efforts to adapt to evolving external landscapes, which indirectly touch upon the regularisation of processes or adherence to evolving norms.

Here is a detailed breakdown of talisis's relationship with authorities and its approach to regulatory compliance, as inferred from the interviews:

1. **Ongoing Regulatory Compliance and Interaction with Authorities:**
    
    - **Fiscal and Financial Regulations:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, explicitly states that a core part of her department's mission is to "cumplir con las regulaciones fiscales" (comply with fiscal regulations). She mentions active interactions with "autoridades gubernamentales como son la Secretaría de Hacienda y Crédito Público la Comisión Nacional Bancaria de Valores, Economía, y y algunas otras" (governmental authorities such as the Ministry of Finance and Public Credit, the National Banking and Securities Commission, Economy, and some others). This indicates a continuous engagement to maintain compliance, rather than addressing pending issues.
    - **Labour Legislation:** Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, highlights the importance of staying "muy de cerca con nuestros asesores laborales para poder pues realizar las las medidas y actualizaciones que sean necesarias, para estar cumpliendo normativamente con esos cambios" (very close with our labour advisors to be able to carry out the necessary measures and updates, to be normatively compliant with those changes). Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, also notes that "temas sindicales" (union issues) and the broader "sociopolítico" (sociopolitical) environment in Mexico can "afectar un poco" (affect a bit) their operations. These references point to ongoing efforts to adapt to and comply with labour laws.
    - **Data Privacy and Educational Norms:** Carlos Granados, CIO, stresses the importance of "cumplimiento de regulaciones internacionales" (compliance with international regulations) such as "GDPR/LGPD" and "Normativas educativas" (educational norms) when designing their AI and technological infrastructure. Román de León, Data Scientist, identifies "la regulación de datos educativos en OM-C37" (the regulation of educational data in OM-C37) as a critical external trend that influences his work. Katherine Romero and Lilian Lozano also discuss adapting to stricter "privacidad de datos" (data privacy) regulations. This demonstrates a proactive approach to evolving data protection regulations.
2. **Academic Accreditations and Reaccreditation Processes:**
    
    - Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, extensively discusses various accreditations. She confirms that both **Universidad Interamericana para el Desarrollo (UNID)** and **Universidad Regiomontana (UR)** are accredited by **Finpes (Federación de Instituciones Mexicanas Particulares de Educación Superior)**.
    - UNID is currently undergoing a "proceso de reacreditación a nivel sistema de todo el sistema" (system-level reaccreditation process for the entire system), aiming for the "nivel más alto, que son 7 años" (highest level, which is 7 years). While this is an ongoing process that requires active engagement and adherence to standards, it is a **reaccreditation for quality assurance** and academic prestige, rather than a pending permit for basic operation. Inge clarifies that this process is not merely about obtaining a "sello" (seal) but aims for the "fortalecimiento de nuestro sistema" (strengthening of our system) and a "mejora de cómo gestionamos todos nuestros procesos académicos" (improvement in how we manage all our academic processes).
    - Harmon Hall also holds specific accreditations such as "TOEFL (Toffeely) and TOEIC (Toic)", which are considered "parte de el valor que ve el alumno y que el mismo mercado lo pide" (part of the value seen by the student and demanded by the market itself).
    - Paulina Adalid, Rector Institucional, notes that UNID is "certificados a través de la red de de la red de universidades duales en Latinoamérica" (certified through the network of dual universities in Latin America), making it "la primera universidad en México ofrece el modelo dual puro" (the first university in Mexico to offer the pure dual model).
3. **Adaptation to Regulatory Context for Growth and New Offerings:**
    
    - Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, mentions that talisis is "limitados realmente con algunas normativas" (really limited by some regulations) when attempting to grow, particularly for certain technical or health-related teachings. He also states that new content and learning resources "van a requerir un reconocimiento de validez oficial" (will require official validity recognition). This implies that as talisis expands into new areas or develops new products, they proactively seek to understand and meet the necessary regulatory requirements, rather than being currently held back by pending permits for existing operations.
    - Juan Arenas, COO, emphasises the need to ally with government institutions "para saber qué es lo que están haciendo y, por lo tanto, sumarnos a los proyectos estratégicos gubernamentales que nos permitan alinear nuestra oferta educativa" (to know what they are doing and, therefore, join governmental strategic projects that allow us to align our educational offer). This reflects a proactive alignment with national educational goals and regulations.
    - Paulina Adalid serves as a key figure representing talisis "ante nuestras autoridades ya sea autoridades educativas, autoridades gubernamentales, eclesiásticas, empresarios" (before our authorities, be they educational authorities, governmental authorities, ecclesiastical, businessmen), ensuring strong relationships and compliance.
4. **Internal Process Challenges (not external permits):**
    
    - While not directly related to pending external permits, several interviewees highlight internal challenges that, if left unaddressed, could indirectly impact compliance or operational efficiency. Marcela Valdez mentions a "falta de integración entre sistemas" (lack of system integration) and an absence of a "master data bien diseñado y cierres periódicos" (well-designed master data and periodic closures) in core systems, leading to "controles abiertos" (open controls) and "descontrol". These are internal control and data management issues rather than external regulatory compliance problems. Similarly, the widespread call for better documentation and clearer processes is about internal operational discipline.

talisis actively manages its compliance with various regulations (fiscal, labour, data privacy) and undergoes continuous academic accreditation processes, the provided information does not indicate any specific "trámites o permisos pendientes" that are currently holding back its operations or necessitating urgent regularisation. The focus appears to be on maintaining existing compliance, adapting to evolving regulatory landscapes, and proactively seeking recognition for new educational offerings as part of its growth strategy.

To gain a more granular understanding, it would be beneficial to inquire whether talisis maintains a centralised registry of all licenses, permits, and accreditations required for its operations, including their expiry dates and renewal statuses, to proactively identify any potential future bottlenecks.

¿Qué temas están pendientes de regularizarse?

Based on the comprehensive information provided from the interviews, there is **no explicit mention** of any specific "trámites o permisos pendientes" (pending procedures or permits) or "temas pendientes de regularizarse" (topics pending regularisation) that are currently holding back talisis's existing operations or requiring urgent outstanding compliance actions.

However, the interviews extensively detail talisis's ongoing, proactive, and continuous efforts to ensure compliance with various regulations, adapt to evolving external landscapes, and formalise internal processes, which can be understood as an ongoing process of 'regularising' or aligning their operations with best practices and legal requirements.

Here is a detailed elaboration of talisis's engagement with authorities and its approach to regulatory compliance and internal formalisation:

**1. Proactive Regulatory Engagement and Compliance:** talisis's leaders consistently highlight their commitment to adhering to diverse regulatory frameworks:

- **Fiscal and Financial Compliance:** Marcela Valdez, Director of Administration and Finance, explicitly states that a core part of her department's mission is to "cumplir con las regulaciones fiscales" (comply with fiscal regulations) and "gestionar riesgos proactivamente, manteniendo controles internos robustos" (proactively manage risks, maintaining robust internal controls). She mentions active interactions with "autoridades gubernamentales como son la Secretaría de Hacienda y Crédito Público la Comisión Nacional Bancaria de Valores, Economía, y y algunas otras" (governmental authorities such as the Ministry of Finance and Public Credit, the National Banking and Securities Commission, Economy, and some others). This demonstrates continuous engagement rather than addressing a backlog of pending issues.
- **Labour Legislation:** Amalia Ortega, HRBP Director, emphasises the importance of staying "muy de cerca con nuestros asesores laborales para poder pues realizar las las medidas y actualizaciones que sean necesarias, para estar cumpliendo normativamente con esos cambios" (very close with our labour advisors to be able to carry out the necessary measures and updates, to be normatively compliant with those changes) in response to "reformas en el ámbito legislativo laboral" (reforms in the labour legislative field). Domingo Farias, Chief of Staff, also notes that "temas sindicales" (union issues) can "afectar un poco" (affect a bit) their operations, indicating an active management of this external factor.
- **Data Privacy and Educational Norms:** Carlos Granados, CIO, stresses the importance of "cumplimiento de regulaciones internacionales" (compliance with international regulations) such as "GDPR/LGPD" and "Normativas educativas" (educational norms) when designing their AI and technological infrastructure. Román de León, Data Scientist, identifies "la regulación de datos educativos en OM-C37" (the regulation of educational data in OM-C37) as a critical external trend that influences his work, implying ongoing adaptation. Katherine Romero and Lilian Lozano also discuss adapting to stricter "privacidad de datos" (data privacy) regulations, which demonstrates a proactive approach to evolving data protection regulations.

**2. Ongoing Academic Accreditations and Reaccreditation Processes:** A significant aspect of "regularisation" in an educational institution is maintaining academic accreditations.

- Inge Ploennig, Director of Quality and Academic Accreditation, confirms that both Universidad Interamericana para el Desarrollo (UNID) and Universidad Regiomontana (UR) are accredited by FINPES (Federación de Instituciones Mexicanas Particulares de Educación Superior).
- UNID is currently undergoing a "proceso de reacreditación a nivel sistema de todo el sistema" (system-level reaccreditation process for the entire system), aiming for the "nivel más alto, que son 7 años" (highest level, which is 7 years). This is an active and continuous process for quality assurance and academic prestige, rather than a pending permit for basic operation.
- Harmon Hall also holds specific accreditations such as "TOEFL (Toffeely) and TOEIC (Toic)", which are considered "parte de el valor que ve el alumno y que el mismo mercado lo pide" (part of the value seen by the student and demanded by the market itself).
- Álvaro García, Innovation and Product Director, mentions that new content and learning resources "van a requerir un reconocimiento de validez oficial" (will require official validity recognition). This indicates that as talisis expands into new areas or develops new products, they proactively seek to meet the necessary regulatory requirements.
- Paulina Adalid notes that UNID is "certificados a través de la red de de la red de universidades duales en Latinoamérica" (certified through the network of dual universities in Latin America), making it "la primera universidad en México ofrece el modelo dual puro" (the first university in Mexico to offer the pure dual model).

**3. Internal Process Formalisation and System Integration:** While not external permits, many leaders highlight internal challenges in process formalisation and system integration that, if left unaddressed, could indirectly impact external compliance or operational efficiency. Addressing these is a form of internal 'regularisation':

- **Lack of Documented Processes:** Alberto Sánchez explicitly states that "hay ciertos procesos que no están documentados" (certain processes are not documented) and they are "haciendo la tarea de documentar esos procesos" (doing the task of documenting those processes), requiring leaders' commitment for compliance once authorised. Alejandro Madrazo notes that "no existen suficientes procesos suficientemente claros y documentados para poder planear con anticipación" (there are not enough sufficiently clear and documented processes to plan in advance), leading to inefficiencies. Marcos Samaniego also highlights the need for a "repositorio documental de todos los procesos" (document repository of all processes).
- **System Disintegration and Data Inconsistencies:** Marcela Valdez points out a "falta de integración entre sistemas" (lack of system integration) between Banner (core student system) and SAP (financial system), leading to "controles abiertos" (open controls) and "descontrol". Román de León (Data Scientist) states that "demasiados sistemas que trabajan de manera aislada por lo cual hay inconsistencias de datos entre esas plataformas" (too many systems working in isolation, leading to data inconsistencies between platforms). This indicates a critical need for internal regularisation of data flow and system architecture.
- **Need for Central Data Architecture:** Luis Ruiz (Software Development) prioritises to "Construir esta arquitectura de datos que... permita recopilar la mayor información posible de nuestros alumnos docentes y administrativos" (Build this data architecture that... allows us to collect as much information as possible from our students, teachers, and administrators). This is a foundational project to address data fragmentation and enable better insights and compliance.
- **OKR Implementation:** Julián Mendez (Operational Planning & Transformation) mentions that the OKR system is being "pulido" (polished) and adapted, indicating ongoing efforts to standardise and formalise objectives across the organisation.

**4. Adaptation to Evolving External Landscape:** talisis actively monitors and adapts to external changes that might necessitate "regularisation" or adjustments in its strategy and operations:

- **Socio-political and Economic Factors:** Domingo Farias highlights that "el tema político, sociopolítico" (the political, sociopolitical issue) can affect operations due to "temas sindicales" (union issues). Marcela Valdez also points out that a "entorno económico complicado y recesivo" (complicated and recessive economic environment) impacts payment availability and requires careful financial management. These factors demand continuous adaptation and potentially, adjustments to operational models to remain compliant and viable.
- **Market Trends and Competition:** Álvaro García notes that talisis is "limitados realmente con algunas normativas" (really limited by some regulations) when attempting to grow in certain technical or health-related teachings. Juan Arenas, COO, emphasises the need to ally with government institutions "para saber qué es lo que están haciendo y, por lo tanto, sumarnos a los proyectos estratégicos gubernamentales que nos permitan alinear nuestra oferta educativa" (to know what they are doing and, therefore, join governmental strategic projects that allow us to align our educational offer). This proactive alignment helps ensure their offerings remain relevant and officially recognised.

While the provided sources do not list specific, outstanding "trámites o permisos pendientes" for talisis, the organisation is clearly engaged in a continuous and proactive process of managing compliance with existing regulations (fiscal, labour, data privacy, educational), undergoing academic reaccreditation, and actively working to formalise and integrate its internal processes and data architecture. These ongoing efforts are crucial for maintaining operational efficiency, ensuring quality, and adapting to the dynamic external environment, which collectively contributes to the overall 'regularisation' and long-term sustainability of the institution.

To gain a more precise understanding of potential future regulatory bottlenecks, it would be beneficial to inquire whether talisis maintains a centralised and actively managed register of all licenses, permits, and accreditations, including their respective expiry dates and renewal statuses. This would enable the proactive identification of any upcoming mandatory regularisation processes and their associated timelines and requirements.
